Here begins the life of saint katherin of senis the blessid virgin
Audi filia et vide
HEre daughter and see fructuous example of virtuous living to edyfycacio^ of
thy soul and to comfort and encrese of thy gostly labor in all werkis of
pity: For as I trust by the gracious yeftes of our lord Jhesu / thy will is
set to plese him and to do him secuyce in all holy exercise by the virtue of
obedyence under counseyll and techinge of thy gostely governors / And for as
much as I feel by long experyens the inward affeccions inclynyng with pity to
comfort of all that have need both living and deed therefore to strength and
comfort of thy will and of al other of thy gostely sustere^ which our lord*
has graciously chose to serve him night and day in prayer and meditacio^ and
to labor bodily in time of need to socour and help of the seek and the pour
/ Here I purpos by our lordis mercy only in his worship with trust of his
grace and leave by help of your prayers to translate in english tongue the
legende and the blessid life of an holy maid and virgyn which was and is
called Katheryn of seen.

This legende compyled a worshypfull clerk friar Reymond of the order of saint
domynik doctor of deuynyte and confessor of this holy virgyn / But in this
translacion I leave of the two prologues which in the beginning the same clerk
made in latin. The which passes your understanding / And to touch all
matters only that longs only to your lernyng by cause that much manner of her
virtuous living shall be rehersyd in especial in chapytres of this book: which
in general words he touches shortly in his prologue: I leave of also points
of diuynyte which passes your vnderston dyng and touch only matters yt
longs to your lernyng / Now tha^ as I said in the beginning / Here daughter
and see what thou herest or redest of this holy maid and vyrgyn. And that thou
give full credence to that I shall write / The veryte may be preuyd without any
feynyng biscryptures of her confessors and verefyeng of creatures which late
lived in earth / Also the vytnes I purpose to put in at the end of each
chapter / as that worshypfull clerk did / Which compyled this book in
latin. Therefore that all our work begin and performed in the name of the
holy trynyte: This book shall be divided in three parties and each part of the
book shall be departed in to diverse chapyters / which chapyters been compyled
to gyder in the beginning in manner of a kalendre that ye mow redely find:
What matere in the book ye desire to here or read:

The first part of the book shall be the birth and the holy werkis of that
maid from her chyldhode and tender age In to the time that she was spoused
merueylously and gracyously to our lord*

The second part conteyneth the manner of her conversation from the time of
her despousacion to our lord. And what our lord wrought in her in to the time
yt she passyd out of this world /

The third part shall show the passing out of this world of the same maid
with miracles which our lord wrought for her in her life and after: and thus by
the mercy and grant of our lord almighty this work shall be termynyd to the
lawde of that holy. Trynyte to whom be honor and glory ever without end Amen:

Capitulum j THe first chapter of the first part of this forsayde blessed
maid and virgyn katheryn treteth of her progenyte and of other matters which
byfyll touching her or she went out openly abroad: And of her fader and mother
and of the condycions of her / C ij Of her birth and of merueylous werkynge.
which our lord wrought: And showed in the chylhode of this holy maid and
vyrgyn: C iij Item of the vow made of her vyrgynyte and of other virtuous
living and miracles which befyll till she came to the age of abylyte to be
wedded to man: but wedded was she not and never would / C iiij Item how her
fervor of devotion was wythdrawe which our lord suffered for encrece of more
grace following / and of her strong patience with which patience she suffered
in her faders house many Iniuryes / C v Item of the victory which she had of
them that desesed her and that was by a culuer the which her fader saw by a
vysyon of saint domynyk / C vj Item of the hardenesse of her bodily penance
and of afflyccion^: And what persecucion she suffered therefore of her mother /
Ca. vij Item of the last vyctorye that she had in a bathe: And how she took
the habyte of saint dominyk which she had long desired tofore: Ca viij Item
of the begynnyge and fondament of the relygyous state of the susteren of the
penance of saint domynyke: And wherefore come the manner of living of the
susteren / C ix Item of her wonderful encrece / and how she profyted in virtue
and holy living / And that she should be leuyd in all things which she
rehearsed to her consessour of graces do to her lord / C x Item of a noble
doctryue and notable which our lord gave to her in the beginning and of other
doctrynes in the which he founded her manner of living Capitulum xj Item of
merueyllus victory of temptacions by another manner of doctrine give to her of
our lord / And of a famylyaryte or homlyhed which she had with our lord
which has not beherde to fore / c xij Item of her merueylous despousacio^
with the which she was wedded in faith of our lord and to our lord with
arynge / C xiij
HEre begins the second part in the which is showed
Capitulum j the conversation of this holy maid and vyrgyn with men. And how
the yeftes the which she had received of our lord pryuely enclosed within her
self. Were openly showed to the world / And first how our lord bad her that:
that she should be conuersaunt among men: C ij Item of merueylous deeds which
she had in exercise and of miracles which befyll in the beginning of her
conversation among men: C iij Item of wonders which she did in help and in
comfort to the necessyte of them that were pour and nedy: C iiij Item
merueylous deeds which she did in lowly and besy service to them that were
seek: C v Item of the synguler manner of lyuinge: And how they were desceyued
that grutched with her merueylous fasting Capitulum vj Item of the wonderful
rauysshynge and excesses of her mind from her bodily wits and great
reuelacions showed to her of our lord / C vij Item of sum miracles graciously
wrought by this holy maid and virgin about the health of sowles C viij Item
of sum miracles do in her life by her about the life and help of mennys
bodies / C ix Item of miracles vrought by this holy maid and vyrgyn about the
delyueraunce of them which were acombred and vexed with fendes: C x Item of
the yefte of prophecye. And how by that yefte she delyuerd many me^ and wymmen
fro perils both of body and of soul: C xj Item of miracles which our
lord wrought by this holy maid and vyrgyn in herbs / breed / and wine / And
other things that had none life: C xij Item of the often resceyuynge of the
holy sacrament of the altar And of miracles the which our lord did to her
touching that holy sacrament / and other holy relyques of saints / Ca xiij
HEre begins the third part wherein is rehersyd
Capitulum j the deyeng of this holy maid and vyrgyn and miracles that were I
showed after her death: And first of the witnesses which were present at her
passing and enfourmed the auctur of this book which and what they were / Cap
ij Item of the merueylous things which befyll a year and half to fore the
death of this holy maid and vyrgyn / And of the martyrdom that she suffered
bodily of the wicked fendes whereof at ye last she had her bodily death: C
iij Item how this holy maid and vyrgyn desired to be unbound from the body
and be with christ / And that is preuyd by a devout prayer which she made /
And is put in the end of another book which she made: and what is in that
book generally and shortly it is written in this book with the same oryson: c
iiij Item of the time that she passed and when she passed out of this world /
and of the sermon which she made to her gostely dyscyples and susteren tofore
her passing / And how she informed them in general / and in special how they
should govern them when she were go^ / And of a vysyon which was showed to a
matrone in the hour of her passing. Ca v Item of tokens and miracles which
our lord wrought after her death of this holy maid and vyrgyn both tofore
her beryeng. and after that is to say of miracles which were know: And for
many that were not know: Cap vj Item of the mighty and strong paciens which
this maid and vyrgyn showed openly from her first age and young in to her death
by the which virtue clerly it preuyd that ryghtfull she is worthy to have the
name of holiness in gods church in earth* when she is made so fair and
glorious in gods church in heaven / and in this chapter is a recapitulacion
of all that is said to fore: For worthynes and also for werynes of reders / And
also for if each man may not have al this legende they may have the substance
of this martyr tofore her compendyously rehersyd in the last chapter /
The first chapter of this first part is of the progenye of this holy maid
and vyrgyn glorious saint katheryn of seen and of other matters which befyll
touching her: or she went out openly abroad And of her fader and mother and of
the condycions of them / Capitulu^ primu^
IN the cite of Geene in Italye and of the prouynce of Tuskane there was a man
his name was Janes or Jacob and his fader was called in the common speech of ye
contree Beuencasa: This James was simple virtuous without fraud or deceyte to
any man dredynge god and fleyng all evil: After the death of his fader and
mother he took a wife of the same Cite / her name was lapa: She was a woman
without such malice that is used among men that been now in our time / all be
it that she was full besy about that longs to household and about meynye and
servants as it was known openly to all that knew her while she lived here
in earth / when they both were joined to gyder in matrymonye and lyuyd
virtuously in symplycite / suffycient habondaunce they had of temperall gods
/ and they both of gentle and commendable birth. Our reverend lord blessed
lapa graciously and fulfilled her plentuously with the birthe of children as an
habondaunt vine in the house of Jacob which was her husbond. For each year
almost she conceived and bare a sone or a daughter and often fythes ij. sons or
two daughters / After time this Jacob was passes out of this world: Lapa his
wife as for a synguler laud and commendacion / rehersyd and said to master
Reymonde the confessor of this holy maid and vyrgyn and glorious martyr
katheryn that she was ever of so like dysposycion and so moderate in word /
that what occacion ever came or trouble or trybulacion / he exceded never in
speech by hasty ne angrye word / but when he saw any of his meyny grieved or
herd hem speak angerly or bitter words / anon he comforted each of them with
a glad ^here and said in ye manner of that contree. A brother good day be to
the: be not troubled: speak not such words which falls ne seems not us to
speak / And in special lapa his wife wherseth that when on a time one of his
neybours dysesyd him and wrongfully asked him a great som^e of monye which he
owed not by none reason* and so much he vexed him that simple man with the
might of other friends and supplanted him with great wrongs that he brought
him to the loss of all his gods / And in all this time: this good man might
never suffer in his presence a man to curse him wrong ne to speak of him harm
in no wise / In so much that he blamed his wife Lapa with soft words: and
said suffer dear wife / ye good day be to the for our lord shall show him
therrour. and he shall be our defendour: which words were found southe
afterward: for the veryte was showed openly as like to a miracle: And he for
pain that he had in his conscience delyuerd again how much he had errid
in his wrongful persecucion to the good man Jacob / These words said Lapa to
master Reymonde to whose words he yaue full trust / for as it was know to
all that knew her: she was of so much symplenesse at her age of xxiiij year:
that though she would have lied: she ^^wde not have feyned such a lesyng:

And so was the commyn testymonye of all tho that knew her husbonde. Jacob
that was he a man full simple by Innocencye and ryghtfull: always fleyng from
evil: Also this good mannys softenes in speech was so virtuous / that all
his meyny namely wymmen dame sels taught in his soole might not speak ne here
no word that were not semely or dyshoneste: In so much that one of his
daughter which was called Bonauentura was wedded to a young man which was
called Nycolas of the same Cite with whom were conuersaunt many other young men
of his age by cause he had another fader ne mother / And these men and he
without any refreynynge of tongue spoke each to other* and he with other: And
they with him foul words of dyshoneste matter. This Bonauentura at the last
took thereof so great an heaviness that she fill in to such sykenes that fro day
to day more and more she waxed lene / and vanysshed almost away and right
feeble /

Her husbonde saw this and asked her the cause of her heaviness and sickness
/ And she answered and said. I was norysshed in mine faders hours. and there was
I never wont to here such words as I here now every day / And so was I
never taught of my fader and mother / wherefore know it for sothe but this
dishoneste of speech be avoided fro this house within a short time / ye shall
see me deed: when her husbond herd this both he avoided that ungoodly
langage* and the felawshyppe and therwyth he was edefyed much more than ever
he was before* as well of the virtues lyuinge of the fader and mother as of her
daughter / that was his wife / And anon he forbode his felawes never more to
speak such manner words in her presens and no more they deed: and so the
softenes and the honest of Jacob his house amendyd in moderaunce / And the
dyshoneste of Nycolas house which had weddyd Jacob his daughter

Ferthermore ye shall understand ye Jacob used the craft of making of colors
wherwyth woollen and wolle clothes ben dyed: This craft used both he and his
sonys / In that contree they ben called dyers. wherefore full wonderfully god
ordained that a dyers daughter shol be made the spouse of the Emperor of
heaven: As ye shall see by gods grace after in this book: Sum of this that I
have showed in this chapter / was know to the more part of the cite / And
som^e her confessor had of the said maid katheryn and of her mother and of
many relygyous persons and of seculers / which were neybours and of kynrede to
the same Jacob and to his wife.

Of her birth and of the merueylous werkinge which our lord wrought and
showed in the chylhode of this holy vyrgyn and maid / Capitulu^ ij
When this foresaid Lapa which was like a fructuous vine by fulfyllyng the wine
of Jacob her husbonde in bryngyng forth full often both sons and daughters /
It befyll about the last time of the berynge of children by the ordinance
and die sposycyon of our lordis mercy that she conceived and brought forth; two
daughters / freell and febyll by nature. But much more freell by of bodily
strength as seemed outward* but strength and stabylnesse they had in the
sight of god.

When Lapa the mother besely beheld them she thought well that she suffysed
naught to nourysshe them both forth with her own milk / wherefore by a good
auysement she committed that one to smother noryse / And that other she
wythhelde and kept stylle to be norysshed forth with her own milk: And so
it befyll by the ordinance of our lord / that she chosed that daughter to her
own keeping* which our lord of everlasting time had chose unto his spouse
Both they resceyued the grace of baptysme And all be it that they were of the
nombre of gods chose children / Yet the foresaid maid was called katheryn and
that other was called Johan This later suster when she had received this
grace of baptysme in the same grace. she went forth to heaven / For in short
time after she passed out of this world. Katheryne abode stylle sukkyng on her
moders breasts by gods ordinance she should draw to heaven a long cheyn^ of
soulis / And for as much as Lapa ye mother consyderyd that katheryn abode and
that other was deed: She nourysshed her more dyligently hopyng that she was
chose to abide and be gods child

And often sythes this mother lapa would say to master Reymond her confessor
to this holy maid that she louyd katheryn passyngly above all the sons and
daughters that ever she had /

She said unto him also that she conceived so often that she might never
nourysshe any child of her with her own milk: Katheryn she nourysshed forth
in to ye end of the time yt she neded to be under the nourysshe / And in all
that time she conceived not / as it seemed that our lord for that daughter
had granted her a time of rest of traueylyng of the birth of children: and
in a token that she might come to the end of conceyuyng and birth: in that
daughter which should after ateyne and get the end of all perfection /

But yet this mother Lapa after the nouryssyng of katheryn* ones she conceived
and bare a daughter which was called Johan: And there she made an end of
beryng of children after that she had bo^en xxv children /

When this maid was thus brought forth and hallowed to god: And when she had
left the milk: and took to ete bread while she went about alone: She began
to be so acceptable and so byloued to all tho that saw her and so wise: and
wonderful words she spoke: that uneaths her mother might hold her in her
own house / Each man about of her neybours and of her kynrede lad her home
with them / and glad they were who might have her to here her wise speech /
And that they might have felawshyp and the gladenesse of that young maid. So
that of a manner gladdenesse and of a passing solace they called her not by her
own right name katheryn: but Eufrosyna: and what meued them to call her so:
they wist not them self / but she afterward sum time would say and suppose
that it was a mystery by cause she purposed to follow saint Eufrosyne in living
/

Her confessor that wrote this legende supposed that the young maid in her
chyldis speech used sum manner of sownynge that nyghed or acorded to that n^me
Eufrosyne. And so in manner as they would reherce her words they called her
so by that name: Nevertheless what ever it was that appieryd she burgenyd out
in her chilhode as a tree by any such showing what fruit was brought forth
Afterward in her old age the wisdom and the prudence of her speech and
connyng and the sweetness of her holy conversation might not be rehearsed with
tongue lygthly write with pen by them that knew only the veryte of this /
which had very experyence: She had also an Inward werkynge which showed
well* not only by her speech but by her co^uersacion where thorugh many mennys
sowlis were draw to god: And had thorugh her grace great lykyng and savor
in god in somoche that all heuynesses were excluded of all mennys hertes which
were conuersaunt with her* and not only that but all things that noyed the
soul was put away. Also the remembrance of each noye or angwysshe was take
away / And of this followed each man so great rest and stabylnesse / of soul
which they had before that every man woundred of them self / and made Joye
with a new manner of gladdenesse / and each man in his own soul cried and
said: Here it is good for us to be* Make we three tabernacles for our dwelling
place /

And of this none wou^der for douiles* he was there hid inuysybly in the
breast of his spouse which was transfygured in the hylle / As saint Peter
said and other appostles:

Now ferthermore to our purpos this chosen maid in her full tender age soon
began to wax and was comforted with the holy ghost in token that she should be
soon fulfilled with the dyuyne wisdom / About her age of five year when she
was taught to say the salutacion of the angel / Aue maria: She recordyd it
besely and said it full often / And when she could say it as she was enspired
from heaven: She began to great our lady going upward on a stayere and coming
dou^ward on the same stayere at each grees of the stayere to worship our lady
with an Aue maria / This she told her confessor afterward in the secret^^esse
of confession. By this ye may s^e that she that first in the beginning showed
forth first plesyng and acceptable words to men after that young age she began
to stye up from things that were inuysyble.

After this holy beginning the encresed every day* And than as it pleasyd our
lord the was vyse^ed with a gracyous and a wounderfull vysyon to stere her and
to show here her gifts of grace of the holy ghoost: And to show other how a
little plant should be brought forth and so nourysshed in to an him tree of
Cidre by the moyster of the holy ghost About her age of vj year. It befyll that
this chosen maid with her brother Steven sum what elder than she went to
her suster Bonauentura / Of which suster is made mention before / perauentur
on someuer end or to look how she ferde as the manner of friends of kynrede is
so to do /

when she had do that they were bode to do in her going homward again by
the way which is called in her tongue wallis piacta / This holy may lift up
her eyes: and against her over the church of the freer prechours she saw in
the air a full fair chamber ryally aparayed with all riches and honest /
where our lord Ihesu Christ in a trone Imperyall clothed with pontyfycall
vesture having on his head a myter papal /

And with him were saint Peter and saint Poule / and saint Johan Euan gelyst.
And when she beheld all this she was first a stonyd /

But by a vysement stably she stood still and with a louyngyng heart devoutly
she looked on her savior both with bodily and gostely eyes / And anon our
lord drew her love to him mercy fully set his even of his mageste upon her
graiously and louyngly with a manneuer smylyng chere / And reched out his right
arm toward her / and over her* and gave her his blessyng with the token of the
holy cross / And after the manner of other Bysshoppes and prelates /

The grace of this gift of god was spedfull and so effectuously put in her
that anon she was transformed and rauysshed in spyryte unto our lord whom she
saw / And behylde with so great gostely liking / and not only her gooyng /
and her way was out of her mind: but fully she had forgoten her self. And
often the went in the way beside men and bestes / By nature dreadful should be
as a child: but ever the eyes and the head were upward abydyng upon that
blysfull vysyon and none doughte so she would have abide but she had be
touched or take away by sum other body as long as that vysyon had endured:

But at the las^e whiles this was showed to the maid* Steven her brother held
forth his way and was passed her a great space wenyng that she had followed
him: But when he turned him and saw her not follow / he turned again and
saw his suster fer^e be hynde stondyng still in the way and look up in the
fyrmament /

And then he cried after her with alowde voys and called her she answerde not
and take none head. Then he went nere cryeng afterher: but his voys helped
not:

He woundred and went then and drew her by the hand and said: what do
thou here why come thou not forthr she anon cast down a little her eyes as
she had awaked of an heavy sleep and said / A if thou saw that I saw / thou
would not have let me from this holy vysyon:

And anon as she had said^^*o words She lift up her eyes again to be hold
more up that she had seen /

But the vysyon was all wythdrawe and cesyd / as his will was which aperyd to
fore: And that might she not bear without a sharp stroke of sorrow /

And anon she vengyd her on her self with sore weeping for sorrow that she
cast down her eyes: And from that time and hour / This young maid and
vyrgyn saint Katheryn began to wax old in virtues and sadness of manners and
to have a wounderfull wit and a felyng body bot^e by grace and by nature /

In so much that her deeds were ^other chyldysshe ne as a young woman.

But they seemed rather to all men that they came of the wysedom of a great
worshypfull age:

So that anon was showed that the fire of dyuyne love was kyndeled in her
heart / by the which virtue her intellection was made clear. Her will was
fervent her memory was comforted and all her outward werkyng showed in all
things the rewle of gods law:

And as she said in confession to hyrconfessour full mekely and lowely that she
learned and knew at that time with out techyng of any body or any redynge or
heryng / only by the ^nfusyon of the holy ghoose / the leuyng and the manners
of the folly faders of Egypt / and the living of many other Saints / and
specially of the life of Saint Domynyk*

She had so great desire to follow the living of the holy fadres and Saints
that she might no thing else think / but how that she might come thereto.

And by that cause many new things began in that holy maid / that her holy
living and deeds brought all men in to a wonder. For after that time she
sought out where that she might have a pryue place to abide in preuely when
she would use bodily afflyccyons / and when she would occupye her in prayer
and holy medytacyons*

In that place at certain times she scourged her little tender body with a
little scourge. She left of all manner pleye^ and dysportes / and besely gafe
her to prayer and medytacyons / full stylle she was and gaf all to scylence
every day more and more / ageynste the condy cyon of children less bodily mete
she took then she was wont to fore. And that is not wont to fall in
children that he wexynge.

Exemplum.
By the exsaumple of this young maid / many damse^^ys of dwelling there nigh /
and of her age were steryd to god by grace / and gadred to here of her holy and
gracyous wordys / and after her power to follow her holy werkys / where thorugh
it fill that all tho children at certain times ^amen to gyder in to a preuy
place of her hows where she dwelled / as she had chosen to fore her self /
and all they scour gyd hem self as she did. And each of them said a
certain Pater noster / and of Aue maria / as Katheryne bad him say.

All these werkyngee were but tokenys of gretter meruaylles that should follow
after that.

For as her mother told full often to Master Reymond.

And she when he asked her might not deny hit / that full often going upward
and dounward the grees of her faders hows vysybly to all their syghte that
saw her. Swyf^^ly she went in the air and touched no grees with her fete /
and this fylle namely when she would flee a way out of company / and
specially from the syghte of company of men.

And for as much as she had a gretely king in the beginning to say her Aue
maria. And to great our lady there with in going up and down on her faders
grees. Therefore it is to suppose that this miracle was showed there rather
thanne in another place.

Forthermore for as much as she had knowing of the life of holy faders of
Egypt by reuelacyon / therefore with all her strengthes she was steryd gretely
to follow hem.

In so much that in ye young tender age full feruentely she desired to be in
the wilderness as the holy faders were in old time / but she might not be
think her by what manner way she might perform her desire / and by cause it
was not ordained of god that she should dwell in so solytary place. Our lord
suffered her to stand to the wit of her proper nature as in that.

And she might no more know what she should do as touching that purpose / than
her own chyldes wit would show her. And right so it befyll that she with
her fervent will to her purpose she overcame the tendrenesse and the frealte of
her age / but yet had she not the parfyte vyctorye. For erly on a morowty de
she thought to go to the deserte or else wilderness and abide in a solytary
place / wherefor by chyldys prouydence she purueyed her of a lofe of bread and
of no more. Forth she went toward her susters hows that was wedded / which
hows was fast by the gate is clepyd the gate of saint Ansanye. She passyd her
sustrer hows / and forth she went out at that gate / and so did she never
before / and so passyd forth till she came to a way out of the Cite where she
saw no hows stand nyghe there as she did in the cite.

And then she thought well she was nyghe the deserte / yet went she somewhat
forther / and at the last she found a little cave under a bank / which
plesyd her well* And forth she went in with a glad heart wenyng to her that
she had fond the wilderness which that she had desired. And all be it
that she it had not yet our lord almighty god whom she beheld long to fore
and receyned his holy blyssyng / which gladly acceptyth all holy desires /
all be it that our lord had not dysposed his spouse to have that manner of
living / yet would not he suffer that deed that she did of good desire to
pass away with out a token / to sheweher that she did was acceptable and
plesyng to him. And anon as she began to pray there fervently / she was I
lift up little and little from the earth / and the body went up as high as
the height of the cave would suffer / and so she stood in prayer fro the morrow
in to none.

This maid perceived well that she was areryd from the earth / and as for
that time she wend it had been the wor^hyng of her enemy / which would with
his frauds and dysceytes let her prayer and desire that she had to the
deserte / And for that cause she besyed her and enforced her the more stablye
and fervently to pray. At the last about the hour of the day when our lord
after his passy on of the cross was take down fro the cross / she descendyd
little and little as she ascendyd. And by Inspyracion of our lord she had
understanding and knowing that the time was not yet I come where in she should
not put her body in such afflyccyon for our lord. Ne that she should leave
her faders hows in such manner / wherefor she turned as she came. But when she
went out and saw she was allone and beheld the gate of the Cytee long and
full fe^re to her age and feblynesse dredynge also that her fader and mother
should wene that she had be lost. She could no more but began to pray and
committed her fully to god.

And anon in a short while by the ordinance and might of our lord she was
borne up in the air and set in the gate of the Cytee with out any harm /
And anon she went home in all the have that she might or could. This she
told to a Cosyne of here is / which was called Laxa. But to her fader and mother
all this was hid and unknown till she came to elder age / for they wend
she had come fro her susters hows that was wedded. Of this that is showed in
this chapter in sum party. Lapa her mother told to master Reymond

Which was her last confessoure / and in sum party her self / and of sum
Laxa her cosyne not wythstondyng that he had great sweetness of all that is
I wrytton and said a fore / Save at the last both of her first confessor /
which was I nourysshed in her faders hows / and of many worshypfull and true
matro^s of neighbors nyghe / and of other beside nygh to her fader and mother /
and to her /

Of her vow made of virgynyte and of other virtuous living and meruaylles
which be fill till she came to the age of abylytee / to be wedded to man / but
wedded was she not ne never would / Capitulu^ iij
SO much virtue and grace was in that vysyon / which is rehersyd in the next
^hapytle to fore that all worldly love and affection was with drawn out from
the heart of this holy young maid / and only the holy love of goddys sone and
of the glorious maid and mother of our lord Ihesu christ / stylly and
steadfastly was prented in her heart* Wherefore she set all thing at naught
/ so that she might ouely win our lord her savior. And anon she had clear
understanding only by the techyng of the holy ghoost / that is full semyng and
according to our lord and our maker of naught to be served with all purytee
and ^lenues both in body and in soul. Wherefore she desired fully to have and
keep the clennesse of virgynytee / and for that she thought well and knowing
her by the techynge of god that our blessed lady goddys mother was the first
that found the life of virgynytee / wherefor this maid conceived in her heart
that up that matter she would have recourse to our lady for help and counseyll.
And when that she came to seven year age / she took great auysemente as though
she had be of sadness of xx year of age and contynuelly she prayed our lady
queen of angels and virgynes that she would wouchesauf to help her and get
her of our lord a parfyte way to the techynge of the holy ghoost / where by
she might do that were most plesynge to god / and most spedefulle for health
of her soul. And in each prayer ever she showed her desire to our lady how
sore she desired to live an aungelslyf / and in the life of virgynytee. And in
all this time the love of the everlasting spouse was more fervent fro day to
day in this maidens heart / which love steryd all her soul with out any
cessyng unto an heavenly living. And when this wise maid saw how fervent her
spyryte was in that desire / by cause she would not quench the spirit /
which that freely and gracyously had granted that she asked by a hot
kyndelyng of desire. Upon a day thanne she chose her a preuy place / where no
body might here her / and where she might speak all a loud with a high voys
what ever she would say there with all lowness of body and soul.

Thus spak she to our lady and said

O most blyssedfull Lady and most holy vitgyne / which first among all
wymmen thou halowedest for ever thy virgynytee to our lord with making to him a
vow / of whom thou were made mother of his only sone. Thy pity which may not
be spoke ne told of tongue lowely I beseech and pray that be none of my
merytes and notwythstondyng mine unworthiness wouches auf gracyous lady to do
me so much grace / that thou me spouse to him only whom I desired with all
the strengthes of my soul / and that is thyn holy sone my lord Ihesu christ
and here I make to him and to the fulle promysse that I shall never take other
spouse / and I shall keep to him my virgynyte vndefowled after my might and
pour / Loo maidens that read this / Loo vere ye may se how ordynatly all the
yeftes and virtuous werkyng and dedys of this holy maid were dysposed and
ordained by that everlasting wisdom / which myghtely dysposeth all things
in softnes. In the age of syy year she saw her spouse with her bodily eye /
and took of him his blyssynge. In the age of seven year she made a vow of
virgynyte. Takes head also by what auysement and what order she kept in
making her auowe. First she desired and asked to have him to her spouse /
whom her soul louyd. After that desire and askyng she forsook every manner
spouse behotyng to him troth and feyth for ever lasting. This petycyon might
not be denied. Takes head also whom she prays / and for whom she prayed /
and how she prays. First she prays that lady / which has properly inacte
the lyberalytee and the fredome of all graces / and can not but ever grant
and give grace. Be a man never so foul for sin / she holds her self
dettour to all both to wise and to unwise She despyseth none / she opened her
hand to each man that has need / and stretched out her pawmes to each pour
man / and shows out her self to all folk as a well that never faylled. How
should that gracyous lady not here that little maid so Innocent and fervent /
which puttyth not away from her grace sinful men / and women of elder age.
How should not our glorious lady receive the purpose of virgynyte of that holy
maid / which gracyously first among men found out the holy and clean lif
of virgynytee. How should our merciful and pyteuous lady deny this little
maid her sone / which drew him from heaven to the earth / for he should be
give to all that belyued on him. Now ye have seen whom this maid prayed Sith
now I pray thou for whom she prayed She asked that same / which he him self
taught for to ask which is asked. She sought that same which he byddeth
all men to seek that shall be sought. And he him self that shall be sought
may not put away ne put of. And the petycyon of such a thing must nedys have
grant after our lords promise where he said Askyth and ye shall have /
Speaks and ye shall find. He said also in another place. First sekyth the
kingdom of god and his ryghtwysnesse.

Therefore when this maid and so besely sought so tymely in so tender
chyldys age the sone of god / which is him self the kingdom of god / How or
what manner might it be / but that she should find what she sought / or have
that she asked / Ferthermore now sees in what manner she prayed or asked that
she desired / and ye shall clearly see that her prayer might not be done
away ne voydyd / She dysposed her self to receive that she asked / not only
for the time that now is / but for all the time that is to come / She remeuyd
all her obstacles / she clothed her with a plesable clothing of pouerte to
him for ever of whom she asked her desire / She bond hyrself / and oblysshed
her with a solemn vow as to fore god / And so straytely restrained her
self / that never the world ne the fend should let her dysposycyon /

In all this time there faylled her no condycyons / which a prayer should have
/ but that prayer must need be herd that she asked for her self / she asked
fulle mekely that was helthefull / and that was all health / feythfully she
stood and stedfastely / and to represente her perseuerau^ce. She made a
perpetuell vow where by she remeuyd all that should be obstacle for her
petycyon. Here may ye sekerly conclude that nedys she most be herd of our
lord / thinks then sekerly that as she asked so she resceyued of our lord.

And took her lord and her love for her everlasting spouse of his blysfulle
mother as she desired / and by help of that glorious lady she was coupled for
ever to her dear sone by a perpetuell vow of virgynyte / as it shall be proved
with the help of our lord by a clear token in the last chapter of this first
party. But now ferthyrmore ye shall know that after this vow this maid
began every day to wexe more holy and holy. And in that tender age she began to
take battle with her flesh / which as yet began never to be rebel. But for
all that she purposed to take a way from her flesh all flesshly mete as
much as she might. Wherefore when flesh was leyde to her / as it fylle
often / either she leyde it to Stephen her brothyr or preuely little and little
she voyded it / that no body should perceive it. She continued always her
dysplyens / of which I spoke a fore / and encresed hem more sharply either
allone by her self / or with other young maidens. Also a great well of othyr
sowles health began to be kyndelyd in her / and that was wonderful in such a
chyldes heart / and syngulerly she loved all tho saints / which labored
specially a boute the health of man's soul. She had also knowing only by
the techynge of god that Saint Domynyk ordained the order of friar prechours
for love of the feythe of holy church / and for the health of man's soul.
Wherefore she had that order in so much reverence / that when she saw frerys
of that order passing forth in the way by her faders how se / she marked well
where they went / and when they were passyd fulle mekely and deuoutely she
kyssed the steps of their fete. From that time forward / there wext a great
desire in her soul to go unto that order that she might profit man nes soul
with other brethern of that order / but by cause she saw a great obstacle in
that she was a woman. Therefore she thought to follow Saint Eufrosyen as me^
clepyd her in childhode wonderfully as for a pronostycacion / that right as
saint Eufrosyen feyned her a man / and went in to a monastery of monks / in
the same manner this maid is purposed to seyne her a man / and go in to far
contree where she was not know / and take the abyte of the order of friar
prechours / where she might help sowles and save them from perysshyng. But yet
not wytfstondyng that same thought and purpose abode long in her mind. Our
lord suffered not that thought to be performed in dedene brought to execucyon /
for ye love was put from her mind to another end / and our lord would also in
another manner fulfill her desire. In all this time this maid wexte fast in
body and encreced in age / but much more her soul encreced in virtue. Mekenes
wext fast / and devotion encreced / feyth was more clear / hope was gretely
strengthed. Charity multyplyed her fervor. And of all this virtues was gendryd
a virtuous / and a worshypfull sadness of maneres / and of relygyous put in
the sight of al men which considered her dedys. The fader and the mother were
astonyed / her brethern and susteren wondered gretely.

All the meyne of her faders hows meruaylled beholding and perceiving so
high wisdom in so tendyr age.

And among many notable wise words and dedys / one I will show you here in
co^mendacyon of that maid. Hit befylle at that time after seven year and to
fore ten year age that for devotion that her mother had to saint Anthonye. She
would have a mass I said in the worship of the same Saint / wherefor she
clepyd Katheryne her daughter and took her a certain of candelles and a
certain of silver and said.

Goo daughter to our parysshe church and pray our parysshe priest to sing or
do sing a mass in the worship of saint Anthonye. And offer these candelles
and this money up to the awtre. This maid was glad to do all thing that
might torn to the worship of god / and anon she went to the church and
performed her moders byddyng

But for devotion that she had to here mass / she abode stylle to the end
of the mass. And when all was I do / she went home ageyn / but her mother
wend she would a comen anon ageyn / anon as she had made oblacyon to the
priest And for as much as her daughter tarried so long after her semyng. When
she saw that she was come / she thought to blame her daughter and said. Cursyd
be the wicked tongues / that said thou sholdeste no more come again. This was
the manner of sum men to say her langage to her name that tarried to long
out. This maid then of great wisdom herd what her mother said / and held
her stylle a while / and spoke no word again. But after a good space this
maid drew her modre a fyde / And with great sadness of her mekely spak to her
modre and seyde A lady modre when ever I trespass or do aghast your biddyng beat
ye me with a rod as you thinks best that I be more ware Another time for it
is worthy and right full that ye do so But no thing I pray you for my defautes
curses never good man ne badde / For it is not semyng for your degree And to
me it is a full great affliccion^ in heart / while her modre herd these wordys
sche wondrid gretely And no merueill was to here her lytill daughter teache and
so wisely inform her In somoche that she had no spirit more to blame her at
that time for the wysdom that she saw in so young alitill thing Never the les
she would not that her daughter had know that / therefore su^what she thought
to speak again and turned to her daughter and seyde / Why were you there so
long / the daughter seyde mekely again modre I herd that mass that yebadde
me goo to / And when it was I done I turned home ageyn without any tarieng for
I abode nowhere till I come home again Thoo was the modre by tho wordis more
edyfyed than she was to fore and went to her husbonde / and said Thus and thus
has thy young daughter I spoke / He than as a good man gafthankynges to god /
and bare it stylle privily in his heart / And seyde naught again Loo ye
mayden^s that here or read this book of this oo point all be yt that it be one
of the least Yet mow ye well perceive how our lord encreceth his grace all
weye in this young maid till she come to ye years of abilitee to be weddyd /
of the which years ye shall see in the next chapter For of this chapitre I
make now an end

But yet ye shall understand that I had these that be contained in this
chapter of the same maid for the more party and sum I had of the modre
and of other dwelling in her fadres hows whyse she was of that age.

How her feruente devotion was draw which our lord suffered for encrece of
more grace following. And of her strong pacyence with the which pacyens she
suffered in her fadres hows many Iniuryes. Capitulu^q^rtu^
AFter the wonderful and virtuous course of living in the first years of this
maidens tender age / our lords will was in sum light defaute to suffer her
to fall as he suffered fulle often sum of his holy saints / to that intent
that they should the more myghtely arise up again / and live more warly / and
strenght hem to atteyne to the right way / and the heythe of perfeccyon and
gloryously have the vyctorye of the fend / which is ever enemy to man's
soul. These words I say here / for when she came to the age of the years
of abylyte to be wedded / that is to say to the twelthe year of her age or
little more / then after the manner of the contree she abode still at home and
came not out of her fadres hows. And the fader and the mother then and her
other friends and kynne / by cause they knew not the may dens purpose / they
bethought hem and besyed hem to seek about where that this maiden might
worshypfully and parfy tably be wedded and to what prosone.

Her mother supposed that for the great wisdom that her daughter had / she
should have be wedded to sum man of great kyneede / where for she besyed her
fast about the bodily apparayll and array of her daughter / and taught her to
wasshe often her face / and to kembe often her head / and to make her fair here
/ and to void all thing that should be dyshoneste / or should make foul her
face or her neck /

That when any man came to ask after her for marriage she should be the more
semely and fayrer. This holy maid was all of another purpose and had made
another vow. All be it she showed it not to her fader ne mother / wherefore
utterly she thought no thing to do as her mother bad her / touching such
curyosyte. She besyed with all her strengthes to plese god / but no man in
that wise. And when her mother had aspyed that she had no will to that
manner of living / she was dysplesed / and clepyd to her Bonauenture her other
daughter which was late I wedded before / And bad her trete so her suster /
that she might array her in bodily apparayll as the manner was of wymen in that
contre that should be married / and do as she had bad her do to fore. Her
mother knew well that Katheryne loved Bonauenture fulle tenderly / and
supposed that she should be brought in to that more lyghtely by her
suggestyons thanne by any other. And so she was as ye shall see after. For by
suffraunce of our lord she was brought so Inn thorough speech and example
of her suster Bonauenture by many manner ways / that at the last she assentyd
to her business in apparaylle of her body / after the will of her mother / not
wythstondynge that stably she kept her purpose never to have husbonde. But
after the grant to her sustre and followed her will / in such array / she
maad so much sorrow when that she was confessyd thereof with terys and
sobbyng that each body should suppose that she had do sum grievous sin: She
used often to be confessyd generally: and always wha^ she came to ye point she
accused her self full hard with weeping and sore sobbyng But the confessor
all be it he knew that a virtue it is of god: and lowely sowles to see in
them self defaute where none is. And where it is but little / it seems him
full great / Nevertheless for asmoche as she accused her self / and demed her
worthy everlasting pain, for that sin / saving the mercy of god / There he
asked her whether she purposed or wylled in all that time to do against her
vow: She said nay, for it came never in her heart. Also he asked again
whether she did it to the plesaunce of any man. In special: or to the
plesaunce of all men She answered and said: there was none somoche pain to her
as to be hold men or to be seyne of men / or to be there men should find her /
wherefore when her faders men yt learned dyers craft in her faders house came to
any place or chamber where she was. she fled as fast away as adders had
come to her so that all men wondered / She would never goo to the wyndowe ne to
the door of the hows to see how men went by the way / Then^e he said why
deserved ye that deed which was but for a bodily ornamente everlasting pain:
namely when the apparelle was not to excessyuely / She answered and said that
to excessyuely she loved her suster / And as her thought more tha^ god as at
that time wherefore she wept without remedy and did hard penance: Her
confessor would have replied again and said All be it there was sum manner
excess of love it was but little: And that deed as of him self was not I do
for no wicked or evil entencion / but for vain plesaunce of her for the time
and that was not against the precepte of god / She herd how her confessor
replied / she lift up her eyes to god / And with a loud voys cried and said.
A my lord god what ghostely fader have I now which excuses my sins / and
with a sore grutchynge against her self / she turned to her confessor and
said / Fader think ye that this wretchedfull and most unworthy creature of
god which has received of my maker of naught so many gracyous yeftes without
my labor / And wythouten any merit should occupye any time in arraye and vain
apparelle of this roten flesh which might or induce a dedely sin: I wene
she said hell suffyseth not to punysshe me: had not the pity of god do
gracyously and merciful with me /

After these words her confessor durst no more speak of that matter / But than
after that he besyed him to know if that blessed soul had ever in her life be
kept wythouten any spot^e of dedely sin:

So that she had kept fully hole her vyrgynyte both of body and of soul:
Not only from the sin of flesshely steryng / but also of all manner of sin
And after that he knew how virtuous and how clean a soul she had / This
witness and record he bare of her conversation and both said and wrote that
he could never perceive ne find another by her general confession ne special
confession as often as ever she was confessyd* And that was right often: that she
had offendyd against the precepte of our lord: But if it were that is told
before the which he might not suppose it were against the bidding of god / Ne
he trowed none dyscrete man would suppose it / And also he said that he found
her ever so clean fro venyall sins that uneath he could perceive by her
cotydyan confession any manner offense: It was openly known not only to her
confessors that knew her conscience: but to all that were conuersaunt* with
her that never or seldon she offended in word: For either she occupied her
time in prayer and contemplacion or ellis in good edyficacion of her neighbors
/ And as for her time of slepyng / uneaths she would grauute to her a quarter
of an hour And when she should ete her mete* yet it may be called a mete. ever
she prayed and thought holy medytacyons thynkyng of the things that she had
learned of our lord in her soul / More her confession: Master Reymound bears
a true record of her for the time yt he knew her and had cure of her
conscience / that it was more pain to her for to ete her mete, than it was to
an hungry man for to be wythdrawe from his mete. And a great tourmente it was
to her body after time she had ete: than it was com^ely to a fenerous man in
rennyng offhis fever /

And this was one of the causes why she would ete her mete as it shall be
declared within forth for to tourmente and put in pain her body: In what
manner of trespaas might such a soul be occupied: that always was occupied so
with our lord god / And yet not wythstondyng such good occupacions. She
accused her self so sharply in confession and so wyttyngly put her self in
trespaas and offenses / that if he confessor had not know her
conuersacyon: He might have supposed that she had trespased where she
trespased not, but rather deseruyd mede /

Loo ye maidens that heren and reden this book: all this process is for no
thing else I said but by that ye perceyuen this little defaute / In the
which this holy maid yield her self so mekely gylty /

Ye may understand thereby what per feccyon shows thereafter by the gracyous
yefte of our lord the which her confessor reherseth in this wise.
Bonauentura: right as she was besy before for to array this holy maid as the
world asks / Right so eftsoon she besyed her for to enduce her in such
array by her counseyll to the same apparaylle /

She might in no wise inclyne the may dens heart another general another specy
all that she should show her bodily presence wylfully to the syghte of man /
to that intent oonly that she should be desired the sooner to be wedded. all
though her fervor of prayer: and of sweetness off medytacio^ was slaked and
wythdrewe^ from her for a time:

At the last our lord would not longer suffer that his spouse the which
had so specially chosen should be withdraw and tarried from his special
service / he wythdrewe from her in this wise- In a time when the same
Bonauentura. the suster of the holy maid should bring forth a child she was
yet young y: nough of age for to bear children / Take heed maidens therefore and
see by this / How our lord is displesed with them that been about for to
let and wythdrawe them that would serve him specially in maydenhode and
chastyte of living /

This Bonauentura as it is rehersyd after was always full honest in her manner
of living both in word and deed / But by cause that she besyed her to draw
her suster to wordly things the which desired to serve our lord specially /
She was smyten of him and punysshed with a full sharp death Nevertheless our
lord yet wrought full mercyably with her / for as it was showed afterward by
reuelacyon to this holy maid / she was in purgatory / and suffered many grievous
pains. And by the prayers of her she was delivered of pain and restored to
bliss / as she showed afterward preuely to her confessor. When her suster
Bonauenture was passyd out of this world / thanne this blessed maid Katheryn
clearly perceived the vanyte of this world / and be ganne more feruentely and
more gredylye trewely for to be turned to the lovely ghostly clyppyng of her
endeles spouse Jhesu christ / claymyng and accusynge her self gylty with Marye
magdalene / falling down full streyte to the fete of our lord plenteuously
shedyng out terys axynge Inwardly his mercy / praynge and thynkyng vncessably
for her sins / that she might deserve to her with Marye magdalene the words
of confort of our lord as he said to Marye thus. Remittu^tur tibi peccata
tua. That is to say / daughter thy sins by foryeue the. And so she began
to have a synguler affection to Mary magdalene For thanne in that time she
enforsed hyrself with all her myghtys to conferme her to Marye magdalene to
have the more grace in forgyuenes of her sins.

Therefore afterward by encrece of devotion this follow thereof that our lord god
the spouse of holy sowles / and his blessed mother our lady Saint Marye gave
Mary magdalene to this blyssyd maid in to a maystresse and to a mother as it
shall be declared more openly with Inn forth by the help of Jhesu.

After this the fend enemy to all mankind sorowyng that thus his pray was
wythdrawe / and delyuerd all hole from his power / the which be little and
little enforced to draw it to him. And also considering / that this holy
maid encreced more and more to run quyckely to the tabernacle of mercy of
her spouse Jhesu. He thought felly and wylely to let her of her ghostly
purpose by the meyne of her faders howsholde / besyeng him by aduercytees and
persecucyons to draw her holy to the world / that she should not be occupied
in such ghostly excercyse puttyng in to the the mind of her fader and mother
and also her brethern / that in all wise she should be wedded. That they might
so by her mean purchase sum manner of kynrede / about this business the
fend enduced hem so hyely / that in asmoche as one of her daughters was passyd
out of this world / they should be about to recover the harm of her that was
deed by her that was a live. So ferforth that they were about to seek an
husbonde for this holy maid.

When this maid perceived and considered the wyles of her ghostly enemy by
Inspyracyon of our lord Jhesu. A none myghtely and besyly she continued in
prayer and medytacyon and excercyses of penance to have grace to flee the
conuersacyon of men / and so showed by open tokenys to her friends / that in
no wise she was in purpose to be wedded to no dedely ne corruptyble spouse.
Sith it so is and was that she had taken so gracyously to her spouse in her
young tender age the vndedely king of endeles bliss

When the fader and mother and kynne perceived verily that this holy may de
showed perseuerau^tly both by tokens and by word / that she wylled never to
be wedded to none erthely man / they thought to bow her heart / by a another
mean for to consent to their purpose.

They called to them a friend of therys a friar prechour the which they loved
specially / and prayed him entyrly that he would goo and counseyll that holy
maid that she should consent to there will. To whom the friar answerde and
said / he would do that he might. But when he came to this maid by
communycacyon he found her so steadfast in the purpose of maydenhode that by
conscience he was so enduced to give her holsum counseylle and said. Sith it
is so that thou art dysposed to serve our lord god in maydenhede / against
which purpose thy friends ben about to let the. Show the steadfastness of
thyn holy purpose / and cut a way all thyn here of thy head / and
peradventure they would cesse of there pursuyte. As soon as this blessed maid
herdethys his counseyll / she wrought there after as though she had I herd
it of god. And took a peyre of sherys anon and cut away her herys / in the
which she supposed she had sinned grievously / and that that she hated so much
/ she cut it away right gladly fast by the he de / And when she had I do /
she couerd her head with a Coyf / and so went forth all against the common
custom of other maidens of the world / with a kerchyf on her head after ye
doctrine of saint Powle / And when her mother Lapa aspyed this that her daughter
Katheryn used thus to cover her head customably /

She asked her why she did so / to who me this maiden gaf none clear answer /
by cause she would nethyr lie ne tell the truth. With that the mother went
to this maidens head and took of her kerchyfe with her own hondys. And so
perceived yt her here was cut awaey Tha^ne was the mother sorrowful in her heart
because her fair here was cut away waylynge and cryenge in this wise.

Aa daughter what haste thou do.

Anon the maid keuered her head efte sons / and went a side To the cry of
her mother came both the fader and the children meruayllyng what it might be

When they knew the cau^^ of her cryeng / they were hugely ameuyd ageynste
this maid / of the which trouble was begone the secounde bataylle against
this maid more sharper than then was the first. But yet to this maiden our
lord gaff the vyctorye / that thoo things which seemed lettyng to her holy
purpose was to her great help meruayllously for to knytte her to our lord more
myghtely Therefore they pursued her openly rebukyng her and thretyng her in
word and deed saying thus. Thou wretched creature trowest thou for to escape
thus that thou shall not fulfill our will because that thou have cut away
thyn here / hit shall grow ageyn will thou nyll thou / and though thyn heart
should to breast / yet shall you have an husbonde. And thou shall never have
rest unto the time that thou haste consented to our will.

And with that they made an ordinance that Katheryne should no more have no
pryue chamber by her self to dwell Inn / but that should openly be occupied
in the common service of the hows. So that the place and time of prayeng and
vnyeng and knyttyng to Jhesu her spoufe should utterly be with draw from her
And also that she should see her self so much the more in despyte that she was
made a common servant. After this ordinance this holy maid was put to all
manner fylthe business / and the foul of the kechyn. Suffryng every day
repreues / and every day also wrongs and rebukyng and dyspytable words were
multeplyed against her / that most of all ouercomen wymmenys hertys.

For as hit was supposed / her fader and her mother and brethern hadden fond a
young man of whose kynrede they weren gretely well apayde. And therefore they
steryd and Inpugnyd her the more sharply that she might the sonner be bowed to
their consent. But where that our ghostly enemy the fend / by whose wyckednes
and tretcherous works all these things were wrought / and down wend for to
with draw this maid from her clean purpose. There by the help of god she was
made most strengest for she was in no wise meuyd ne stered of all that was
done to her. But she made her a pryue chaumbre / by help of the holy ghoost
in her own soul / fro the which pryue chaumbre she made an ordinance in her
self / never for to go out for no manner of business And so it was done in
deed / that she the which first had an outward chaumbre assygned to her /
sometime stood with out and sometime went out. But afterward when she had made
her selue in her soul a pryue chaumbre that might not be take from her of no
creature in earth / she went never out. These ben tho heavenly vyctoryes that may
not be taken away fro crystis special in earth / ouercomynge with out any
doubt all stylly enemies

As holy writ seyth. Regnum dei infra nos est That is to say / the kingdom
of heaven is within us. And also the prophet Dauyd seyth. That all the joy of
our lords daughter is within forth. Within us with out any doubt / there is
a clear understanding / a fr^ will / and a retentyf mind. Within us also is
the gracyous Infusyon of the holy ghoost / the which makes perfyte these
ghoostly myghtys rehearsed before / and ouercometh and throws under foot all
outward aduersytres. Within us if we ben true vylners of virtue dwells that
ghest / the which said and seyth.

Confidite ego vici mundum. That is trusts feythfully that ye shall overcome
your enemies / for I have overcome the world that great enemy. In this
blessed lord / this holy maid Katheryn trustyd so hyghely that she made her
with Inn her self a chamber by his help / for whose love she charged not for
to lose the chamber made of man's hands without forth. But now one thing
shall I say / that master Reymond the confess sour of this holy maid beryth
record of that when that he should walk outward by cause other while of great
outward business and occupacyon that nedys must be done: This holy maid
oftymes warned him and said / that he should make within his soul a pryuee
celle / of which pryue cell he should never goo out

And all be it that he understand her not / but so ouerly so lyghtely. Yet
nevertheless afterward when he considered more wyttely her words. The words
that Saint Johan said in the Gospel fell in his mind where it is rehearsed
of crystys dyscyples in this wise. Hoe autem non cognouerunt discipuli eius
primum. Sed quando glorificatus est ihesus tune recordatisunt. That is crystys
dyscyples knew not all thing of him as touching his passion first but only.
But after time when he was reysen fro death to live / and gloryfyed / thanne
they knew more openly and clearly / And so in the same manner wise / both to
master Reymond her confess sour and to tho other that were conuersaunt with her
/ it happyd meruayllously that they perceived more openly and clearly both her
dedys and her words afterward / than whenne they were with her presently /

Yette shall I tell you of another holy conseyt and a blessed ymagynacyon of
this holy maid / that the holy ghoost taught her / by the which she overcome
all wrongs and despytes as she told pryuely to her confessor / axyng of him
mekely how she might be perfytly glad among so many despytes / And thanne
she brake out and said / that she had such an ymagynacyon in her self that
her fader represented our lord Ihesu Christ our savior and her mother our
blessed lady Saint Marye And her brethern and other many of the household
betokens the holy appostles of our lord and other dyscyples of his.

And for this blessed ymagynacyon she served hem all the more gladdely / so
that they were all a meruaylled thereof.

And by this blessed ymagynacyon she wan another great profit / and as oftr as
she served and made mynystracy on / ever she had in mind her her spouse
Ihesu Christ. Whom her thought she served. And so she being in bodily kechyn
was all way with that holy place that is called Sancta sanctorum. And as often
as she served at mete / so often she fed her soul with the presence of
our savior. A high and richesse of endeles counseyll / by how many diverse
and meruayllous ways delyuerest them that trusten in the from all manner
dyseses / and bryngest them in to the haven of endeles rest / delyueryng them
both from the pytte and the swolowe.

When all this was done / this holy maid considering euyr more in her soul
ye mede and the reward I ordained for her of the holy ghoost / suffered gladly
and naught paynfully / all the wrongs that was put to her. And also she
encreced contynually the course of her labor the more / that she might have a
full joy in her soul. And by cause that it was not suffered to her to have a
chamber by her self / but for to have her chamber openly as other had.

Therefore by an holy a^uysement / she chose the chamber of Stephen her brother
that had nether wife ne children. Where by days time when he was absente
she might be allone. And nyghtes time when he slepte / she prayed after her
desire / so that night and day she sought to see the face of her spouse
Ihesu Christ / knockyng at the door of his ghoos^ly tabernacle with out
cessyng. She prayed our lord vncessably that he would wouche sauf to be the
keeper of her virgynytee / saying and syngyng in in soul with Saint Cecylye
this holy verse of Dauyd the prophet Fiat cor meum domine et corpus meum
immaculatum. That is lord Ihesu I pray that mine heart and my body be kept
clean vnderfowled to the / and so in scylence and in hope she was made strong
in our lord right meruayllously. For the more torment and persecucyon she had
with out forth / the more she was fulfilled with ghoostly joys within forth /
so ferforth that her brethern perceyueng her steadfastness sayden betwyne them
seluen thus we be over come. Her fader that was most Innocente of all
consyderyng pryuely her deeds / perceived that she was ladde every day more
and more by the holy ghoost / and naught by the lyghtnes of yonthe.

All these that been rehearsed in this chapter / her confessor master Reymond
had it by reuelacyon of Lapa this maidens mother / and of lyxa her brother wife
and of other also that were in her faders hows / But as for other things that
other folk might not know / he knew by tellyng of this holy maid in
confession /

Of the vyctorye which she had of them that desesed her / And that was by a
culuer which her fader saw / and by a vysyon of S^ynt Domynyk Ca v
IN the mean while that this holy maid was put in such reprove and shame /
it happyd up on a day that she entered in to the chamber of her young brother
Stephen. And prayed devoutly leuyng the door vnshett for it was forboden to her
by her fader and mother that she should not shette the door.

Casuelly then it happened that the fader entered in to the chamber seeking a
certain thing of his sons that he had need to. And as he looked about / he
saw his daughter more gods daughter thanne his / prayng in a corner and
knelyng / and a little white culuer resting up on her head / the which culuer
fled out of the chamber wyndowe when the fader was entered in to the chamber
as him thought Anon the fader axed the daughter / what culuer that might be
that fled so out of the chamber / to whom the daughter answered and said /
that never she saw culuer ne other bird in the chamber. Then had the
fader great meruaylle / and kept all these words pryuely in his heart. Fro
that time forward there began gracyously to encrece in that holy maidens
soul an holy desire / which nevertheless was begone as it is reherced a
fore in her chyldehode / and now afterward it was renewyd for tuycyon and
disease of keeping of her maydenhode or virgynytee / and that desire was no
thing else but for to receive the habyte of the order of friar prechours the
which order Saint Domynyk was both foundour and fader. There she prayed both
day and night to our lord that he wouchesauf to fulfill her desire.

And thereto she had a great devotion to Saint Domynyk / as it is rehearsed a
fore to a worthy and a fruytfull lover of sowles. Almighty god therefore saw
how wisely and how myghtely his daughter as a young knight faught in battle /
and with what fervor of devotion she besyed her to plese him with all her
desire / he would in no wise dysceyue her ne defraude her of her holy purpose.

But for the more sekernesse he comforted her with such a vysyon.

This holy maid on a time had a vysyon in her sleep that she saw many holy
faders / and many diverse fou^dours of ye order of ye friar prechours / among
whom she saw saint Dominyk that she knew well I now / holdyng in his hand a
fair white lylye / the which lylye semyng to her was all a fire as ye busshe
yt Moses saw / and yet was not brennyd. When this holy faders al in general
and each in a special gaf her counsel for her more mede yt she should chese
oo Relygion of their ordinance in ye which relygion she might yield due
service to god. She turned her self hole to saint dominik / and so saw in
spyryt how yt ye holy fader saint dominyk came to her and brought in his hand
an habyte of sustris the which susters ben called sustres of penance of saint
Domynyk Of ye which susters there was ne yet is no little no^bre in ye cite of
Senee. And when this holy fader saint domynyk came to this maid he comforted
her with such words and said Dought be of good comfort / and dread no manner
of peril for right as you have desired this habyte: she thought she received it
and thankyd almighty god and his worthy confessor Saint Domynyke not with a
little gladness but with ioyefull teres that so perfyghtely had comforted
her: And so with weeping she awoke and was restoryd to her bodily wits.

And when she was awaked she caught comfort and bodily strength of this vysyon
/ and took so great a boldenes of the trust that she had in our lord /
that the same day she called her fader and mother and brethren togyders and
said to them boldly in this wise / Sometime ye said unto me / and tretyd me
long time thereof that I should be wedded to a corruptyble and to a dedely man
and though I had abhomynacion of such weddyng in mine heart as ye might
clerly perceive by many diverse tokenes if ye had I would yet for the
reverence that I should show to my fader and mother by the bydyng of god unto
this time I excused me never clerly to you / but now by cause I may no longer
be still I shall declare to you openly mine heart and purpoos / The which
purpoos it is not conceived of new: but of chyldhode unto this time* therefore
I will ye know it that in mine chyldhode I made avowe of virgynyte and serve
our lord savior of all the world / and his blessed mother glorious vyrgyn
marie. our glorious lady / not chyldely but with a sa^ and a long avysement.
And for a great cause / I made avowe also that I should never take husbond but
him alone: Therefore now sith I am come by the sufferaunce of our lord to a
more perfyght age and knowleche and vnderston dyng wit / wete ye right well
this is the same purpoos which is so mighty and stroonge in mine soul that it
were more possible hard flynt stones rather to be made nesshed. than mine heart
should be wythdrawe fro this holy pnrpos and therefore the more ye labor about
this thing / the more time ye lose: Wherefore I counseyll you that ye leave of
all manner such tretyng of wedding as touching mine person / For therein shall
I never fulfylle your will / by cause that I should rather be obedyent to god
than to man / therefore if ye will have me such one in your house that I now
serve god in this purpoos and for to be a commyn servant to serve you all / I
am ready in all that I can or may to do you service gladly: And if ye will
receive me but for this cause that ye will putt me out of your house / I do
you well to wete that in no wise mine heart may be wythdrawe fro this holy
purpos /

I have an husbond and a spouse christ Jhesu so rychely and so myghtely yt
will not suffer me in no wise to lack no thing / But he will mynystre to me
all that me needs:

When she had said all these words all that herd her speak fill in
weeping / and by cause of her plentnously syghynge and sobbing / they might for
that time give none answer: They consyderid to the holy purpos of this holy
maid ye which they might not with say ne wythstonde: and they behylde also
how still the maiden had I kept her: how clean and how pure unto yt time / and
how bodily she declared her conscience by words of great prudence / and also
over more they saw openli that she was rather diposed for to forsake her
faders house than for to break her holy purpoos and so they had no more trust
of her weddyng / wherefore it lyked them better for to weep than for to give
her answer /

Within a little while after when they had cesyd all her weeping: the fader
yt loved her so tenderly had dredde of god and dred god / so hyghely had
mind of the coluer that he saw and of many good deeds of the which she used
/ The which deeds he gretely merueylyng gave her such an answer and said /
Dear daughter god forbede it that we should any thing will or desire against
the will of god. For the which will / and fro the which will we know well
this holy purpoos comes fro / Therefore it is so that we ben taught by long
experyence. And now openly we see that thou art not steryd herto by the
lyghtenesse of chyldhode: but by fervent charity of god / Make thy vow
therefore freely / and do as the lyketh and as the holy ghoost techeth the:

And fro this time forward we shall never let the from thyn holy purpoosne
thine ghostely exercise / but only pray for us besely that we may be made
worthy to the promys and the byheste of thyn ghoostely spouse whom thou haste
chose by his special grace in thyn tender age: Then he turned him to his
wife and to his children and said none of you from this time forward be to my
ne dear donghter grievous. None be so hardy from this time forward to let her
in any wise to suffer her to serve her spouse freely / and she to pray for us
be sely /

We might never have found a better husbond to her then he is. the which
vochesauf to be so nere of our kind for to wedde our daughter and have her to
wife / Therefore we have none cause to pfayne us sithe it so is that we have
received now for a dedely man* vndedely god and man to be her spouse /

When the fader had said these words with weeping and with weylyng both of
them, self and also of other that herd them and him speak and namely of ye
mother that louyd this maid in manner flesshely. then^e this holy maid Katheryn
ioyefully thanked our lord that brought her to this vyctorye and also her
fader and mother with all manner of lowenes: dysposyng her self to use
profytably the license that was granted to her And this is the end of this
chapter:

But now I will ye known that redyn or heren this book that Master Reymound
confessor to this holy maid knew never by reuelacion of the fader that saw
the coluer the which restyd on this blessed maidens head for the fader was
deed or tha^ Master Reymou^d knew this blessed maid. But he knew it by
reuelacio^ of Cosyns that dwelled in the faders house. the which cosins
recorded and bare wytnes that the fader saw such a culuer with her often times
And therefore he had her in great reverence. and he would in no wise that she
had be lettyd or troubled /

Of the vysyon that she saw of saint Domynyk both master Reymound and her
confessor before him knew it by tellyng of this holy maid. And when master
Reymound examyned her of ye words that she said last to her fader mother and
brederen: and how she byhad her in her pesecucions: she told him all by order
mekely as it was /

Of the hardenesse of her bodily penance and of afflyction: and what
persecucion she fuffred therefore of her mother Capitulu^ vj
When this devout maid had received so large a license that was granted
her of long time desired before / She began right quyckely for to dyspose
merueylously all her life to the seruyse of god: At the beginning she asked to
have a little chamber to her self / and so had de it: wherein she purposed to
tourmente her body with penance as in a wilderness that she might have the
more fredome of soul for to serve our lord / How much and how hard penance
she used in tourmentyng of her body / And how great love she had in seeing of
her spouse in that little chamber: there may no tongue suffer to tell /
Nevertheless I have rehearsed some what in general of her great penance / And
now I purpose to tell you maidens in special under few words the hardness
of her penance / so that ye of the great virtuous herbs of her holy living
may taste somewhat of the fruit that grown about the herber both of the
first and of the last / And for the condycions and the kyndis of the fruit: it
shall be declared by the help of god afterward And the cause why that in this
place is rehersyd som^e what of her fruit full virtuous living is for nothing
else / But for the maidens should be the more able and redyer to ghostely
excercyse: In this little chamber that was granted her: often times she
considered swetely the ghostely werkis of our old faders of Egypt. And in
ghostely werkys was to her so much the more merueylous, and that she had
the true knowleche thereof in her faders house without ensample or doctrine off
other / First I shall tell you of her abstinence of mete and drink fro her
chyldehood in to the time that she came to that age / She ete full seldom
flesh as it is rehearsed before / but when she was come to this age and this
special fredom. she forsook utterly etyng of flesh so fer forth that
belong of custom and use that she had in forsakyng of it:

It was so light some to her that it was a pain to her for to smelle it as she
told her confessor preuely in confession and by cause ye should have none
gretter merueylle hereof. I shall tell you of another great abstynence / When
her confessonr perceived in a time that she was greatly wasted and feblyd in
body for she received none such mete and drink that febyll folk should be
comforted with / He gave her counseyll that she should put in her cold water
that she drank / sugar or a lytyl sugar roset: Whereby her spyrytys might the
more be quyckenyd / With that she touenyd to her confessor and said / A
little life there is left wytt in me the which me seems ye would it utterly
were quenchyd /

And when her confessor had asked her why and knew her excusacion / He
understood by her words that she had so used her to bitter metes and
unsavory drinkys. that all manner sweet thing was noyous to her body / by cause
her dysposycion was turned in to a custom: And so it was to her of etyng
f^esshe. as it is rehearsed before: And when she should drink wine as the
contree foryeuyd after the time she had license to keep her chamber: she
medlyd that wine so with water that it lost both his taste and his savor /
and also a great part of his color / But afterward when she was xv year of
age she left all manner of drynkyng of wine and used to drink cold water:
And all manner soden mete out taken bread alone / She wythdrewe fro her by
little and little every day somewhat / and within a lytyl time after she held
her to bread and raw herbs /

At the lasie when she was twenty year of age or there about. she left etyng
of bread and held her only to raw herbs: Then afterward she came to such
an high state of living. nonght by use and kind as it shall be declared
