openly ynogh wythinforth by the help of god / But oonly by miracle that all
be it: her body was oppressyd gretely with many diverse sickness and great
traueylles: The kyndly of dygestyon in the body had no place in her: and the
stomach also used not the might and the use of his office of defyeng:

And yet the strengthes of the body notwythstondyng her strength living both
in mete and drink were never the febly er: so that than her confessor
records of her / all her life was miracle. She might never do that she deed
by strength of kind as physyens said and told afterward to her confessor:
but oonly by miracle.

All these things shall clearly and play nely by the help of god openly be
declared within this book afterward. But as for the conclusyon of her
abstynence fro the time that her confessor Master Reymound knew her as he
records of her is this that she lived not with no mete ne drink that was
nourysshynge to her. ne she had none comfort of none kyndely strength: And
yet nevertheless she suffered gladly all manner dyseses and labors: How came she
to this state of living trow ye trewely not by bodily excercyse and use. But
rather by fulness of ye spirit I shall tell you in what wise ye fulness off ye
spirit som^e time rebonudeth in to the body. there it is made subject and
acordyng to the werkys of the spyryte for there the spirit of a gostely
creature is fed with the gifts of gostely graces / the body suffers the
more pacientli above natural strength of his own needs: who would be in dobute
hereof I trow none reasonable creature / whether martyrs in her holy martyrdom
suffered not gladly above natural strength tormente and myserye of their
bodies in her passions / I trow yeis /

And fro whens comes this trow ye / but of fullness of the spyryte / This is
often times known by experyens in our days: that if a man or a womman be
occupied in gods service devoutly /

He reketh never how long he fasteth and never to speak with creature / but
when he ceseth of the special devotion / And is occupied in outward bodily
besynes / it is hard for him for to fast and do as he did before / Whens
comes this grace / but oonly of the fulness of the spyryte that conforteth the
body: the which accords to the werkis of it / and all be it that this is a
gift above nature yet naturally the spyryte otherwhyle communeth with the
body: And the body with the spyryte both in good and evil In these words I
deny not / but that there ben sum the which may fast more esely than
sum. But symply for to fast and absteyne long time together in this life / me
seems it is inpossyble by nature thus much is rehearsed of her great
abstynence for this time / Takyth head also of another thing that this holy
maid tourmentyd her body with: beside all her abstinence / She made to her a
bed al of bordes without any other stuff: otherwhyles she would sytte or
stand in holy medytacions and other while knele and pray: and always when she
would sleep she lay coun without any doing away off her weryng clothes. For
she weryd always woollen both next her body and without some time she used the
hair or the cilyce, and yt she left afterward by cause as her confessor
supposed / That she that was clean within eschewed vnclen^es without that is
engendered of the cilyce or of the hair / But for the hair she used an iron
chain next her body euyr syttyng fast to her sides without any remeuynct or
ease / unto the time it endented the skin / And made a mark there upon as it
had be forbrennyd: As her ghostely daughters and her felawes told after ward
to Master Reymond her confessor / the which ghostely daughters and felawes
often times for diverse sekenesses that she suffered constreyned her for to
change / her clothes and for to wasshe away the sweet.

And therefore her confessor afterward by cause of her great sickness that she
suffered a lytyl before that she should be deed constreyned her by obedyens that
she should leave her cheyne. All be it she would not do it by her good will.

Evermore she continued in wakyng till the day dawed on the morrow as it shall
be declared more opynly here afterward. After that by little and little our
lord gave her grace to overcome sleep / that uneath she would sleep half an
hour in two days: And vnnethys she would receive that half hour but as
sekenes coustreyned her thereto /

And she would say otherwhyle to her confessor that the most traueylle that
ever she had. was for to overcome sleep / It was so hard a bataylle for her
or she might have the vyctorye of it. Yet more over as her confessor recorded
off her if she might have found any body that cowde had understand her and
commyned with her of virtue: And of the goodness of god it should not grieve her
though she had been without mete or drink and slepte an hundred days and an
hundred nyghtes she should never have be weary but rather the fressher and she
gladder /

She told often times to her confessor that she was never so well refrysshed
in spyryt in this life / as when she might find with whom she might commyne of
the goodness of god: And that knew well tho the which were conuersaunt with
her.

This was openly perceived in her when she might have leyser to speak off god /
that tho things of virtue the which were hyd in her heart / appieryd strongely
by ghostely gladness in the body outward / And when she had no leyser to
talk of our lord then she was feeble: Hereof bears witness her confessor:
Master Reymound / to the worship of god and of his own shame that oftymes
When this holy maid would speak of the goodness of our lord and of the great
myseryes that he showed to her. by cause of the long time of her contynuaunce
in spekyng And also by cause he was far from her loving as he said him self
/

He fill in a slombryng / and always she continued forth in speaking: For she
was reysyd up by love in to the breast of our lord / nothing perceiving that
he was a sleep. till a long time afterward:

And when she perceived that he was a sleep / with a great voys she awoke him
and said: why lose here ye the prouffyte of our soul for a little sleep:
speak I to a wall or to you /

Ferthermore she desired above all this to follow the stappes of the holy
fader Saint Domynyke / And that was in this wise / she received every day
theyes dyscyplyne with an iron chain: The first dyscyplyne was for her self.
The second for all tho that were a live And the third for them that were
deed /

Thus we read in the legende of saint Domynyk that he used contynually / and
therefore she used the same long time afterward. But after time she was feblyd
with sekenes that she might no longer use hit. And when her confessor axyd
of her pryuely how and in what wise she used that manner of penance / with a
great shamefastenesse she knowleched to him. That in every dysciplyne she
occnpyed an hour and an half / so that for the most party the blood followed
foo the sholdres down to the fete. Loo maidens what perfeccyon was in this
holy maidens soul / that thryes in the day let her self blood for goddys
love / shedyng her blood for his blood. See^ye not in what virtue she was of /
that with out any exaumple or Informacyon of any man in earth that used such
great penance with in her faders hows

Redeth Saints lives and writing of holy faders of Egypt / leueth none
unsought / but sercheth over all / and espy whether ye find any like to her.
Ye shall find Saint Powse the first heremyte lived long in deserte. But a
crow brought him every day half a lof to his mete. Ye may also find saint
Anthonye a full holy liver and did great meruayllous penance / and yet he
went to diverse ankrys about / and of each of them he gadred sum flowers of
virtue. Ye may also find of Saint Hyllaryon an holy liver. Yet as Saint Jerome
seyth / he was first informed to virtuous living of Saint Anthonye and to went
to deserte and there myghtly ouercam his enemies. Ye may find also of Macharye
and Arsenye and many other which is long to tell of / that had techers to
virtuous living / one or moo / both in word and also in exsaumple / what in
deserte / or in Relygion And this holy maid had nethyr her doctrine to virtues
in Relygyon / another in deserte But in her faders hows without any Informacyon
or exaumple of any man in earth / and there to came to a great perfeccyon of
abstynence / notwythstondyn ge the manyfolde lettyng the which she suffered in
her faders hows Shall I yet say more of this maidens commendacyon I pray you
lystene a little while and I shall tell how holy writ makes mencyon yt
Moses fasted twyes forty days / with out mete and drink / and Ely ones /
and our lord Ihesu christ also as the Gospel says / that they fasted more by
many years continued Holy writ tells not. Saint Johan baptyst though he
were in deserte he lived by honey soukeles and herbs. But symply that he fasted
I find nowhere I wryton.

Of Marye magdelyne allone her storye makes mencyon of her life that she fastyd
every year forty days to gyder with out mete or drink three and thyrty years
following / leuyng in a Roche of the sea. There for I trow it was that our lord
and hye blyssed mother committed her to this holy maid for to be her may
stresse and her mother as it is somewhat I touched before. And as it shall clearly
be de declared afterward by the help of god. By this may ye know that this
holy maid had a special yefte and a synguler grace of god. Not that she is
preferryd in holy living above all the Saints / the which ben rehearsed
before.

For that were a full odyous comparyson. So for to make such lykenes between
Saints / among which saints our savior Ihesu Christ is I nempned / to whom
for to lyken any saint in comparyson of holy living / that should be even with
him / it were blasfemye / al tho other saints which ben named / they be not
rehearsed for to make likeness in merits of living / but that ye shall
consydere and take heed first of the great magnyfycence of our lord Ihesu christ
/ that every day by his gracyous plentuous largenes mult^plyed his new yeftes
and grace / where with he arayeth ghostly and makes perfyte his chosen sowles.
Another also that ye shall consydere and take of the great synguler worthynesse
in her was no Iniurye ne wrong to other saints For holy church syngeth and
seyth specially / and syngulerly of every saint by him self. These words of
Salamon. Non est inue^tus similis illi. That is none I found like to this:
These words must be understand of the great might and large fredom of our
lord / making holy and perfyte his chosen sowles. The which may and will
endowe and arraye every saint syngulerly with a special yefte of grace with
out any wrong of other. Of all this matter now I shall cesse and proceed forth
in the first purpose By these condycyons of abstynence of this holy maid / may
be understood clearly that she was lene in body / that with so many herdenes
of penance and sharp afflyccyon^ was so often times tamed / and all was for
to make her body buxom and subgett^ to the service of the soul. On a time her
mother Lapa told to master Reymond her confessor* Thought that her daughter
tormented so holy her body in penance / she was of so great might and
strenghte in body / that she would with out any greuaunce life up on her
sholdres a borthen that was I now for an horse for to bear / and bear it up in
to an high garet above two long steyers For she was that time as she said
twyes so great in body thanne she was afterward at the age of xxxviij when she
had continued in so great penaunces. Hit was no meruayll and so it is / for
but if it had naught I be that our lord had kept her by miracle / hit had
be no meruayll though she had be all wastyd away. For at that time when that
her confessor master Reymond knew her / she was a full slender creature and
that was no meruayll. For the spirit encreced in virtue / the weyker wexxd the
body as though it were overcome of the soul / and not wythstondyng all this
she would ever labor gladdely and namely for the health of sowles. All be it
she suffered great sickness in her body / for the spyryte which was so strong
within sustained and comforted the feeble body with out. Now shall I cesse here
of / and torn ageyn to the first matter of this chapter. When this holy maid
had full grant and license of her friends for to serve our lord in her
little chamber assygned to her / and there began full fervently for to styghe
up ghoostly to her heavenly spouse. The serpent our ol de enemy the fend
though she had overcome him diverse times before. Yet he cessed not for to
assaylle her estesonys.

He steryd Eve his daughter. Lapa this maidens mother by a carnal love that she
had more to the body of her daughter than to her self / for to let her of
her penance For on a time when the mother came to her daughter / and aspyed
how she beat her self with an yren chain / she cried waylyng with a loud
voys and seyde. A daughter what doste thou / thou art but deed / for thou
sleest thy self / allas who has cou^seylled my daughter herto / who has
steryd her to do this.

And so with cryeng and waylyng this old womman tormented her self as she had
be a wood body with t^ryng of her clothes and of her here / for she thought her
daughter was but deed. By the noise of this cryeng all the neghbours were
styred about for to come Inn and see what this old woman eyled. When they
came they saw how this holy maid had made her a bed all of bare boordys
where on she rested when she would sleep.

And with vyolence her mother took her out of the chamber and brought her to
her own chamber there she lay / for she thought that she would make her sleep
in her own bed with her. And when this holy maiden saw this / by wisdom of
spyryte she showed great gladness in chere and kneled down a fore her mother
prayng her mekely with esy words that she would wouchesauf to put away all
her steryng and vnpacyence and be esy / for she was ready to obey to her as she
would have her ready for to lie with her as she would bydde her. When she thus
wisely p^syd her mother for to keep her in quyete / she laid her down by her
in that one side of the bed / and had there sweet medytacyons that she was
wont^ to have. After time her mother was a sleep / she rose up pryuely and went
again to her holy ghostly excercyse. The fend eftsoon had envy herto that
she should so encrece in virtue / styred her mother the second time ageyn her.
But there ageyn this holy maid used this prudence by cause she would no more
make *her mother sorry with her / she took pryuely a post and leyde it in her
bed under a shete and clothes abouen / that the mother when she would comen and
vysyte her should suppose that it had be she / the which had lay there under
the clothes.

And yet never thelesse she kept her common ^^stome of hard lyeng / as she did
a fore / hit was not long time after / but that the mother aspyed this well /
and when she had aspyed it she said to her daughter in this wise. Daughter I
see well all my labor is in vain / I may not change the from thy purpose /
ese it is to me for to let it over pass lightly. And therefore go and sleep
there on thou art I wont^. And so she was ouercomen with the stedfastnes of
this holy maid and suffered her ever afterward to live as the holy ghoost
styred her. Thus ends this chapter. Sum things there ben rehearsed there
Inn that her confessor master Reymond knew and had reuelacyon of by the
holy maid Katheryne* As is of her great abstynence and other sharpness of
penance / and of her manner of worchyng in them / and sum thynkes he knew by
reuelacyon of her mother Lapa / and some of other diverse matrons that were
conuersau^t with her. But some things he knew by him self / namely of her
synguler and gracyous yefte of abstynence.

Of the last vyctorye that she had in a bathe. And how she took the abyte of
Saint Domynyk Which she had long time desired to fore. Ca vij
When this holy maid was restoryd ageyn to her devout excercyse the more that
she perceived that the enemy of all mankind was besy for to let her / the
more fervent she was in her ghostly excercyse. Every day she wayled and every
day she wept / axynge and prayng our lord devoutly that he would wouchesauf to
give her grace to resceyue the abyte of saint Domynyk that she had long
desired. The which thorugh his great ^yt^^ was be hot her by our^ holy fader
Saint Domynyk in a vysyon. For she was never seker in her self to keep the
purpose of maydenhode unto the time she resceyued that holy abyte she wist well
that after time she were arrayed with that abyte all manner speech of her
weddyng should cesse / and she should be suffered for to serve her ghoostely the
more freely. Wherefore she prayed her fader and mother that they would give her
leave to be one of the susters of penance of sayn t^ Domynyk / that been called
in common speech of the Cite of Senee susters of the mant^ll. And ouermore she
prayed to the same sustres that they receive her to the same abyte among
theyr^ holy nombre. To this axyng the mod was not well apayed / all be it she
said not ones nay / but ever she was about as much as she might for to
withdraw her from her great penance that she used. And for this cause she
purposed on a time for to go to an hoot bath / or for to be bathed and her
daughter with her. That as soon as this holy maid had felt any manner comfort
and solace to the body by that bathyng by little and little she should have left
her great penance* This was not done without will of the fend / the which
besyed him in that he might to with draw such a fervent soul from the
ghostly calling of her heavenly spouse He taught this sinful wo^man Lapa this
maidens mother full pryuely his malycyous wylles Nevertheless by cause there may
no counseyll preuayll ne have the maystrye against the counsel of god This
holy maid that was armed with the armere of vyctorye both in her right side /
and eke in her left side turned all the fend is treacherous wylles to great
profyt^ of her soul. When she came to the bathe / she found a new manner
bathyng in her soul / how that she should tormente her body among the
delycyous bathes. She went to the condyt^ there the hot water came Inn to the
bathe and there she satte all naked and suffered pacyently the hot water brenne
her tender naked flesh the which was more pain to her / then when she
beat her with a cheyne Now shall I tell you how her confessor knew it. In a
time her mother Lapa t^lde master Reymond before her daughter how they went for
to be bathed / and then this maid pryuely told him how she was bathed / and
how wisely she asked leave of her mother when she was there that she might be
bathed by her self when all folk were gone. For she wist well if her mother had
seen her she might not do as she did And then her confessor axyd her how she
might suffer so great he te with out peril of death. This maid answered to him
and said full symply / that when she satte in that bathe / she thought besyly
upon the pains of purgatory and of hell / prayng to our lord whom she had so
hyely offendyd / that he would wouchesauf to torn mercyably tho peynes that
she had deserved in to that temperall pain that she suffered gladly. Of his
mercy she had so great gladdenesse in her heart / that all the pain was right
sweet to her and therefore her body was no thing hurt there by / though she
felt pain. When she had told this tale / her confessor went home / and she
again to her penance that she was wont to use And when her mod yt perceived /
she had no more hope tho of her chaungyng. But yet she cessyd never with out
grutchyng of the penance that she used. Of the which grutchyng this maid her
daughter lyghtt^ly suffered hit over pass with a defeere having myude rather of
her holy purpos / and excyted and steryd her mother every day that ^he ^hold go
to the sustres of penance of saint Domynyk for to pray thom that her daughter
might receive them abyte of penance that she had so long time desired: The
mother seeing that she might have no rest for her daughter / she went to the
susters of penance and prayed that her daughter might receive the abyte
among them.

To whom they answered and said. That it was not her custom to receive maidens
/ ne young wymmen to that abyte / but only wedowes of sad age and of good
name and fame that would fully give hem to gods seruyse For sith it is so that
susters of that abyte be not enclosed up / but eueryche of them lived at home
in her own hows / hit were full necessary that each of them were of such
sad age yt they might and could govern them self saddely. The cause why
these susters of penance answered thus / it shall be declared by the help of
god openly I nough in the next chapter that sueth. When the mother had this
answer she went home and told her daughter / the which answer was to the
daughter full gladsome / and to the mother not full heuysom. Nevertheless yet
this holy maid mystrusted not / for she wys^ well her purpose should be
fulfilled that was behot her of so glorious a fader as Saint Domynyk. And
therefore ef^sones she prayed her mod that she should not cesse / but go to
these susters ageyn and pray them with asmoche instaunce as she could / that
she might receive that abyte. The mother did so / and brought ageyn the same
answer as she did first Then ne sone after it happed that this maid fill seek
in body / the which sickness comynly young folk ben vexyd with or tha^ne they
come to a sad age. And yet p^raduenture that passing he^^ that she suff^ed
in the hot bathe might be cause there of / al be it that it was the will of god
yt it should be so. All the skin of her body was full of bladders and byles /
that uneath she might be know. And there to also she had a strong fever. The
mother seeing that her daughter was so seek all though she loved her sons and
daughter tenderly Yet this daughter whom that she nourysshed with her own
milk she loved more tenderly / and therefore she was the more sorry of her
disease. And she knew no cause where of this sickness came For such a
sickness might not come of abstynence / but rather of supfluyte. And also that
same time it was common sickness to young children and young maidens And therefore
she could not deem where of the sickness came / and what ese and remedy she
might do there to / she did both in words of comfort / and also in deed /
syttyng all way by the beds side by her. But the seker ye daughter was in
body / ye strenger she was in her holy desire / wayteng after leysyr to
constreng her mod in manner for to pursewe to fulfill her desire wisely and
swetly she said to her mother.

Good dear mother if ye would I were hole and ferd^ well / I pray you beth
about yt my desire may be fulfilled for to receive that abyte of penance.
Else I wot well that our lord and saint domynyk the which have called me to
there service woll so ordeyne for me / that ye should no longer have me in this
life. When the mother herd this oft^ and many times rehearsed to her / she being
a ferde lest she should have deyde / went to the same susters ageyn and prayed
them so entyerly of the abyte / that they were overcome with her prayers and so
granted her in this wise. If your daughter be noght over semely in body / and
over f^y^^ in beauty / we shall graun^^ your axyng and receive her And if she
be to fair we dread us of the peril of slandre / and of malycyou^ living of
men in these days. And for this cause we dare not consent to receive her in
no wise.

To whom the mother answered and said

Comes and see her and eve ye the dome whee she be fair or not. There were
sent two dyscrete matrons chosen among them with Lapa for to see this maid
both of dysposycyon of her body / and also for to search her desire of soul
When they come they found this maid lyeng seek in a bed / and therefore they
might not clearly know the dysposycyon of her body for sickness.
Nevertheless as by her words they knew her fervent desire of soul to the
service of god / and were greatly astoyned there by. And also glad seeng so
young a maiden pass in virtuous ^yuyng many old matrons / wherefor they took
her leave ioyefully gretely edyfyed by her words and told their felawys with a
great joy what they hard and saw. When thise susters herd this / by
counseyll of the frerys they received her with oo will and one assent^ among
them sendyng word to the mother / that also sone as ye maiden were hole / she
should bring her to ye friar prechours / that she might r^ceyue the abyte of
Saint Domynyk / the which she had so long desired in presence of the brethern
and the sust^en of the same abyte as the custom is. When the mother told these
wordys to her dought she was glad that she wept for joy and thanked our
lord and saint domynyk that had fulfilled his promys and byh^st.

Thanne she began to preye to god that she might be hole of her bodily
Infyrmy^^ / for to fulfylle her holy purpose in receyuyng of the abyte / lest
she should be let and delayed of her desire / for that bodily seke^^sse. And
there she was first glad of her bodily sickness with meke suffrau^ce.
Afterward she was as heavy thereof besekyng our lord with besy prayers that he
would wouchelauf to deliver her with out any taryeng of that sickness the
which let the purpose of her desire / and as she prayed our lord granted
her / for with in few days afterward she was hole.

Our lord would not always of his goodness deny the axyng of such that
conferme them ever with all their business to fulfylle his will For what ever
she axyd or desired she referred it to him who me she loved with all the
myghtes of her soul / and to who^ service she offered her self all hole body
and soul / whom she was restoryd of bodily hele. All be it the mod was
about to tarry her of her purpose longer time. She made such Instau^ce to her
mother / that the day and hour was assygned when she should receive her abyte /
the which abyte she received with a great ghostly gladness / when the mother
and the daughter were come to gyder to the church. The friar that had the
charge of the susters arrayed that holy maid with that manner of abyte in
presence of them all of the colors of white and blak in token of Innocence and
me kenesse / the which abyte holy faders of Saint Domynykes order ordained for
to be had. So that by the whytnes is understand Innocencye / and by the
blaknesse mekenes. For as master Reymond her confessor records and writes*
There was none abyte so well according to her conuersacyon of living both
Inward and outward. Then this maiden with all her might ^^o that time
forthward mortyfyed her body in sleyng of the old lust of sin with all his
branches of pride / in the wynnyng of the very meekness / the which
meekness betokens the mantell of black that she had received. Alsoo she
besyed her with all her myghtes for to keep the Innocencye of virgynytee and
maydenhode / not only of body / but also of soul to her endeles spouse Ihesu
christ / the which is very light for to receive by him fayrenesse of virtuous
living / the which fayrenesse is betokenyd by the white cote under the
mantell. If her abyte had be all black or all white / tho two things
meekness and Innocencye might not properly be understand thereby. And if her
abyte had been graye russeth / it might represente mortyfycacyon. But not
properly puryte and clennesse of soul.

This was the cause why the susters at the beginning denied her this abyte lest
she had not be able to bear it in meekness and clennesse of heart / dredyng
of her young age. When that holy maid had received that abyte / hit become
her better than it did the matrons.

Therefore it had not be well do / that it had be denied her / which abyte was
ordained a fore of holy faders in token of Innocencye. Sith it so was that she
passyd in clennes all the chastyte of wedowhode. Of one thing her confessor
Master Reymond records and writes that / that abyte had never his full
perfeccyon in the Cytee of Senee unto the time that holy maid had I take
upon her for to were hit. She was the first maid in that Cytee that took it up
on her / the which many maidens afterward received also. So it might be song
of her that verse that Dauyd the prophet speaks of. Adducentur regi virgins
posteam. That is to our lord god endeles king / many maidens shall be brought
Inn after this holy maid Katheryne.

How this maiden encreced it shall be declared afterward by the help of god /
But now I shall make an end of this chapter and proceed forth how this holy
abyte began of this holy Relygyous estate / lest for defaute of knowing there
of / the opinion and the fame of this holy maidens virtuous living might be
lessenyd thereby in sum mennys hertys / as for the matere the which is
reherced in this chapter master Reymond records and seyth that he had it
by relacyon of her mother / and of her self And as the abyte it needs no proof
/ for it is known openly enough.

Of the beginning and the foundamente of the Relygyous state of the susters of
penance of Saint Domynyk / and where of came the manner of living of tho
sustren. Capitulum viij
All tho that will read this present chapter following / they shall find
written as it is recorded of many feythfull creatures in diverse parties of
ytalye / many worthy actys and dedys of our holy fader Saint Domynyk. That
glorious worthy confessor of Christ / Tutor and defendour of the feyth of holy
church Saint Domynyk also techer and enfourmer of the good state of perfyte
lyuers overcame myghtely both in Tholose and also in Lombardye. What by him
self and by his brethern / many heretykes: So that in the time of his
canonizacion at Rome was prouyd openly a for our^ holy fader the pope that an
hundred thousand heretykes and more were turned by his prechyng and showing of
miracles in lumbardye alone /

Nevertheless that venomous doctrine of the heretykes had so enfected the
people sowles that almoost all the possessions of holy church were in laymennes
hondes keeping it as here own heritage And that caused Bysshoppe^ to goo about
and beg. For they had none power never to wythstonde her here^ye for the
defaulte of temperall substance / ne for to releue clerkys and pour folk
after the dew of her office / This considered our holy fader Saint domynyke
and might in none wise suffer this myscheff in holy church for the great and
entyrly love that he had thereto he chaas a worthy life of pouerte both for him
self and also for them that should be his folowers

And then began to pursue forth for the right of holy church assosyeng^
to him cert^yn lay people that d^ed god and that he knew well and so co^myned
with them of the ordeynaunce of an holy living that should recouere again the
rychesses of holy church and defended it myghtely ever afterward / and
faithfully against heretics by common assent such a life was so granted and
ordained.

For there that our holy fader Saint Domynyke found any well willing folk to
such a living / First he enduced them for to swear that they should keep and
observe all the things that should be reherced to them to the vterest for to
put her goods and her life therefore in Jeoperdye: and le^te this holy living
should be let by such that we^^ wedded / He made also wives to swear that
they should also not let her husbondes to maynten in such a pour living the
right of holy church: but rather should help them to her power in all that
they might: And to either party this holy fader saint domynyke he byhote them
sykerly if they kept this purpoos: endeles life for her mede /

Tho men that took this holy life upon them were called friars of Crysico
knyghthode / Nevertheless by cause they should beknowen fro other by sum token
and that they should have sum manner of besynes above the usage of other lay
people: He gave them the color of his own habyte that both men and wymmen of
the same knyghthode of Ihesu christ should were white and blake.

So that either color should apere outward in token of innocencye and
mekenes: Evermore he assigned them to say a certain nombre of Pater nosters:
and Aue maria. That they should be occupied at every hour of divine service
day^ by day* when this was do after time saint domynyk passed out of this
world to bliss of heaven and by encresyng of miracles was canonyzed in the
court of Rome: The f^^res and suster^ yt first were called of ye knyghthode of
Ihu cyr^^ to amo^^ synguler* worship of the fou^der of saint domynyk changed
her name by a co^mi^ ass^t / and were called f^^ers and susters of the penance
of saint domynyk / and ye cause why them thought yt her first name should be
changed was this / they saw that by the merytes and miracles of saint domynyk:
and by the prechyng of ye friars their cursed heresye was cause / wherefore
them thought yt it was not much needful to be occupied in such outward
battle of prechyng but rather wythinward battle against her gostely enmyes /
they chose therefore to be called friars and susters of penance / At ye last ye
no^bre of friar prechours encresyd so hugely / among whom was one as a clear
shynnyng sterre: Saint peter both martyr and maid / the which was martred of
heretykes for the right of holy church: And destroyed more heretykes after his
death / And so this company of wulues that were about to destroy gods unite
of holy church were utterly avoided and peace was yelden to all holy church /
wherefore the cause of that name of knyghthede sesyd and channged in to a name
of penance / Nevertheless this manner of state of loving descends and
remains only to men a while: And there wives ben left soole living by them
self a relygyous life never afterward desyryng for to be wedded: by cause of
the relygyous that they kept with her husbondes a fore / But the state the
which they began they kept to her lives end /

This consyderyd and beheld other wydowes that purposed to keep them in
wedowhode desiring to follow susters of penance of Saint domynyke / For
remedy of her sins they prayed the friar prechours that were in Italye to
inform them of the manner of living / The which was ordained of Saint
Domynyke. By cause the manner of living was not hard: A blessed fader of the
same order / the which was called Munyo wrote that manner of living / and took
it to these wydowes: the which manner of living in to this day is called
among them a rule: All be it they it may not properly be called so / In as
much as encludeth not within it the three pryncypall vows that other relygyous
folk have / And after time that this nombre of susters thus encresed in
diverse parties of Italye / Our holy fader the pope in tho days the which was
called honoryus perceived that good living of these susters granted them by
bulle that in time of Interdyction that they might here her dyuyne service
among the friar prechours / And so our holy fader the pope Johan the which
came after him he had made the constytucions of Clementynis against the
vyrgyns and by gardys: He declared the bulle of the same decretall or
constytucion that it should not be understand of the same susters of penance
of Saint domynyke: For by that Decretall the astate is not repreued in any wise
/

Loo maidens by this ye may under stand why that state of living was found in
wymmen only: And why the susters answered so at the beginning to the mother of
this holy maid / that were not wounte to receive maidens to that state of
living: but oonly to wydowes approuyd in sadness / these things that been
written in this chapter for the more part Master. Reymound found them
written im diverse places of Italye: But some matters he herd and understood
them with inquysycion of many holy faithful and old friars and susters of
Saint Domynyke And thus ends this chapter /

Of the wonderful encrece and how she prouffyted in virtue and holy living /
And that she should be byloued in all things which she rehearsed to her
confessor of grace done to here of our lord Capl ix
How this holy maid in receyuinge of her habyte made none byhest to the three
pryncipalle avowes of relygyon / by cause that the estat asked it naught: As it
is rehearsed before Yet nevertheless she purposed to kepefull steadfastly tho
three pryncypal avowes i^ her self. As for the vow of chastyte there was none
doughte of / For she had made avowe of maydenhode before in her tender age. as
touching for her obedyence: She purposed oonly for to be obedyent to that
friar that was master of the susters and to the pryoresse of the same susters.
But also to her confessor the which obedyence she kept to her lives end /

For as she said by her live when she should pass out of this world: She
had never mind that she brake onis her obedyence / Neuerthels by cause there
were sum the which had envy off her holiness both bacbyters and liars
that said the contrary /

I do you to understand maidens that thowe this holy maid had none other
tourment while she was living in earth but oonly indiscreet byddyng and
mysseyng of her souereyns: she might have been in manner a martyr by the great
patience the which she suffered: Her confessors understood nonght ne gave none
credence many times to the excellent gift of grace that she received of god /
Ne gave none reverence to the werkys of our lord that wrought in her
merueylously / And therforre they would have made her living after the commyn
living of her susters / not consyderyng ye opyn tokens of grace that were
showed in her diverse times.

But rather they myghi be lykened to ye pharysens that seyth the opyn miracles
the which our lord wrought: And yet they grutched by cause he helyd a man upon
the sabat day seeing thus /

Non est hic homo a deo qui sabbatum non custodit: That is this man is not of
god hals that keeps not his sabat day This holy maid when she had received
her habyte of penance* she besyed her what she cowde to obey to her souereyns
/ and thereto she durst not forsake ye way of virtuous living / the which our
lord taught her by him self / so that between these two / she was sore
angwisshed in tourment that there may none tongue tell it ne pen write it /
Was this not trought ye maidens a martyrdom for her / I trow yeis / A a lord
god often was it said to her in repref yt all her vysyons come naught of god
but of the fend /

Notwythstondyng that they the which saw in her many merueylous works and
that thereto they might see that all her life was miracle / as it shall declared
more clearly here after / Now was this a strong martyrdom as me seems

And as touching to pouerte of lynyng she kept so perfyghtly that virtue
pouerte that she being / in her faders house and household where great plente
was of temperall goods: for her self she took no thing but that she would
give freely to pour folk / And thereto her fader gave her a special leave /

She loved so much pouerte that as she said preuyly to her confessoure she
had never joy of her faders house by cause temperall goods were so
plenteuosly used therein:

And therefore she prayed our lord hertely that he would vochesauf to tak away
that richesse: And bring her friends to pouerte seeing in this wise. Lord
whether this good that abounds so plentuously in mine faders house by that
good I should ask for mine friends / and naught oonly of good everlasting / I
know well lord that among these temperall goods there is much peril
medeled among: And therefore I would naught mine friends were encombred with
them.

When she had thus prayed / our lord of his goodness herd her prayers: and
suffered he friends Fader and mother and other of her kynne to fall to right
low pouerte by many merueylous chances without any trespaas of them: As it
was well know to all tho that knew them whiles they lived / By this may ye
know that this maiden kept full dewely the three pryncipall vows of relygyon:
That is obedyence / chastyte and pouerte / all be it that she made none avowe
openly when she received her habyte of penance /

Now shall I tell you of her perfection after time she had received her
habyte when she had received habyte as our holy fader Saint domynyke promised
her / she began anon sweet virtuous living and sought occacions and causes
for to constreyne her self more streyghtly: than she did before that she might
the more deuoutlye love her spouse Ihesu seeing to her self in this wise: Lo
thou have now take up on the a manner of relygyon thou may no more live as thou
have do thy seculer living is goo: And a new relygyon is come: after the
which reule thou must needs be reuled /

S^est thou not the color of thyn clothes the needs now fro this time forward
to keep perfyghtly pouerte and clennesse of body and soul, which be tokeneth
by the white cote: The needs also to be deed to the world: the which
betokenneth by the blake mantel / therefore see to thy self how thou gouerneste
the for thou must now goo in the streyte way that few walken ynne: For the
more sekernesse therefore of keeping of her pouerte and cle^nesse /

This holy maid purposed her to keep silence full streyte / and not for to
speak but when she should be shryue / And as her confessor both said and wrote
that was before Master Reymound* three year contynuelly she kept her silence /
but when she would beshryue She kept her also contynuelly in her chamber / But
when she would goo to the church for her mete she had none need to goo out /
It was little and soon do. For she used to ete none manner of mete that was
made by the fire out taken breed alone as it is rehearsed before /

Also she made an ordinance in her own heart never to come to mete but with
weeping: so that ever before mete she would offer to our lord teres for to feed
her soul first / And than afterward would she sustain her body with mete /

Her faders hows was to her as a wilderness and deserte / notwythstondyng the
confluence of people that were therein.

Beside all this what wakyng what prayers what medytacions and what teres she
used. I trow there is none tongue cowde tell /

She made also an other ordinance in her self that when her brethren the
freer prechours stepte. she would wake / And when the friars had tongue the ij
peel to matyns and anon erst would she seye than her spouse Ihesu Christ in
this wise Loo lord mine brethren And thyn servants have I rested the^ in to
this time / and I have prayed for them to the that thou sholdest keep them fro
deuelys and fro the ouercomyng off the fendes / Now lord they be arise to
pray to the / therefore lord I pray the keep them / and give me leave to
rest a while / And so she lay down upon hard bordes / and a stoke under her
head instead of a bolster /

Our lord Ihesu her gracious spouse seeing all this in this maid the which
gave her all these graces would not suffer so able and so dylygent a dyscyple
to be untaught without a perfyght mayter Another man ne angel: But he him self
would be her informer of virtue: Anon as she was shett up in her chamber our
lord Ihesu Christ her well beloved spouse and savior of all mankind /
appieryd to her and taught her and informed her fully of tho things that
longs to the health of soul as she her self told privily after ward to her
confessor and said to him these words:

Fader understands this for a truth that I was never taught ne informed any
thing that longs to health of soul: of man ne of woman but oonly off mine
lord Ihesu the spouse of my soul other by his inspyracion or else by his
open apperyng spekyng to me as I now speak to you:

She knowleched also to her confessor that in the beginning of that vysyon
when it apperyd openly to her bodily wits / so that she perceived with her
bodeli erys a voys / she began to wax a ferd lest it had be a deceyte of the
fend that often times transfygureth him in to an Angel of light: the which
feer in no wise dysplesyd our lord but rather he commended that feer and
said /

As long as a man or a woman lives in this life. they should ever be aferd /
for so thou may find written /

Beatus vir qui semper est pauidus / That is to say blessed be that man that
ever is feerfull:

Ferthermore our lord Ihesu Christ said to her: Daughter wylt thou that I
shall teache the how thou may know mine vysyon from the vysyon of the fend.
To whom this holy maid answerde full mekely and prayed him that he would
vouchesauf to teache her

Then said our lord thyn soul may esely be taught by Inspyracyon and by
word for to dyscerne between the one and the other / But by cause that I would
it might prouffyghte as well to the other as to the / Therefore I shall teache
the by word.

Doctors of holy church whom I have taught the truth seyn / and soothe it
is / that mine vysyon begins with a dread but ever in the passing it sets
a soul in great rest and sekernes / It begyn^eth with a manner of bytternes
But evermore more and more it wexith sweet / And the contrary heart does the
vysyon of the fend: It gives in the beginning as it seems a manner of
gladdenes or sykenes / or else sweetness / But when it passes away / ever
it encreseth in the soul dred and bytternesse This is the trewest knowleche
for to know mine ways from the fendes ways

The way of penance and the keeping of mine preceptys and commandments in
the beginning it seems hard and sharp / But the more a soul prouffyteth in
keeping of them: the more esely it waxith The way of sin in the beginning
seems full delectable but ever in encres thereof a soul is made more and more
dampnable /

But yet shall I give the another token for to know mine vysyon from the vysyon
of the fend / Understand this for a sothe / that sithe it so is that I am
truth ever of mine vysyons the soul of man receives a great knowleche of
truth: and by cause that the knowleche of truth is full necessary to the
soul as well to her self as to me that she may know me and her self / of the
which knowleche she passes out fro her self in settinge little by her self
and honors and worshyppeth me / The which condycion properly is called the
condycions of mekenes. Therefore it were full needful that a soul should thus
know her self / And so be made meke by vysyon.

The contrary is of the vysyon of the fe^de. sithe it so is that the fend is
fader of lesynge and king of all the children of pride / And he may not give
but that / that he has as his lesyng and pride. Therefore as of his visyo^ / a
soul seems much by her self and is made glad and (...) Joye / The which is
properly the condycion of pride: and so she is by left swellyng and bolnyng in
pride: Then^e therefore if thou examyne and dyscusse dylygently in thy self:
may know whether vysyon come to the of truth or else of falsenesse / if
it come of truth: it makes thyn soul meke / if it come of falsenes and by
desceyte: it makes thyn soul proud.

Then this holy maid when she had herd this / she kept this wholesome
doctrine full dylygently in her soul and told it afterward to her confessor
and also to other for her edyfycacion as it shall be rehersyd wythinforthe by
the help of god. And then began our lord to showed this holy maid visyons
and reuelacyons plentuously: so ferforth yt uneath might be found two men so
homely in conversation to gyders: as our lord Jhesu and she were to gyders /

For whether she prayed or read or had medytacions or walked or slepte o wise
or other: she was comforted many times when she spoke with other she had
reuelacions or vysyons and spoke in her soul to our lord whiles her tongue
spoke outward to other / But that might not long continue for her soul was
so wonderly I draw up to her spouse Jhesu that within a little while
afterward. She was rauysshed out of her bodily felyng. Out of this rauysshyng
came many merueylous things that follows afterward* as well of her great
abstynence as of her merueylous doctrine: And also upon miracles the which
our lord showed in her by her lyffe / now than lest there be sum that would
be in doubt whether this holy maid had such reuelacions or not. I shall
tell you how her confessor Master Reymound preued it whether her reoelacions
and vysyons were true or not / At the beginning when Master Reymound herd of
her hye co^uersacio^ of living he began to wax homely with her in comunycacion
with her / for he could not feel it verily yt such reuelacyons in her might be
true the which mystruste was for his better / And therefore he inquired by
diverse menes and ways to know whether they came of god. or of the fend: Or
whether they were falls or true:

For then came to his mind of ypocritis the which regnyd in his days / and
that he found many dyscetys / and namely among wymmen / whom ye devil
dysceyued with ye vice above all other creaturs

Hit came also in to his mind how ye first womman Eve was deceived / and many
such other / and therefore he doubted the more of this holy maid. While he
stood long thus in such a doubt / it came to his mind / that if he might by
her prayers get of our lord one great contrycyon for his sins above the
customable contrycyon yt he was wont to have / by that might he know that all
her vysyons reuelacyons and dedys come of the holy ghost

For there may none get such a contrycyon / but by yefte of the holy ghost.
And all be it that there is none living that can say whether he be worthy of
god hate or love Yet hertely contrycyon for sins is a great token of grace
Master Reymond had not so sone thought this / that he went to this holy maid
/ and prayed her hertely / that she would pray for him to our lord / yt he
wouchesauf to for give him the sins the which he had done To whom this holy
maid answered and said that she would full gladly. Than said master Reymond
that he might not be easyd in his desire by her prayers only but if he had
there of a bull that his sins were for given Of whom this holy maid axed
with a smiling chere / what bull he desired to have. He answered that in token
of a bull he axed one great contrycyon for his sins / the which contrycyon
this holy maid said he should have all ready. Then that time hit seemed to
master Reymond that she understood clearly all his thoughts / and so he went
from her. On the morn it happed master Reymond for to be seek and lay don in
his bed / whom kept one of his brethern a devout man the which was called
Nycholas of Pyse. The place there he lay in seek was an hows of sustres in as
much as he caught his sekenes sodeynle Jorneyng by the way. When this holy
maid perceived that he was seek. She a^os up of her bed not wythstondyng
that she was seek her self of the fevers / and other diverse passions / and said
to her felawe Goo we and see we how srere Reymond does fare. And her felawe
answered and said that it was no need / and though it were need / yet was she
more seker than he Nevertheless yet she come to him and axyd how he ferd.

Anon when he saw her he meruaylled gretety and said to her as fe^illy as he
might speak. Aa lady why come ye hither / ye be agrete dele seker than I am.

Thanne she began to speak of the goodness of our lord as she was wont to do
and of our unkindness against him.

With that master Reymond her confessor arose up out of his bed gretely
comforted by her words / and sat in an other bed beside / having no mind
yet of the words that the holy maid spoke to him at even before All this while
she continued in spekyng of the kyndenes of our lord / and of our great
unkindness.

Suddenly in time of her devout comunycacyon came to his mind a clear
consyderacyon of his sins / that him thought he stood before the ryghtwys
Jugement to be condemned to the pain for his wicked living right as a thief
that stood before a temporal Juge. Him thought also that he saw in his soul
the great benygnyte and the mekenes of our lord / that gracyously delivered
him fro the pain that he was worthy for to have / and not only that / but
also he clothed him with his own clothes / there he was naked / and had him in
his holy hows / and fed him and nourysshed him / and accepted him to his
service / and there to by the synguler grace of his end. Loo the goodness /
his death / unto life / his dread unto hope / his sorrow unto joy / and his shame
unto worship. By these consyderacio^s and clearly knowynges / and syghte of his
soul / the wyckettes of the wyndowes of his hard heart were broken up and
opened / and the wellys and ryuers of weeping terys aperyd plenteuouly / by
cause that the foundament and the ground of his trespassys were showed so
clearly to him / in so much that he wayled and that he was aferde last by
such great plente of sorrow / his heart and his breast would have to barst When
this holy maid saw that she was still and suffered him a while to be fed with
his own terys / for therefore she came. Within a while after he cessyd little
and little / and bethought him meruayllously of this new grace / thynkyng also
of his petycyon the which he axed of this holy maid the day before / with
that he turned to her and said / is this thy bull that I spak of to you
yesterdaye. She answered and said ye laynge her hondes upon his sholdres seyeng
thus / have in mind fader of the gracyous yeftes of our lord. And so went
home to her chamber / and he abode stylle with his felawe gretely edyfyed and
comforted. Another time the same master Reymond had another excellent token of
this holy maid with out any axyng before Hit happed on a time that this holy
maid was vysyted by diverse sekenes / and lay seek in her bed. And sent
after her confessor desyryng to comen with him pryuely of other new
reuelacyons / the which our lord had showed her great sickness began to
speak of the goodness of our lord / and of the reuelacion that he showed her
that day. He heryng so great reuelacyon^ and wonderful showed to her / and to
none other that ever he herd of / having no mind of the grace that our lord
had give him before by prayers of this holy maid. He bethought him of
somthynges that she rehearsed and said to himself thus / whether it be all true
that she seyth. When he had thought thus / he looked suddenly in her face /
and saw that her vysage was transformed in to man's vysage berded / the which
vysage beheld him steadfastly / and made him sore aferde. Hit was to his sight
a semely long vysage of myddel age / not having to long a berde / but of a
reasonable assise colored after whete / showing in his syghte a mageste after
the mageste of our lord Jhesu / and might in no wise for that time see none
other face / but only that face. Of this sight he had so great a fere / that
he lift up his arms and began to cry and said. Oo who is he that looks upon
me. To whom this holy maid answered and said. He that is sees and beholds
you with that word / that dredefull face vanysshed away / and the maidens
vysage appyred to him clearly. This was no feynyng thing but a true / as he
records and bears wytnes in his wrytynges He records also for the more
confyrmacyon of that miracle that after that sensybly vysyon / he had so
clear a knowing within himself im his soul by ghostly Illumynyng of the matter
that the holy maid spak to him / of the which he will not pupplyche it
openly. That him thought he felt in experyence that thing the which our lord
said to his dyscyples when he behote them the holy ghoost seyeng to them thus

Et que ventura sunt annunciabit vobis. That is when ye have received the holy
ghost / he shall show things that been to come Loo For the mystrust that he
had to her words our lord of his gracyous goodness wouchesauf to teache
him clearly by him self / he afterward for to bear wyttenes to other that her
reuelacions weren and ben true pryntyng steadfastly in his mind / the great
graces that he showed to Saint Thomas of Inde / for he that would not be taught
and enfourmed by open tokenes of gracyous gift / the which he received by
this holy maid he was taught and informed by example of such a disciple that
was mystrowyng as he was For after time he had received a gracyous token of
conpunccyon of our lord a fore by merytes of holy prayers of this holy maid /
yet he continued in mystrust of her reuelacyons that they were not true.
Wherefor our lord himself / showed him self openly to his outeward wyttys /
that he might thereby know by open experyence that he spak in her so that it
may be said that he showed him then to master Reymond / the which mystrowed
as he did some time to saint Thomas of Inde by bodily felyng. And right as he
cried afterward and said this word Deus meus et dominus meus.

That is my god and my lord So may this mystrowynge renuwed say after thise
two vysyo^s of this holy maid / that she is and was the very spouse and the
very discyple of our lord god. All these ben rehearsed to you maidens / that ye
should be in no doubt / ne despise the reuelacions and the vysyons / the
which ye shall here by the help of god afterward All be it that no wytnes
may be found of record save she allone / but that ye should here hem / read
hem / and understand hem with reverence. And also that ye may learn there by
holy examples and doctrynes / the which our lord has showed in such a
vessel by kind seek and bryttell. But by grace meruaylously made strong and
precious. And thus I make an end of this chapter. All thoo things the which
master Reymond was taught and enfourmed of this holy maid / he has declared
them openly in this chapter. Outake one thing that he was charged by her to
keep it pryuely of a certain reuelacion as it is rehearsed a fore.

Of a noble doctrine which our lord gaf to her in her beginning / and of other
doctrynes in the which he founded her manner of living. Capitulum x
Sith it so is that the ground and the foundament of trust and believe touch
the reuelacyons of this holy maid by the help of god / is declared in the
chapter that goth before. Therefore now I shall proceed forth and show you the
spyrytuall edyfycacyon of this same maid. And by cause that true sowles and
feythfull ben fed and edyfyed by the words of our lord. Therefore I shall
tell you and show you a notable doctrine of ye which this holy maid was
taught of our lord him self. This holy maid told to her confessors among
whom master Reymond was one / that in the beginning of her vysyons our lord
appyred to her when she prayed and said to her in this wise. Know thou not
daughter who thou art / and who I am if thou know well these two words /
thou art / and shall be blessed Thou art she that art not / and I am he that am.

If thou have the very knoweleche of these two things in thy soul / thy
ghostly enemy shall never dysceyue the. But thou shall escape gracyously all
his snares / ne thou shalt never consent to any thing that is against my
commandments and precepts. But all grace all treuthe all charity thou
will win without any hardenesse And now is this a bryef word and a great
and in manner Infynyte and endeles. Oo this is a great wisdom expressyd under
few syllables Whether this be not that leng the that bread / that heythe and
that depthe the which saint Poule desired for to have with all saints / I
trow yes. Oo dear maidens consydereth and beholds meruayllously this
Incomparable tresoure / the which is found in this holy maids breast. For
our lord Jhesu that vndeceyuable troth seyth to this holy maid thus. If thou
know these two things in thy soul / the fend shall never deceive the Me
seems it is full good for you to make here three tabernacles or dwelling places
unto the worship of god / that excellent doctou^ the which t^ched the
understanding of these fruytfull words

Another to the love and devotion of this holy maid Katheryne. The which
received the holsom doctrine of this few fruytfull words And the third to
the ghostly tresoure of valor of all tho the which fynden life in this few
fruytfull words. In the understanding of thoo fruytfull words / now be
founden and had ghostly richesse so plenteuously that it shall no need be to
all tho that have so found this ghostly richesse / for to beg of other A
whether this bryef fruytfull sentence be not true / where it is said.

Art not thou she that is not / I troweyes. Every creature is made of our maker
Jhesu christ of naught So ferforth that if our lord Jhesu christ our maker would
cesse for a time / be it never so little fro conseruacyon of his creature that
he has made. Anon that creature should torn in to naught / when so ever a
creature does sin / the which sin in him self is naught: Ne of him self he
may no thing do or think that is ought. As Saint Poule seyth. And that is
meruaylle / for he may not be ne have being of him self / ne yet be conserved
of him self in his being. And therefore the apos^le said. Qui se existimat
ali^uid esse cu^ nichil fit ipse se seduci^. That is he that wenyth he be ought
/ he is naught / he decey ueth him self. Se^st thou not maid how noughty a
creature is A creature made of naught / ever of him self ^owyng to naught by
sin makes him self naught / as Saint Austyn said / for he may no thing do
that is ought by him self / but rather that is naught / as our lord said.
Sine me nichil po^^stis sacere.

That is without me ye may do right naught / the which naught is sin.

Therefore ye may well clearly know by this that a creature of him self is naught

And that knew well Saynt^s before this time / the which by knoweleche of this
very wysdom excluded vera^ly out of their sowles all manner of sin.

What manner of Inflacyon of sin may entree in to such a soul the which
knows her self naught How may she be joyful in vain glory of any good
work that ever she did / the which knows well I nough that such good dedys
come never from her / but fro god How may such a soul enhaunce her self by
pride above other that holds her self naught. How may a soul that thus
sett^th her self at naught / Inwardely despise other / other have envy to
other.

How may any creature have vaynioye in outward richesse / that now has
despised all his own joy of him self. I trow such a creature is taught by
the words of our lord endeles wysdom where he said Siego quero gloriam meam
gloria mea nichil est. That is if I seek mine own joy / my joy is naught Also
how may such a creature that knowed him self in no wise his own / but only
his that made him / see of all outward things / this is mine / sith he him
self is not his. How might make such a creature to have delectacyon in
flesshely sins / that every day restreyneth him self by such manner
consyderacion of naught

Loo maidens by this bryef fruytfull words / thou art naught / ye may
consydere / that all manner of sin is and may be excludes. That other bryef
fruytful word that our lord said to this holy maid is this. I am he that
am / whether this bryef fruytful word be a new word / ye forsothe both new
and old. This is that old word that our lord said to Moses in the sussh /
the which semyd brennyng when he said. Qui est misit me. That is say to the
children of Israel He that is sent me to you. Hit is also now a new word /
by cause it is new reherfed to this holy maiden in like words that she the
which by the first bryef fruytfull sentence was I taught to know her self
nough / should learn by the next fruytfull senten^e to ask our lord ought /
the which is the endeles well of all essencyall being. By these bryef
fruytfull sentencys may ye know that a creature is naught of him self. For all
that he has of virtue / and of being comes of god maker of all creatures.

Almighty god maker of al creatures has only of him self and of none other
endeles perfeccyon of essencyall being.

For he might never form and make all thing of naught / but if he had an
Infynyte virtue of essencyall being in him self. Wherefore all that ever our
lord Jhesu / that sovereign master taught his spouse in tho two bryef
sentences as it is rehearsed before / is no thing else but this / that she
should know her self as she is / and our lord verayly as for her maker in the
depnes of her heart / and then she should be blessed. In the same wise I
find I written that he said to saint K^theryne the virgyn and marter. When he
vysytre her in prysone / Daughter know me for thy maker. Of such manner of
knoweleche comes all manner of perfeccyon and all ordynate setting of the soul
/ What is he that may not love so large and so free a gyuer with all his heart
/ and all his soul / what is he that is not styred every day more and more to
love such a lord that first er thanne he made his creatures / he loved hem
not for their deserve and merit / but only by his Infynte goodness /

What is he that ferth not and dredeth contynually to offend in any manner of
wise / so great and so dredefull a maker so mighty and so large a gyuer /
so gladsom and so free a lover. What is he that may not gladdely suffer all
manner of dyseases for such a lord / of who me he has received / and
receyuyth day by day / and hops to receive without any deubte so manyfolde
goodness.

What is he that should be weary / or tormented by sekenes to please so amyable
a lord. What is he that endeyneth to keep reverently and louyngly in his mind
the blessed words that such a lord wouchesaue to his creatures.

What is he that will not gladdely obey to the commandments and pretho
things that the soul loves ye which desire may not be had wiwout work:
so ferforth that in as much it loves so much it werketh / And yet
nevertheless it trusts naught in her own work as in her own self: but only
in our lord that worched in her:

The cause of this lovely desire is noothynge else / but the very knoleche off
god that he is aulterd / therefore among all other merueylaus things of this
holy maid: she held that doctrine the which our lord taught her syngulerly
to be worshy p^ed / To the which wurshypfull doctrine yet shall I add more
to / For but if I be greatly dysceyued all they come out of the first notable
doctrine. Often times this holy maid was wou^t to common and to speak to tor
confessoure Master Reymound of the worthynes and condycions that our lord
loved off a soul / And she said that such a soul perceived not ne sees not
ne loved her self ne none other soul ne had none mind of none creature:
This was a full hard word to Master Reymound for to understand and therefore
he prayed this holy maid for to declare it. Then she said a soul sees
her self that she is verily naught of her self and knows perfyghtly that all
the goodness with all the myghtes of the soul is her maker /

She forsaked vite^ly her self And all creature and hedeth her self fully in
her maker our lord Jhesu in so much yt she sends fully and pryncypaly all
her ghostely and bodily werkynges in him In whom she perceived that she may
find all goodness and all perfection off blessydnes and therefore she shall
have none will to goo out from such inward knowleche of him for nothing /
And of this vinte and love that is encresed every day in such a soul: She is
transfourmyd in a manner in to our lord that she may neither think ne under
stand ne love ne have no mind but god or else in god / she may not see her
self ne none other creatures but only in god / Ne she may not love her self ne
none other but only in god. Ne she may not hane mind in her self ne of none
other but only in god: ne she may have no mind but only in her maker: Right
as a man that is under a water and swymmeth under the water nether sees ne
touched nothing but water and that is under the water / And thing yt he is
above ye water he neither touches ne sees of that yt is above ye water it shy
neth under the water for that he may perceive and yet none other wise but in
the water / And as they may byshewed in water as long as he is voder the
water: Right so fares it of a soul that is hyd in the love of god:

All this she learned of our lord that dyuyne love the which never teched
error to his meke dyscyples: ne gives them cause to coueyte any thing with
out him / For ever her ghostely excersyse in is him /

Another time this holy maid reher syd in presence of her confessor Master
Reymound and to many other that were called to clennes of living: A full notable
doctrine and a virtuous the which is good for pure maidens to know / Whose
chaste living is full spe^yally to god /

And the more ye ben met ner to god by sweet meke maydenhede the sonner ye may
understand that virtuous doctrine / And it is this that a soul the which is
virtuously I met to god as it is rehearsed before: As much as it has of the
love of god / So much it has of the hate of her own sensualyte. For of the
love of god naturally comes hate of sin the which is do ne against god /
the soul the^fore consyderyng that the rote and the beginning of sin
regneth in the sensualyte and there pryncypally is roted: She meued and storyd
hyghely and holyly with all her merytes against her own sensualyte / not for
to utterly destroy the rote For that mayr not be long the soul dwells in
the body living in this lyffe But ever it shall be left a rote namely of small
venyall sins: Whereto accords right well saint Johan when he says thus / Si
diximus quia peccatu^ non habemus / ipsi nos seducimus etc.

That is if we say that we have no manner of sin in our sensualytes namely
of venyall sins* we desceyue our self / And by cause she may not utterly
destroy that rote of sin thus in her sensualyte as it is said before / She
conceived a great displesaunce against sen sualyte and of her sesu^lyte /

The which dyplesaunce spyngin up an holy hate and a dysplrsyng of her
sensualyte by the which the soul is ever well kept fro her ghostely enemies
There is no thing that keeps the soul so strong and so syker as does
such an holy have: and that felt well the Appostle when he said / Cum
infirmot tunc forcior sum et potens /

That is when I am feeble and syke in mine sensualyte by hate of sin / Then I
am the stronger and mighty er in mine soul / Loo fader of such hate comes
virtue and of sweet febylnesse and sykenesse comes *strength / And of such
displesaunce comes plesaunce.

Such holy hate fader have ever with you: For it shall make you meke and ever
to feel meke things of your self / it shall make you pacient in aduersyt^ /
and temperate in prosperyte / And set you namely in all honest of virtue:
And it shall also make you loved ^oi^^e god and man:

A / a / now is that a paynfull soul and full of woo that has not this bliss
For where that such holy hate is not. there is much vnordynate love the which
is the stynkyng thorroke and canell of all sin: and the cause and the rote of
all evil concupyscence.

Al such and like words this holy Maid comyned day by day / with such
dread in commendyng of holy hate of sin and in despysyng of vnordynate love:

But when ever she perceived that any defaute of sin or of sin i^ many
creature that comyned with her or in any other / Anon she would be styred to
compassyon and said / Loo brethern loo susteren the cause of this tr^spaas and
this sin is nothing else but an vnordynate love of your self: The which
vnordynate love is norysshed of pride and of all vices /

Does all your besynes for the love of god to put^e away such vnordynate love
of your own self out of your own hertes / And planteth therein holy hate of
sin for certain that is the right way of perfection and amendment off all
sin /

Loo maidens how well this holy maids doctrine accords to the words of
Saint Poule where he said thus

Quod virtus i^ infirmitate perficitur That is virtue is made parfyghtly i^
sekenes and febylnes and that was wha^ he prayed to our lord to remeue away
his temptacions / To whom our lord answered and said thus / Sufficit tibi
paul gracia mea. That is it is Inow to the paul mine grace / that is for to
hate sin and wythstonde it: Then brake out saint Paul and said:

Libenter gloriabor in infirmitatibus meis vt inhabitet in me virtus cristi:
That is I shall gladly be Joyefull in minsekenes and febylnes by laboring in
hatyng and understanding of sin: that the virtue and the grace thereof may be
inhabyted in mine soul: See ye not now how these holsom doctrynes of this holy
maid ben grounded upon a steadfast stone of truth the which stone is Christ
In as much as they acorden with holy wrytynges of doctors: Thus ends this
Chapter* but I pray you all that shall read it or here it that they mekely
consydere the merit and the deserte of this holy maid / when our lord vou
chesaf to inform her in virtue by his own proper person* And also that would
give credence wythouten any oath to her words: For he was a faithful doctor
that taught her / And thus I make an end of this chapter.

Of the merueylous victory of temptacions by another manner doctrine give unto
our lord / and of a famylyaryte and holiness which she had with our lord
which has not be herd to fore / Capitulum xi
IFynde written that when king Salamon had done make and raised up a toure
for to keep the Cite of Jherusalem fro enemies /

The king of Babylone was wood with all and raised up an host for to destroy
that toure if he might As Soon as king Salamon perceived that he would come with
an host for to destroy that toure / He ordained to be made merueyllous
strong wallys round about the toure so myghtely and so mighty walls that
when ever they came to assail it with any manner of shot: their darts should
merueylously turn again and wound or slay the host

Right so the king of Babylone that is the king of pride and enemy of peace
the fend of ghostely enemy consyderyng that king Salamon auctor and
conseruatour or keeper of peace had raised up an high virtuous toure the
which was this holy maid Katheryn to the defens of Jherusalem that is holy
church dredyng thereby feste she should be cause of many creatures health as
she was in deed: both by good ensamples of living and also by her holy doctrine
/ he waxed wood with her and turned to her with all the spyryte of his malice
for to destroy her with many thousand whiles. But almighty god that mercyable
and peasyble lord suffered that to be done for to encrece the victoryous blessed
endeles crown of his spouse / and thereto he strengthed her over all with
mighty ghostely armor for to overcome him so that she wan^ more of virtue in
time off her battle by ouercomynge of the temptacyons / Then she did in
time off peace whylys she was without temptacions and so all the fend whiles
turned again shamefully to him self / Our lord enspyred her to ask him by
prayers for to have the virtue of ghostely strength wherefore she prayed many
days and long time / At the last after such long and devout prayer our
lord vocheu^saufe to here her Gracyously / and taught her in this wise sey^ng
thus Daughter if thou will get the virtue of ghostely strength thou must
follow me all be it that I might by mine goodly virtue overcome all the power of
the fendes by many manner ways of ouercomyng:

Yet for to give you ensample by my manhede / I would not overcome him but only
by taking of death upon the cross that ye might be taught thereby if ye would
overcome your ghostely enemies / for to take the cross as I did: the which
cross shall be to you a great refresshyng in all your temptacyons if ye have
mind of the pains that I suffered: there upon of temptacyons:

And certain the pains of the cross may well be called refresshyng of
temptacion / For the more pain ye suffer for mine love: the more like ye be to
me in passion / needs ye must be like to me in Joye / Therefore for mine love
daughter suffer pacye^tly bitter things and none sweet things / And daughter
in none wise for thou shall be strong enough^ for to suffer all things
pacyently* When this holy maid had herd this holy lesson she foryate it
naught but bare it ever quykly in her mind. And ever afterward had Joye and
delight in trybulacions / so ferforthe that there was no thing in earth so
great refresshyng to her: as was passions and trybulacyons / For by sweet
sufferaunces of trybulacions she wyste well that her crown encresyd in the
bless of heaven:

After time that king Salamon our lord Jhesu Christ king of heaven ande of
earth had armed his blessed toure this maids soul by sweet mighty and
holsom doctrynes / he suffered enemies to come and preue that toure / if they
might by any way or wise destroy it.

The king of Babylone our ghostely enmye the fend with all his cursyd
company come and byseged this blessed toure thorugh the sufferaunce of god
round about with many wretchid temptacions / But first he began to assail
this maid by flesshely temptacions whom not oonly he tempted by thoughts
withinforthe ne by yllusyons and fantasyes in her sleep: but by opyn vysyons
waking both in seyeng and herynge and seeing.

He tempted her in many manner off wise by taking upon him a body off the air*
shame it is to here in how foul flesshely sin he tempted her / And therefore
I shall not rehearse them / but to clean sowles it is delectable to here

How this holy maid overcame such foul delusyons: and therefore that shall I
reherce: When this holy may de perceyned how besy the fend was to bring her
to sin / She arose against her self* myghtely and punysshed her body by
weryng of the cheyne in so much that the blood followed / And thereto she
walked more then she^ was wont to do in church that almoost by use of the
which the sleep was taken away from her:

And yet would not the fend sece fro his bata^^^e that he had begone. but
he took upon him a body of the air as I have rehearsed to fore with a great
nombre and an horrible company with him and came and stood before this holy
maid as thought he had compassyon of her and cou^seylled her and said: O
wretch why tourmentest thou thy body in so ydell / what shall thou win by
such tourment off pain: wenest thou that thou may continue therein to thyn
last end then may thou never continue therein I warn the well: but if
thou wylt slay thy self and so it were better for the for to sese off this
great folly then so to slay thyn own body: Yet have thou time that now for
to have joy in the world / thou art young / and therefore thou may the
sonner recouere thine strength of thy body again /

Notwythstondyng thyn great penance that thou have do / live as other wymmen
do take an husbond and bring forth children to encrece of mankind: If thy
desire be to plese god / trowest you that holy wymmen have not be weddyd /
Think on Sara and Rebecca / Lya and Rachell. how they were weddyd and brought
forth children and yet weren holy wymmen. Whereto have thou tabe upon the a
synguler life that thou may in no wise continue /

All the whiles that such words and many other like. the fend with his
cursyd company multeplyed against her / She prayed ever deuoutlye and
com^aunded her living to her spouse Jhesu / and kept her heart keys all the
whiles that the fendes stood before her and she answerde none word to them but
thus: I trust in mine lord Jhesu Christ and not in mine self / other word
might they never have of her but always she continued steadfastly in her devout
prayers:

And afterward she told to her confessor master Reymound / and thaughte many
other that were conuersaunt with her this lesson for a general rule / that
when temptacions arysen in us we should never despise ne make questions for
that is she said that the fend seeks off us for to fall in questyons with
him / He trusted so hyely in the great sotelte of his malice that he should
overcome us with his sofystycall resons / Which we should not make questyons
with him ne answer to his questyons / I shall tell you by ensample: Right a
chaste woman to her husbonde should not answer to the sotelte maundes that
wonteth to make to her / but rather bow away from him if she would escape
sin / Right so is a soul the which is coniuncte to our lord by chaste
love should never make questyons ne answer / the questyons to the fend that
cursed auout^^er our enemy: But rather turn her to devout prayer and
command her to our lord / that she consent not to his sotell demau^des /
for by virtue of devout prayer and steadfast faith we may overcome all the
sotell temptacions of the fend: Thus in this wise this holy maid crystis
spouse overcome her enemy so that he cesyd of the kind of temptacions
against her and turned him to another abhomynable kind of temptacions that
was this He brought before her the likeness of me^ and wymmen medlyng togyders
in the fowlest wyses that might be devised / Spekyng to gyders foul dyshonest
words in so much that this cursyd company ran abonte her with ellyng and
