cryeng for to stere her to such abhomynable sins /

O lord god what traueyle had she than in her soul that was so constreyned
to see and to here that thing that she had most in abhomynacion / al be it
she closed her eyes / and stopped her eren.

And there to yet she had another torment for her spouse that our lord Jhesu
was wont to vysyte her and comfort gracyously. Seemed as for a time far from
her that another vysybly ne vnuysybly he showed to her his help / as it seemed /
of the which she had full great sorrow in her soul / all be it that she
cessyd not of her great penance / but ever continued there Inn and in devout
prayer. At the last she bethought by Inspyracyon of the holy ghoost of a
certain fleyte / the which she told afterward to her confessor and to many
other. For to eshe we there by the sotell temptacion of the fend and it was
this. It happed she said that other while devout fervor of a soul leuyng
our lord Jhesu other by sum certain sin / or else by new sotyll
temptacyons of the fend wexyth dull and slow / and other while it is I
brought to very coldenesse. In so much that sum vnwytty folk consyderyng
that they ben destytute so fro ghostly comfortes / the which they were wont
to have leave therefore their ghoostly excercyse that they were wont to use of
prayer / of medytacyons / of redyng / of holy comynycacyons / and of penance
doing / wheby they be made more ready to be overcome of the fend For he desired
no thing else of crystys knight but that he should put a way his armor /
by the which he was wont to overcome his enemy.

A wise knight of our lord Jhesu christ should not do but thus / the more he
sees him self dull and sloth or cold in devotion / the rather he should
continue in his ghoostly exercise / and naught for to make them less / but
rather encrece them.

Another thing also this maid ferned of our lord Jhesu and used for to say
it her self in edyfycacyon of other. Thou vile wretchyd creature art thou
worthy any manner of comfort in this lyffe / why host thou not mind of thy
sins / what supposest thou of thy self wretchyd syn^er this is not I nough to
the / trowest thou that thou art escaped by the mercy of our lord fro ever
lastyng dampnacyon. Therefore thou sholdest be well apayed you wretch though
thou suffreddest / the peynes and derkenes of soul all the days of thy ^^f
why art thou thanne heavy and sorrowful to suffer such peynes. Sithe by gods
grace thou shalt escape endeles peynes / with christ Jhesu without any doubt /
thon shall be comforted endelesly / if thou suffer this peynes pacyentely /
whether thou have chosen to serve our lord only for the comfort / that thou
may have of him in this fyf / nay but for the conforte / that thou shalt
have of him in the bliss of heaven. Therefore arise up now and cesse not of thy
ghostly excercyse that you have used / but rather encrece more there to.

With these darts of mekenes this holy maid wounded the provide king of
babylonye her enemy the fend. And strengthed her self gretely with such wise
words / and as she knoweleched to her confessor master Reymond / there was
such a multitude of fendes in her chamber as her seemed / ^he saw with her
eyes about for to styre her to foul thoughts of sin that she fled her
chamber for a time and kept her self more in the church thanne she was wont
to do. All be it that she was pursued thither by their sotyll temptacyons / yet
nevertheless she thought that she would follow the steps of Saint Jerome
fleenge and hydyng her self by dales and hills in eshewyng of such
abhomynable temptacyons.

And ever when she came home fro church to her chamber / she found so many a
multitude of fendes there Inn / seyenge dishonest words / and doing the
abhomynable dedys of lecherye / and as her seemed rennyng about hyder and
thither / as it had been a passing swarm of flies

Thanne she took her to prayer / and so long she prayed to our lord unto the
time that heuysom compayne were I swaged somewhat fro their abhomynable
temptacyons. When these wretched temptacyons had continued many days to gydres
/ In a time when she was come fro church to her chamber and fill down to
prayer / sone after there appyred a gladsome beme of the holy ghoost / and
opened her soul / that she should have in mind how that not many a days a
fore she had asked of our lord the virtue and the gift of strength. And
what doctrine our lord had give her for to get the gift of virtue and of
strength.

And anon she understood the meuynge of the foul temptacyons of the fend /
and conceived there by a great gladness / that our lord had give her such
strength to overcome them / and purposed ever afterward to suffer mekely and
gladdely all such heuysom temptacion / and all manner dyseases for the love of
her spouse.

Than one of the fendes that was more bolder thanne any of that other and more
wicked spoke to the holy maid in this wise. What thynkest thou to do wretch /
thynkest thou ever to keep this caytyf life / know it well we shall never cesse
to pain the and heavy the to thy death unto the time thou consent to us / To
whom the holy maid answered having in mind the doctrine the which our lord
taught her seyeng thus: I have chose pain for my refresshyng And therefore it
is not hard to me for to suffer them: but rather dylectable for the love of
my savior as long as it pleseth his mageste that I shall suffer them as soon
as she had said that word anon suddenly the abhomynable company of fendes
vanysshed away all confused And after that a great unspeakable lyht of heaven
appieryd and shynned all her chamber / and in that light apperyd our lord
Jhesu christ as he hynge upon the cross when he shed his precious blood and
called the holy maid to him and said: Mine own daughter katheryn: see thou
not what I suffered for the be not heavy therefore for to suffer for me / After
that he came more nerre to her in another manner of lyknesse for to comfort her
and thank her for her glorious victory that she had won Then she after
these words: of saint anthonye seyde to him thus / O my lord Jhesu where were
thou when my soul was so vexyd with such foul fylthy temptacions:

Our lord said again I was in thy soul and in thy heart / Then said she
again / A lord saving always thy truth and the reverence of thy mageste / how
may it be that thou sholdest dwell in so foul a heart: that was replete with
so many fylthy thoughtis and uncleanness /

Our lord said eftsoon, whether caused tho temptacions and tho thoughts in
thyn heart gladness or sorrow delectacion or weylynge /

She answerde nay lord / But great soro we and weylynge / Our lord said
then. who was cause of that sorrow and weylyng: But I that dwelled in thyn
heart: if I had not be there thylke foul thought should had partyd thine
heart and so thou sholdest had dylectacion in them /

But my presence was cause why theymyslyked the: when thou would had put
them fro the with dyplesaunce and myghtest not as thou would thou weptyst /
and were sorry / and all this made I that was present wythinforth with in thyn
heart and defended the from thyn enemies: And suffer the without forth to
troubled as much as was nedeful be and spedefull to thyn health / And when the
time that the bataylle was fulfilled and ended by me. I sent the with out
forth my bemys of light And anon the derkenes of the fendes fled / for they
might not abide there my light is who was he the which enfourmed the now last
that tho pain were to the full holsom for to win ghostely strength by. And
that thou sholdest suffer them patiently as long as it was liking to me: but
only that shyneth in the beme

And by cause thou offredes^ thy self hertely to suffer tho peynes patiently
for my soul Therefore they were freely with draw fro the by showing of my
preserce / And therefore daughter that have so trewely overcome by my virtue /
and not by thine: thou have deserved there by more grace of me then thou
wenest:

Wherefore fro this time fortherward I shall show me to the more famulyerly and
more homely than I have do before / After time this vysyon was ended she was
belefte in so much plente of sweetness that no pen may write it to ye
full. There belefte in her heart syngulerly amerueylous sweetness of that
word that our lord called her his daughter /

When he called her mine own daughter katheryne* So that she prayed her
confessor Master Reymou^d wha^ that ever he would call her he would vouche
sauf to call her on the same wise that euyr her sweetness might thereby be
renewed in her soul / Fro that time fortherward our lord Jhesu her spouse
was with her right homely for he apperyd to her often times other while him self
allone / other while he brought our lady his blessed mother with him /

Other while saint Domynyk there while both to gyders.

Also sometime he brought with him Marie magdalene / Saint Johan the
Euaungelyste / Saint Poule the Appostle and other moo such as he lyked / But
for the more party he came him self allone and spoke with her as homely / as a
friend would speak with his most homely friend / In so much that both to
gyders would walk up and down in her chamber / as two relygyous men or two
clerkys seeing psalms or hours to gydres / And this she be knew often time
afterward to master Reymound her confessor full ferefully. O now was this a
merueylous thing / O what this was a merueylous showing and an homely that
never has be herd before.

Nevertheless maidens ye need to be in no doubt thereof if ye mekely and
Inwardely consydere the depthe of the goodness of our lord:

For to eueryche of his chosen souls he gives sum synguier gift and grace
whereof they may have an excellent Joye above other* that not only the heythe
of his souereygne magnyfycence apperyd in all his saints at onys but in
eueryche by him self sum synguler grace. For right at it is seen all day yt
one man is not like another / but has sum manner of dyfference / Right so
eueri saint in heaven has sum dyffere^ce of som^e synguler grace given of
god fro other / Therefore it is not to merueylle gretely though sum special
grace be seyde of one that is not found thereof / And by cause I have rehersyd
of seeing of there psalms I shall tell you maidens how this holy maid learned
for to read for by techyng of man or of woman learned she never She told ones
to her co^fessoure master Reymond that she had a desired to kunne her
mattyns and therefore on a time she prayed one of her susters to get her an A
/ b / c / to teache her for to know her lettres: And she had I traueylled
sore many wekes to gydres: and did spend her time there aboutes for to know
her lettres: And might not come thereto / She bethought her to complain to our
lord that heavenly master for myspendyng of her time / prayeng him that he
would vouchesauf to teache her if it were liking to him and spendefull for her
so for to kunne to read And else lord thy will be done / For it is Inow to
me if it be lykyng to the ye I be simple of living / and for to spend my time
in holy medytacions / Now is this a merueylous thing She had not so soon
ends her prayer but that she could read lyuelye her psalms as redely as she
had been any kunnyng clerk / when her confessor perceived that he was
gretely astonyed / For as much as she could not spelle ne know uneath no
lettre the which was ordained of god as he supposed for a merueyllous token in
her: After this / this maid gate her books of gods seruyse / for to say
there matyns and her howrys theri^ And among all other verses that she said /
she marked the verse that every hour begins with that is: Deus in
adiutorium meum intend / ^n^e adadiuuandum me festina / And kept that verse
specially in her mind to her lives end. And often times she would reherce yt /
Soon after that she encresyd in her soul merueylously in perfeccion of
contemplacion / And then cessyd little her vocal prayer because that she was
so often times rauysshed in to the heythe off contemplacion / so ferforth that
by cause of such often rauysshyng she might not often times perform ne make an
end of her Pater noster / For her soul was rauysshed fro her outward wits
as I shall declare to you here afterward by the help of god. For thus shall I
make an end of this chapter: All this that is contained therein her confessur
had som^e other by knowleche of her pryuely / And sum by relacion that she
told to other As it had be told of another and not of her self to the more
edyfycacio^ of them

Of her merueylous disponsacyon with the which she was weddyd in faith to our
lord with a ring. Capitulum duodecium /
AS this holy maid encrecyd and profyted more and more day by day in grace
and in virtue / there came an holy desire to her soul to pray our lord to give
her the perfyte degree off feyth: By the which faith she might be more able to
him ^oythouten any chaungynge then she was a fore: Anon forth she prayed to
our lord that he would vouchesauf to encrece her faith and make it so perfyte
in her that it should never be hurte^ne throw down by violence of any manner
aduersarye: To whom ouce lord answered in this wise / I shall dyspouse the to
me in faith / yet she prayed the same often times aftyrward and ever had the
same answer of our lord again At the last it happened a little a fore the
beginning of lent in the days when ye people made an end of eting offlesshe
and in manner made vein and ydil festys in seruyng of the womb*

This holy maid closid her up in her chamber Sekyng by fasting and prayen ge
the gloryus and gracious face of her spouse ^hu axyng specyaly by fervent
prayer vncessablythe same that she axid before of the virtue of faith that he
would vouchesauf to encrece it and make it perfyggt in her / To whom our lord
apperid and said. By cause that thou have putt away and flelde all manner nf
vanytes of etyng of slesshe these days for my love* And set the dylectacion
of thyn heart fully in me this time / where all other about the and namely in
the same house that thou dwell in: maken festys and ioyen therein. I shall
therefore make a solemn feste of dispousacion between the soul and me. And so
as I behyte I shall dispouse the to me in faith / Our lord had not so soon
said this words. That our lady his glorious mother / And his blessed
Euangelyste saint Johan / and the glorious appostle saint poule / and saint
Domynyke the fader of her relygion apperyd and with them Dauyd the prophet
brengyng in his hand a sauter of musyke: First our blessed lady gods mother
came to this holy maid / and took her hand In her holy hand stret chyng out
her fyngers to her sone prayleng him that he would vonchesuf to wedde this
maid to him in feythe. The which devout axynge our lord granted her and
brought forth a Ring arrayed round about with four precious margarete stones
/ And in the over part off the ring was enclosyd a right fair dyamant stone
/ That ring he put with his holy hand upon the fyngre of this maidens right
hand seyeng to her thus Loo I dyspouse the to me that am thy maker and thy
savior in faith the which disposycion shall be confermed and kept in the
vndefouled unto the time you shall halowe everlasting weddyng with me in the
bless of heaven / Therefore douhter now fro this time fortherwarde work
myghtely and put away all manner of doubt for now thou art armed with the
strength of the feith / for to overcome thereby all thyn adversaries / And thus
this gracious vision cessyd: But ever afterward* this ring bylefte up on this
holy maids finger not to other folks syht but to her own sight for she be
knew many times and often to her confessor master Reymound with great dread
and fere that she saw ever that ring upon her fyngre / And there was never
time but that she saw it / Loo maidens ryht as saint katheryn the martyr
virgyn and queen. After her baptym was dyspoused to our lord as ye legende
makes mention / Right ye may consydre now how this holy maid katheryn /
After so many victoryes of temptacions of her flesh was solemply dyspoused to
the same lord: And ye consydre the coudycyons of this ring / ye shall^welle
see that the tokene acordeth that that is betokens to She axed steadfast
feythe / what is strenger than a dyamaunt stone: it wythston dyth all manner
hardenesse and it persyth the hardest thing that is /

but that stone it self is broke only with the blood of a goote. Right so a
strong feythfull heart wythstondeth and ouercometh with his strenthe all
manner of aduersyte / But the mind of crystys precious blood the which is
called in holy write a goote the which precious blood he shadde upon the
cross for mankind: that stroge heart is re lentyd and al to broste / the four
precious Margarete stonys in the ring betokenyth no thing ellis / but four
purytres and clenes yt which was in that holy maid / that is clennes of her
entente clennes of her thout clennes of her speech and clennes of her workynge
All these shall be declared by the grace of god more largely here aftyrwarde I
supposo that this dyspousacion^ was no thing else but a confirmaciou^ of
godis grace And the token of this gracyous confyrmacion^ / was ye ring the
which only apperid to her and to none other for this cause that she should not
fere ne dread to deliver other owte of the wretched world by her prayers / and
by the help of that special grace that god had endowed her with. One of ye
princypall causes after holy doctors why ye almighty god vouchesauf of his
synguler preuylege to show to som^e that they ben plesaunt to him and in
estate of grace is in this wicked world for worship for his intent is to
send them / For to fight with this wicked world for worship of this holy
name and health off souls as he did to his Appostlis on wytsondaye / the
which token / specyal tokenes of grace: Right so this holy maid above the
condycion of all other wymmen after time she was thus confermed i^ grace / she
was sent openli for the wourshyppe of god to procure health of sowles / as it
shall be declared by the help of god here afterward more openly / And
therefore I trow it was that she took of our lord the token of confyrmacio^ of
grace that she should boldly and myghtely do execucion of that / that our
lord commanded her / Thus shall I make an end of this chapter and of the
first part of the legende of this holy maid saint katheryn of Scene to the
worship of the holy trynyte and to health of sowles / Regnaute semper in oi^us
scis domino nostro Ihesu cristo / qui^ cum patre almoque spu^isco^ viuit et
regnat deus Per oi^a secula seculorum Amen /

Here begins the second party in the which is showed the conversation of
this holy maid with men / And how the gifts which she had received off
our lord pryuyly enclosed within herself were openly showed to the world /
And first how our lord bad her that she should be conuersaunt among men /
Capitulum Prymum
^After time that this holy Maid was despoused as it is rehearsed before / our
lord began to draw her litill and little to the conversation of men / And
that was full mennerly and mesurably not for to wythdrawe utterly fro her his
dyuyne presence / but rather as much as longs to the mesure of perfection
for to encrese it as it shall be declared openly afterward / And therefore in a
time when he appyred to her and had taught her of the kingdom of heaven and
showed her many mysteryes / And also to seye the psalms and the hours of
dyuyne serui^ce as it is rehearsed before / forthwith he bad her that she should
go down to mete with other of her moders household and afterward that she
should come again to him When this holy maid herd this she sobbyd and wept
and fill down to his feet for sorrow and fayde to him these words / O sweet
Ihesu lord why put you me away fro the / and if I have offendyd and
displesyd the master / Loo lord there is mine body at thyn feet / punysshe it
and I shall gladly help thereto / and suffer me not good lord to be punysshed
with so^ sharp and so hard a pain to be departed in any manner of wise fro
thin blissed presence / what have I to do with that mete I have mete that they
knew not of whether receives anon more life by bodily metes or by ghostely
metes /

Lord as thou know well I have fled the conversation off men / that I
might the sonner find / and now sithe I have found the by the mercy and
graciously thou haste showed the to me though I am unworthy should I now than
forsake this precious tresour And put me to the conversation of men eftsoon
and so ben found reprobable in the faith / A nay lord suffer not that be so
for thine infynyte goodness / wha^ she had thus long wept and weyled with
sweet sobbyng words / our lord said to her / suffer now dear daughter for
it is full semely to the that thou shodeste fulfylle all manner of virtue that
not only it be fruytfull to thyn self / but also to other by mine special grace
it is not mine intent for to dysceuere or depart the from me in any manner of
wise. But rather I shall have the to me more strenger by medytacions of
neighbors charity Knew thou not well that in thise two things scondeth the
perfection of mine commaundementys that is in love off god and love of thyn
neighbor / I will therefore that thou will fulfylle the verof these two
preceptis that thou may go to heaven not with one wynge but with tweyne / Have
daughter how of thin young age thou have had hither to a yele and a love of
health of sowles / and by me it has be encresyd in so much that in thyn
young age thou purposed the to feyne the aman by cause thou myghtest the sonner
be received among the order of the friar prechours in strange contrees that
you sholdest not be known so for to prouffyte to the health of mennys souls
and for yt synguler love that thou had to mine servant Domynyk / thou
desyrest with a great honor his habyte that thou now have received / the
which domynyk pryncypally for health of souls I ordained that order why
merueylest thou / and wey lest thou so / if I bring the to that / that thou
have so long desired / With these words of our lord / this holy maid was
gretely comforted and said unto him like as our glorious lady glorious vyrgyn
marie said to gabriel such words Qn^o fit istud / A good lord in what wise
and what manner may this be done / Our lord said again as mine goodness shall
dyspose and ordeyne / Then^e she as a good dyscyple and a true follower of her
master Christ Ihesu said lord thyn will be done in all things and not in me
for I am derkenes / and thou art light / I am she that is naught / and thou art
he that is ought I am she that is vnwis / and thou art he that is endeles
wysdom of ye fader / But yet I pray the lord in what manner of wise may this be
that you seyste now that I wretch than am so freell should be so profitable to
mannys soul Thou know well lord that men setten little store by women's
words speak ye never so virtuously as it were not semely / Ne lyuest thou that
wymmen should be more conuersaunt among men / To this our lord answered in
manner as Gabryell answered our glorious lady glorious vyrgyn Mary / and said
there is none word that comes fro gods mouth impossible at him for to be
done / Am not I he the which has made mankind both man and woman and the
shappe of every either / And where that I will enspyre mine grace al is one to me
both man and woman / the neck again in his kind / But by cryeng of one of
this maids susters to her that she should cese she left of / And after time
that her spyryte was restoryd again to the bodily wyttys she felt her neck
so sore as thought it had be smyten with many great strokys / There as the
holy maid told it afterward to her confessor master Reymou^de if her mother
had put never so little more strength than she did to ryghting of her neck
as she was about* she should have broken her neck / with such manner passing
out of the body / The soul of this holy maid was often times rauysshyng* so
that other while by vyolens of the spyryte / the body was left up fro the
earth / as marie Magdalene was in time of her rauysshyng as it shall be
declared afterward more openly /

But now I shall tell you of a miracle that befyll in the beginning of her
rauysshyng / It befyl in a time when this holy maid tournyd a spete or a
broche with flesh by the fire of hot brenning coals, her soul was enflam^ed
and burnt in the mean while with the fire of the holy ghost / And anon she
was rauysshed fro her bodily wits seasyng for ye time of her tournyng of her
spytte / Wha^ her brothers wife the which was called Lysa perceived this
knowing the condycions of this holy maid* she took the spytte of her hand and
let her alone / and when the mete was ynow* and also folk had suppyd / yet
she bylefte in the sarauysshyng / Then Lysa bethought her to abide upon her
unto the time that she had do / She brought her husbond a bed and her
children and came again to aspye how she did / and found here fall down in
to the hot brennyng coals with that Lysa weyled and cried and said Alas alas
katheryn is all brennyd and ran to her anon and pullyd here out of the fire.
A and found her clothes nothing hurt ne burnt ne having no manner of tastyng
of the fire, ne yet more over there bylefte nomaner of ashes upon her clothes
/

Loo perceive ye not maidens what virtue of gostely fire was within this maids
soul by whose might the strength of that outward natural fire was utterly
wytdrawe / See ye not how the miracle of the children which were cast in to
the oven for to be brent was then renewed in this holy maid. And this
miracle was not onys showed in her but often times:

Onys it befyll her as she was in the church of the friars when she was so
rauysshed: she bowed her head down to a pyler. in the mean while / in the
which pyller there were certain images of diverse saints at the reuerens of
which saints there was a man styked up a wax candell brennyng the which
candell fill down upon this holy maids head in time of her rauysshyng / And
so it brennyd upon her head in to the time the candell was all wasted / And
so she had no harm: Was not this a merueylous thing and a wounderfull that
ye candell brennyd upon her head till it was wasted and hurt nothing her
kerchies And when the candell was all burnt / It quenchyd upon her head as
though it had be quenchyd upon a stone or upon earth.

Of this miracle bare witness many of her susters that saw it and told
afterward to her confessor / Master. Reymound: One of the susters which saw
it was called lysa / another Alyxa / and the third Francisca. Yet beside as
this it befyll like unto the same of her in diverse places of the world there
that she came: Namely when she was about to edefye men^ys sowles to virtue /
than the fend by his malice was gretely stered against her by the sufferau^ce
of god: and so ferforth that in the presence of many of gods servants he
kast her in to a fire /

And whiles other were about to draw her out with weeping and weylyng she
smyled upon them and come out of the fire by her self and was nothing hurt
neither in body ne in her clothes / Then she said to them that stood about
beeth no thing aferde: For it is mine ghostely enemy the fend that has do
this miracle and this records diverse that saw it to master Reymound her
confessor /

Another time also in her chamber by her beds side there was an erthen pan
with brennynge coals in the which brennyng coals the enuyous fend cast her
with such a strength that her head was the first that fill in the fire and so
the pan to braste for vyolence of the stroke / and yet her head was in no
wise hurt: She arose up and said with smilyng there to a devout woman which
was called Gabryell / Loo how this malycions enemy werketh:

Like to I ride in vitas patrum of a woman that was called Infracia: and
therefore it is none merueyle though our lord suffer the fend to work such
things in his derlynges and chosen children / sythen it so was that he suffered
him to work as hard things in his person / wha^ he suffered him to set him
upon the pynacle of the temple / And upon the hye hylle /

Tus by such merueylous things our lord wrought merueylously in his maiden
katheryn so that she encresyd more and more by his grace every day in his
perfection and as much that love was both rote and cause of all her werkys:
The charytable werkisof her neybours passed all other werkys. And the
charytable werkys was in double wise that is both to body and soul.

The first shall I tell you of the dedis of charity and of mercy that she did
to her neighbors that were syke in body / And afterward of the deeds of
charity and of mercy that she did to them that were seek in soul /

The next chapter shall declare openly of diverse merueylys that our lord
showed in her in helyng of pour folk And also of a merueylous charity that
she showed a nemptis hem that were seek in body / The witness of this chapter
is rehearsed within the same chapyter /

Of woundres which she did in health and in comfort to the necessyte of
them that were pour and nedy Capytulum iij
When this holy maid Katherin perceived yt the more mylder she was to her
neighbors the more gracyous she was to the syghte of her spouse Ihesu / she
applied her ever afterward to socour and help them in her need with all her
heart largely /

And by cause she would nothing have of her own as her own in her own
possession* Right as a very relygyous woman that had ordained in her own
heart to keep the iij pryncipall vows of relygyon as it is rehearsed before in
the first party / lest she should be found gylty of withdrawynge other mennys
good against the will of ye hauer / she went to her fader and besoughte him
mekely and lowely that he would give her leave to give alms after her
conscience to ^ore folk of the goodis of god I give him in his household / To
the which her fader granted her the more freely in as much as he know well
that she following perfyghtly the steps off of our / And granted not oonly
to her thus in pryuyte between them both: But also afterward to all that were
in in his household he gave in commandment that no body should let his
dear daughter for to give alms of such goods that our lord had give him
in his household though she would give to pour folk all that ever he had in
his household / As Soon as she had this license* she began to depart the
goods of her fader to pour folk: Nevertheless in as much as she lived with
a gift off dyscrecion: she departed not that good to all that would ask /
But to them that she knew were need folk / all though they asked not /
among all other nedy folk there came two he knowleched that there were many
pour nedy householders a little beside the Cite of gene that had great need and
were sore ashamed for to ask / after time she knew that she forgate it not
but that she arose up erly in ye morrow as saint Nycholas did and bare on her
sholders home to their houses both wine and oil and other things that was
needful / And as god would when she came she found her dorys open And she put
within the doors that she brought: and drew the door to and fledpreuyly her
way

It befyll in a time that she was seek in body so that fro the sole of her
foot to the top of the head the body was swollen / that she might not arise
up of her bed ne stand on her fete* And she herd say than / that there was
a pour wydowe a little beside, the which great hunger and great need with
her sons and daughters: For compassyon that she had of this pour woman and
of her children: The next night after she prayed our lord that he would
vochesauf to give her so much strength for a time yt she might goo and so
oour that pour woman / Anon she aroos, up erly upon the morrow and filled her
sack of her faders: where and her great vessel or a flacat of wine and
another vessel with oil: and what that she might ever find beside forth the
which might be necessary to mannys lyuelood and all these she kept in her
chamber: all be it that eueryche of these was for her berdem ynow for to here
alone yet she bare all at onys to the wedowes house sum thereof she trussed
upon her sholders sum up her right arm and sum up her lift arm and sum
thereof bonnden onder her gyrdell / and by miracle that was heavy ynouht to bear
eueryche by him self / she bare it all at onys esely without any pain or
greuau^ec She knowleche after ward both to her confessor Master Reymou^d and
to other of the friars: that the berdom wayde no more to her than thought she
had lift up a little wase of straw: and yet in truth if it had be
trewely wayed

It should have wayed an hundred pound of weyte or there about Er than the
common bell of the Cite was roungen erly in the morrow it was not lefull never
one to walk in the cite: aft time it was ronge this holy maid waited well her
time and took her Journeye with her burden / All be it that she were young and
all forbolnyd bysekenes: yet she ran to the pour wydowed house so fast as
though she had felt nothing of pains ne of the burden / And wha^ she came
nyghe to the pour wydowes house her byrthen waxit heavy and greuo^ to bear / so
that her seemed she might not bear it a paas further / when she perceived this
she understood anon yt it was our lords will and prayed him devoutly with
trust that he would vouchesaufe to ese her / Anon she was esyd of her byrthen
/ and came to the pour wydowes house and found her door half open / As preuyly
as she could she drew her byrthen within the door / and yet it made such a
noise that it woke the wydowe. And she fled as she might for sekenes but that
was not full far / but for her sekenes encresyd more and more / by the
ordeynaunce of god that uneaths she might remeue her out of the way /
wherefore she spak to our lord with wei lyng chere and in manner in smylyng chere
/ and said good lord why have thou so dysceyued me / it is good to the to
shame me here / it is thy will that mine folly be pupplysshed to all folk here
about have thou now forgete thy mercy that you haste showed to me thyn
vnwourthy* I pray the lord yield me mine strength that I may come home to mine
chamber / in time she spoke thus and these words and like to these / She
enforced and strengthed her self that she might go forth seyeng to her own
body thus / thou most needs forth though thou sholdeste deye by the way and
therefore goo forth what with going but more with crepyng forth she went little
not so fer / but that the pour wedowe arose up and aspyed by the habyte who
it was that did her that benefet

Our lord then considered that she was gretely tourmentyd in her going /
restoryd her again to the strength that she had before / but not so
perfyghtely / So that with great hardynes she came home er then it was light
day. And lay down in her bed right feeble as she did before thus our
lord touched and touched her by sickness as him lyked / Loo maidens here ye
may see the miracles of saint nycholas been renewed in this holy maid / and
not only by miracle / But by many miracles: now shall I proceed forth and show
you the virtuous living of saint martyn / How our lord showed him in her:

It befyll on a time when this holy maid was in the church of the freyers
There came to her a pour man and asked sum help of her for the love of god.
This holy maid perceived well that she had nothing that she might give hi^
For she was not wont to here neither gold ne silver / she prayed him that he
would abide a while till she came from home / For gladly she would and
plenteuously give alms of such things yt she had at home in household /
Then ye pour man sade if thou have any thing for to give me here I pray the
to give me for I may not abide so long / it was to suppose by this that it was
another yt apperyd in the pour man his lykenes and not he that it seemed / This
holy maid was both that she should goo fro her with out somewhat she bethought
her what she might give him to fulfylle his need / Anon it came to her mind
of a little silver crose that hynghe by her bodies yt which for that time she
had in her hand she pulled away that little cross and gave it gladly to the
pour man / when the pour man had that cross he went away fro her gladly
and asked no more alms ye day of none other man as though he had come for the
cross alone / The next night following when this holy maid prayed as she was
wounte to do Almighty god our savior apperyd to her having that same little
cross in in his blessed hand arrayed with mani precious stones and said
daughter know not thou this cross / this maid answerde to him and said /
she knew it well but she said that it was not so fair araied wha^ she had
it / To whom our lord said again / yesterday thou gave it me this gladly
with great charity and love the which love and charity betokens by these
precious stones therefore I behote that at the day of dome before all ye
company of angels and men / I shall show the this to encrece of thy joy /
For I shall not head ne suffer to be hyd the deeds of mercy that been do by the
/ with this our lord cesyd of that aperycion. and she thanked ourlord / and
ever after was I steryd to do more such alms as it was well proved
afterward / another day also it befyll when deuyn service was do at the
friars after time that the people was goo out of the church and she bylefte
behind alone with one of her susters for to pray* as she came dounward fro
the chapel the which was ordained / for the susters of penance / our lord
apperyd to her in likeness of a pour pilgrim at the age as her seemed of ij.
or iij and thyrty year half naked and asked her that she would give him clothes
for the love of god / Theen^e she was that time steryd to do deeds of mercy
more than ever she was: she prayed the pour man that he would abide a while
unto the time she came down again fro the chapel: and then she would help
him of sum clothes / She went up again to the chapel and did of herk
ertyll under the which kertell she wered next her her body here cote that was
without sleues and gave it with a great gladness to the pour man / After time
the pour had received it he asked more of her and said / A / a. good lady I
pray you sithe ye have give me a woollen clothe / give me lynen clothes for to
were next mine body / Then she said to him come after me and thou shall houe
gladly and she went a fore and her spouse Thesu unknowing to her in a pilgrim
lykenes followed her. When she came home she went thither where the lynen clothes
of her fader and of her brothers layen / and brought out both a sherte and
other lynen clothes and took gladly to the pour pilgrim / Yet when the pour
man had received that he asked more and prayed her that she would give him
sleues to his kertyll for to cover his arms /

With that she went her in nothing heavy of his crawyng but gladly sought
about for his sleues / At the last she found a new cote of a maiden
servant of the house having and hangyng upon a perch the which was never
werid there of she took away the sleues and took it gladly to the pour man /
yet he asked more and said / Lady thou have now clothed me, he thank the for
whose love you have do it but yet I have a felawe lyeng in an hospytall her
beside the which needs gretely clothes. If ye will send him any clothes I
shall bear it to him in your byhalue full gladly / yet this holy maid for his
multyplyeng of asking was never the weryer But rather the more fervent for to
do alms largely She be thought her where she mygth have a clothe to clothe
with this nedy man yt lies in the hoospytall Then fill to her mind that all
the meyne of the hou / sold were right loathe to given alms out take her fadre
allone / and therefore ye shytte up all her clothes under lok and keye / lest
she should find them and give them in alms. Ouermore she considered
dyscretely that she had take I nogh away of the maiden servant of the
household / and therefore she would take away no more of hyres by cause she was
nedy her self. Thanne she dysputed with her self whrther she should give him
her own cote or not / by cause she had no moo but one / charity said yes /
but hone ste said nay. At last charity oueroo me honest / that is for to say
charity that longs to the soul / overcome honest the which had
compassyon upon the body

She thought if the pour man should go away without sum clothe / it should be
slanderous to other / and if she had given her own coote and goo naked than
should she had slandred sowles / whose souls she ought for to love more than
the body And therefore her seemed that sowles should not be slaundred in no wise
for no temporal alms. And thanne she answered to the pour man thus. Trewely
dear friend if it were honest and lefull to me for to give my cote that I were
thou sholdest have it gladdely. But by cause I have no moo / it were not semely
that I should give away this. And therefore I pray the hold me excused / for
gladdely would I give it the if I had any moo. Then the pour man smyled
upon her and said well lady I see well if thou had moo thou would
gladdely give me / therefore I thank the / fare well. When he was borned fro
her / this holy maid perceived by certain signs that it should be he the
which was wont to appear to her and was often times conuersaunt with her /
she was in manner of doubt / but her heart brenned in love. Nevertheless in
as much as she held her self to comyne occupacyon of household as she was
wont to do The next night suyng our lord Jhesu christ appeared to her / as she
prayed in lykenes of that pour man holdyng in his hand that cote that the
holy maid gaf him arrayed with clear shynyng precious stones / and said to her
thus Dear daughter know thou not this dote / she answered and said yes / but
she gaf it not so arrayed: To whom our lord said again. Thou gave me yester
day this cote so freely and so charytable that it voyded away fro me the pain
of cold Therefore I shall now give the a cote / the which shall be Inuysyble
to men / but to the it shall be sensyble. Out of mine holy body I shall take it
/ and hyue it the / by the which both thy body and thy soul may be keuered
and kept from noyous cold unto the time yt they shall be arrayed in joy
without an end a fore my saints and angels. Anon forth with he took out a
clothe of a sangueyne color with his holy hondes out of the wound of his side
shynyng all about to the quantyte and mesure of the maidens body. Where with
he arrayed her with his own holy hondes and said. This clothe I give the all
the while thou dwell in earth in token of thy clothe of joy / that thou
shall be arrayed within heaven Thus this vysyon cessyd. After that the holy maid
had so great grace in receyuyng of that ghostly gift / not only in her
soul but also in her body / that fro that hour in to her endyng day / she
neded never to were moo clothes in winter thanne in somer. For were the wedder
never so cold she used no mo clothes than a cote and a kertell. For ever
afterward as she seemed she felt that ghostly cote upon her / the which our
lord gaf her / and that was the cause that she felt no cold. See ye not
maidens of what worthynes this holy maid was that followed Saint Nycholas in
gyuyng of atmespryuely / and followed saint martyn in gyuyng of her own clothes
the which our lord allowed by his holy apperyng to this blessed maid. And
there to gaf her a sensyble and an everlasting token / for to feel in earth how
plesau^t alms deeds ben to him. Me seems that when our lord said to this
holy maid that he would she we her that little cross at the day of dome the
which she gave in alms And also that he would array her with a clothe of joy
/ in heaven is no thing else but a sikernes of endeles health. And thereto an
excellent joy in bliss for her mede

Therefore maidens set not little by such reuelacyons and such tokenes / for
sykernesse of endeles health only causes so great joy and so great comfort
in a soul that it were impossyble a tongue to tell it or a pen to write it.
What follows after such a sykernesse of joy trow ye to a soul. Trewely
encrece of all virtue of pacyence / of strength / of temperaunce of business
/ and delygence in keeping of her self / in holy works of feyth / of hope / of
charytr / and of such other virtues.

And all that were hard to such a soul a fore ben made by such comfort
right esye Loo what grace such predestynacyon notefyed to a clean soul
wercheth.

Another time also it befyll that this holy maid fulfilled with compassyon
perceived that there was a man the which made him pore wylfully for gods love
and lacked mete / wherefore she took preuely a lynnen bag and filled it with
eggs / and bare it with her preuely under her ^oote to refresshe with that
pour man when she met with him. She came to the place there that the pour
man dwelled / and entered first in to the church there beside for to pray. And
when she was entered / she bethought on our lord so Inwardly / and anoue her
spirit was rauysshed / so that she was fully for that time wythdrawe from her
outward wyttys / as it is rehearsed before.

When she was thus rauysshed / it happed suddenly that the body bowed to a
pyler casuelly on that side that the eggs were on / so that she lened fully
upon the bag with eggs / thanne was there in the same bag for gotten a fore
a thymbyll as tayllours sown with / the which thymbyll was broken in three
parties by burthon of her body / but the eyren that charity hyd there were hole
and in no party broken. Now was this a meruayllous thing that the eyren were
hole / and the thymbyll of coper was to broke / so our lord showed there his
miracle in the charytable eyren. For our lord showed his help not only by this
holy maid to nedy folk / but also he showed his miracle in her by works of
his godhede

And for to declare the more openly / I shall tell you a meruaylles thing / of
which meruayll were wytnes both men and wo^man about the nombre of xx of
this maidens faders household Her mother Lapa told master Reymond her
daughters confessor that after time her daughter this holy maid had leave of
her fad to give alms. It befylle that the meyne of the household had drunk
among them a certain vessel of wine / so that the remenau^t the which was
left was not fresshe for to give to pour men / in asmoche she had in custom
to give them of the best for gods love. She went her than to the next
vessel of wine there beside in her faders seller / and tamed that for pour
folk And gaf them largely there of every day as they neded many days to gyder
/ and it was not aspyed of the meyne. At the last when the first vessel was
done / the boteler mynystred drink to the meyne of the vessel the which the
holy maid had tamed. Yet the holy maid left not therefore / but always she
gave there of to the pour folk / and ye more the meyne drunk / the more
largely she gave to pour folk / and it was not aspyed / ne the wine was never
the vnfressher ne never the less in the vessel / but allewaye kept his
estate / both in fullness and in fresshenesse. All the meyne of the household
gretely meruaylled there of that the vessel continued so long / and the wine
was so good and so fresshe / for it was well know a fore / that such a
vessel of wine might not last over xv days or xx days at the ferthest
Nevertheless it continued not only xx days / but a full month complete And
yet it semyd that the vessel was no wise lessened.

All the meyne had meruayll there of yt the wine was so good and so fresshe and
lastyd so long. For better wine them seemed they tastyd never It was unknow to
them all how that might be / but the holy maid knew well I nogh yt it was by
miracle of our lord / by cause of the alms that she gave there of the more
largely to the pour folk. And therefore she gave there of the more largely to
pour folk openly that all the meyne might see it and yet it seemed never the
less in the vessel. O month was passyd and an other began to enter / and yet
the wine continued ever like fresshe / and like full as it did first in to the
time the grapes were ripe for to make new wine. Whenne the g^apes were ripe
and vessellys were ordained for to be filled with new wine / the master of
the wine bad and commanded / that the vessel which co^tynued so long with
old wine / should be emptyed and fyllyd with new wine One of the servants
made ordinance for to empte that vessel by fyllyng of botellys / and yet it
seemed never the less. At the last the vessel was undone for to be gawgid
to know there by what was left in the vessel / and it was found all dry as
though there had no wine be there Inn many months before Then all the
household were more amexuaylled of ye miracle then they were of the
habundaunce of wine before.

Loo maidens what miracle our lord showed by gyuyng of alms deed of this holy
maid Katheryne / the which miracle was openly afterward known in the Cite of
Seen Thus ends this chapter. The wyttenesse of this matter contained in this
chapter ben rehearsed in this chapter.

Of meruayllous dedys which she did in lowely and besy seruyse to them that
were syke. Capitulum iiij
This holy maid had a meruayllous compassyon in her soul of pour folk and
nedy But yet she had a more excellent and a more meruayllous pity of seek
folk / for the which pity that she had of them she wroughte many wonder
things / whom I shall rerce by the grace of god / for the more edyfycacyon of
them the which shall read or here this holy legende. And though it seem to
sum incredyble / yet shall I not leave therefore. In the cite of Seen there was
a full pour womman / and a syke that for need and wantyng of temporal gooddes
/ she was constreyned to lygge in an hospytak in the same Cite where she
supposed to have and find remedy of her syknes / that she might not have by
her self / it happed thanne that she was received in to a pour hospytall of
the same cite / in the which hospytall uneath she might have that she nedyd
Her sykenesse encrecyd so hyghely that she was a lepre tho^ugh out all her body
/ then all that ever were with Inn the hospytall eshewed her te more / and
dysposed for that she should be sent to the spytellhous without the town /
the which was ordained for lazaros and not for to abide among them. When
this holy maid perceived this / she went full of charity to the same
hospytall / and vysyted the pour leprous womman / and mynystred to her not
only the substance of temporal gooddes / but also the help of her own
mynystracyon. For every day on the morrow / and every night at even / she
vysyted the same seek womman by her own person consyderyng in that same
leprous womman her spoust Jhesu with her ghoostly eye. And therefore she served
her to more besely / the more dylygentely / and the more mekely / this holy
maid served her the more prude and unkind / the seek womman was against her.

For so often times it happeth in them that been not meke / that the more mekenes
there is showed to them / the more proud they be. And there that they should
thank our lord for the kyndnes which is showed to them / the show rather
Iniuryes and wrongs / right so did this seek womman to this holy maid when
she saw that she was served so customably every day of this holy maid / she
began to chyde her when she was not served to her plesaunce. It befyll other
while that this holy maid was long at the church / and continued sometime
longer then sometime / and that was the cause often time why she was tarried fro
that seek wo^man And after when she came late to the seek wo^man / she would
chyde her shappely / and said to her soornfully many such heavy words. O lady
queen welcome / where have ye ben so long lady queen / a now ye be a great
lady that so long have been at the frerys / have ye talkyd I nough with the
freres lady / with such like words and many like these / she did what she
could to styre this holy maid to wrath / yet was she not styred by her words
/ but rather served her as she would her own mother / and comforted her as
lowely / and as mekely as she would her own mother / seeing to her right thus O
good mother / for gods love be not dyspleased with me / for though I have be
long I shall mende all thing anon. Than she hyd her fast and made a fire /
and ordained besyly for her mete / and for all other necessaryes as she would
for her own mother / so that the seek womman in all her vnpacyence meruaylled
of her pacyence This rebukynge continued long time / and yet was that holy
maid never weary of her seruyse / but rather continued / many folk had meruayll
thereof. But her own mod Lapa was gretely troubled with al and cried upon her
that she should leave that minystracion lest she were a lepre as ye seek woman
was / and oftymes she said to her Daughter I wot well thou shall be a leper if
thou continue in service of this seek woman / and that may I not suffer / And
therefore leave of I charge the / To whom this holy maid excused her honestely
and said that she had it of our lord that she should not leave the
minystracion of that pour woman / And so she e^ed her mother / and she
continued forth in her holy mynystracion. Then the fend perceived that she
might not be overcome by sweet reuelyng / he turned him to another while by
the suffraunce of our lord and made her hondes leper the which touched the
lepers body of the seek woman in so ferforth that every body yt saw her said
that she was a leper yet would she not sece thefor but rather desires to be a
leper than for to se^e of holy ministracio^ / she despised her own body and
rought never what befyll to her so that she mightserue our lord That lepers
sekenes continued upon her many days /

But her seemed full few day in comparyson of great love that she had to our
lord. That blessed lord the which tournyd all thing to god in his lovers
after time he consyderyd the ghostely strength of his spouse this holy maid:
he would not suffer that the lepers sykenes should long endure in her / Within
a little time afterward it happed by the dysposycyon of our lord that lepers
woman should pass out of this world / So that in a time of her passing this
holy maid was with her and comforted her besely and blessydly.

When she was passed she washed deuotly that lepres body and arrayed it to the
berynge / And when her dyryge and her mass was done / she beryed her with her
own hondes / And as soon as she was buried / the leper passed away fro her
hondes as though she had never no ne sykenesse thereof / But rather her hondes
was more fayrer afterward then any place of her body / as though she had
never be touched with any spyce of lepre. See not ye maidens what encrece of
virtue this holy maid wan by this deed of mercy / charity the mother of virtue
stererd her to do that charytable deed of mercy and meekness conpeled with
charity the which made her to be subject and servant to the seek / And also
pacyence was conpeled with that charity the which made her to suffer pacyently
and gladly the seek wommans rebukynge:

And yet ferthermore to this deed off charity was knytte wythouten any doughte
sekernesse of clear faith / By the which faith she beheld ever her spouse
Jhesu in her soul as often as she mynystred to that woman.

And yet nevertheless she failed none hope, by the which she continued to the
last end in her holy mynystracyon. After all these holy company of virtues
followed an open miracle in clensyng of that lepre by the death of this pour
woman the which she took by her mynystracyon. This is a gracious miracle and a
merueylous yet should ye see and here a more merueylous thing that followed if
ye lysten / and here it besely / In the same Cite of Gene there was a susters
of penance of Saint Domynyk seek yt which was called after the manner of
speech i^ ye country Palmaria / ye suster Palmaria was so gretely styred to
hate by excytacion of ye fend against this holy maid katheryn / yt as often as
ever she saw her or herd herd her speak or herd speak of her. she was hyghely
troubylyd in her soul so ferforth that she showed all the tokenes of malice
against her both in ba^bytyng of her pryuyly and openly and also in cursyng /
As Soon as the holy maid perceived this / she showed to her all manner of
myldenes and mekenes for to pees her in that that she could: but always her seek
suster despised all her meekness to the vtterest and set none price by her
Then this holy maid ran by prayer with a fervent deuote heart to our lord
Ihesu her spouse prayeng to him specially for her seek suster that he would
vouchesauf to give her grace of forgyuenes the prayers were as a brennyng fire
ascendynge up to our lord askyng of him both mercy and dome / all be it that
the intent of this holy maid was nothing else but for to ask mercy for her
and no ne dome / yet it was lykyng to our lord for that time not for to give
his mercy without dome / there showed our lord his great dome but if
byrrayers of this holy maid / He showed a more gretter mercy / he smote
mercyably to that suster Palmarya in her body that her soul shol be made hole
/ but what hardynes of obstinacion was in that seek suster / And what swetenes
of charity there against was in his spouse katheryne / It was clearly showed
afterward by ryghtwysdom evermore he encresyng in this holy maid katheryn the
love of sowles by showing of a wonderful fayrnes of that susters soul / the
which was first by ye right wisdom of him I demed to be dampened for her
obs^ynacie / but merytes and prayers of this holy maid / it was afterward
saved / When our lord had smite that suster palmarya in her body by bodily
sekenes to that intent only that her soul should be more hole / yet would she
not sece of her malycyous hate that she showed without cause to this holy maid
/ But rather was more grievous to her after her sekenes then she was in her
hele / The more froward she was to the holy maid. the more mekenes she she wed
again to her and would often times full charitably be with her and do her service
both with loving words and deeds Yet was that seek suster harder then any
stone against her that neither by charytable words ne deeds ne seruyces she
would not be pesed / but ever was grutchyng upon her so ferforth that she bad
her goo out of the house that she was inn with a wood violent spyryt This
consyderyd our lord that rightwis judge / he leyde his hand of ryghtwysnes upon
that enmye of charity / and touched her so / So suddenly that both without
shryfte and housell she drew fast to the death of body and soul: When this
holy may herd her of / Anon she went to her chamber and bysoughte our lord by
devout prayer for that soul lest it should peryche by occasyon of her / Such
words she seyde to our lord in her soul in time of her prayer as afterward
she was be know to her confessor / Lord whyder I wretch am I bore to the
end by occasyon of me souls I made like to yt should be put to endeles peynel:
^and wylt you suffer lord yt by occasyon of endeles da^pnacion to mine suster to
whom I should be an instrument of everlasting health: A mine good lord put
away such an orybyll dome sor the multitude of thyn great mercy / It had be
better I had never be borne / than soulis I bought by precious blod should for
me be dampened

O lord be these thine byhestes the which thou behotest me by thy large mercy
I should be profitable to the soul hele off mine neighbors: be these the
fruytes of health that I should bring forth for that mine suster should be
dampened / and none douwte mynsynne is cause thereof and of her pain / For other
fruit bring I not forth but sin alone / But yet shall I not cese to ask
mercy unto the time I have sum comfort of mine susters sauacion in this wise
this holy maid prayed more in soul then in word outward and for that she
should have the more compassyo^ of her susters soul: our lord showed her in the
mischefs perile that her susters soul was inn comered and wythinne that sight
our lord answered her and said that he might not suffer it of his ryghtwysnes
but that such a malycious hate and an obstynate must needs be punysshed /
Then the holy maid fell down a fore our lord in prayer and said: Lord I
shall go never out of this place in to the time, thou have showed methy mercy
for my suster / punisshe me lord for her sin for I that am cause of her
trespaas should be punisshed and not she therefore merciable lord I beseech the
for thy great mercy and thyn endeles godenes that you suffer not mine susters
soul goo out of her body in to the time that she have received that grace and
thy merci Loo maidens that prayer was off great strength that her suster soul
might not pass out of the body unto the time our lord showed his plentuous
mercy in her. notwythstondynge the seek woman lay adrawyng on three days and
three nyghtes so that many folk that knew her merueylled and sorowed for her
that she suffered so long a pain. and yet in all that time this holy maid
continued in her devout prayer / never cesing unto the time she had overcome
in manner of our lord by meke teres / Then^e our lord by her devout prayers
graciously sent his mercy unto that soul / and gave her clear knowing to know
her trespass / and also gave her suffycient contrycion to health of her soul.
As Soon as this holy maid perceived that by reuelacion that she had such a
grace she went to ye seek susters chamber for to comfort her / And when the
seek suster saw this holy maid she did her reverence with great joy as she
might whom she had first in great repreue and so she accused her self with
speaking and tokens making and asked her mercy and forgyuenesse of her trespaas
as she might speak and so she was shryue and hoselyd and passyd out of this
world with great contrycion / When she was passed out of this world. then
our lord showed to this holy maid her soul in so great bryghtnesse and
fayrnes / yt as she knowleched afterward to her confessor it might not be
told ne spoken with mannys tongue / Yet was not that the fayrenesse that she
should have in bliss endelesly but oonly the fayrenes that she had in her
first creacion and in receyuyng of her baptysme And then said our lord to
this holy maid, loo dear daughter by the I have receyned this soul yt was
lost / is this not a fair soul and a semely / Loo is he or she that will not
do her besines for wynnyng of such a fair soul / if that I am ye most
souerayn fayrnes of whom comes all manner of virtues fayrnesse was so oucome
through love of fairness of man^ys soul yt I would come down froheue^ to earth
and shed my blood for to rau^som it / much ye then should labor so either
for other ye so fair a creature be not lost. for this cause I have showed the
this soul yt you may ye more her afterward be ^^erid for to win souls to me
/ and also that thou may stere other to the same grace / This holy maid then
thanked our lord for his blessed reuelacion prayng him mekely with all the
affeccion of her soul that he would vouchesaf to give her that grace ever
afterward that she might see the fayrnesse of every soul of all tho the which
been conuersaunt with her: so the more be steryd for to win her health / the
which grace our lord granted her and said / by cause thou haste despised
for mine sake all manner of flesshely conversation and art knytte to me in the
spyryte the which am the most souerayn spyryte / and also haste prayed so
besely and so deuotily fore this soul / therefore now I give thy soul clear
sight by the which thou may perceive and behold both the fayrenes and the
fylthes of every soul that is present before the / So that as thy bodily wits
before this time have perceived the condycions of bodies right so from this time
forward thyn ghostely wits should perceive and consydere the conditions of
the spyrytes not only of tho the whilche ben I presented to the / but also of
all other for whose help thou shall pray though they never be presented to thy
bodily sight / The grace of this gift was ever after ward so spedefull in
this holy maid that fro that time forward she perceived more clerly the
qualytes and deeds* of ye sowles of them the which aperyd before her than of
her bodies / so ferforth that in a time Master Reymound her confessor
complained to her of som^e that grutched upon her by cause that she suffered
many diverse persons to knele before her and would not bid them stand up / To
whom she aus^terd in this wise. God knows fader that I am occupied about the
consyderacion of her sowles that I perceived nothing in manner of outward deeds
/ Then asked her confessor of her and said wheder^ye see her sowles / To
whom she answered thus / Fader under confession I show to you that after time
our savior had I give me such a grace that I saw the fayrnesse off mine
sufters soul the which was ordained to be dampened for her trespaas by his
right wysdom he delyuerd mercyable by mym prayers showed me afterward

He fayrenes there apperyd afterwar uneath before me / but that I saw the
condycions of their sowles and therefore fader I am syker if ye had onys seen
the fayrenesse of a reasonable soul / ye would suffer an hundred times bodily
death if it were possible for the wynnyge off a soul / there is nothing in wis
world that may be lykened to her fayrnesse wha^ here o^fessour herd / this he
prayed her yt she would vouchesaf to tell him all the process how she come to
such a reuclacion / Then this holy maid told him all the process as it is
reherced before all be it though she told it but shortly and me kely of the
trespass of her seek suster done against her / But her confessor afterward
inquired the sothe of that odyous crime of her susters ye which knew the^
both well ynow / Ferthermore to the more co^fyrmacion of these things that
benrehersed a fore master Reymound her confessor records of her yt he was
often times a speker between her and the pope gregori xj For she was an ytaly
could vnd stand none latin / and the pope Gregorye could understand none
ytaly. and therefore Master Reymound her confessor that could both was a
speker between them Among all other communycacions that this holy maid
communyd with pope Gregory. she complained her of the court of Rome / And said
that the that paradyse should be of virtue / there she found stynche of cursed
vices then the pope asked her by her confessor how long she had be in the
court / To whom she answered suddenly with a meke boldenes to the pope in this
wise / to the worship of almighty god I dare well say that I perceived much
more the stynche of sin the which is used in the court of Rome at home in
mine own cite there as I was borne: then they that has sinned and sin
every day: Then the pope after this answer held his peace: And was
merueylously astonyed: but her confessor master Reymound merueylously marked
he words and with what auctoryte they were spoken to such a wourthy prelate:
Also often times it befyll both to master Reymound her confessor and to other
that followed that holy maid in to diverse countrees: where neither she ne they
came before yt there come to her and to him many unknown persons semely arrayed
for to comin with them of virtue semyng as though they had be virtuous folk:
But in truth they encombred with wretched sins. whose sins she perceived
anon wherefore she would neither speak to them netourne her face to them. And
when she saw that they abode long; Then she brake out a little her voice
more than she was wont to do and said to them such words: First we should
amend our life fro sin and goo out of the deuyles service: and then to
speak of our lord: Wha^ she had said such words she went fro them as soon as
she might goodly. And afterward her confessor and her felawes found it sothe
that they were e ncombred with wretched sins in the which sins they
co^tynued wythouten repentance / Another time also she spoke with a woman: ye
which woman seemed an honest woman but in soth she was the concubyne of a man
of holy church and that was great pity: As they spoke togyders the wymmen
might not look upon the maidens face: by cause ever the holy maid turned
away her face fro her. Of this thing her confessor had great merueyle: And
in a time asked her why she did so / To whom she answered and said Fader I
am syker and ye had felt that stynche of sin that I felt in her / ye would
have cast out all that is in your body for sqweymusnes / Loo maidens all
these ensamples have I set here for ye should know what excellent gifts of
grace our lord gave to this holy maid by cause of her meke living: Ouermore
our ghoostely enemy the fend perceyuyng that this holy maid wan great
virtues by the service that she deed to seek folk He thought by sum manner of
will to wythdrawe her fro that holy besynes: and yet might he not For the more
that he was about to let her. the more she encresyd virtuously by that
occupacion / It befyl in a time that one of the susters of penance which was
called after the manner of the country Andred / This andred was touched by the
suffrau^ce of our lord with a grievous infyrmyte and that was in this these.
She had upon her breast a sore the which was called a cancer. And that
fretid the flesh round about / and it was so corrupt that there might
none come nyghe her for stynche / But if they hylde her nose / And so there
was few or none that might suffer to come nyghe her.

when this holy Maid perceived this. she understood that our lord had
received that seek suster to her keeping / Then anon she came to her that
with a glad there she comforted her and she served her gladly to the last end
of her sekenes / that seek suster took her service the more freely in as much
as she considered that all other forsook her / this holy maid left no thing
undo yt was longyng to her seek suster encresyd never her abhomynable stynche
never so much / She stood by her and opened her wound / washed it and wept
it / and coueryd it* and yet never she hyldeth she her nose for no stynche ne
showed none token of lothsomnes / ne never was heavy ne wroth of service ne weary
about her. but gladli did her dilyge^t service / so that her seek suster had
merueyle of the great stedfastenes / and of the great sufferaunce and of the
great fulness of love and charity that was in so young a maid / Of this great
love and charity that she showed to that seek suster ye fend had great envy
and was about to let that deed of mercy and of charity after his power.

First upon a day as this holy maid was about to vnoouere her wound for to
wasshe it and wype it and to refreissh it again* there came out such an odoure
of stynche that uneath her stomach might suffer it: But almost she was brought
to a vomyte. As Soon as she perceived that / she arose against her self with an
high wrath and said to her skeymons flesh in this wise whether ye wretched
flesh haste abhomynacion now of thyn suster the which our lord boughte
with his precious blood / you may fall every day in ye same sykenesse that
she is in or in verse: trewely thou shall be punysshed therefore / Anon she
bowed done to the sore and hyld her nose and her mouth open against the wound
so long unto the time she felt in her self that her skeymousnes was goo /
and so she over came the flesh that was contrary to the spyryte / The seek
suster beheld this and cried to her merueylyng and said cecedere daughter
corrupt not thy self with this foul stynkyng sore /

This holy maid for all her cryenge would not arise up unto the time she felt
her enemy was overcome and so she arose up and he avoided away fro her for a
time / But he consyderyng that he might not have the maystry of her wrought
wylyly against her by her seek suster / He put in her heart such an heuenes
against this holy maid that she lotheth her service / and by little and little
that malice so encresyd that lothenes was turned in to an hate. For though
she knew well ynow that there was none that would serve her but she / But yet
she s^cyd not of that pryuy hate but brake out against her in to a suspycious
g^losye. for that is the condycion of them yt lyuen in hate ever lyghtely for
to leave a suspycious thought of them that they hate: And at the last she began
to image ne and bear her an hand that when she was not present with her she
was about sum actuell sin flesshely in sum other preuy places*

Yet would not this holy maid never s^ce of her holy seruise about her
notwithstondyng suspycious ymagynacions I put against her / For she well that
wylecome by the devil and the more besy she was about her the more wrathful
was her seek suster against her by exortacion and excitacion of the fend that
ever hated the deeds of charity / In so much that he steryd that seek suster
to slander this holy maid openly of ye filthe of vnclen^e and that scland was
so open / that at the last when that it came to her susters he ryng / sum
of the oldest / and of the sted fastest came to this seek suster for to know
the truth Thanne the seek suster as she sdau^dred her a fore / right so she
continued in the same sclaund to her susters / accusyng her full foul actuell
uncleanness Of the which foul accusacy on / these sustres were gretely a
meruaylled and styred against this holy maid / and so was called forth a fore
them / and sharply rebuked with many repreuable words axyng of her how she
would suffer her self so be deceived for to lose her maydenhode. To whom this
holy maid answered full pacyently and softely / seeing thus* Trewely ladies and
sustres by the grace of our lord Jhesu christ / I am a maid. And never would
she say other word in blamyng of her that so had accused her / but only thus.
Trewely I am a maid / trewely I am a maid. Yet for all this she cessyd never
of her seruyse / all be it that it was full heuysom to her for to here such
words and sclaundre But yet first she served her seek suster / and afterward
went to her cha^b^e for to pray / for that was her most comfort in all such
dyseases. There she prayed in soul more then in words by mouth / and yt
was in this wise. O almighty god and my dear beloved spouse / thou know well
that the name of maids is tender / and lightly for to catch sclaundre / and
namely of such maidens that have chosen the to be their spouse / and that was
ye cause why that thou would / that thy glorious mother our lady Saint Mary /
was committed to Joseph / that was called and spoused her husbond for to keep
her name of virgynyte without sclaunder Thou know lord that all this
sclaundre / the which is put upon me is come by the fend ^he fader of
^esynges / by cause I should cesse of the besynes the which I have begone for
thy love. Therefore lord I pray the help me / that know well I am gylteles
/ and suffer not this wicked enemy the which was ouert^ row by thy passion
to have the maystrye of me.

When she had prayed thus long to our lord weeping plenteuously. Our lord
appyred to her as she knowelechyd afterward in confession to her confessor
master Reymond. Holdyng in his right hand a golden crown arrayed with
precious margaryte stonys. And in his lift hand a garlonde of sharp thorns
/ seeing to her in this wise Dear daughter it is needful yt thou be crowned
with own of these two crowns / and therefore chese whether thou have lever
have of this two. Ch^se now whether thou had lever be crowned with the
sha^pe crown of thorn in this ly^ / and that other to be reserved to the in
ever lastyng life. Or else for to have this precious crown. and for to have ye
other after this life. Then this holy maid said.

Lord thou know well that I have forsake mine own will / and chosen for to
do after thy blyssed will / therefore I dare not chese no manner thing without
thy plesaunt will. Nevertheless by cause thou will that I shall answer I say
thus that I chese rather in this life ever to be co^fourmed to thy blessed
passion / and so for to suffer peynes for thy love. After these words anon
she took of our lords hondes the garland of thorns fervently and put it
myghtely upon her head with a manner of vyolence / that the thornys percyd her
head round about / as her thought in so much that she had a pain long
afterward in her head by prykynge of the thornys / as she recorded her self
openly to master Reymond her confessor. Than said our ford to her thus / in
my pour is al thing / and as I have suffered this sclau^der to be areysed /
right so it is in my power to cesse it. Therefore thou shall continue in that
holy seruyse as thou have be gonne / and give no stead to the send that would
let the / I shall give the full vntorye of thine enemy / that what that ever
he has Imagyned against the it shall torn to his own head for thy more joy
/ and his more pain. Thus was this holy maid comforted / and so bode stylle
in that holy seruyse. But when this sclaundre came to her mother Lapa / all be
it yt she was seker enough of her daughter / she was gretely styred by this
sclaunder and said to her with mighty spyryte in this wise Daughter have I not
often said to the / that thou sholdest no more serve that stynkyng woman / loo
what reward she has give the for thy besye seruyse She has sclaundred the
full foul to all thy sustres / if thou ever serve her more or come to her /
never shall I call ne name the my daughter afterward / ne thou me thy mother.
Now was this the soty lest will of all. For there the fend might not have the
maystrye of her by sclaunde ryng of her seek suster / he began with a manner
of pity to let her of her holy seruyse by her moders mouth. Then was this
holy maid astonyed somewhat for her moders words. And at the last she went to
her and knelyd before her seeing to her thus. Sweet mother whether our lord
would be pleased if we leave undone the dedys of mercy to our negyhbours for
their unkindness.

Whether our savior left to raunsom us by suffryng death on the cross for the
reprouyng words and obloquye of men. God knows mother and your charity also
if I left this seek suster / and would do her no seruyse / there would none do
her seruyse. And so she should deye for defau^^. Should we be cause and occasyon
of her death / she is now a little deceived of ye fend / perauenture here
afterward our lord will give her grace for to know her trespass. By such
words and like to thise / at the last she wan her moders blessyng / and went
to the seek suster ageyn and served her so gladly as though she had never said
evil of her. These ke suster was than astonyed / and perceived then that she
had do amysse / and began to have sorrow and contrycyon in her heart of her
sclaunder that she had put upon her. Then our lord showed mercy to her. And
for to make the good fame of his maid / he showed that seek suster in a time /
as she lay in her bed a gracious vysyon / that he wouchesauf to show to
this holy maid upon a day / when this holy maid went to her / chamber
after her seruyse that she had do to that seek suster. That same seek suster
saw as she lay in her bed about the holy maid a great light coming don
from heaven / of so great mirthe and swetenes that it made her for to forgete
utterly all her dyseases / what this might mean clearly she wist never / but
she looked about here and there. And beheld the maids face transformed or
tra^sfygured / that her seemed that she was not then Katheryn Lapais daughter
/ but rather like to an heavenly creature gloryfyed / and that light beclypped
her round about. And the more she beheld her / the more she yield her self
gylty in her soul to our lord / of the sclaunder that she putt^ upon that
holy maid. When this vysyon had tary^^ a while the which appyred to the
bodily eyes of that seek suster / as it came so it passyd away / after the
which passing the seek suster was long after comforted / and also sorrowful
for her trespass

And anon she axed mercy of the holy maid with sobbyng terys that she had so
wyckedly trespassyd against her / and sclaundred her full falsely. Loo maidens
by that outward light / our lord gaf her an Inward light / for to know how
falsely she was deceived by the fend. Anon forthwyth when this holy maid
herd how mekely she axed forgyuenes. She went to her mekely and took her in
her arms and kyssed her / seeing to her thus full comfortably.

Dear mother I am not dysplesed with you in no wise / for I wot well it was the
fendes malice / and not youres / but I thank yon with all my heart / for ye
love me in that ye would I were kept clean And therefore I wit you no thing of
all this / but the fend that has wrought all this so malyciously against me /
