with such words and like these. This holy maid comforted her seek suster and
did her seruyse as she was wont to do / and when she had do / lest she should
have spend her time in vain / she went to her chamber and occupied her in
prayer.

In the mean time that the seek su ste knowleched her gylty with weeping and
waylyng before all thoo that came to her and said openly before them all that
by dysceyte of the fend / she sclaundred ye holy maid wrongfully. And she
axed forgyuenes of hem all. For she said that she knew well enough yt this
maid was not only pure and clean from flesshely sins / but also she was
holy and fulfilled with the holy ghoost / and that she knew well. Then sum
of the saddest of her susters axyd her pryuely and wisely how she knew that
the maid was holy / and what tokens she had thereof. She answered steadfastly
with a fervent spyryt that she knew never before what was swetnesse of the
soul and ghoostly comfort unto the time she saw this holy maid before her
transfygured or transformed and ouercouered with an unspeakable light. Eftesones
then her susters axyd her / whether she saw that sight with her bodily eyes.
But she could not tell it with no thing the fayrenes of that light / and the
swetnesse that she felt in her soul for that time.

Then ye holy maidens name began to encreace virtuously over all / for there
the fend was about to dysceyue / and to hinder her name / there the holy
ghoost enhauncyd her name virtuously. But in all this right as she was never
the sonner throw down by an evil fame / right so she was never the more
enhauncyd in her self by elacyon for such a good name

She continued ever forth in her holy seruyse and did her business / ever for
to know her self that she was naught / but yet her ghoostly enemy the fend
cessyd never for to let her / eftesones he tempted her in her holy
minystracion by squey mousnes of the stomach. In a time when this holy maid
wesshyd her seek susters horrible wound / there came such a savor out thereof
that she was in point to cast out all that was in her body. Then she rose
against her self and so much the more vyolently that she had the vyctorye of
another temptacyon by the grace of the holy ghoost / and said to her self thus
Trewly wretch thou that have so much abhomynacyon thou shalt receive it
within the. Anon she took all the wesshyng of that wound / with the matter
and fylthe and went aside / and dra^ke it of preuely / when she had so do
all her te^ptacyon of abhominacion cessyd

This was told afterward to master Reymond her confessor in her presence to
whom she addyd and said pryuely / that srth^n she was borne in this world /
she etc never ne drank so sweet ne so good a savor of no manner mete ne
drink.

After this glorious vyctorye that same night suyng our lord Jhesu christ /
appyred to that holy maid / showing to her his five blessed wounds / the
which he suffered for our health and said thus De re daughter many bateylles
thou have ouerpassyd for me and by my help thou have oue coome them / yet
hither to / for the which vyctoryes thou art to me right welcome / but
specially yester day thou plesyst me gretely in that / that you dyspysedest
thine own nature and kind for my love thou receyuest a drink the which was
abhomynable and dedely. Therefore right as in that thou pass^st thy kind and
thy nature Right so shall I give you a drink that passyth the custom and the
kind of man With that he held his arm of her neck and brought her mouth to
his blessed wound in his side / and said to hi^ thus. Drink daughter out of
my ^y ^ the drink of health / by ye which thy soul shall be fulfilled with
so much sweetness that it shall ^^bou^de in to thy body the which thou have
so meruayllously despised for my love. Then this holy maid sowked out of the
pype of life coming out of his blessed wound with her mouth of her body / but
much more with the mouth of her soul / long time to gyder full plentuou^ly
an unspeakable drink of ever lastyng health. At the lost by the ordinance of
our lord she cessyd and yet thursty not withstondyng she had enough. Now
maidens I pray you consydereth mekely this virtues act of this blessed maid.
Beholds I beseech you the rote of her charity / where with she was moeued to
take upon hit folowely a seruyse for to serve seek folk*

Also beholds how long she continued in that seruyse / not wythseondyng the
great lettyng that she had by abhomynacyon of nature. Beheld also the great
stedfastenes that she had in abydyng not wythstondyng the foul sclandres the
which were put upon her / and at the last she behold a notable co^clusyon /
how after time she had received that holsom drink out of our lords side.
She was fulfilled with so much habundaunce of grace that she etc never ne
might etc afterward in such a wise as she did before as it shall be declared
more clearly within forth. For as touching this chapter I shall make an end
There is no thyn ge written ne reherced in this chapter / but such as master
Reymond this holy maids confessor knew it out her by confession of her / or
as he found by writing of her confessor that was before him / or of certain of
her sustres / the which were true and sad of leuyng.

Of her synguler manner of living / and how they were dysceyued / that grutched
with her meruayllous fasting. Ca V
AFter time our lord Jhesu the endeles spouse of this holy maid had proved her
in the oven of manyfolde trybulacyons / and also had taught her to overcome her
ghostly enemy ye fend by diverse bateyll / it were right semely yt he should
reward her in this life with sum special gift of grace But by cause that
souls as long as they ben in the body may not fully receive the fruit of
virtue / as it is had in bliss endelesly

Therefore it is full needful as for the fulfyllyng of the dyuyne prouydence of
our lord that every chosen spouse of his in earth should yet dwell in earth /
and nevertheless yet shall be endowed with some specyal reward of mede for this
cause / it was that our savior wouchesauf to begin in his spouse and in his
handemayde Katheryne / this wretched life a manner of an heavenly living. And with
that manner of living he would assocye her to erthely folk Therefore which
such a manner of reuelacyon he enfourmed her. It be fill in a time that this
holy maid prayed in her chamber / where our lord apperyd to her and said in
this wise / wete right well dear beloved daughter that thine abiding in earth
shall be fulfilled with so many meruayllous gifts of my grace / that it shall be
cause of studieng and Incredulyte to many man's hertes / and specially to
flesshely me^nys hertes / that known not the manner of my gracyous gifts. And
also many that louen the / they shall be in thought and suppose that my passing
love the which werche in yt should be dysceyte For I shall give so great
habundau^ce of grace in thyn soul / that it shall meruayllously rebounde in to
thy body / by the which thy body shall receive and have a meruayllous manner of
living / the which has selde be herd before Ferthermore thyn heart shall be
so gretely kyndelyd to health of souls / that thou shall forgete in manner
thyn own kind and change althy first conuersacyon. For thou shall not eshewe
and shun the company of men and wommen as thou were wont to do but rather for
their soul health thou shall put the to all manner of labor to thy power and
might. Of this manner of living many one should be sclaundred / and so of many
thou shall be ageyn said that the thoughts of their hertys may be known by
their words / but look thou be in no wise aferde ne troubled / for I shall
ever be with the and deliver thy soul from treucherons tongues and liars.
Therefore work myghtely that the holy ghoost shall teache ye / for by yt I shall
delyuere man's soul out of the fendes power / and by mediacion of my special
grace I shallede them to heaven. When our lord had said these words / and
often times had rehearsed to her the same comfortably as touching that point.
Where our lord said to her that she should not be a ferdene troubled She
answered as she beknewe afterward in contessyon Thou a^t my lord and my god /
and I thy wretched servant / ever more thy will be done / but have mind of me
good lord god after thy great mercy and help me / and thus vanysshed and
cessyd this vysyon. This holy maid bethought her and kept well in her heart
wha this gracyous chau^gyng should be in time coming. Fro that time afterward
fro day to day / the grace of our lord Jhesu encreced in her heart / and the
holy ghost habounded in her so much / that she her self was astoned thereof /
and wext feeble in body and said as the propheet said these words Deficit caro
mea et corpus me um deus cordis mei et pers mea deus inete^nu^ That is my body
and my flesh sebled and de^ailleth / but good lord by ye governor of mine
heart and my part wythoutenende And eftesones she said as the same propheet
said in another place. Memor fui dei et drlectata sum and exercitata sum / et
deficit spiritus meus That is I have mind of my lord god / and have therein
great delight / and I hau^ce me in ye ghostly delight / and therefore my spyrytes
and strengthes of my body wexen feeble and defayllen This maid wext seek in
body for the love of our lord / and her sekenes had no remedy but by weping and
waylyng / and therefore she wept and wayled every day / and yet by such weeping
and waylyng she might not so cour her sekenes Than our lord put in her heart
that it should be good for her as for a souereyn cemedye to her sekenes often
times to be housled / that so she might receive that lord yt she loved / by
sacrement of the autre. Of whom she might not yet be fulfilled fully in this
life / as she should be in heaven bliss And netheles yt was cause of more love
and encrece of gretter sekenes. But yet for a time it made satys faccyon by the
virtue of the feyth to ye ser ^yse of her charity / that brenned contynuelly in
her heart by in sufflacyon of the holy ghoost. After time she had in custom to
be comuned and houseled as it were every day / all be it though she were often
times let by sekenes of body / and so for besynes that she had of men's
souls She had such a desire often for to be house led / that but if she were
her body should su^^^^ great pain / and in manner it should feeble and defayll
and right as the body had par^^ of the haboundaunce of the spyryte by affluence
that habou^ded fro within forth Right so it might not be but if it had be
per^eyner of the anguysshe and disease that the spyryt suffered This matter shall
be de da^d more largely by the help of god afterward. For now I shall tell you
of the meruayllous living / yt she leued as touching her body / master Reymond
records thus of this holy maid / as he knew well by her confession and also
by writing of her confessor before him / yt after time she was vysyted by ye
foresaid vysyon / she had so much plente of graces and ghoostly comfortes / and
namely when she had received our lord Jhesu in ye blessed sacrement of the
autre / that it reboundyd in to her body by a copyous affluence / that the
kyndly consumpcyon of dygestyon in her body had no place / but it chau^gyd so
the kind of her stomach that the receyuyng of mete was not now ned full to her
/ for she might not receive mete without great torment of the body / and if she
should algates ^te her body suffered right great pain / for it might have no
kyndely dygestion / but nedys it must by vyolence come out again yt she etc
there that it went June. It is not lefull to write with a pen how often and how
many peynes this holy maid suffered for receyuynge of bodily metes This manner
kind or condycyon of living in the beginning was to many folk / both to them
of the household and to other that were conuersaunt with her so Incredyble that
they named this synguler gift of god either a temp tacyon or else a sottyll
dysceyte of the devil. In to this error fill master Reymond her confessor
as other did yt wend she had be disceyued of her enemy ye which oftymes
transfygured him self to an angel of light for to deceive souls* And
therefore he bad her etc her mete every day / and give no credens to such
desceyuable vysyons that would let her fro her mete. Then said this holy may
de to her confessor that she found well by experyence yt she was more hole in
body when she received no bodily mete / tha^ when she received it. Yet for
all such excusacyons he would not cesse of his precepte / but badde and
commanded her yt she should ete. Then she as a true daughter of obedience
obeyed to his byddyng / and ete her mete unto ye time by sekenes she was almost
deed. Then she called her confessor master Reymond and said to him thus.
Fader if I be to much fasting were I cause of mine one death / were I a sleer of
mine one body / he answered and said yes Then she asked eftesones whether it
be great sin to be deed by etyng or by abstinence / he said by etyng. Then
she said sythen it is so that ye see me wexe feeble and nere to the death by
etyng as ye know well by experyence: why will ye not fobede me etinge as ye
would forbede me fasting in such a caas: To this reso^ he could not answer /
but by cause he perceived that she was nyghe to death by euydent tokens / he
said to her daughter: do as our lord taught the / For they ben merueylous
things to me that I see our lord work in the / Many grutchynges there was in
the household against her for this merueylous living by cause they knew not
the gracious werkynge of god in her / And thereto also they stered her
confessor master Reymound to repreue her albe it: it was of^^ times against
his will / and what great dysese she suffered of other there can none tongue
tell by cause she was so obedyent and so grounded in mekenes that could
another excuse her self ne wythstond the will of her confessonr what that ever
^^ badde her do for one or other / she wist well that ye will of god was
contrary against all their domes And on the other side she was aferd for the
dred of god to forsake obedyence that she was bode by her confessor / And
thereto she was loathe to notefye the truth to them carnell pepse by cause the
could not sauore such a ghostely truth: therefore what she should do she
wist never / Thus she suffered much angwyshe in this conflycte / But among
all these conflictis she ran to her pray: and for a souerayn remedy / she
wept plentuously before our forde teres of sorrow and of hope besechyng him
mekely with much instaunce that he would vouchesaf to show his will to all
tho that were contrary again ste her manner of living / And specyafly to her
confessor whom she was most loathe to offend / She would not reherce the
word of the Appostles that they said to princes of the law when they said
thus /

Oportet obedire deo magis quam homini b^. That is we should rader obey to god
than to man: But for to seye so she was loathe lest it should have be answered
her yt the fend trans^igureth him often times in an angel of light / And
therefore she should give none credens to every spyrit Ne should not leave to
much to her owna wit but to do after counseyll:

In this devout prayer our lord herd her graciously as he did in many other
and often times illumyned her confessor his soul and changed his counseyll /
But now I shall sece of this matter and proceed in the process of this holy
maidens living / The first time that this special grace befyll her she was so
full of the holy ghost that fro the beginning of lenton in to Ascenci^on off
our lord she was without bodily mete or drink ever glad and merry / This was
none merueyle for the fruit of the spyryte is charity joy and peace / as saint
pouse says. And as our lord says him self / A man lives not always with
bodily sustynaunce: but with the word that comes out of gods mouth And for
as holy wryt says: Juseus exside viuit / That is the ryghtwysman lives by the
faith / On ye asce^cio^ day our lord granted her that she should ete as she
told afterward preuely to her confessor. And so she did for she ete bred
and potage of wortes and other raw herbs and also other lenton metes / for
that meruey lous body about kind might not recey^ue none delycat^ metes. After
that day she tournyd again to her simple fast yt she had begun a fore /
and so by little and lytill she tournyd that simple fast in to a costome
contynuelly that was never herd in to tho days / Her confessor master
Reymound berith record and says that often times he knew that her body was not
comforted by none bodily mete ne drink / but only with cold water unto the
time she was brought to such a febylnesse that him thought and other moo that
she was almost deed / But as soon as she herd say of any need that should be
done to man^is soul. / she caught strength suddenly wythouten any bodily
comfort that she was able to goo as mightily as ever she was without any
greuauuce a boue the commune strength or of other the which followed her and
never wae weary. Whereof came this grace trow ye / but only of the spryte that
comfort and quickens the body merueylously above kind namely of such a
body that is subject to the spyryte in all ghostely works / By this may
every ghostely man understand that all this holy maidens life was above kind
and full of miracle /

In a time when she had fast so long and lived without mete and drink /
Her confessor master Reymound asked her wheder she had any time any manner of
appetyte to mete or drink / To whom she answered thus / I have so great swetnes
that our lord gave me by receiving of that blessed sacrament off ye altar his
own precio^ flesh and blod yt in no wise I might desire none manner bodily
sustynaunce of mete or drink. Then^e her confessor asked eftsoon whether she
had any appetyte to mete ye day that she was not hosylyd / She said nay for
wha^ it happed that she was not hose lyd / the presence and the sight of that
blessed sacrament and not only the sight of ye blessed sacrme^t but also the
presens of that presie the which she knew well had that day said mass and
I touched that blessed sacrament comforted her in such wise that she had
none mind of bodily mete / This holy maid stood both full and fasting
wythoutforth fasting / and wythinforth full / wythoutforth dry: and
wythinforth moist with flodes of quyk water and in all manes of chances she
was ever glad and iocu^de / But the fend might not suffer this that the she
should thus be endowed by such gracious gifts. but by his venyms woodnes of
malycious envy / he steryd both spyrytuall folk and temperall folk /
Relygious and seculer against her / for that syuguler gift of fasting /
merueyle not though he styred ghostely folk and relygyous against her / for in
such but if their own love of them self were fully quenched by grace regnid
more perylous envy than in other / and namely when they see another do the
which them thinks is vnpossybyle them for to do / Search wisely now and
aspye whether this was not soth among the holy faders dwelling in thebayde /
there was a seculer man that came to the great congregation where: Phatomye was
abbot for to receive the habyte among them / And when he was received to the
habyte to ye holy congregation the covent saw how merueylously he lived / And
they might not do as he did / They came all with one voice gretelysteryd
against Phatomye / and bad him either put out of the congregation that new
monk / or ellis they would not abide with him / Loo if such envy reigned
then in tho days among such yt were hold ryht ^fyght folk / What envy
tro we ye myht regne among our ghostely folk yt lyue^ in these days / it is
none wonder therefore thou ghostely folk grutched with this holy maids fasting
/ For sum there were that said there is none living gretter than our lord /
for our lord yet ete and drank whiles he lived in earth and his blessed
glorious mother our glorious lady glorious vyrgyn marye and all his appostles
/ and also whom our lord bad that they should ete and drink that was set before
them / and so they did: How is that that now is living in earth that might
pass them or to be like to them. I trow none / Sum there were also that
said and afermed that saints before us taught by word and by deed that there
should none take upon them a synguler living passing other but all should live a
common perfyght living Sum there were also that were preuy bachyters and
said that the end of that fasting should be vicious: And therefore they gave
counseyll to other for to take none ensample of her for she is deceived There
were also other carnal people and open bacbyters that said her fasting was
but a feigned thing for to win thereby veyn glory / and therefore it seemed to
other that she fasted but preuyly she ete / All this was no thing but envy
against whose falls doers and falls opynyons: I purpos to reple by the help of
god / As for the first there we sum a legged for them our lord / and our
blessed lady gracious virgyn mary and all the appostles that they lived a
common living without any great fasting. the^ ne should it sywe that saint
Johan baptyste was more holy than our lord Jhesu Christ / for our lord said
him self of saint Johan that he was come and never ete ne drank but fasted /
But the sone of man is come that both ete and drank / The same also should
sywe that saint Anthony macharye / Illarion / Scrapion and many other holy
faders: the which uses many merueylous fastings above the common life of the
appostles should be gretter then the appostlis. Ouermore if these forsayde
grutchers will reple against me and said that saint Joha^ in wyldernes and
these holy fathers of Egypt fasted not symply without mete and drink / but
sometime they ete / what would they say than of mary Magdalene the which lived
in a roche of the sea xxx / year together without mete bodily or drink as her
story makes mencyon of the same place there she lived in it shows i^to this
day / that never might come thy der man ne woman to bring her mete ner drink
whether she was gretter than our blyssed glorious vyrgyn lady glorious virgyn
Mary that never fasted so ne lived in such a roche. What will they also say
of many other holy faders that lived here many years without mete or drink and
passyd out of this world and enspeciall of one we read yt when he had received
ye blessed sacrament of the altar without any other bodily sustynaunce of mete
and drink he lived many years / Therefore if such grutchers never learned. let
them learn now that the gretenesse and lytylnesse of holiness is not mesured ne
demed only by fasting but by charity. thus let the^ learn never to make them
Juges of things that they know not: In a like manner sum said off saint
Johan when he came and fasted that he had a devil within him / And when our
lord was come that fasted / not they said to him that he was a deuourer of
mete and drink. and a great wine drynker / this last sentence is suffyciant
ynow to stop the mouths off such grutchers /

The second grutchers the which hate^ syngularyte of living / it may lyghtely
and es^y be answered and thus it is though a man should not take upon himself
any new synguleryte that never was held before. if that god work in him /
hemaye not refuse but needs must work it and use it with thankynges else the
synguler yeftes of our lord should utterly be despised /

Holy write says that a right wise man should not search ne seek curyousey
high things above him and anon afterward it followed this that many things
benshewed to a right wise man above his wit. What is all this to mean*
nothing else but a man should not seek by him self but if our lord above him
and showed to him many great merueylous things that he should resceyue and use
with thankynges / therefore as this holy maid deed / who may sey that she did
it of synguleryte of her self to whom our lord vouchesaf to give her ye
gift by his synguler ordinance. In such manner of wise this holy maid
answered when she was I asked why she ete not as other did / all be it that she
answered in other terms I coueryd with mekenes / when she was asked why she ete
not as other did / She said that our lord had smite her for her sins by
a synguler passion of infirmytes: wherefor she was let to ete her mete as other
did: Gladly she said that she should ete but she might not / therefore she
said I pray you pray for me / that he vouchesaf to forgive me mine sins
wherefore I suffer all these sykenesses / As though she had said thus / god
does this in me and not I in mine self / And also less any manner of spyce of
pride should appyre in her ever she said she suffered that infirmyte for her
sins: And yet she said not against conscience: for she supposed stedfastely
that our lorst had suffered her to fall in to the grutchynge of men for to
punysshe her sins / For what manner of evil be fill to her / She wyted it her
sins and what good that ever was wrought in her she put it to our lord /

This same sentence is a good answer to the thrydde preuy bacbyters that
sayden and ever conseylde to other for to be ware of the end of such synguler
fasting / For the end must needs be vycious the which is not of god / How
may the end of this holy maids fasting be vycious the which come of god and
not of her self as it is clerly declared before / Also there that they said
that she was dysceyued of the fend / how may that be that so often overcome
the dysceytes of ye fend / But now I set caas that she might so be dysceyued
of the fend what was he than that held and kept her body in such kyndely
strength perauenture they would say the fend. Then^e would I wett if he kept
her soul in such ghostely gladness and peace / sithe it so was depreuyd fro
all manner simple delight or delectacion / This fruit of the holy ghost may not
be in none devil is power to give: for ye appostle says yt the fruit off ye
holy ghost is charity / joy and peace I would not suppose yt all this should be
directed to ye fend / Therefore all such sclau^ders and bacbyters of virtue
should be answered rather by silence than by word / Every virtuons man should
eschew them and suppose yt they ben vnwurthy to have an answer / This holy
maid did what she could every day to stop her mouths lest they should be
sclau^dred in her / In that yt she came to mete every day to ye meyne of ye
household therbi for to know whether she might or not as other did / And yet
otherwhyle she would assaye for to ete / and it was so great pain to her that
all yt saw her had compassyon of her / For her stomach might not defye her
mete and the kyndly consumpcion of natural dygestyon had none use in her: But
all yt entryd in her in to the stomach come out again by the same way there
it went in / This caused in her many diverse passions / For all be it that
this holy maid received not in her stomak any mete the which was mete wurthy
as for that time: yet she spet out fro her great matter off flewme as other
folk did the which might not be by nature: But if the stomach had
received sum substance before / and thrfoere our lord wrought merueylously in
her above nature / Also as for drynkynking of cold water she received it
gladly to refresshe her chykes and her throat: This manner of life she lived unto
her I aste end for grutchers and for them that were slaundred by her fasting
/ Her confessor Master Reymound perceived how great pain she suffered by
vndygestyon of her stomach and all for to stop grutchers / he conforted her
for co^passyon that he had upon her that she should leave and ete no more
rather than for to suffer such a pain /

And let theymgrutche ynow To whom she answered smylyngly fader is better for
meto suffrein this lyfefor my sins thanne for to suffer pain endelesly /

Her grutchyng is to me profitable by cause I shall be delyuerd of pain
wythouten end for the pain that I suffer in this life should I fle the
ryghtwysnes of god / Nay god forbede it our lord does to me great grace by
cause he gives me mine pain in this life /

So her confessor could no more answer to her but held his peace in this /
wise Of all her enemies she had the maistry what so in manner of the fend and
of grutchers / and so she taught other to do every day: So yt in a time when
she comynyd with her confessor of the gracious gifts of our lord / She said
who so could use the grace of our lord He should ever have the vyctorye of
all things that fallen to him / And then^e she turned to her confessor and
said to him. so I would that ye did as often as any new thing byfalleth to
you be it prosperyte or aduersyte thinks with in your self and says often
this / I will wanne somewhat and ye do so ye should soon be rich in virtue.

Loo maidens have mind of thysnotable doctrine for thus I make an end of this
chapter / The wytnes of all things. the which ben write therein / Is this
holy maid either by her opyn deeds or ellis by her words. And also her
confessor the which was a fore master Reymound.

Of the wounderfull rauysshyng and excess of her mind for her bodily wyttees
/ And of great reuelacions I showed to her of our lord / Capitulum vj
rIght as our lord granted to his spouse this holy maid a synguler living
as touching her body* right so he vysyted her soul with great merueylous
confortes of reuelacions / First for the great habou^dant graces with her come
that bodily strength yt she had about kind. Wete ye right well yt fro the
time that this holy maid had I drunk of our lords side the drink of life as
it is rehersid a fo^^ / many great graces were habou^dant i^ her yt often times
and often times as it had be in manner contynuabyl / She was occupied in actuell
co^templacion and her spyryte was lowyd to our lord that for the more part she
by left without felyng in her bodily wits / So that as it is rehearsed in
the first party her arms were found often times so styf in time of such
actuell contemplacion that rather they should break then bow / Her eyes were
all closed her eres herd none noise were it never so great and her bodily
wits for that time were sequestered fro her own werkynge This should be none
merueyle to noman if they would take heed to yt syweth Our lord began to be
so homely with her and brennyd her soul with so much haboundante fire of
love not oonly in pryuy places / but also in open places as well stondyng as
going / that she the which had these great graces by knew it plainly to
her confessor she could find none words for to tell expressly the grace
that she felt /

For in a time when she prayed to our lord feruentely with the Prophet Dauyd
seyeng devoutly these words /

Cor meum crea in me deus / et spiritu^ rectum innoua in visceribus meis /

That is prayng our lord specially that he would take away her heart and her
own will and give her a new heart after his will / She had such a comfort
that her seemed that our lord Jhesu come to her and opened her lift side and
took out her heart and went his way: and belyfte her with out her own heart:

Afterward it befyll that she commynyd with her confessor / and among all
things she said that she had none heart in her body / the which words her
confessor s^^rned her in a manner and blamed her for she said so / Then she
rehearsed eftsoon and confermed her words trewely fader as much as I may
feel / yet after the felyng of mine body me seems I lack mine heart for our
lord apperyd to me and opened mine lest side and took out mine heart and went
his way / Then the confessor said that it was impossible that she should
live with out an heart. she said nay there is nothing impossible to god. And
therefore she bad him give credens that it is so

For often times after ward she rehearsed that she lived without heart with in a
few days afterward it befyll that she went to a chapel of the friars where
susters of penance were wont to knele / And when all were goo home it befil
that she continued in her prayers so that she was fro her self by rauysshyng
and at the last she awoke of her rauysshyng and went homward / And as she
went by the way suddenly a light of heaven bicliped her: And in that light
aperyd our lord holdyng in his hand a reed shining heart in lykenes of a
mannys heart / At the coming of this heavenly light she was aferde that she
fill down upon the ground / Then came our lord to her and opened her
lyftesyde eftsoon and pute in her body that heart the which he hylde in his
hondes seeing to her thus /

Loo dear daughter as I took away thyn heart the last day / right so now I
give the mine heart whereby thou may live endelesly: and when he had so do
he closed the wound again that he made open in the flesh / Nevertheless
there by left a merueylous mark in the lykenes of a wound heled in the same
place ever afterward / where as her felawes told her confessor Master
Reymound for often times they saw it as she could not forsake it to him when he
askid it of her whether it were so or not. Out of that meruayllous gracyous
heart that was so I given her of our lord came out many meruayllous werkys And
yet many moo meruayllous reuelacyons haboundeth within forth. She came never
afterward for to be hoseled / but that there was showed to her many synguler
gifts of grace. Often times she saw a little child in the prestys handys / and
other while a well grown child / and other while an hot brennyng oven of
fire. And when the priest received that blyssed sacrament / it seemed to her
that the fire entered in to him. But when she should be houseled often times she
tastyd so great an odor of that blyssed sacrament that almost her body
defaylled. Evermore also whether she saw or received ye blyssed sacrament She
received with all a new joy in her soul / so that many times she should
dance in her body for joy / making a noise that her felawes might here her /
the which told it afterward to her confessor / and he inquired the truth
whether it were so / and found it true and so wrote it for a perpetuell
record.

That sown and that noise was not like other manner common sownes of men / but
as it had be a noise above common course of kind what meruayll was that though
she made a joyful noise above kind. Sith it so was that she had received an
heart above kind For after time that she had received that new heart as it
is rehearsed before / she seemed that she was not the same that she was before /
and often times she said to her confessor.

See ye not fader that I am not the same that I was before / but rather changed
in to another person. O would god fader ye knew that I feel / for I true
verily if a creator knew that I feel in my soul / he should be resolved and
made right esye were he never so hard. For my soul is full of melodye and
joy. And it is meruayll to me how it may abide in the body. There is also
great hot brennyng of dyuyne love therein / that this outward materyall fire
seems me in co^paryson of that fire rather cold than hot. Also of that
ghoostly hot is kind led in my soul as me seems so great a love of my
neghbours that my thinks I might gladdely suffer for them bodily death with
great joy. And ouermore out of that ghoostly hot is come to my soul a
renewyng of purytee and mekenes / in so much that me seems I am brought to
the same purytee and mekenes / that a child of four or a five year age is Inn

All this she told to her confessor preuely and to none other. After time
that this holy maid was thus fulfilled in her soul of such plente of new
gracys that were many notable vysyons showed to her / of whom sum I shall
reherce by the grace of god.

First our lord Jhesu and his blessed Mother and Marye magdalene appyred to
gydres to her and comforted her in her holy purpose / whom our lord axed and
said. Daughter what desyrest thou / She with weeping chere answered and said

Lord thou know what me needs better than I / for I have no will but thine
/ ne none heart but thyn heart. Then came to her mind how Marye magdalene
committed her self fully to our lord when she satte and wept at his fete.
With that she felt the same sweetness of love that Marye magdalene felt that
time when she wept. Wherefore she beheld Marye magdalene. Our lord perceived
that and for to fulfill her desire he said. Loo dear daughter for thy more
solace and comfort I give the Marye magdalene to be thy mother. To whom thou
may trustely go to and be comforted / for to her specially I commytte thy
governance For this great gift this holy maid thanked our lord with gpete
mekenes and reverently and devoutly she commended her ghoostly governance to
Marye magdalene prayng her that she would wouchesauf to take her under
governance. Sith our lord had specially committed her to her.

Fro that hour ever afterward the holy maid called Marye magdalene her mother
/ the which was not do without great mysterye as me seems. for as Marye
magdalene lived xxxiij year in a ^oche without bodily mete / and all that time
was I occupied in comtemplacyon.

Right so this holy maid fro that time that she was endowed with these new
graces unto the age of xxxiij year afterward / which year she passyd out of
this world. She was so occupied in dyuyne contemplacyon that she had never
need all ye time of bodily mete And yet as Marye magdalene was take up in to
the air by angels seven times in the day / where she herd the pryuetees of
god Right so this holy maid for the more party all her years she was
rauysshed fro her bodily wits by strength of the soul that was occupied in
contemplacyon of heavenly things / and so praised our lord with angels / in so
much that often times her body was lift up in to the air / of the which
many men and wommen that saw her for that time bare record Ouermore in that
rauyssheng she saw many meruayllous things and spoke preuely in time of her
rauysshyng many high words of contemplacion / of the which some I shall tell
you afterward Her confessor saw her ones in a time rauysshed fro her bodily
wits in the same wise as it is rehearsed before / and he herd her speak
preuely / then he came nere for to lysten clearly what she said / and he
herd that she said formably these words in latin. Vidi archana dei. And that
was said often times / other words said she none but thoo When she was
restoryd again to her bodily wits / she cessyd not to rehearse these same
words co^tynuelly / and it is no more for to say / but I have seen the
pryuetres of god. Then her confessor desyryng for to know why she rehearsed
tho words so often / axyd her in this manner of wise. Good mother why rehearsed ye
so often the words and will not tell me what ye mean as ye were wont to do.
She answerde I may not say none other wise. Her confessor axed her why / and
what is the cause / ye were wont to declare me many things that our lord had
showed to you / why will ye not do so now / then she said. I should have as
great conscience thereof if I should declare to you that I have seen with my
langage that is so imperfect / as I should have if I blasfemed our lord / or
Inhonoured him / for there is a great dyffrence between the understanding or
intellecte of the soul Illumyned of god / and the expressyng of words they
seem contrary each to other / therefore as for this time I can not tell you what
I have say / for they ben unspeakable For this skylle me think that she was
well committed by the dyuyne prouydence of our lord to Marye magdalene / that a
faster should be knytte to a faster / and a lover to a lover. And she that had
so high contemplacyon to her that was so high in contemplacyon. Also her
confessor rehearsed of her / that after time she saw that vysyon of our lord
and his blessed mo^ and Saint / mary magdalene / that for that tymeit seemed her
that her heart went Inn by the side of our lord in to his heart and was made
both one / so that she felt her soul / all for melte and relented by the /
strength of his dyuyne love / and that she: ^^yed in her soul and said. Lord
thou / have wounded mine heart lord you have wounded mine heart. And this was on
saint margaretes day as she told to her confessor in preuytee. Hit befell
also in / another time the morrow after Saint. Laurence day that this holy
maid came to the church for to here mass / and kneled next to the auter as
she was wont for / to do / for to see the blessed sacrement and because that
she should not let the priest at theautre by her great sobbynghir confessor
came to her and warned her that she / should constreyne her asmoche as she
might fro such great sobbynges / lest the pressed were let by her. Th^nae
anon she mekely as true obedyent maiden satte ferther fro the altar and
prayed to our lord that he would vouchesauf to Illumyne her confessor that he
might see and know / whether such sterynges of the spyryte of god might be
mesured of man. Then by virtue of that prayer her contessoure / had so
perfyte knoleche of feuoure of / devotion by experience that he knew fully by
that / that such feruoures of the soul might not be kept within / but needs.
by strenthe of dyuyne love yt must break out. Ferthermore oftyme when she: was
not houseled she desired in her soul for to receive the blyssed sacramet of /
the aulture And oftymes she would break out and say devoutly thus. I would.
receive my lord Jhesu crystys body / with that our lord would appyre to her
as he was wont to do / and to fulfylle her desire / he took the maidens mouth
and put it to his blessed wound of his side and bad her receive of ^s flesh
and of. his blood as much as she list. Then she received plentuously of our
lord breast / that she seemed for pure love she / should had dyed / by cause
of the great / swetnes that she felt in her heart. Hit befyll also upon Sanyt
^^exis day / that this holy maid prayed to our lord devoutly that he would
vouchesauf to grant her bre^nyng desire for to receive his: flesh and his
blood With that she had d^a reuelacyon yt she should be houseled / on the
morrow doubteles / for it was forbeden her of the freres that she should not so
often be houseled. Then whane she had this confortable reuelacyon. She.
prayed our lord yt he would wouchesauf to clenie her heart against the time she
should receive him that she might the more worthily receive him. In time that
she / prayed thus / she felt a reyne comenge / down in to her soul in manner
of a great. haboundant flood / not of water or of such other lyquore / but
only of blood medelyd with fire the which as her seemed purgyd and cleansed so
myghtely ^^ rsowie. that by strength of that tire it re^o^ded / in to the body
and cleansed also her body. After this on the morrow she was ^oseek that by no
way it seemed to her she / might not goo one foot. Neuertheless she doubted no
thing of ye promysse o^ our: lord / but trustyng to him fully began to: go to
church. And when she was come / thither / she knelyd down in a chapel beside
an altar Then came to her mind how she was enfourmed / yt she might: not be
houseled of what pressed she list / but of such that been assygned to her* with
that she desired her confessor should say a mass at that same altar: Anon
our / lord gaf her comfort that he should sing there. Suddenly our lord
then touched the heart of her confessonr with deuocio^ that he sholdesaye a
mass that day / for he was in no will for to sing that day / ne / he wyste not
that the holy maid was come to church. Then at the steryng of our lord he
dysposed him to mass / and went to the same altar there the holy maid was
and abode our lords behest / at which altar also he was never wont to sing
And when he came he found there this holy maid axyng for to be houseled for
charity Then he rceyued that it was the will of god he should sing that day.
He said mass / and at the end of the mass / as the manner is he came for to
housele her this holy maid at the altar end where she was ready for to
receive / that blessed sacrament. Her confessor beheld and saw her vysage
all shynyng read / and al for wepre with terys / the which was to him a great
meruayll / and Wuth that devotion she received that blissed sacrament. And
after time she was houseled / she was so plenteuously replete of our lord /
that all that day she might speak no word to no creature. On the morrow her
confessor axed her what / her eyled / and what now grace she received ye
other day a fore / by cause she was / so shynnyng read when she received that
blyssed sacrament / she answorde thus. Fader of what color I was that time I
wot nere / but this I know well wha^

I unworthy wretch received that / blyssed sacrament of your hondes / it drew
me some to it that all other thing save that allone wexed to me lothesom not
only temporal things and dylectacyons. of the world / but also other
comfortes and pleysaunces / were they never so ghostly / wherefore I desired and
prayed yt all such ghostly comfortes should be sequestryd from / so that I
might pleese god and end lesly be I knytte to him And also I prayed him that
he would take away my will and give me his will / and so he deed right mercyably
and said to me thus. Loo / dear daughter now I give the my will by the which
thou shalt be so strong that what ever hap to the fro this time for the
ward thou shall never be changed / nestyred and right so it was / She was.
ever afterward despised and set little by of all folk / and was never the
more / styred ne troubled ageynsthem. Ouermore yet this holy maid said to her
confessor. Fader well will ye wete how / our lord served me. Trewely as a
mother served her little soukyng child whom she loves tenderly. A mother
suffered / other while her child stand a far from her while she shows him
hirtete of her breast / and suffered him to weep long time after hit / but all
that time the lawhed At the last when she has suffered it to / weep long time /
she gothe there to with a lawhyng there and beclypped it in her arms and kyssed
it and so gives it her / breast or she tete. Right so ferde our lord with me
/ that day he showed me his / blessed wound in his side stondyng all. a far
from me. And I for desire that I had there to put my mouth to that / blessed
wound and wept haboundantly Then our lord said after time yt he had so
suffered me to weep / he came to me gladdely and took my soul in his. arms
and put my mouth to his wound. And then my soul for that great desire
entered all hole in to his blessed wound / where I found much swetnesse and
knowleche of his godhede And yfye wystye would meruayll that mine / heart for
gretnesse of that joy and love. to barst not. And ye would be astonyed how I
might live in this life with such a great passing hete of love. Also another
thing befyll her the next year se wyng upon the same day as she was a boute to
receive the blyssed sacrament of the altar / when the pressed held the
blessed sacrament in his hands before her / and taught her for to say thus.
Lord I am not worthy that thou sholdest enter in me. Then when she had de
received him / her seemed that as a fysshe entered in to the water / and the
water in him / right so her sowfe entered in god and god in her And so she
felt her self all I draw in to our lord / that uneath she might come home to
her chamber / And when she was come home / she laid her down upon her hard
bed / leyng long time still and moeuyd not. At the last her body was take up
in to the air and stood the re a while to gyder as three wytnessys bears
record / the which names I shall tell you afterward. Then afterward she
came down and lay upon her bed all weyke and feeble / and spoke softely many
blessed sweet words. And hye contemplatyf words that it steryd her felawes to
weep the which herd them. And among thoo swetr words she prayed for many
folk / and for som^e specially by name / namely for her confessor that was
that same time in the same momente in the church / and thought for that time
on no thing that should styre him to devotion But suddenly by her prayer he
felt a meruayllous devotion / that never he assayed before / consyderyng and
meruayllyng how that new grace camto him so suddenly / that hour while he
thought thus / suddenly came to him one of this holy maidens felawes and said

Trewely fader Katheryne has much prayed for you this day such an hour.

Then anon he know that such a new denocyon came to him at that hour by
Katherynes prayer. And he axed of her felawe what she prayed / and she told
him that she prayed for him and for other that our lord would wouchesauf to
grant them everlasting life / and that she putt forth her hand and prayed him
for to grant that. Then she took down her hand again semyng to her al
sore / and with great syghenge she said thus. A lord worshypped mote thou be /
for that was ever a common term in her mouth for to say when she was seek and
sore trauaylled. When her confessor herd this / he went to her and prayed
her tille him all her vysyon. She as meke obedyent maid told him all the hole
bysyon as it is said before / and when she came to that matter where she prayed
for special friends she said to him. Fader when I prayed for you and for
other / that our lord would wouchesauf to graun te you everlasting life / with
that I had a comfort that it should so be / and forthwyth I asked a token of
our lord / that I might know it should be so / not for none Incredulyte / but
rather for a notable memory. Then he prayed me that I should stoetche out
mine hand / I did so / and he put in my hand a nail and closed the nail
so fast with Inn mine hand. Then I felt a great pain in mine hand as
though an yren naylle had be smyten thorugh myghtely with an hamour / so
that me seemed to mynowne sight / thought it be Jnuysyble to other / I have a
mark of Crystys wounds in mine hand.

Also for contynuance of matter I shall tell you another meruayllos thing like
to this that befylle in the Cytee of Pyse As master Reymond her last
confessor bears record. In a time this holy maid came to the Cite of Pyse /
and other many with her / among whom master Reymond was one the which holy
maid was received in to a worthy man's place of the same Cite beside a
chapel of Saint Crystyane. In the which chapel master Reymond said mass
at the holy maids prayer / and there he houseled her after her desire / as she
used to be contynuelly when she had received that blyssed sacrament she
was anon rauysshed fro her bodily wits / and all that time master Reymond
and other moo abode till she had do / for to here of her sum ghoostly
comfort as they were wont to do after such rauyssheng. Suddenly as they
beheld her / the body that lay prostratr upon the ground was raised up / and
she kneled upon her knees stretchyng up her arms and her hondes with a clear
shynyng vysage. When she had so long kneled with closyng and styf arms / at
the last she fill down suddenly as though she had be dedly wounded / and
anon sone after she was restoryd again to her bodily wits. Then she sent
after master Reymond her confessor and said to him preuely this words.
Fader I do you well to wete that by the mercy of god I here now in my body the
markys of the blessed wounds of our lord.

master Reymone then axed her how that might be and how it stood with her in
time of her rauyssheng / she answer de and said. I saw our lord fastened upon
the cross coming a down and beelyppyng me with a great light By the which
gracyous vysyon the soul was so gretely steryd to me with my lord yt the body
was constreyned by strength of the spyryte to arise. Then out of the holes
of his holy wounds I saw five read bemys come down from him and fastened upon
my body / and was cause why that my body was all forstoeyned.

With that I cried to our lord and said. A a lord god I beseech the that
these wounds appyre not in me to the sight of men outward.

Then suddenly while she said these words er then thoo read bemys were
fully come down to the body changed her colors out of read in to a
meruayllous bryghtnesse / and in lykenes of a pure light they restyd in five
placed of my body / that is upon the hondes / the feet / and the heart.

Then master Reymond axed her whether any of the bemys come to the right
side. She said nay / but only upon the lift side upon my heart / master
Reymond axed her eftesones felyst thou any manner of sensyble pryne in thoo
places.

She answered with a great sygheng and said / I suffer so great a sensyble
sorrow in all tho five places and specyaly in my heart / that but god show a
new miracle it is Impossyble to me for to live long time to gydres in this
body This word marked well master Reymond her confessor and espied where he
could see in her any manner tokenes of pain Wha^ she had told that she would say
they depted a sonder out of that chapel / and they went to gyders home to
their Inn / and the holy maid went to her chamber and there she lay down
femyng to all that ever were about her drawyng to the death. Then was master
Reymond called and other of his feleshyp for to see ye wound thing / when they
were come / they wept sore by cause they wend she should had depted from the^
for they saw her ne^ so feeble nygh so to ye death Nevertheless within a while
after she resorted again to more strength and received mete and then she
spoke eftsoon to master Reymound and said to him as she said a fore that she
may not long live / but if god show a new miracle. Then Master Reymound
called to gyders all her children both men and wymmen prayng them with weeping
there that they would all with one voice pray to our lord that he would
vochesaf to grant us this holy maid katherin our ghostely virtuous Mother and
our maystres the which lythe in passing / for to abide with us a while in
this life and for to conferme us in more virtue:

All they granted with one voice that they so would / than they went all
with Master Reymound to this holy maid ^yeng in transyte saying such words
weylyng and weeping: Mother we wete well that thou desyrest to be with thine
spouse with our lord Jhesu christ / but thy mede and thy reward is reserved
fro the all auf have rewthe on us whom thou forsakest mother And leave us not so
freell without better enformacion of virtue in this wretchyd world / We know
well also thy well byloued spouse whom thou love with so great a desire
will nothing deny the that thou ask / therefore we beseech the pray to
him that he vouhesauf grant the to us for a time lest thou pass fro us. And
we no thyn ge or little edefyed by thy good living For though we pray as well
as we could / We dread us lest he will not here us for our wretchyd living
for certain we ben right vnwurthy to be herd Then^e therefore that have louyd
our health / and that so tenderly and fervently / pray ye for us and win
our lord that we mow not leave yt in this life till we ben more edefyed in
ghostely virtue many such words they said among them with great weeping /
To whom this holy maid answered / ye know well that I have forsake mine own
will / ne I desire never but that / that were to gods will / and all be it I
have desired your health with all mine heart / yet I know well that he yt
which is your health and mine / can better ordeine for you than one creature
can pray for you / his will therefore be done in all things: Nevertheless yet
I shall pray gladly that he vouchesaf for to do that him seems best / When
she had said this word we went a side for a time being in great sorrow unto
the time we know an answer / The next day afterward she called master
Reymounde to her and said / me seems fader yt our lord has condescendyd to
your prayers / and I hope ye should soon have your will and intent* as she
said so it was sone after / For upon the morrow the which was upon a sunday
she received crystis body in ye sacrament of ye altar of her confessor his
hondes / and right as in the sunday before she was brought in great febylnes
by her rauysshyg after time she had received that blessed sacrament / Right
so in this sunday she was greatly strengthed by her rauysshyng after that
blessed sacrament the which was great merueyle to all that were about her /
To whom Master Reymound said: I hope yt our lord has accepted our teres and
co^desce^dyd to our prayers though they ben vnwourthy Then^e within a litil
time afterward she was so quikly revived yt none of the^ all was in doubt but
yt she should live / and yt god had granted fulli her desire / O almyghti god
fader of mercy what wylt you do for thyn true servant and well-beloved children
you co^descendist so benigly to thyn sinful seruauntis: master Reymound then
asked her for the more sykernes wheder the passyo^ of tho wou^des contryned
always as they deed in her body / She answered in this wise: Our lord ^hu has
herd your prayers and thefore tho wounds tourment not now my body as they ^yde
/ but rather they comfort me and strength me / Loo maidens here now ye know
what evcellent of grace this holy maid had / and also ye mow learn that
our lord vochesaf to here sins when thry asked any thing that longs to
soul health:

Yet shall I tell you another merneylous thing that as me seems it passes
all other that I have rehearsed yet / And so shall I make an end of this
Chapter by the help of god /

After time that our lord had received her soul in to his blyssyd wound off
his side and there showed her the mystery est of the glorious trynyte / then
came our glorious lady his glorious mother glorious vyrgin marye and fulfilled
her with the glorious milk of her glorious breasts and tetes / After came mary
magdalene and comynyd with her full homely of her reuelacions yt she had when
she was in desert and other while these three come togydre and gave her many
blessed comfortable words / Yet wanted she not the comfort of other saytes
and the apperyng and namely of saint poule the Appostle and saint Johan
theuangelyst and saint domynyke and saint Thomas dalquino / And oftetymes saint
Agnes of whom she had onys a reuelacion that should be her felawe in the
kingdom of heaven as it shall be declared afterward by the help of god But now
I shall tell you two notable points that befyll to this holy maid when she
had any vysyons of saint poule ye apostle it befil i^ ye fest co^^sacio^ of
saint poule yt this holy maid was so merueylously rauysshed out of her self /
That her thought that her spyryt was draw up to heaven / so ferforth that three
days and three nyghtes she was vnmeuable without bodly felyng so that it seemed
that she was fully deed / But there were sum that understood better her
condycion and said that they supposed she was rauysshed with saint poule in to
the third heaven / At the last by the three days end she was reforted to her
bodly feling But the spyryte was so comforted with that reuelacions that she
stood long *time afterward as she had be half a sleep: and yet she slepte
not: In the mean while Friar Thomas her first confessor and another fellow of
his which was called friar donat of Flerence had a desire to goo for to
vysyte an holy here myte in deserte: but first or than they went they come to
this holy maid hou^^ and found her in on holy sompnolente / and by cause they
would excite her they asked her whether she would go with the^ to deferte for
to vysyte that holy man. She answered to them in the same holy sleep and said
ye / notwythstondyng yt she wist not what she said by cause that she was not
fully evcyted /

But anon as she perceived that word she had such a reuerse of conscience
off that lesynge / that for sorrow the which she took thereof / She was
restoryd fully to her bodily wits /

And as many days and nyghtes as she stood before in rauysshyg / so long after
she wayled and wept vncessabyly yt sy^e / and said to her self: O wicked woman
have thou so well be feed with the infinite goodness of god that thou must
now make a lesyng: be these trenthe^^ that thou haste learned in heaven / is
this. ye doctrine that thou art taught of the holy ghost for to make lesynges.
Then: wist thou right well that thou woldeste / not goo with tho friars / And
yete thou. saydest thou would / and so made a / lesyng to thyn confessor
and to thyn ghostely faders / O meost wicked sin: ce / ye not maidens the
meruaylous ways and manners of our lordis prouydence / Loo lest her
reuelacyons should have by / cause of pride to her Our lord suffered her for to
fall in to such a lesyng / if it may / be called a lesyng / for there was
none ^ntencion of deceyte / and so by that mekenes and lownes our lord
covered her / virtue that the fend should not enter for to destroy them / But
tho things that the saw for that time in her reuelacyons she told not to her
confessor as she was / wont to do of other reuelacyons / for as she said her
self she could find none la^guege that might express tho reuelacyons by
wordene it is not lefull to no man for to speak of hem with tongue as the /
same appostle says him selt / Nonlicet / ho^iloqui: /

Eut the feruoure of her heart the besynes of her prayer* and her holy
exortacyons showed openly ynowe that she saw the preuytes of god /

The which may not be co^mynyd but: they^ that saw them. Ouermore another
time saint poule the appostle arpperid to her and warned her that she should
give her besely to prayer the which she told / afterward to her confessor /
And therefore that she used much / Then it befyll / afterward whiles she
prayed in the church on the vygylle of Saint Domynyke: many reuelacyons were
showed to her of saint Domynyke / and of other saints She was so often occupied
with reuelacyons the same time when she would speak to her confessor she had
reuelacions / Then i^ the next day afterward of saint Domynyke a lytyl:
before even / song time whiles she was occupied / with reuelacions suddenly
entered in to the church a friar which was Bartylmeus her confessors felawe
in whom she / trusted as much as in her confessor for* he was her confessor
absens of her goostely tader / When ^he perceived that that he was come she
ar^os and went / agayst him and said to him that she / would speak with him of
certain reuela / c^ons. Theune they satte down bothetegyders in the church and
she began to reherce how many reuelacyons our lord had / deshewed her of saint
Domynyke at the last she said / loo fader I see now mine* holy fader Saint
Domynyke as I see* you now / And yet he is more nerer me / than ye be /

And then she procedyd forth of many merueylous reuelacyons within a / while
after it befyll that her young brother that was called also Bartylmeus / went by
her / And suddenly she cast her eye a little a side and behylde her brother and
left of the sight of saint Domynyke for that little time and then continued
forth in her tyste matter / But for that / deed she made much sorrow / when she
per ceyued what she had I do / that long after she held her peace and spoke
no more but always wept for that trespaas / When / she had long continued in
weeping / at: the last Friar Bartylmewe prayed her / to proceed forth as she
began / but she migte not for sobbyng uneath speak one word.

Yet as she might speak she said.

O what wretch am I And he shall / do me vengeance for my sins / Friar
Bertylmewe / What sin might that be / then she said / Saw ye not how I
bowed away / mynhede and mine eyes for to behold my: brother that went right
now by / the whiles our lord she wed me many merueylous things / Friar
Bertyimewe say: nay he could not perceive that she bowed in any wise her head
and her eyes a side: Then she said fader yt ye wyste / how our blessed
glorious lady glorious: virgyn mary repreuyd me right now / for that sin: Ye
woide weep also fore / as I and so she spoke no more of that / ma^ie^ of
reuelacyons / but ever co^tynued in weeping unto the time she had made / her
con^e^ion / and thene she went home to the chamber / where saint poule
appleryd to her as she to: de afterward to her confessor and repreuyd her
sharply off the lokyng of that time when she turned her head so a side in so
ferforthe she said that it had be more lever for her / to be shamed of all
the world than onys: ^stsones to suffer that shame: the which she had of
saint poule when he repreuyd he^ / Thene she said to her confessor fader
bethynke you what repreuynge of christ shall be at the day of dome to all
sinners / yt the cepreuynge of one of his appostles is now so sharp and make
me / so much aferd / She said also but if / she had / had comforthe of a
fair lamb that stood beside her whiles the. Appostle repreuyd her / She should
have deyed for sorrow as her seemed wherefore ever after ward she was she more
meker ^ her reuelacyons: Loo maidens how our lord suffered her to fall for her
more mekenes / But now shall I tell you what the* reuelacyons was the which
she had ofsaynt Domynyke. When this holy maid comyned and spoke with Freyer
bertylmewe of her reuelacyons: she said that she saw in deed by a vysyon of
imaginacion allmyghty god the fader brenging forth as her seemed out of his
mouth our lord thu^cryste his endeles sone the which apperid openly to her
in lykenes of mankind: On the lodersyde the blessed: Patryarch Saint Domynyke
coming out of the / breast of almyghcy god the fader shyn / nyng all in ^y^ht /
And the herd of the mouth of a^^myghty god the fader these words: dear
daughter I have brought / forth thyle children / the one kyndely and /
natural being the second person in intrynyte: The oder louyngly and swetely
by adopcion / Then this holy made had great marvel of such comparyson by
/ twene the sone of god and saint Domynyke.

But almighty god the fader to put / away that great marvel expownyd / these
words and said / Dear daughter: right as here mynowne sone whom I / brought
forth of me naturally and eternaly was ever pertyghtly obedyent to me unto the
death by taking upon him mankind: Right so the deeds of Domynyk mine sone by
adopcyon what that ever / wrought fro his chyldehode in to the enof his bodily
life were reuled:

After the obedyence of my^ commau^de tys and never brake onys any manner of:
precepte of mine for the virgynyte ofthis: body and soul and the grace of his
baptyme he kept ever to me vndefoylyd:

And also right as here mine / eternal and natural sone the endeles / world
of my mouth told and spoke openly to all the world that I badde him say: And
thereto bare wyttenes of truth / Right so Domynyke mine sone by adopcyon
preche my truth openly to the / world / as Well Among heretykes as
among faythfus people / and not only by himself but also by other of hi^ and
not only* whiles he lived in earth among you / But also by his successors by
whom yet they precheth and shall preche for right as my natural and eternal
sone sent his dyscyples for to preche right so Domynyk mine sone by a dopcion
sent his friars / And also right as mine natural sone and eternal is mine word
/ right Domynyke mine sone by adopcion is the prechour about of mine word /
wherefore of mine synguler gift it is give to him and to his friars for to
vuderstonde the truth of min words and not for to pass therfro / Also right
as mine natural sone and eternal ordained and dysposyd all his lyff and his
deeds by doctrynes and ensample to health off mannys soul / right Domynyke mine
sone by adopcion put all his besynes to deliver out souls of ye sorrow of
error and of sin / And that was his pryncipall intent / When he began his
order / that is for to say for health of souls therefore he may well be lyked
to min natural and eternal sone sone Ihesu Criste / This was the reuelacioy
the which she comynyd to friar Bertylmewe* when that sodeyn caas of lokyng
aside byfyll to her as it is rehersyd before /

Now I shall proceed forth of the remenaunt of the life of this holy maid in
reuelacions and visyons* but first I would ye knew maidens that for the great
haboundance of greces and open reuelacions and visyons and for the gre^enes of
love therwyth / The which this holy maids soul was fulfilled / She was right
syke in her body / and ever encresid in sekenes more and more for love so yt
she roo^ no more out of her bed but lay still ever newyng the love of her
spose seeing thus / Aswete lovely lord gods sone: and the sone of a maiden*
with such many loving* words she praised our lord and her spouse: She
beleft without bodily mete and thereto her spouse Jhesu Christ the which given
her that fire of love by cause it should bren^e more sto^gely / he apperyd to
her often times / Then ne said she to him that was so febyll off the fire of
love Good lovely lord you suffer me so long abide in this wretched body and
wylt not take me to thyn endeles presence / I have none Joye now off this
wretchid life but only all mine joy is for to seek the / For I love the Ihesu
and none without the: for what that ever I love lord it is for the why am I
there for delayed so long* fro thyn endeles presence / Ha ha mekest and
myldest lord deliver mine soul out of this prison and out of this dedely lif:
To thise words that were said so weylyngly / our lord answered / Dear
daughter when I lived in earth among men I besyed me never for to fulfylle mine
own will but mine faders and albe it that I desired to ete the last paske with
mine dysciples for to be with mine fader as they herd me often times say / yet I
suffered patiently the time that was ordained off mine fader / so must thou do
/ though you desire fervently to be onyd to me perfightely in the bless of
heaven / yet thou must abide the time that I have ordained: Theenne she said to
our lord / lovely lord sithe it so is that it is not kind to me as yet to
pass out of this lyff / thyn will be done: Fiat voluntas tua / But one thing I
beseech ye whiles I live in this earth yt sithe I may not yet be onyd to yt i^
bliss* grant me as long as I live in this life to be onyd to ye and with ye
by part taking of thy blessed passion ye which was granted to her:

For as she asked / so she had / fro that time forward she had so much
experiens every day in her heart and i^her body of the passions of our lord as
she told afterward preuyly to master Reymou^d that she never felt such a
soor and that was in this wise / Often times she would sytte and talk with
master Reymound and teache him of the passion of criste affermyng myghtely that
our lord Jhesu christ fro the time of his glorious concepcion in to the time
of the end of his blyssyd passion he bare ever the cross of his death in his
soul* for the great passing desire that he had for the health of mannys
soul / For when he was conceived he was full of grace and of wisdom and of
charity / And it was none need to him for to encrece in him afterward for he
was perfyght ynow in them at the beginning / Therefore sithe it so was that he
loved so perfyghtly god the fader and mankind in heart seeing and consyderyng
god the fader in trinite in manner depryued of his honor. And also mankind
depryuyd f^o his blessed end / he was so tourme^ted with compassyon in him
self unto the time that he might restore by his passion the dew honor to god
the fader in T^inyte and endeles health to mankind* Also she said the
affliction of his holy desire was none little pain / But it was a great pain:
And thefore it was that he said to his dyscyples on schherthursday at the
soper / Deside^io desideraui manducare vobiscum hoc pascha / That is I have
desired with a great desire long before this time to ete with you this paske /
and the cause was for he gave them in that soper an special ernest of health
the which he would work er then he purposed to ete with them eftsoon /
And therefore she alleggid for her the wordys of our savior where he says in
another place. Pater transfer calicem hu^c a me / That is fader put away this
passion fro me that I shall now drink / the which words she expownyd thus
and said / Perfyght folk should not understand these words as simple folk
done / that our savior asked of his fader to put away and remeue hye
paynefull passion But thus fro the beginning of his glorious concepcton unto
that time of his death he drank ever of that paynfull passion by the great
desire that he had off mannys health / And then the more he draw nere to the
death* the more gredyly he desired that drink* he asked therefore that it should
soon be fulfilled the which he had so long time desired for the health of
mannys soul / that the dryke ye which he had drunk so long before should
then be ended* And thus this was not for to ask a remeuyng away of his death
/ but rader an hasti end of his death: the which our savior declared full
openly afterward when he said to Judas / Quod facis fac cicius / That is friend
that thou shall do / do it anon / Nevertheless though it so were that the
foresaid pains full drink of his desire were to him right grievous for to
drink / yet as right an obedyent child to the fader he said thus /
Veruntamen non sicut ego volo sed sicut tu: Fader I desire that mine will be not
fulfilled but thy will offering him self ready by th^se words for to suffer
daily of his pain full desire as long as it lyked to his fader so that the
first words where he said / Transfer hunc calitem etc. Fader a void this
paynfull fro me / he understood not for to have a voyded his passion that was
to come / But the passion of his desire before by suffryng the death for health
of man's soul for to be endyd. Then said master Reymond. Mother comynly
after exposicion of doctors our lord said tho words as a very man and head
of all his chosen both f^eel and strong / whose sensualyte naturelly dread the
death / that he might by example to all both to freel folk and to strong folk /
that they dyspeyre not / all be it they felt their sensualyt^e kyndely
dredyng the death.

Here to this holy maid answered and said / that the acts and the dedys of our
savior if they ben wisely considered / every creature after his consyderacyon
may find in them ghostly felyng / as it is spedefull to his health. And
therefore sith it is so that feeble and freall creatures fynden in tho words
comfort against their feblenesse / it were right necessary then that perfyt
folk and mighty should find also there Jnne co^fyrmacyon of their strength /
the which might not be but by this exposycyon before* Therefore it is better yt
it be expowned in many manners so yt al may be comforted there by / then in a
manner of wise for one manner of folk allone

When master Reymond herd this he held his peace / meruayllyng of her great
wysdom and grace that she had / for he her de never that exposycyon before.
Another exposycyon of the same words by the same holy maid. Master Reymond
found written in a book that her first confessor wrote and they ben these

In a time when she was rauysshed she learned of our lord that the prayer the
which he made a fore his passion when he ^watt both blood and water seeing
thus

Transfer hunc calicem and^. That is fader remove this peynfull passion fro me

He prayed then for them whom he saw before that would have no part of his
passion / the which was to him peynfull passion. And by cause he loved
ryghtwysnesse / he put a condycyon and said. Veru^tamen non mea voluntas That
is neuthelesse fader be not my will fulfilled / but thy will / and if he had
not putto such a condycyon / it would have followed there on she said that all
folk should have be saved. After time then that he had thus prayed / he was
herd as saint Poule said for his reverence. Exauditus est propter suam
reuerencia^ In exposycion of this words of saint Poule comynly doctors
vnderstonden the same It had be else meruaylle but that the same sone of god
should have be herd. Also she said another time to master Reymond and taught
him that the passions which our our lord god Jhesu Christ ve ray god and man
suffered for the health of mankind were so mighty / that it were impossyble any
man in earth for to suffer but that he should dye and it were possible many
time if that he suffered them. For right as his love yt he had then / and has
yet to mankind vnestymable / and vncomperable. Right so his passion that he
suffered by constreynyng of love allone was vnestymable. Who would believe that
the thorns of his crown should perysshe in to the brain. Or that the bones
of a quyk man should be draw out of their joints For the prophet said of
our lords passion thus. Dinumeraueru^t omnia* ossa mea. That is they told and
nombred all the bones of my body

So then it may be proved yt the pryncypall cause of his passion was love /
the which he shemed for mankind And it might not be showed more conuenyently
than by his passion. By this it seemed that the naylles held him not upon the
cross / but his love only. Ne the strength of man overcame him ^ot / but
love. How were men so strong for to hold him / that at a word of his mouth
they fill down to the ground when they came for to take him Such high
words and conuenyent words of our lords passion this holy maid co^myne with
master Reymond. And yet she said more that she had experyence in her body of
some manner of passion that Christ suffered on the cross* Of all she would not say
for that was Impossyble to any erthely creature. But specially by cause of the
great love that she had to our lord and to his passion the most pain yt she
suffered was in her heart / so that it seemed to her other while that her heart
was to braste and cut a sondre fro that one end to that other.

And for this great pain of love / she was oftymes deed to all mennys sight.

Of this bare wytnes many one / the which were present when she dyed for
the love of Crystys passion allone.

Here of was master Reymond in great doubt. But for to put away that doubt
/ he thought to comen with this holy maid and search the sothe of her whether
it were so or no. When he axed her this. She for great weeping could give none
answer long time to gydre / but at the last she said. Fader would ye not have
great pity and compassyon of a soul that were delivered out of a derke prison
to light / and after time it had see so merry a light / eftesones to be reclused
ageyn in the same derke prysone. I am that same wretch that thus happed me by
the ordinance of god for my sins. Then ne master Reymond axed her where her
soul was fully departed fro the body.

To whom she answered and said thus. That the fervent fire of dyuyne love and
of ghoostly desire was so much in her heart for to live with our lord
endelesly whom she loved. That though her heart had be of stone or of yren it
must nedys to breast. Therefore fader understands this for truth that mine
heart of mine body was then undo and opened fro the ouermost party to the
nether / only by the strength of pure love / so that me seems yet I feel the
markys of that syssure in mine heart. By this ye may know yt the soul was
fully for that time deperted fro the body / and set in the presence of god /
where I saw the preuyt^es of god / that is vn^efull for to speak to any man on
earth For there is no speech in earth that can express the preuytees in any
ma^nis tongue. But this wot I well as often as I here of that matter I am
tourmented so greatly in my soul consyderyng where I was then and where I am
now / that I can not tell my sorrow but with weeping and sobbyng. Then
master Reymond prayed her to tell him how that all this began in her. She
answered and said. After time that I was fed and comforted with many vysyons
and reuelacyons by our lords mercy / I fell seek for pure love and lay down
in mine bed where I prayed our lord Jhesu that he would deliver me out of
this wretchyd world / and oned me perfytely to him The which for that time he
would not grant me.

But he granted therefore as long as I lived in this life / should be partyner of
his passion / in asmoche as it is possible a dedly body for to suffer / and so
she told him all that / that is rehearsed before. And more over she said / loo
fader by such experyence of his passion / I am made so seek by the strength
of love / that my soul desired no thing else but for to be delivered out of
this world And the same fire so encrecyd in my soul that my heart often times
defayled and departed a sonder and my soul was utterly delivered out of the
body Nevertheless it was but a little time and that was my sorrow. Then ne
eftesones master Reymond axed her how long time her soul was out of the body.
She said as they that kept her and were about to have beryed her four hours
or then she reuyued ageyn Yet he axed her what she saw for that time / and
