why came the soul again to the body she answered thus Fader that time my soul
saw and understood joy of blessed sowles / and peynes of sinners. And as mine
mind would suffer me and words would suffyce to express them / I shall tell
you. My soul saw the divine essen cyall being of god / and that is the cause
why I am so loathe and impatient to live in this world / and had not be the
love of him and the love of christian people / for which my soul was restoryd
to the body again / I should had defaylled and dyed for sorrow. The highest
comfort that I have is when I suffer any disease / for that I have the perfyte
vysyon of god / therefore trybulacyons ben not heuysom to me / but comfortable
as ye may know / and other that been conuersaunt with me I saw also the peynes
of dampened sowles / and peynes of sowles that been in purgatory / the which I
can not express perfytely with no manner of words. For if wretched sinners
saw the least pain that is there / they had lever chese bodily death an
hundred times if it were possible / then for to suffer o day the least pain
that is there. But specially I saw hem ponys shed syngulerly that had sinned
in matrymony / the which had not kept hem to gyder honestly as they should
do / but followed the dylectacions of their lustys

Of this master Reymond her confess sour axed her why that sin in special
was more grievously punysshed then other sins / sith it so is that it is not
the most grievous sin She said for this skylle. For they had not so great
conscience of that sin ne so great contrycy on as they had of other sins /
but rather they offended in that sin then in any other That sin the
which a sinner charge not for to remove / by penance is a great sin be it
never so little.

Then this holy maid proceeded forth in her matter and said thus also. Fader
wha^ne I had seen all these joys and these peynes wenyng my self that I had
fully be delivered out of this body.

Our lord said to me / see thou not daughter what joy they lack and what
pain they have that offenden me. Torn ageyn therefore to thy body and tell to
the people their error and their peril. And with that word I was astonyed for
to torn again to the body and sore aferde.

Then our lord said to me / it is profit to mennys souls that thou torn
again / and thou shalt not live the life that thou have lived a fore ne keep
the solytarie allone in chamber / but thou shalt goo a broad to win sowles /
I shall ever be with the / and goo with the both going and coming. Thou shalt
bear the worship of my name and of ghoostly doctrine before great and small and
lay people and clerkys and a fore Relygyous folk also I shall give the both
mouth and wit for to speak that none may wythstande the. I shall also bring
the before bysshoppys and curates of sowles for to confound there pride. Whiles
our lord spak these words suddenly my soul was restored again to my body.

And when I perceived that I had great sorrow / that I wept three days and
three hyghtes to gyders without cessyng And yet I can in no wise absteyne ne
refreyne me there fro / when it comes to my mind how suddenly I was come fro
the great joy unto this prysone of the body What wonder is it therefore fader
though mine heart to breast every day consyderyng the great excellent joy that
time that I had / the which now it is far fro me / but all is done for the
soul hele Therefore there shall no man marvel though I love them passyngly to
whom our lord has bid me warn them of their sinful living / for I have
left for them a great joy for a certain time I wot not how long. Therefore as
saint Poule seyth. They ben now my glory my crown and my joy. All this I
say to you fader and to all other for to put out of your hertes the passion
of grutchyng in time coming when I shall be homely among all men. When
master Reymond herd all this and understood them / after the grace that was
give him / he perceived in his heart / that for the incredulytee and blyndnes
of men / all that she said should not be publysshed. Wherefore he for bade
both the freres and the sustres / that all the while this holy maid lived in
earth they should not pupplysshe that matree.

He perceived also of sum that followed first her doctrine / how they went
backward / for they could not ne might not take her words But lest he should
offend god if he had hid it himself without writing / he wrote it for a
perpetuell record after her dyssece / and not while she lived Now maidens for
to know veraly that all this is sothe I shall tell you wytnes of record that
were present with this holy maid when all these things befyll her In that
same time when this holy maid drew nigh to the death as it seemed and as it is
rehearsed before.

There drew about her wymmen and other ghoostly daughters of herys / and they
sent after her first confessor friar Thomas for do be present at her passage
by prayers and other holy exercyses in comme^dyng of her soul to god. He came
and three freres with him mo to be present at the passing of this holy maid.
But when she was passyd as it seemed. One of the freres took so great sorrow
therefore that by vyolence of his weeping / a vein of his breast was all for
brosyd / where with he caught a coghe and spatte gebettes of blood. Then was
that another sorrow to them that stood about / for both they wept for the
holy maid that was so passyd. And also for her brother the which was not
shappely to live long after in that pain. Then said friar Thomas her first
confessor to that seek friar with great feyth and trust. Brother I wot well
this holy maid is in great reputacyon before god for her good living. Therefore
take her hand and put in the same place of thy sekenes. And I doubt not but
that thou shalt be hole. And anon forth with he did so and so he had health
/ the which he told afterward to all that would here if There was also a
ghoostly daughter of herys that was present then / the which was called
Alyxa / and passyd out of this world sone afterward Moother were that came
Inn for to see whether she was passed or not / and there was none that could
suppose otherwise There were also two other special wyttenessys / that were
about for to ordeyne for the body that it should be beryed. And both were
susters of penance of Saint Domynyk / that one was called Katheryne as she was
/ the which was her felawe long time before. And that other was her cosyn Lysa
/ and thus I make an end of this chapter.

Of sum miracles wrought gracyously by this holy maid about the health of
sowles. Capitulum vij
IF I should reherce all the miracles that our lord showed by this holy maid
/ I might rather make a great book of them than for to comprehend hem in oo
chapter. But by cause I would put away dullness of them that should read or
here this legende of this holy maid I am about asmoche as I may under few
words for to comprehend them in one chapter / that they might know under
few words how great they ben the which I pass over lyghtely. therefore in as
much as the soul passes the body in worthynesse. I shall begin of tho
miracles the which were showed of our lord by her about mennys sowles / and
after that of the bodies

As touching for the first when that Jamys or Jacob / the fader of this holy
maid perceived that his daughter Katheryne was all given to serve and to
please our lord as it is rehearsed in the first party of this legende / ever
he loved and tretyd her reuere^tly and louyngly / for bedyng all folk of his
household that none be so hardy for to let Katheryne his daughter in any
manner wise / what that ever she will have done This is a great cause why that
the daughter loved the fader. And therefore she commended specially her faders
health often times to our lord. And he had such a trust in his daughters
prayers / that he supposed well she might have of god what she would for his
health Sone after the fader sykened and lay down in his bed all seek. When
this holy maid his daughter perceived that / anon she prayed to our lord
her spouse for the health of her fader. And it was answered to her of our lord
/ that the end of his days of this world were come / and that it were not
spedefull for him for to abide longer in this life. Then ne she went to her
fader and vysyted him and examyned him how he was dysposed in his soul / and
found ready and wylfully to pass out of this world / having no lust for to
abide longer / wherefor she thanked our lord hyghly But then she prayed our
lord eftesones / that sith it so is that he had given her fader so great
grace for to pass out of this world without sin / that he would wouchesauf
to grant him also for to flee to heaven / without pain of purgatory. Of this
she had an answer in this wise / that ryghtwysnesse must nedys be kept /
and therefore it were no right / but Impossyble a soul to have the clerenesse
of endeles joy without perfyte purgacyon a fore.

For all be it thy fader has been in his days of good living among all other
wedded folk / and also do many good things that I am well pleased with / and
specially as touching the Yet nevertheless it may not be saving my
ryghtwysnesse. But that his soul must be purged by the fire for to brenne out
the duste of erthely conuersacyon / the which is hardened and endured in his
soul Then said this holy maid to our lord thus My dear well-beloved lord
what may I suffer yt my fads soul by whom I have be so tenderly nourysshed /
and have had so many co^fortes in his life / that it be not tormented in such
pains. I pray the lord for the goodness that ever thou shewdest to man kind
/ suffer not his soul to goo out of his body unto ye time it be perfytly
purged oo way or other yt it need not in no wise the pain of purgatory After
such words / our lord showed his mercy meruayllously / as though he had
obeyed to the voice of his maiden. All be it that the bodily strengthes of her
fader Jamys began for to defaylle more and more to the death ward Yet his
soul passed never out of his body unto the time yt holy and dysputacion
between our lord alledgyng for him ryghtwysnesse. And the holy made axyng grace
and mercy* And at the last after long dysputacion / the holy maid said to our
lord. My well-beloved lord if this grace may in no wise be gotten or granted
without some manner of ryghtwysnesse / suffer that ryghtwysnesse fall on me / for
I am ready to suffer al manner of pain what ever thy goodness will ordeyne for
delyuerau^ce of my fads soul. Then our lord granted her grace and said. Loo
daughter for the love yt thou have to me I shall grant the thine axyng / and
I shall deliver thy faders soul fully out of pain But thou shall be suffer a
pain for him as long as thou lyuest / the which I shall assygne the. This
holy maid thanked our lord and said. Good blessed lord be it to me as you
haste ordained. After that she went to her fader as he lay a deieng / and she
comforted him meruayllously of his endeles health that he was right ioyefull /
and she went not from him unto the time he was passyd out of this world And
when the soul was passyd out of ye body / anon forth with this holy maid was
payned with a sekenes in the side / the which is called Ilica passyo / that
never went from her in to the time she passyd out of this world

And there was never time afterward but she had ye pain as she said / and
other bare record often times to master Reymond. But the virtue of her
pacyence without any com^yson passyd her sekenes / as I shall declare by ye
help of god afterward in the last chapter of the thrydde pertye When her
faders soul was delivered out of the body / this holy maid smyled full
manerly and said / now would god I were as ye ben. And all that time other wept
/ she showed gladness of chere for she might none other wise do For she saw
his blessed soul when it passed out of ye body / how it was received in to
endelesse bliss without any taryeng of the which she was right glad a
little before / she had experyence of the same joy / as it is rehearsed in the
chapter before this

See ye not maidens how wisely the prouydence of our lord was wrought in this
maidens fader. Our lord might if he had would / have purged his soul in many
manner of wyses / and made him able Enough to joys / as he did to the thief yt
hynge on his right side / but he would not without some pain that this maid
should suffer as she axed for her encrece of her more joy / the which pain
was ever afterward sweet to her as her seemed / not without cause for she wist
well yt her sweetness should ever encrece aftward her by grace / and in bliss
by joy / and therefore she might in no wise call ye pain of Ilica passio but
a sweet pain This holy maid told puely to master Reymond yt by long time
aft her fads death / his soul appyred oftymes to her / tha^kyng her for her
grace yt he received by her / and also told her many puy things / and gave
her warnyng of ye assaillyng of her enemy / and thereto kept her from al
ghostly euelys. Right as I have told you maidens of a miracle showed to a
ryghtwysmannys soul. So shall I tell you now a miracle showed to a sinful
man's soul.

There was a man dwelling in the cite of Seen the which was called Andrewe a
full rich man of out wordely things of the world / but full pour off
inwardly heavenly things he was a vicious man / for he neither dred ne loved
god But an hasarder and a cursed blasphemer or a swerer of god and of his
saints / within a while afterward that man was take with a sykenes and lay
done in his bed so seek that every man and leche said he was deed: That
perceived his curat and come to him for to comfort him that he should beshryue
and take penance and make his testament as the manner was in the country / when
he had herdde how the preeste counseylled him. he despised both him and his
counsel: his wife considered / that having zele and love to his soul / she
went after all manner relygyous folk both men and wymmen for to stere him to
god: But yet for all her counseyll they might not bow him to confession and
contrycion of his sins / neither with thretinge of endeles pains ne with
rewards of endeles joys. Then eftsoon his curate came to him dredyng lest
he should have deyed for defaulte of counseyll and said to him as he said
first adding thereto many more holsom words / Yet always that wretched man
despised him afterward as he did before both him and his words / At the last
he fill in despeyre and in to the sin of the holy ghost* and so he drew
fast to the death: This was afterward told to Friar thomas this holy maids
first* confessor And he went to this holy maid house pursuyng for to
constrayne her by all the virtue of obedyens and of charity for to pray to our
lord that he would vochesaf to socour ye wretched soul that it be not
dampened wythouten end /

But when he came to this holy maids house he found her rauysshyd fro her
bodly wits and as long as she was so occupied: he durst not occupye her /
ne durst not long abide out of his house by cause yt might drew fast upon him
wherefore he charged a fellow of here is that was that time with her: ye which
was called katheryn as she was for to charge that holy maid in gods behalue
and his / when she were restorid again to her bodily wits that she would
pray for such a mannys soul that lies in passing / she said she would so:
when the holy maid herd that she had so great compassyon of his soul /
that she prayed our lord* anon devoutly besechyng him entyerly that the soul
should not perysshe which he boughte with his precious blood / To whom our lord
answered and said thus his wyckednes has asserued pain as an horrybly
blasphemy For he has not only blasphemid me and mine saints with his mouth /
But also he has thrown a table in to ye fire for despyte of me in the which
was painted the image of mine passion / And the image of mine blessed glorious
mother / and of other saints: And therefore it is worthy by ryghtwysnes yt he
brenne in endeles fire /

Then she fill down prostrate with weeping to the feet of our lord: and
said lord if thou wylt consydere narowe to the sins of men / who may escape
endeles dampnacion / wherefore come thou down to be born of a glorious maid
and for to suffer tourment of cruel death only for to wait after mennys
sins: and to punysshe them horrybly to endeles pain / why tellest thou me
this and the sins of a lost man that barest upon thyn sholders all manner of
sins whether I am come to the now for mercy or for ryghtwysnes have mine lord
blesfulle what thou saydest to me when you put me forth for the health of
many mennys sowles: I have none other refresshinge in this life: But for to see
mine neybours turned to the / And for the alone I suffer patiently thyn absence
/ if thou give me not this joy what shall I than do Good meke lord put me not
away fro the / yield me mine brother graciously that is now obstynat in heart:

Thus she prayed contynuelly fro the beginning of the night unto the graye
morning all that time weeping without any sleep dysputyng with our lord always
for the help of that soul / Our lord aledgyng ryghtwysnes to give to him
vengeance for his sins / And the holy maid asking mercy at the last our
lord of his endeles mercy gave her an answer and said / dear daughter I shall
show him mine grace for whom you have prayed to Andrewe and said / Dear child
whi wylt thou not beshreue of ye tres pas that thou have done to me / look you
beshryue for I am ready for to forgive the thyn sins / Then was his hard
heart souple by grace that he cried with a great voice to his meyny about him
and said / send for the priest for I will byshryue / For my lord Jhesu crist
has warned me that I should beshryuen /

When his meynye perceived that / anon they went for the priest / the priest
came and he was perfyghtly confessyd to him: and made his testament with great
contrycion he passyd out of this world to our lord Ihesu christ:

O fader of endeles mercy how mercy able ben thy works / and how profounde ben
thyn prouydence whose gracyous werk is ben vnscrutable unto man / thou
suffredest that man to be hardyd in his sins unto the last end femyng that
thou had none torce of him /

But yet at the last thou prouydest for his health / thin servant came to him
for to stere him to grace: And yet al her cou^seylles might not avail to the
meke prayers of thy meke maid thou condescendyst mekely and mercyabyly: And
who gave her that boldenes of heart: but thou who gave her fire of compassyon
in heart for her brother but thou / who gave her the meke teres that bowed to
thy mercy / tree wely none but thou Thou aryssydyst up to thy spouse that she
should bow the to her: Lord these ben thy works that gloryfyest thyn saints:
What is he that will not be coplued to the in love seeing thy mercy so
plentuous*

Loo maidens what mercy our lord showed for meke teres / yet shall I tell you
a merueylous miracle /

It befyll also another time in the same Cite of Seen that there were two
famous thefes and right peryllous the which were take and brought before a
temporal Juge for to be dampened to the pain for the misdeeds: and so they
were put to a cruel tourmente that was called the tourmente of the hot iron
and that was in this wise. They were put in a Carte and tourmentours were ready
with hot yrous for to breune them now in one place now in another of her body
/

And thereto the thefes were so obstynat that neither in prison ne out of
prison there might none creature stere them to be shryue and take penance for
her trespaas / And as they were led by the cite for to make other aferd: they
blasphemed god and all his saintis and specially when they felt brennynge they
cursed the magnyfycence of our lord / so as it seemed by they pain of that
temperall fire that the drew fast to the endeles fire Then our lord Ihesu
of his endeles goodness the which would none body were dampened but all saved he
thought he would let tho wretched sowlis by medyacion of his spouse katheryn
out of dampnacion so that by the ordenaunce of him that this holy maid for
her more quyete was that same day in her felawes house whom she loved
virtuously the which was Alixa whose house stood by the same way where that
this dampened wretches should pass by. Sondenly on the morrow Alyxa herd a
merueylous voice coming by her house / with that she looked out of the wyndowe
and saw all a fire two men the which were dampened to the hot yrens / then
she went in again and told this holy maid and said / O yren / When this
holy maid herd this she went to the wyndowe and looked and turned in again
to her prayers she saw as she said afterward to master Reymound her confess:
sour a great multitude of wicked spirytes about them that brennyd her sowles
within much more than the tourmentours did the body without /

And therefore she was stered with double compassyon for to pray for them to
our lord for to help the wretched sowles out of pain seyeng thus / Ha ha
mekest lord Ihesu why set thou so lytyl by thy creatures whom thou made
to thyn likeness And boughtest with thy precious blood that above all her
bodily torment thou suffrest them to be cruelly tormentyd of spyrytes
wythinforth in her sowles when thou illumynyst so graciously that thief that
henge on the right side / al be it that he took his tourment of the cross
wurthely as he had deserved that he knowleched the very god and man in all
his tourmente / where in the appostles were in doubt: wherefore he deserved for
to here thyn blessed voice when thou saydest thus / Hodie mecum eris in
paradiso / That is* to day thou shall be with me in paradyse: why dedyst thou
this lord* trewely for nothing else: but for you would grant forgyfnes to
such as were like to him / thou despysyd not mary magdalene that great sinner
but thou drewest her to the graciously /

Thou put not fro the puplycane ne the woman of Cananye ne the prince of
pupplycanis zacher But rather thou calledest them to the: therefore by all thy
mercies I beseech the that thou help mercyabyly the souls of the sinners that
been now lad to tourment. Then our lord bowed his mercy to the wretches and
grant this holy maid such gra^e that she went with them in spyryte weeping
and weylyng for to stere them the sonner to repentance / when the fendes saw
that they cried alowde upon her and said katheryne but if thou wylt leave of
thyn ghostely besynes in prayng for these me^ we should so work against the
that you shall travail with a wicked spyryte: To whom she answered again: what
that that god will I will and therefore I shall not leave of that I have bygonne
when these wretches were outward at the gates of the Cite our lord Ihesu christ
appyred to them with his blyssyd blody wounds steryng them to be tournyd /
and thereto byhete them forgyfnes: and so they been of dyuyne light entryd in
to her hertes / and they asked apreste with great instaunce for to beshryue:
and after time they were shryuen / They turnyd there blasphemynge in to
praysyng of our lord ever accusyng them self seyeng that they were wurthy tho
pains and more gretter pains and so with great gladness they went to her death
as they had gone to a great feste / This consyderyd all tho that stood about
merueylyng gretely of that changynge perceyuyng evermore in great deuocio^ of
ye tourme^tours yt they durst no more brenne the^ where they thanked our lord of
his great mercy / For there was none that knew how and in what wise and by
whose prayers this mercy was given /

Nevertheless a devout priest the which her confessor command afterward with
this holy maids confessor merueylynge of the great mercy of god that so soon
turned them to grace / Then^e her confessor asked afterward Alixa this holy
maids felawe how this holy maid was occupied when the man were led to the
death / Then Alixa told him all the process as it is said before: and he
found well by record of her that the same hour katherin left her prayer: tho
me^ dyed and passed out of this world: the which he knew more perfyghtly
afterward by preuy reuelacion of the same holy maid /

After yet certain days after they were passey. some of her felawes herd her
say with a full voice in time of her prayer these words lord Ihesu I thank
ye that thou have delyuerd them out of the second prison it was asked her
afterward what she meant thereby / She said that the sowles of the theefes ben
restored to paradyse / For albe it they went to purgatory after time they
passed: yet she secid never by prayer unto the time they were fully delyuerd
out of pain / Paraue^t now sum ther^en that set lityl by this miracle by
cause if was inuisybyll / but if they take heed inwardly of the words of saint
augustyn and saint Gregory / they should find well that this was more miracle /
than if the bodies had been raised from death to live / For saint gregory said
thus that in the bodily resurrexcio^ the flesh is raised the which shall deye
eftsoon / and when the soul is raised / it shall live wythouten end / yet
shall I tell you another synguler gift of conversation of this holy maid
wan of god / There was one the which was called ^abes among whom there was
one child of his that was called James or Jacob and he was a sinful liver
full of pride and of creuelte / so that yet being young in age he kyllyd two
men full cruelly that every man that knew him was aferd of him ne loved him
not: But every day he lived werse and werse / and had a suster that was called
Shy nochya the which was fully given to vanyte of the world in passing
outrages array of her body albe it she was a maid of her bodi: Her mother ^abes
had thereof great forowe lest they should be dampened for there mysbelyuyng she
went to this folly maid and prayed her that she would vochesaf to speak
somewhat of soul hele with her to her daughter Fracisca and Shynochya but
specially with shynochya / this holy maid as she had ever to sowles great
compassyon granted her that she would gladly and so she did: For what prayer
and monycions of our lord Ihesu Christ was so grounded in the soul that
Shynochya that suddenly she put away fro her all the vanyte of ye world that
she used in pompous array /

And kyt away her here of her head: whereof she was woute be proud of / And
took upon her the habyte of Saint Domynyk and so was made a suster of
penance. And ever afterward she lived in prayers and medytacyons and in great
sharp penance Sone after came her suster Francysca and took upon her the same
abyte / and lived to gyder right deuoutely. Of this herd James or Jacob her
brother that was not ye same time in Seen when his sustren were turned / he
came to ye Cite ward with a young brother of his cursyng and thretnyng with a
great pride all tho that excyted his susters to that abyte. Seeing and cryeng
with a bold spyryte that he would tere away that abyte fro their back and
breng them to his hows there he dwelled To whom his younger brother the which
came with him said / trewely James if thou come to Seen / thou shall be turned
also / and be shryuen of thy sins / with that he cursed his brother bytterly
and said / that he had lever flee both freres and prestys then he would be
shryuen to any of hem all The child oftymes rehearsed his prophecyes / and as
often he cursed: So that at the last he entered in to the Cite as a wood man /
and forth he went to his faders hows thretnyng that he would do great horrible
things / but if his sustren specially Ethynoccyam would do away her abyte and
come home to him All this was not unknown to this holy maid / but she know
it never by creature on earth / but by god.

In the mean while his mother Rabes stylled and peased him / prayng him that he
would abide till the morrow: On the morrow she sent to this holy maids
confessor friar Thomas that he would wouchesauf come and speak with her sone
James And counseyll him for his soul health

He came and with him a felawe friar Bartholomew and spoke to him: But all
their speech as them seemed might not profit in him All that same time this
holy maid Katheryne prayed to our lord for his conuersyon / whiles friar
Bartholomew spak to him:

And then suddenly our lord touched Jamys heart to contrycyon / and he
said to friar Bartholomew that he was well apayed of his suster that she
should serve god: But also he prayed him of confession with great contrycyon /
that he might be shriue^ of his sins and serve god also: He was then so
perfytely shreuen That sum sins which he would never be know ne confessyd
to no man / he was confessyd to him:

So that with Inn a little time after of a wolf he was made a lamb / and of
a lion a whelpe: That all folk that knew him were amerueylled of his sodeyne
tornyng:

His mother Rabes was a meruaylled and all her meyne / and thanked our lord
for that special grace:

Friar Thomas and friar Bartholomew also ioyed in our lord and went for to
tell all this to this holy maid / the which was down / when they were
come to here hows they found her yet in rauyssheng / and her felawe was that
time in her chamber with her / As soon as she was cessyd of her rauyssheng /
and restoryd to her bodily wits / her felawe came down out of the chamber
from her and welcomed her confessor:

Then said her confessor to her felawe: We ben come for to tell Katheryne
that she should thank our lord god:

For James that is turned trewely to god / and is shreuen of all his sins
this morrow tide to friar Bartholomew: To whom said her felawe / right now
Katheryne told me the same that ye say: And when they were were come up to
katheryne she said to them with great sadness in this wise / Faders we been
much bound to thank our savior yt never dyspsed the prayer of his
seruauntis: For the same desire the which he enspyred them with: he fulfilled
in them / The fend wend he should have had away fro us our lytill sheep.
But our fader of mercy has byreiued away from him his pray: he wend to had
away from Christ Shynochia / But he has lost James that he held so strong in
his bonds. For so it happeth ever to him when he reyseth up his head of pride
against Crystis chosen /

Afterward that maid Shynochya ever continued in prayers and holy medytacions
to her last day. And with a great ghostely joy by diverse sekenes ye which
our lord gave her / She passes to our lord out of this world / Then her
suster francisca that lived but lytyl while after followed her in good living
and with a merry smylyng there she passed also to god out of this world:

Ferdermore the said James her brother within a little time after forsook
perfyghtly the world and was made a friar prechours and lived devoutly ever
after / All these things were wrought by the holy ghost and by his spouse
Katheryne granted his grace to all tho yt she prayed for /

Ouermore I shall tell you another merueylous thing that Master Reymound
bears record of him self / In the same Cite of Seen there was a great man
the which was called Nannes and he a wounder wordely wise man more enclynyng
to evil than to good / that man often times because of his great sotyll wit
he loved so much thereto that he made party in the same Cite and great
enstaunce between neyghbore and nyghbore / whereof came a great enmyte and preuy
morderyng the which came by him slyly and by his mayntynaunce / At the last
mean persons came between for to make peace / but he answered ever so wylyly
that he rought never whether there were peace or none as it seemed to them that
herd him / and always he was glad to make vnpeas that he might and to be
avengyd after his desire /

That herd this holy maid katheryne she desired to speak with him for to sece
that evil hatered but he fled her as soon as he knew that she came to him /
Right as the serpent would flee from him that should charyne him: At the last
an holy man the which was called Friar wyllyam of England a friar austyn he
spoke so to him that he graunt^ him that he would gladly speak with that holy maid and here her / But he said he would nothing do as she would counseylle
him /

So then he kep^ his promys and he went to the holy maids house the same
time that master Reymound was there / But that holy maid was not therein by
cause she was gone a little before to procure the health of souls: In the mean
while that master Reymound was therein / there came a messanger to him and said
that Nannes was at the door and would speak with katheryn whereof master
Reymound was glad for he knew well that the holy maid had often times desired
that /

And with that he went and welcomed him and told him that she was out / and
prayed him that he would not think long for she would come anon / And then
they went to this holy maids chapel when they had sytte a while there he
thought long and said to master Reymond. Thus I behete friar Wyllyam / that I
should come hyder and here this holy lady Katheryne speak / therefore sith she
is out and occupied / I may naught abide here wherefore I pray you excuse me to
her / for I have much thing to do / master Reymond was heavy here with that
she was so long / for to occupye the time till she came / he axed him of the
manner of pees the which he knew To whom this Nannes answered* Sire I shall
tell you the sothe / for to thou that been a pressed and a relygyous man / and to
this holy maid / of whom I here a great name of holiness. I shall not lie
but say the sothe. Therefore what that ever I say to you I am not in will to
do by your counseyll. Sothe it is that I am he the which that lets ye pees
by twene him and him and that pees and that pees. And yet it seemed by my dedys
that it am not I that let it by cause it is done by other / but I maynteyn
them pryuely there to / for if I allone would consent to have pees / al should be
well cessyd But I purpose in no wise for to consent thereto / wherefore it
needs not for to counseyll me and preche me / for I shall not consent in any
manner wise Loo now I have told you that I have hid from other / tarry me no
longer and hold you apayed / yet master Reymond prayed him to reherce it
again / for to occupye the time / and he would not / at the last by the
dysposycyon of god the holy maid was come Inn.

When that Nannes saw her / he was right sorry But master Reymond was glad
As soon as she saw that erthely man / she took him with an heavenly charity
and sat down to gydres / and axed him the cause of his coming. Then he
rehearsed to her all that ever he said to master Reymond with the last
negacyon. This holy maid began then to show him what peril he stood Inn
so that she touched him over all / but as a deef serpent he stoppyd the erys
of his heart that he would not here her counseylles / that considered this holy
maid anon. She sat still and turned Inward and prayed our lord in her heart
and axed his gracyous help When master Reymond aspyed how ghoostly she was
occupied for him. He occupied him with sum words hopyng in the mean while of
some help of our lord by her prayers / within a while aft Nannes said to them
both thus. Loo I will not be so unkind / but that I will do nigh all yt ever
ye will bid me / but somewhat I shall grant / and then will I goo fro you. I
have made four debatys which continued yet Of that oo debate I will give you
leave do wi^h all as ye will and cesse it as ye will / with that he roos up and
would have go out / and in the rysyng he said to him self thus O lord what
comfort may this be / yt I feel now in my soul of that word that I spak of
pees / and soon after he said more A a lord god what virtue and strength may
that be that holds me and drawed me now / I may not go hens / ne I may not
deny no thing O who is that / that constreyneth me now. O who is that / that
holds me now with this he wept sore and said I am over come and I may not
wythstonde it. Then he kneled down on his knees to the holy maid and said
with weeping chere.

Holy maid I shall do what ever thou bydde me do: Not only of this matter but
also of all other what that ever it be.

I know well now that ye devil has had me bound in his chain hyder to /
but now I shall do what ever ye counseyl me to do / counseyll my soul how it
may be deliuerd out of ye fendes pour I pray you. At these words the holy
maid turned to him and said. I thank god brother that thou have perceived
what peril thou stodest Inn of the mercy of our lord / whereof I spoke first
to the / but thou ^ettys^ little thereby And then I spak to our lord / and he
herd my prayers. Therefore now good brother do penance for thy sins by times
/ lest a sodeyne trybulacyon fall upon the Then anon with great contrycion
he was shryuen of master Rymond of all his sins / and afterward by help of
this holy maid he made pees with all folk / and also with god by counseyll of
master Reymond. But within a few days after he was take by the Justyce of
the Cite and put in a streyte prison / and it was a common saying yt he should
be behedyd. Then master Reymond herd that / he came to this holy maid with
a sorrowful che^e / and said Loo mother all the while Nannes served the fend /
he had no disease / but always ^speryte And after time now he is turned to god
/ all the world is against him where of I am a ferde by cause he is yette but a
young brau^che / lest he be all for broke by this tempest / and so fall in
despeyre. I pray you therefore pray for him to god / that he whom ye have
delivered from the deuelys pour by your prayers / help him also and defend
him from his adversaries Then she said to master Reymond why be ye sorry for
him for whom ye should be glad. Now be ye seker that our lord spares him
and will relesse him from endeles pain by that temporal pain.

First when he was in the world / the world loved that was his And now he is
passyd out of the world / the world begins to hate him. First our lord
reserved for him endeles pain / but now of his mercy he has changed his
endeles pain in to temporal pain And of his desperacyon be thou no thing
in doubt / for he that has delivered him of hell / will deliver him
gracyously out of this peril / and as she said so it was / For within a
while after he was delivered out of prison / though he had great loss of his
temporal goodys / where of this holy maid was no thing sorry / but was
ioyefull and said that our lord of his mercy has do away fro him the poison
yt he was poisoned with. And at the last he had so many trybulacyons / and his
devotion encrecyd so much that he gaf to this holy maid a fair paleys of his
under his letter and seal yt was two mile without the Cite. Of the which
paleys she should make a monastery of sustres of penance. Then this holy
maid by special license and auctoryte of her holy fader the pope Gregory the
xj made there a monasterye in the worship of our lady to all her ghostly
daughters and called the monasterye the monasterye of our lady. And Nannes that
man the which this holy maid converted was governed ghoostly by master
Reymond and lived after a blyssed life.

Abouen all these matters if I would reherce all the conuersyons of evil lyuers
/ all the roburacyons and the strengthes of seek folk All the comfortes of
desolate folk or them that were in trybulacyons / all the exortacyons of them
that were in ghoostly perellys / the which our lord has meruayllously
wrought by his spouse this holy made. I might make many great books. Who could
tell how many wretched sinful lyuers she has delivered out of the fendes
bondys /

How many obstynate folk she has brought again to their own knowleche. How
many she had made forsake and despised the world And how many tempted folk in
fonle sins she has delyuerd out of the fendes danger by her prayers and
doctrynes. Nevertheless ye shall say as saint Jerome said comendyng our lady
/ I might say that if all the membrys and lym^ys of my body were turned in to
tongues / they should not suffyce for to tell all the fruit of souls / that
this holy maid has purposed to heaven by the help of almighty god / master
Reymond bears this true record / that he saw a thousand or moo both of men
and wymmen coming down fro the mounteynes and other vyllages longyng to the
shyre of the Cite of Seen / coming for to see and here this holy maid as
though they had be called by an Inuysyble trompe / the which not only by
her words / but also by her lokyng were styred to compunccyon for to be
confessyd of all their sins with great contricyon / and so their went two
confessors of whom master Reymond was one as he seyth him self / and they
confessyd her sins with so great contrycion that each man might well know
that there was grace given of god in her hertes / and that was not onys ne
twyes but oftymes.

Wherefore the foresaid Pope Gregorye that was that time had so great joy /
and delight of the wynnyng of so many souls that he granted by bull to
master Reymond and to his felawes / that all thoo the which would come and
vysyte this holy maid / and after desyren for to be shreuen / they should here
them and assoylle them as much as the bishop of the dyocyes might do.
Therefore master Reymond bears record and seyth / that there came many
sinful wretches to him and to his felawes / the which were never shreuen a
fore of the sins / the which they were shreuen to him and to them.

And they stood often times fasting fro the morrow till even / by cause of great
concours of people / and yet they might not suffyce for to here all that would
be shryuen

All that time this holy maid prayed and thanked our lord ioyefully that the
fend had lost his prayer. There is no pen that can express the joy of
her heart that she had that time of wynnyng of souls. Thus much is rehearsed
in this chapter of the ghostly meruayllous things that our lord wrought by
his spouse. This holy maid Katheryne about the health of man's souls.

Now shall I tell you in the next chapter what god wrought for her about the
health of bodies / and so shall I make an end of the next chapter. The
wyttenesse that needs to be rehearsed in the end of this chapter / ben
rehearsed a fore in the same chapter / and that suffyceth enough.

Of sum miracles done in her life by her about the life and health of mennys
bodies. Capitulum viij
I Shall tell you maidens a wonder meruayllous thing. And yette it is light and
esye to them Enough / with whom is found none vnpossybylyte. Lapa this holy
maids mother was a womman of great symptenesse and Innocencye. Yet she had
for that time little affection to Inuysyble things. And therefore she was sore
aferde to dye and pass out of this world. She caught a bodily sykenes / and
it encreced day by day more and more. When this holy maid this understood. She
prayed to our lord deuoutely for her that he would wouchesauf to socour her
mother with health / that brought her forth and nouryshed her. She had an
answer anon from heaven that it was best for her for to pass now out of this
world / or then she have more aduersytees that been to come. As soon as she
wyste this / she went to her mother and said to her wyttely such sweet words.

Mother if our lord sweet Ihesu will call you to him out of this world /
dyspose you to be confourmyd to his blyssed will / and beth no thing sorry.

Then the mother desyryng not for to deye / prayed her daughter to pray for
her that our lord would wouchesauf to grant her bodily hele / and speak
no more to her of her death. This holy maid prayed then our lord hertely and
feruentely that he would wouchesauf take her naught out of this world in to the
time she knew that her will were more confourmed to his will.

Our lord granted her / her axynge and suffered her mother to be seek for a
time / and not for to draw to the passage of death. And then this holy maid
was made mean between god and her mother for to pray that one / and exhort
that other. Our lord she prayed that he would not take her against her will.

And her mother she exorted and admonysshed with sweet words that she should
confourme her and consent to the will of god. Nevertheless though in manner she
bowed our lord to her prayers yet she might not enclyne her mother will by her
exortacyons.

Then our lord spoke to his spouse Katheryne and said. Tell thy mother that
she has now no need to pass out of this world / but time shall come that she
shall desire for to deye / and then^e she shall not have it / and that was sothe.

Hit befyll that she lived in to a great age / and saw many aduersytres in her
days / as well of persons as of their goodys / in so much that she said
often times in heryng of many folk such words. Whether our lord Ihesu has
put a soul in my body / that it shall never be delivered thens So many
children and daughters great and small young and old ben deed / and I may not
deye

Now I shall cesse of this matter and proceed forth in the first matter that I
began Lapa this holy maids mother was of so hard heart that she would in no
wise dye ne by confessyd / ne think in no wise on her soul hele.

Then our lord for to appyre more meruayllously in his spouse Katheryne
denied in manner as it seemed his first grant. And suffered Lapa to draw fast
toward the death without confession When this holy maid perceived that / she
lift up her eyes to heaven with wypyng terys and said to our lord thus. A a
lord god ben thise thy behestys that thou have granted me / that none of my
faders household should perysshe / is this thy mercyable byheste that saydest my
mother should not pass hens against her will.

I see well now that she shall dye without sacramentys of holy church Therefore
I beseech the by all thy mercyes that thou suffer me not to be deceived / and
that I goo not hens a live unto the time thou haste yolde to me my mother
reuyued in soul and body.

These words and these meruayllous cause herd three wimmen of Seen that were
present.

When her mother as it seemed by syghte and felyng was deed / so that they were
about for to go home again to their howses leuyng Lapa there for deed / if it
had not ben that the holy maid prayed as she did / and therefore they abode the
longer. Of the manners of these wymmen I shall tell you afterward.

This holy maid continued long in prayers / at ye last our lord herd her
prayers gracyously / and quyckened the soul and the body again of Lapa / that
she lived afterward unto ye time she was four score year of age and nine with
great torment of heart for many aduersytres that she suffered as it was
prophesied to her before by her daughter this holy maid.

Of this miracle were witness one Katheryne and Angelyna sustres of penance /
and also Lysa this holy maids cosyn they were present when Lapa was leyde
forth for deed and herden how this holy maid prayed to our lord thus.

Lord ben these thy behestys that thou behote me as it is said before. Of the
remeynaunt of her age / when she was restoryd again to life / bare wyttenes
many one. Lo ye maidens here may ye know of what merit this holy maid was
with our lord Ihesu that delivered her faders soul out of purgatory / and
reduced her moders soul in to her body again meruayllously.

Another meruayllous thing shall I tell you. It happened that there was a common
pestylence of bocchys reygnyng in the Cite of Seen / so that it oppressyd
both men and wymmen / young and old to the death / that comynly they dyed
within two days or three at the ferthest / the which sekenes feryd many a man.

Then master Reymond went about to vysyte seek folk / and comforted them
in god no thing chargyng of the Infeccyon of that pestylence touching his
bodily death / so that he might win souls. When he had so vysyted them
for werynes that he had in going about / he restyd him in a church of our
lady / where to he had a great devotion / and namely for the person of the
same church was a blessed liver and well known with this holy maid Katheryne
/ the which person was called Sir Mathewe.

It befyll few days after that master Reymond went out by the morrow for to
vysyte seek folk as he was wont And as he came by the church of our lady for
devotion that he had to our lady in that place / and also for affection that
he had to the person sir Mathewe / he went for to look how he ferde.

Suddenly when he was entered in to the church / he saw sir Mathewe bear up in
to his chamber semynge as he had be deed by vyolence of that pestylence For
he had lost both color of his face and strength of his body / and also his
speech.

Then master Reymond axed of other about what him eyled. They answerde and
said / that the night before about one after mydnyght / he was up for to
vysyte a seek body And with Inn little time afterward he was take with the
pestylence Here of was master Rymond right sorye and followed him up to his
chamber as other did and then ne satte down by him.

Within a while after when he was laid in his bed / he recovered his
spyrytes again and called master Reymond to him prayeng him of confession /
and so was shryuen clean of his sins as he was often wont to do.

After time that he was assoylled master Reymound axed how it stood with him /
and he answered and said again / that it grieved him so sore in his grynde or in
the flank / that it seemed to him / his thygh would fall away / and not only
the thygh / but also ye head fares as though it were departed in four parties
/ by pain and ache that he suffered there Inn.

Then master Reymond touchyd and tastyd his pou^se and found well that he
had a passing fever Wherefore he had his menye that they should bear his water
to leches and so they did But master Reymound followed soon after to know
verayly what the leches would say. To whom the leche said thus.

This man is take with the pestylence / and therefore I dread me that the hows
of our lady shall want and lack a good person.

Then axed master Reymond / whether he might be help by any manner remedy
of medycynes / he said that he should assaye. But he had no great trust in
no medycynes by cause the sykenes was right grievous. Thus master Reymond
departed from him with great sorrow ever prayeng by the way to our lord in his
soul / that he would wouchesauf to save his bodily life Yet a while for his
example to many:

In the mean while this holy maid herd say that sir Mathewe was seek / whom
she loved tenderly for his virtuous living. Anon she went home to him / and
as soon as she saw him she cried to him and said.

Arise up sir Mathewe / arise up for shame / is it now time to lie a bed.

Suddenly then at her calling / the fever and the bocche went away fro him
as though he had never had hem / and then he roos up without any taryeng
goodly / so that in his rysyng he said smylyngly and ioyefully / that the
virtue of god restyd in that holy maid.

Then the holy maid went away and fled the preysyng of men. But as she
went out of the hows / the met with master Reymond. To whom master Reymond
said full sorowfully.

Mother whether thou will suffer this man to dye / that is so dear and
profitable to us. All be it that she wist well enough what she had to done /
yette she said to him of mekenes such words.

Fader what words be these / whether ye wene I am god / that may deliver men
fro death.

Then said master Reymond to her again with a great spyryte for sorrow
that he had of his death Say this to whom that thou lust / but to me tell no
such things that knows how our lord does with the. I know well that what
that ever thou axyste of god thou shalt have.

Then this holy maid bowed her head to him and smyled. And at last she
looked up with a glad chere upon him and said. Be of good chere fader / for he
shall not dye at this time.

With that was Master Reymound glad / he knew well that god had give her
great grace / and so he departed from her and went to sir Mathewe for to look
how he ferde. Whom he found syttyng in his bed / and with gretr joy
rehersyng the miracle of the holy maid.

To whom Master Reymound said in confortynge of him that the holy maid
told him.

Sir Matthew said then to master Reymond. What trow ye she has do / he said
he wist ne^ for she told him no word thereof. Sir Matthew with yt aroos up out
of his bed and sat down by master Reymound and told him all the hole
gladly how the holy maid was there and said to him as it is rehearsed before
Soon after sir Matthew ete and drank none seek mannis mete / but hole ma^nys
mete / and that was a great merueyle / he was mercy and glad that vnne the he
might speak a word that same day in the morrow / Of this miracle were
witness: one Friar Nychol that came with Master Reymound and other prestes
and clerks of the house of our glorious Lady glorious vyrgyn Mary xx. or there
about / But now I pray you maidens takes head that infydelyte off curyous
hertes dysceyue you not in this miracle / Sum will say to you perauenture
that it is none great merueyle though a man be helyd of such a common sekenes
as is the feueres and pestylence for all day such a thing happeth / To whom
it may be asked again what merueyle that was when our lord heled petre his
wyffes mother of ye fevers / al day it happeth that men ben delivered of the
fevers be it never so grievous: why is it than of petris wyffes mother rehearsed
for a miracles in the gospel. But now takes head ye curyous vntrowyng hertes
take heed whether it be not he the which heled this man Mathewe that heled
petris wyffes mother: In helyng of petre wyffes mother he commanded that her
fevers should goo fro her / and so it did anon without any taryeng* And she
then arose up and mynistred our lord at mete

Right so in this miracle it was the same lord that spak in the holy maids
breast the which heled petrys wyffes mother / and so sir mathewe was both off
the fruers and also of the pestylence / What was the cause trow you / trewely
for the mynystracion that he should show to our lord in time coming for
wynnyng of souls / so then the intent following is cause of the miracle that
goth before / and thereto he was made so perfyghtly hole that he ete forwyth
hole mete and mennys mete as thought he had not be seek before now I sithe I
have told you of the miracle done to the health off bodies. I shall tell you
a another by the help of god /

A lytyl beside the Cite of Seen there was a devout woman that was one of the
susters of penance of saint Domynyke the which herd and saw much off the
virtuous living of this holy maid / she drew much to her afterward and was
under the counsel of this holy maid / and did her reverence as to her mother
After it befyll on a day that this devout suster was on hye on a solier of her
house for certain things that she had to do And suddenly the solyer fill down
and the woman underneath * all the raftre treys brosed so her that she was
draw out half ded or soon after to be deed / At the last by the help of
god she was brought to bed and began to reuyue and felt that pain of her
heart brosour: and complained her sore with weeping and weylyng / Leches than
were sought to do the besynes for to hele her* but yet for all her lechecraf
she might not turn her in her bid without help of other: When ye holy maid
katheryn herd thereof / she had compassion in heart of the suster and came to
her and comforted her in penance and in her dysese / But when she perteyued
that her dysese was so passing pain to her

She touched the places of her body that were paynefull as though she would
anointed them with her hondes:

Of the which touching the suster was well apayed supposyng faithfully by the
mercy of god that it should be to her great ese / She had not so soon
touched her side but that she was all hole as though she had felt before none
pain / Then the seek suster prayed her that* she would touch the oder side
as she did ye side by cause the holy maid then supposed that it was ese to
her / She did so as she badde her and in the same wise her dysese went a way
in that place after her touching as it was in the other side: so then at the
last the holy maid touchyd over all her body there she felt dysese / and all
dysese was clean a voyded / At the last when she was all hole she turned her
about by her self wythouten any help that all might see verily by her tokens
that she was fully hole: Nevertheless yet she held her peace till tfe holy maid was a goo lest she should have troubled her mekenes if she had told
it her i^ presence / but afterward she told it both to leches and to
neighbors and said thus katheryne the daughter of Lapa has heled me by her
touching / All they had me rueyle thereof and thanked god that had give
such gracious virtues to the holy maid katheryne / For they wyste right well
that the holiness might not come but of god and therefore they thanked him / This
miracle Master Reymound knew by tellyng of other: But now I shall tell you of
anther yt master Reymound him self knew and saw it

In that time when the great pestylence continued in the Cite of Seen as it is
rehearsed before: there was an holy recluse in the Cite of Seen and was called
Scu^s that louyd the which was touched with that same pestylence: when this
holy maid perceived that she ordained that he should be brought to the house of
our glorious lady glorious vyrgyn mary the which was called also ye house of
mercy where she her self with her felawes vysyted him and ordained for althynge
that was needful for him in his sekenes and at the last she came to him her
self and told him preuyly in his ere and said thus / Fader dread you not for
thou shall not deye for this sickness at this time / but she would tell not
thing of this to Master Reymound and to her felawes the which prayed her to
pray for him that he should live / For it seemed to them that she was in doubt
off his life as well as they were / and therefore she ordained for him medycins
for to be heled by: wherefore Master Reymau^d and all her felawes were sorry by
cause all they louyd that holy man for his good living: Then at the last his
sekenes encresed more and more and drew fast to the death as it seemed: whereby
all that saw him supposed he should deye and prayed for the good passage of his
soul:

And also the holy man wend he should have deyed right anon / In that same
point of death this holy maid came and rouned in his ere and said to him ye
second time / fader dread you not for you shall not deye at this time for this
sekenes he understood her well all be it yt his wits were in party dystraut and
alienyd fro him for the greuousnes of the pain and he gave more credence to
her words then he did to his actual pain of death / and so it fill
afterward that the holy maids words o^came ye deeds of kind and nature /
Nevertheless he continued in such transite passing ye common time of other mani
days to gyder / but at ye last as ye spirit was in passing as it seemed /

The holy maid came and said now ye third time in the seek mannys ere thus

I charge the spyryte in the name of our lord Thesu Christ that thou pass not
/ Anon the spyryte resorted quycly again to the body / And then the holy man
took strength to him: and ros up and asked mete so within a little time he
was all hole and lived / Afterward that the holy maid was passyd out off this
world many years that holy man yt was called Scu^s both in name and in deed /
After time he was hole he told to Master Reymound and to other more what the
holy maid said to him in time of his sekenes preuyly in his ere / And he felt
the might of her virtuous words whereby the spyryte was called a gayn that was
in the point of passing

And he afermed it to all folk that it was none natural cause that restoryd
him again to his life but only the might of god I showed by his spouse katheryn
/ To whom folk gave credence by cause he lived in great virtue of holiness and
was known a famous man in the Cite of Seen by xxxvj year. to gyder without
any repreue in his living:

Ferthermore maidens I shall tell you of another miracle that this holy maid wrought in master Reymound After time that the great pestyle^ce was so
breme in the Cite of Seen as it is rehearsed a fore that all folk fled by
cause that it was so infectyf. So that men and wymmen deyed, without comfort
and counseyll and keeping master Reymou^de bythought him that he was bound to
love mennis soul castyng none peril for his one bodily death by enfection of
that pestylence purposed him to goo about the Cite and vyseted seek folk and
comforted them and did it in deed / Nevertheless by cause he was alone in
party in so great a Cite for to visyte and comfort the seek / that uneaths he
might have time or space for to ete and to rest. He was so sent after fro
one house to another /

Soon after in a night it befyll he took his rest and was wakyng at a certain
hour for to serve god: He felt a greuau^ce of a pestilence both in his grynde
or flancke: and for fere he durst not arise but lay still and by thought him
off the passage out of this world / he desired gretely that it had be day
that he might goo and speak with this holy maid katheryne or then he were
more seek. In the mean while he had a fever and the head ache as the manner
was off that pestylence sekenes so that he was gretely payned and tourmentyd /
But yet he said his matyns as he might: when it was day he called to him his
felawe and went to gyder as he might to the holy maids house and found her
not at home for she was out to vysyte a seek body /

In the mean while him thought she was so long and he so seek that he might
no thing do / but lay down there in a little bed / prayeng all tho that we
ren in the house that they should send for her as soon as they might / She was
sent after and came anon and perceived yt he was sore seek / she knyled down
before his bed and crossed him on the forhede with her hand: And then she
began to pray as she was wont to done in her soul / Master Reymound beheld
how she was rauysshed a fore him hoping of som^e synguler grate for the
prouffyte of his soul or of his body abode her long as him seemed / within a
half an hour afterward or there about he felt all his body sterid to
avomite: wening yt he should have cast. But yet was it not so / but him
thought that out of every* part of his body was pulled out with a manner of
vyolence sum manner of corrupcion / And so began to wexe better at ese than he
was / yet or than the holy maid was fully restoryd again to her bodily wits
he was all hole save a lytyl fevylnes bylefte in him / After time this holy
maid had purchased of our lord that grace of the health she se^yd of that
rauyshyng and badde her felawes should ordeyne sum mete for him / when he had
received mete of her holy hondes she badde him lie down and ^este a while he
did so as she badde him: And wha^ he awoke / he was as strong as though he
had not be seek / Then^e the holy maid said unto him / fader gooth and
labors now for the health of sowles thanketh almighty god that has
delivered you fro this parylle: he went forth to his custumably besynes and
thanked god that had give such virtue to his blyssyd maid / Such a like
miracle our lord wrought by this holy maid to Friar Bertylmewe in time of the
same pestylence / But yet that miracle was ye more by cause her long time was
oppssid in that sekenes than Master Reymou^d

And by cause it was in all wise like else / therefore I pass over and reherce
it not: But I would ye understood may dens that this holoy maid showed not
oonly the dyuyne miracle of curacion in time of pestylence but also in other
times / and yet not only in the Cite of Seen but also in other places But
therefore one I shall declare at this time whereby ye may understand all other
if ye take heed wytely thereto

It befyll soon after that the general pest^lence the which is rehearsed before
/ ye many folk both men and wymmen as well relygyous and seculer / But
specially certain mynchis of the Cy^^ of ^yse herd of the famous name of this
holy maid katheryn desyreden to see her and here her speak / And by cause it
was notlefull for them to goo out and seek her therefore they prayed her as
well by lettres as by messengers that she would vouches ^f to come to ^yse
seyeng to her that there she might win many a son le the which should be to
our lord great worship / Albe it that this holy maid eschewed always for
to go fer about the contre / yet she was so often prayed with so many
messengers or messages that she was almost constr^yned thereto by prayer of
lettres and messages: Then she had a recource to prayer as she was wont to
done and asked our lord mekely declaracion of that doubt that she stood in
and what she should do / sum off them that were counseyllers to her said
that it was best for her to goo: and som^e said nay: within a few days
afterward she had an answer of our lord as she beknewe afterward to master
^eymound that she should not tarry: but algatys she should goo to speak with his
seruauntys and his spouse dwelling in the same Cite of Pyse: Then as a t^ewe
obedyencer by leave of Master Reymound her confessor she went to Pyse whom
followed afterward Master Reymound with a certain of his bredren for to here
confessyons: For many there were that came to her wha^ they herd her speak so
^eruent words of love / were steryd thereby to contrycion / And le^t they
should be let fro true conuersacyo^ and fall again in to the fendes snares
after such co^puccion she would beidde them go to confession and be shryue
without any taryeng / And by cause her confession was often times delayed for
defaute of confessors / therefore often times she desired that she might have
confessors by her to whom she might send such repentance: And therefore
Master Reymound and his two felawes had power of the pope by bull for to
here and assoyle all tho that were endu^ed to confession by this holy maid:
Wha^ she came to Pyse she was received in a burgeys house that was called
Gerardus the which Gerad upon a day brought with hi^ a young man of xx year
of age all seek of the fevers to this holy maid besechinge her that she would
pray for his health for he told her that he was vexid. xviij / months to
gyders with the fevers so that it was none day but that he had it / And
thereto it was so mighty to him that it had brought him so low / and that is
well seen by his chekes and by his body: And^^ might never by none medecyn be
made hoole / Then the holy maid had great compassyon in heart of that
young man / she asked him how long it was a goo that he was shryue of his
sins and took penance / he said not many a year / therefore it is said she
that our lord has give the this ^oorge for thou have not purged thy soul by
holy confession so long time. Therefore sone goo forth anon to confession
and cast out that venim the which enfecteth all thy body: when he was
confessyd and ^ame to her again she put her holy hand upon his sholders and
said to him thus. Goo sone in pee^ of our lord ^hesu christ for it is his will
that thou be no more vexed with tho fevers as she said it was fro that time
forward he was not vexed therwyth. Within few days after he came again to the
holy maid / and thanked her of her curacion and said openly before a^ folk
that he had never the fevers sithe she a voyded it by the virtue of our lord /
^ff this bears wytnes Master Reymound for he saw that miracle: And other
witness there were ynow by Gerad and the childs mother and many other
afterward the young man puplychid that miracle by all ^^e contree such another
byfyll in the Cite of Seen / but much more* merueylous by cause the sikenes
was more perylous /

There was a suster of penance of saint Domynyke in the same ^yte off Seen
that was called Gemina the which loved well this holy maid: she had a sekenes
of her throat the which was called the s^ynce / by contynaunce of time the
sekenes encresyd so that it made her throat so straight that vnethe she might
draw her brethe* but almoost often times was strangelyd / Then she went to
this holy maid and prayed her as she might speak seyenge thus / mother I
shaldeye but ye help me / this holy maid had so great compassyon of her
that she took her holy hand and crossed her throat*

And anon without any taryenge the sekenes avoided: and so she that come with
great sorrow: went home with great gladness / And told it soon after to her
confessor /

But by cause sum what I have told you of curacions done to the body by this
holy maid to diverse persons therefore I shall tell you now of a great
notable miracle that our lord wrought ^i this blessed holy maid /

It befyll that this holy maid went in a time fro Pyse to Auyoun with whom
went two good devout young men that wrote the lettres that this holy Maid
would send: The one was called Neryus that afterward ^as a devout recluse.
And the other was called Stephene that was afterward a monk of the charterhous
/ And a good vyrtuous liver thereto / to the same ^yte of auyoun went als^
master Reymou^d It happed when they were entered in to the Cite of auyoun the
foresaid Neryus was seek with a merueylou^ sykenes in his bowellis that he might
have none rest / neither night ne day / But cried and wayled often times and
he might not lie in his bed but creped about on hondes and on feet and sought
rest / and yet might none find

This was told to the holy maid and she badde master Reymound send afleches
to help him: For other comfort would she none give master Reymou^d did so:
and there was none leche that might ese him but rather he was the more payned /
I trow for that end allone by cause our lord would work that myrarle in his
spouse katheryn / At the last leche said to master Reymou^d yt they might not
prouffyte in him / And therefore they had none trust in his lyffe /

When Master Reymound had told this to his company as they sate^ at the
mete Stephene the fellow of Neryus roos up with a great spyryte and went to the
holy maids chamber sytyng down on his knees and prayed her mekely that she
will not suffer his fellow Neryus to deye in such a strange contree:

To whom this holy maid answerde thus / sone why art thou heui thou sholdest
not be sorry for thy felawe / For our lord will reward him in bliss for his
pacyence in sufferyng of that sekenes / Then^e he said again / dear mother yett
here mine prayer at this time and help him for I wot well ye may and ye will /
Then she said well sone I see well that thou art not in will to conform the
to the will of god as I have told the / Therefore sithe I see that thou art so
tourmentyd for him / come to me to morrow when I go to here mass and be
houselyd and reduce this matter to mine mind / And I shall send up thyn prayer
to god / And thou shall pray for me that I may be herd Then stephen was
well apayed with this vyheste^erly / on the morrow / he met with this holy
maid going for to here mass / As Soon as he aspyed her / he fyldoune on his
knees and prayed her that she would not forgete him of that he spoke to her the
day before.

After time when she was ho^elyd she was rauysshed from her bodily wits and
prayed our lord for that seek man:

Soon after she was restoryd again to her bodily wits and came to the same
Stephene smylyng the which abode her there of an answer and said unto him
thus: Sone thou have the grace that thou have asked / Then he asked her
whether Neryus should be deliuerd of his sekenes She said ye: with that he went
gladly to his felawe and badde him be of good there for he shall be hole / and
so he was full tendaunt about for to recover him / In time of his
mynystracion about hi^ it happed the same Stephene to be seek and lay down in
his bed of a passing fever / When the holy maid knew that she had great
sowwe and went to him and asked him what sekenes he had: And she perceived by
touching of his ponse that he was vexed with a strong fever: Anon with a
great fervor o^^ spyryte she said thus / I charge the fever by the virtue of
obedyence that tho^ goo out of this man / then went the fever a way and he
wos up all hole with out any taryeng / and thanked our lord of his great
grace that he showed to his spouse Katheryne. Another notable miracle I shall
tell you of a suster of penance / the which was called Johan dwelling in the
Cite of Seen In a time that our holy fader pope Gregory that lived that time
was in the cite of Seen at the byddyng of our holy fader Gregorye / this holy
maid was sent to Florence to make pees between him and his rebel children of
florence / ye which mat is to long to tell here But this matter shall hau^ a
chapter by hit self afterward by ye help of god And when she was come to
Florence / and with her a felawe of here is / the which was called Johan / for
to trete for the pees between our our holy fader / and that rebel people. The
people set little by her words / but s^laundred her meruayllously and set
her at naught. Then ne she was counseylled for to withdraw her a while unto
the time that they were cessyd of their malice. She did so / but yet she said /
that she would never pass out of that cite in to the time they were accorded /
and pees were cried thorugh out all the cite of Florence / and as she said so
it was. Then she went a side and was lodgyd a little beside the cite / where
suddenly her suster Johan was seek in her foot / so that her foot was all
forswo^land there with for pain of her foot / she had a great ^eruent axes /
and so she was in double wise tormented that she might not goo with her. Thy^
holy maid was heavy thereof and would in no wy^e leave her behind / le^t
s^launder should spryng

She prayed to our lord for help / that he would wouche^auf mercyably to help
her fel^we / all the while that she prayed her suster was a sleep And when she
awoke she was all hole as though she had I had no sykenes. Anon she arose up
and went with this holy maid as quykly as ever she did before. Of this miracle
many one thanked our lord that saw it / the which had wrought so gracyously
by his spouse Katheryne. Yette shall I tell you another meruayllous thing that
our lord wrought by her in the cite of Tholetane. When this holy maid was
entered in to the Cite of Tholetane / she took her Inn / and anon she went in
to her chamber as she was wont to do In to ye which master Reymond was come
on the popes message. Suddenly then he herd in the stretys of the Cite of
wymmen / that an holy womma^ was come and entered in to the Cite Then ne soon
after came men / and after wymmen to her Inn and axed where this holy maid
was. They of the Inn might not hyde her / but they suffered wymmen only to goo
in to her and speak with her.

Then there was one of the wommen that had a little child / whose whombe was
meruayllously swolle. And they prayed this holy maid that she would take that
child in her arms / at the beginning she refused it / by cause of vayn glory
/ but at the ^ast she was overcome by pity / and did as they had her / as soon
as she took that child in her hondes / anon ye child delivered from him
much wind / so that at last his belly aswagyd / and was as small as ever it
was / and so the child was hole. All be it that master Reymond saw not this
miracle / yet there was so open speech thereof in the Cite of Tholetane yt it
came to the bysshopys ere / and sent after master Reymond and prayed him that
he might speak with ye holy maid / for the child was neuewe to a vycary of
his. And than this holy maid came and spoke with the bishop of many virtuous
matters. Many moomeruayls our lord wrought by this holy maid that been not
written in this book.

But these few I have written to you maidens by cause that ye shall the sonner
give credence that our lord Jhesu Christ dwelled in this holy maidens soul /
the which principally wrought all these meruayllous werkys / wytnes of tho
matters ye which ben reherced in this chapter ben reherced before in tho places
where these my racles were showed / and thus ends this chapter.

Of miracles wrought by this holy maid a boute the delyueraunce of them which
were encombred and vexyd with fendes. Capitulum lx
Owre lord all mighty Ihesu cessyd not to show outward ye Fertue that he gave
Inward to his spouse Katheryne by many meruayllous works. The virtue therefore
of our lord Ihesu christ angmented so myghtly in the breast of this holy maid /
that not only it was showed to seek bodies as it is reherced before / but also
it was showed in voydyng of wicked spyrytes as it shall be declared in this
chapter by the help of god. There was in the Cite of Seen a man / the which
was called mychael that used the craft of writing / when he was passed in years
of age by consent of his wife / he was in purpose to leave ye world / and serve
our lord more specially then he was wont. And also for to make two daughters
of his mynchyns in a monasterye in the same Cite of Seen endowed in worship of
saint Johan the Enange list and so his list was fulfilled. And at the last by a
pryue dome of god / one of his doughts the which was made a mine then that was
called Laurencyana of vill year of age or there about / was vexed with a fend
so yt all the monasterye was vnquyeted by her vexacyon. And at ye last by common
assent they sent after her fader and delivered again his daughter / for they
would no more have her in the monasterye as long as she was so vexed.

When she was take out of the monasterye / the fend spak within her by ye
childys mouth many wondre things and all in latin words / so many herd
questyo^s and there to pupplysshed many pryue sins in sclaunder of many folk
/ by ye which it might well be understand yt he was no good spyryte Of this
vexacyon her fader and mother and other of her friends were right sorry / and
went about to diverse relyques of sentes for to seek help and grace that her
daughter might be delyuerd of that spirit And specially they trusted gretely
in the relyques of saint Ambrose the which was a friar prechour / to whom our
lord granted a synguler gift / to put away wicked spyrytes / so that his
cope if it had be laid upon any creature that had be vexed with a wicked
spirit it should be avoided / where fore the same child was brought to the
friar prechours and leyde upon a tomb of saint ambrose / and his clothes were
leyde to the child / and the fader and the mod prayed in the mean whyl the
help of god and of ye sent yt the child might be socourre. But yet for that
time were they not herd. Not for no sin that ever they did But I trow be
cause yt the syguler remedies was reserved to this holy maid. Then was it
counseylled to the fad and mod for to present her daughter to Pratheryne the
holy maid / they sent to ye holy maid prayenge her yt she would help their
daughter. And she sent ageyn answer and said / that often times defayled and
departed a sonder and my soul was utterly delivered out of the body
Nevertheless it was but a little time and that was my sorrow. Then ne
eftesones master Reymond axed her how long time her soul was out of the body.
She said as they that kept her and were about to have beryed her four hours
or then she reuyued ageyn Yet he axed her what she saw for that time / and
why came the soul again to the body she answered thus Fader that time my soul
saw and understood joy of blessed sowles / and peynes of sinners. And as mine
mind would suffer me and words would suffyce to express them / I shall tell
you. My soul saw the divine essen cyall being of god / and that is the cause
why I am so loathe and impatient to live in this world / and had not be the
love of him and the love of christian people / for which my soul was restoryd
to the body again / I should had defaylled and dyed for sorrow. The highest
comfort that I have is when I suffer any disease / for that I have the perfyte
vysyon of god / therefore trybulacyons ben not heuysom to me / but comfortable
as ye may know / and other that been conuersaunt with me I saw also the peynes
of dampened sowles / and peynes of sowles that been in purgatory / the which I
can not express perfytely with no manner of words. For if wretched sinners
saw the least pain that is there / they had lever chese bodily death an
hundred times if it were possible / then for to suffer o day the least pain
that is there. But specially I saw hem ponysshed syngulerly that had sinned in
matrymony / the which had not kept hem to gyder honestly as they should do
/ but followed the dylectacions of their lustys

Of this master Reymond her confessor axed her why that sin in special was
more grievously punysshed then o there sins / sith it so is that it is not
