the most grievous sin She said for this skylle. For they had not so great
conscience of that sin ne so great contrycyon as they had of other sins /
but rather they offended in that sin then in any other That sin the
which a sinner charge not for to remove / by penance is a great sin be it
never so little.

Then this holy maid proceeded forth in her matter and said thus also. Fader
wha^ne I had seen all these joys and these peynes wenyng my self that I had
fully be delivered out of this body.

Our lord said to me / see thou not daughter what joy they lack and what
pain they have that offenden me. Torn ageyn therefore to thy body and tell to
the people their error and their peril. And with that word I was astonyed for
to torn again to the body and sore aferde.

Then our ford said to me / it is profit to mennys souls that thou torn
again / and thou shalt not live the life that thou have lived a fore ne keep
the so lytarie allone in chamber / but thou shalt goo a broad to win sowles
/ I shall ever be with the / and goo with the both going and coming. Thou
shalt bear the worship of my name and of ghoostly doctrine before great and
small and lay people and clerkys and a fore Relygyous folk also I shall give
the both mouth and wit for to speak that none may wythstande the. I shall
also bring the before bysshoppys and curates of sowles for to confound there
pride. Whiles our lord spak these words suddenly my soul was restored again
to my body.

And when I perceived that I had great sowwe / that I wept three days
(...) end of this chapite / It needs not for to reherce the witnesses of
every act that was done in this chapter / for it is made mention of forthwyth
at every act i^ the same chapter /

Of miracles which our lord wrought by this holy maid in breed / wine.
herbs* and other things that had none lyff: Capitulum xj
BY cause at the beginning wha^ Adam was made our lord ordained a rewle to all
tho that obeye^ to him perfyghtly / that all things should obey to them.
Therefore maidens in this next chapter I shall tell you how to this holy maid
obeyden all creatures by cause she obeyed perfyghtly to god: In the time that
this holy maid lived in the Cite of Seen: it befyll yt there was a wedowe a
young woman called alixe the which with a great favor drew to this holy
maid / so that she thought she had so great affectyon ^o her* that as her
seemed she might not live without her: And therefore she took the habit of the
susters of penance and for soke her own house / And hired her an hows by side
the holy maids hows that she might the more often be conuersaunt with her.
When she had do thus the holy maid was often times in her house with her /
and fled for a time her faders house / It happed afterward in ye same year
that in the Cite of Seen there was a great sharsyte of breed corn so ye
stynkyng whete was drawn out of the earth and out of dyches the which was
bought of Cytezynes of the same Cite as that time for good where by cause there
might none other begoten for none price / Of the which stynkyng whete / Alyxe
the sorsayde wedowe must needs be ye / or else she should be without br^d /
Neu^rtheles in as much as it was nyghe ye time of herwest her old whete was
failed and brought to the marcat Alixe wist thereof that new whete was comen
she purpose to cast away the old s^ynkyng whete and beye new: but because
the hole Maid was in her house she would nothing do without counseyll of her
wherefore she opened her purpos to her semyng thus / mother sithe our lord heth
do mercy with us in syndyng of new whete I am in will to throw mine old
s^inkyng whete* To whom this holy maid answered thus / if ye will not ete of
that old corn / give it else to pour folk yt haven none* Alixe said than yt
she should have great conscitence for to give the pour folk so stynkyng
whete she had lever for to give them of the best whete

Then this holy maid badde her ordeyne water and bring to her that stinkyng
whete that she purposed to cast away for she said that she would make bread
thereof for pour folk / as she said so it was / First she made her dowe and
after she molded loves of that little qua^tyte of whete: And it encresyd so
plentuously in the moldyng that both Alyxe and her servant weren gretely
astonyed that sagen such multyplycacio^ of loves For as them thought so many
loves might not be made of such four little quantyte of whete as this holy maid made and set forth for to be bake / and also there was none stynche of
tho loves as it was of the other that were made of the same whete before / when
they were bake they were set fourth on ye table for to be eten: and in ye
etyng there was found none bitterness no stynche / but as they said that eten
thereof / they eten never betyr bread. This Alexe sent for her confessonr and he
came with certain of his brethren for to see* that miracle and like as it was
said to him in quantyte encresyng and in qualyte right well amendyd: To these
two my^acles / the third was addyd to and that was this / the breed was
largely given to pour folk and to other yt would ete thereof and yet was it
never ye less in nombre / but always was it found ynow in ye breed hutche:
were not this trewely three fair miracles / for first she put away the stynche
of that corn: and afterward encresyd the loves in the muldyng / and at the
last she multyplyed ye loves in etyng of the breed: in so much that they
might uneath be distribued by many wekes togyders neended / so yt xx year
after or moo there were sum yt kept of that breed for a relyke:

Then master Reymound her confessor asked her how ye miracle was done / She
answered and said that she had so great zele or love to pour folk lest they
should spylle for defaulte and so tender love to our lord lest his gift should
be despised that she went with a great fervor for to make breed of that
stynkyng whete:

And then our blessed glorious lady glorious virgyn Mary with a multitude of
angelis stood by her and help her to molde / by virtue of her holy glorious
hondes she trowed that the loves encresed / for tho loves that our glorious
Lady glorious vyrgyn Mary molded / she delyuerd to this holy maid / And she to
Alixe and to her servant for to be put in to the oven: what marvel is it
maidens though tho loves were sweet sithe the holy glorious hondes of our
blessed glorious lady gloryons virgin Mary molded them / consydereth therforre
good maidens and takes good heed of what merit this holy maid was to whom
vouchesaf our blessed glorious lady glorious vyrgyn mary stand by her and
help her in that miracle for to make us understand that right as bodily
lyuelode encresed in that holy maidens hondes / Right so ghostely liuelode
should encrese by her blessed exortacion:

Now sithe I have begone of breed multyplyed by miracle therefore I shall
continue forth in such in such in such a like miracle was done in the last
end of her lyff when she lived here in earth: Of the which miracle were
witnesses lysa her cosyn and a suster of penance the which was called Johan
for both they were with her when she was sent after by our holy fader pope
vrbane the vj to the court of Rome / And when she was come to the Cite she
r^sted there with a certain nombre of her ghoostely children that she had
noryssched in virtue the which followed her fro the parties of Tuskan in manner
against this holy maids will / som^e for prechyng of ghostely grace of our
holy fader / and sum for pilgrimage and visitacions of saints the which
desired to go specially in this holy Maids company by cause they might be
fed with the swetnesse of her blessed conversation /

Then this holy maid had made an ordinance among them that they should
not have about them neither gold ne silver. But oonly they should live of
pour alms / And that they should be herbourd in an hospytall /

And also the wymmen eueryche off them a weke should mynys^re lyflod such as
they had received of alms to all^ her felawes that other myghten be
occupied in the mean while in prayers / and in holy contemplacyons and about
their pylgrymages / wherefore they were come to the Cite When this ordinance
was made / soon after it happed that this Johan / the which is reherced before
mynystred to other as for her weke. In whose weke it befyll casuelly that she
lacked bread when her felawes should go to mete / and then badde this holy
maid here before / that when she lackyd bread she should warn her over even
that she might goo and make sum ordinance. But Johan had forgete that / when
her felawes were come to mete Johan would have set bread before them / and she
found no more but a cantell that would uneath se^ue four to their mete / and
there were in nombre of persons xvj Then Johan went to this holy maid and
knowleched her negligence all sorry and shamefast / seyeng that there was no
bread but a little that uneaths would suffyse to four / each of them to
resteyne a little. To whom this holy maid said A suster god for give it you /
why have ye so neglygently brought us to this last need / might ye not have
warned me as I bad you / well well bid gods servants go sytte down

Then said the mynyster that there was but a little bread / yet bid them
sytte down said this holy maid to her / and serve them with that little / and
bydde them begin with that little till that god ordeyne more. After these
words the holy maid prayed while they et^. Johan fulfilled her byddyng and
divided to every man a little / and they as hongry folk and gredy by long
fasting ete fast / wenyng that they should no more mete have. And also the
suposed that that little bread should soon be do But always they had ete
enough / and yet the bread might not defaylled And then they axed what the
holy maid did / it was told that she prayed Then they said all by virtue of
her prayer our lord fed them as he fed five thousand men with five louys /
and so they thanked god. When they had all ete / yet there was such plente
left that pour folk had enough.

Now yette shall I tell you of another miracle that master Reymond bears
record of / the which was done after time that this holy maid was passed out
of this world in to the bliss of heaven. In a time hit happed master Reymond
by counseyll of the Pryour of the freres and the covent / would do sum
solemn reverence to the head of Saint Katheryne this blyssed virgyne / after
time that it was translated out of the Cite of Rome to the freres that dwelled
at Seen. He set a day and bad to mete all her ghostely children that she had
nourysshed in virtue. In the which day the freres were fully auysed to give
her a solemn reverence / and also to feed that day all her ghoostly children.
When the day was comen and the solenpne was done. The friar that kept the
botrye of the covent looked what bread he had for the Covent / and for the
gestys / and he found scarsely enough for half the Covent And then were
there in Covent fyfty or there about and of gestys twenty / when the Pryour
herd here of he was sorry. Nevertheless yet he served the gestyn first with
that little / and then the Covent with a little quantyte among them all / and
yet belefte enough So then eueryche of the Covent and of the gestys had
plenteuously enough / of that uneath as them seemed that little nombre of louys
might had suffysed fyfe a fore. When they had all eten / the Pryour and the
Covent came thither there master Reymond satte with the ghoostly children of
that holy maid Saint Katheryne / and rehearsed a fore them all that miracle.
Then said master Reymond these words. Loo friends this holy maid Saint
Katheryne in the day of her solempnyte will not leave us without sum miracle /
with whom she was so famylyer whiles she lived in earth. Often times when she
was with us living in this life she showed this miracle among us And therefore
for to show us that she now accepts our obseruaunce this day done to
gods worship and to herys / she had showed the same miracle eftesonys after
her passing / wherefore yield we thankyng te almighty god. Yet furthermore our
lord showed meruayllous things by his spouse Katheryn in vnlyfely things / as
in flowers where in she had often times great delight by cause she florysshed
in virtue her self. And in other vessels of household that were lost and
destruyed and of thoo meruayllous things I shall tell you.

This holy maid was sum time in the Cite of pyse / herborowed in a worthy
man's hows of the same Cite / the which man loved well this holy maid.

After time she was there a while / she was gretely feblyd in body by often
excess of spyryt in rauyshyng / so that as it seemed master Reymond and other
moo that saw her. She was brought nigh to ye death / wherefore master Reymond
was fore aferde lest she should have dyed / he bethought him what remedy he
might ordeyne for to restore her to longer life / and he wist never what he
might ordeyne for her as for eggs and wine / and also other letuaryes he knew
well that she might not ete. Then he came to her and prayed her that she
would receive a little suker in her water that she drynketh / to whom she
answered thus. Fader I see well that ye will take away fro me that little life /
the which is left in me by such sweet drynkes / for I do you well to wete
that all sweet thingi^ to me dedly Then master Reymond and the souerenys of
the hows bethought hem to gydres what remedy they might ordeyne against her
feblynes At the last it came to master Reymond mind that he had see that
often times feeble folk had be wesshen / sum time with vernage about the
temples in the pouses of the body / and so were restored of strength and
greatly comforted Then master Reymond said to the souereyne of the house
thus. Sir sethe it is so that we may not put no comfortable remedy within
her body / let us* use sum remedy without on her body. Then said the
sovereign of the hows / that he had a little beside his hows a neighbor that
had a vessel of vernage / to whom he said / he would send to for to have
a botell full thereof / for he knew well that he should have it full gladly. A
messenger was sent to him / and told him how this holy maid was feeble /
wherefore he prayed in his maystrys behalf that he would wouchesauf to send her
a botell of vernage. To whom the neighbor answered thus that he would send
him all ready / but certain he said his vessel was emptyd / and therefore he
prayed him to hold him excused / for I wot well in all my hows is no drope of
wine / and that I am right sorry fore. Nevertheless to be seker come and see /
and then bear witness of the troth to my friend as thou see.

Then forthwyth he took the messenger with him all against the messengers
will / and brought him to his wine seler / and showed him that same vessel of
vernage / the which vessel seemed by outward tokenys that it was void many
day before / yet nevertheless the good man did more for to see the truth that
it was void / he drew out the spygot / that was in the vessel / and drew it
out in his presence / that he should see that there was no wine Inn. As soon
as he had done so / the vernage came out and ran upon the ground
plentuously / he was sore astonyed and stopped the vessel again / and called
all his meyne / and axed of them whether they had put any* wine of vernage
in that vessel. All they said nay / they knew no wine there in three monthys
a fore and more. And it had be a great meruayll that without them any lyquor
had be put there Inn.

This was af^rward notefyed to the neghboures about / and all they said it
was a miracle as it was The messenger came again with a great meruayll
gladdenes bryngyng with him a botell of vernage / and told all the miracle as
it was / so that all thoo that herd it thanked our lord that wrought such a
miracle in his holy maid Katheryne / and many one aftward when this holy maid
was hole / came for to see her / seyeng with great meruaylle such words / how
may this be that drynketh no wine by miracle. By such words of the people /
this holy maid caught great sorrow in her heart as she knowleched afterward to
master Reymond. And with such sorrow and waylyng / she prayed to our lord in
her soul more then in her mouth seyeng such words: A good lord why
suffrest thou me to be so tormented in heart that I shall be to all folk shame
and reprove. All other servants of thine may live among the people save I
allone. O good lord who axed of thy myldenes wine. I by Inspyracyon of thy
grace have kept me fro wine long time And now I am made to all people for wine
in s^orne and reprove / I pray the lord for thy great pity / make that wine
for to vanysshe away / that this same which is deuulgyd among men now
cesse. Our lord of his mercy herd her prayer and made the vessel of wine to
decrece / so that suddenly there it seemed full to all men's drynkyng the which
drank thereof of devotion by cause of the miracle it was decrecyd to the lies /
and so all tho that praised it before for miracle / held there pe^s afterward
for shame* And master Reymond and other moo of her ghoostly children were
ashamed of their great praysyng before. But the holy maid was Jocunde and
glad thankyng our lord her spouse that had delivered her of such open
praysyng of men.

Now I pray you maidens takes he de how our lord kept this holy maid from
vain glory / and set her in a perfyte ground of meekness by these two
miracles. By the first he gave her matter to worship him that wrought that
miracle without her wetyng in that / that he filled ye vessel of wine. By the
secounde he gave her matter to follow him in mekenes / in puttyng away of vain
glory / the which was put upon her. By the first our lord showed what
virtue of miracle she was endowed with By the secounde he showed what wisdom
she was fulfilled with. For there that mekenes is / there is wysdom.
Nevertheless yet the secou^de miracle in emptyng of the vessel was gretter
then the first in fyllyng of the vessel / and that seemed well by a
simylytude that Saint Gregorye makyth in his dyaloges betwyne the virtue of
pacyence and showing of miracles / whether he seyth that the virtue of pacyence
passes showing of myraclee. Why then may not the virtue of true mekenes /
the which is never without wysdom pass with out any comparyson showing of
miracles / the which come as well by pride as by mekenes. A bestely man may in
no wise perceive this / and that is no meruaylle. For Saint Poule said that
prudence of the flesh is in no wise subject to god. Loo maidens now have I
told you what miracles our lord showed by his spouse Katheryne in vnlyfly
creatures / and thus I make an end of this chapter The witness of this
chapter also ben expressyd before with Inn this chapter there that the
miracles ben declared.

Of the often receyuyng of the holy sacrament of the altar / and of the
meruaylles which our lord did to her touching the holy sacrament / and other
relyques of saints. Capitulum xij
IT was known to all that knew this holy maid while she lived in earth / what
excellent love she had in reverence and devotion about the worshypfull
sacrament of the aultre.

Our lord his flesh and his blood so that for the often receyuyng thereof /
hit was a common seyeng among the people that Katheryne the holy maid was
houselyd every day and lived there by allone without any bodily mete. And all be
it that they said not always truth / yet I suppose they told it mekely
gyuynge honor to god that ever apperyth meruaylous to his chosen Nevertheless
be cause she received it so often / all be it that it were not every day / yet
there were sum that grutched with all / against whom may be brought wytnes
enough of holy faders that they did the same. But first I shall tell you what
the use was of holy church in old time. Saint Denis seyth in a book that he
made de ecclesiastica Jerarchia / that in the beginning of holy church / the
feruoure of the holy ghoost was so haboundaunt in the hertes of feythfull
creatures both men and wo^men / that they received the sacrament of the
altar every day Furthermore the doctrine of holy church techeth this / that
every feythfull man is bound in no dedely sin if he have actuell devotion /
it is not only lefull for him / but also merytorye for to receive that
excellent worshypfull sacrament Whoo then durst forbede such a feythfull
person and such an holy liver in any manner wise for to win so often great
mede in receyuyn^ of that worshypfull sacrament. Trewely I doubt not thereof /
but that such a creature had great wrong if it be denied when it is mekely
vxed. But if they would say utterly / that it is not lefull to no creature be
he never so feythfull / ne never so perfyte ne deuote for to receive that
blyssed sacrament often. To this I shall tell you what answer this holy maid
gave to a bishop in presence of master Reymond that said these words
aforsayd to her. Alledgyng for him the words of Saint Austyn where he seyth
thus. Every day for to receive the sacrament of the altar another I praise ne
blame it* to this obyeccyon answerde this holy maid in this wise to the
bishop. Fader if Saint Austyn blame it not. Ye alled ge that holy doctor
against your self.

Ouermore now shall I tell you what Saint Thomas A^uyne seyth of this doubt /
whether it be spedefull to a christian man often times or every day for to receive
the sacrament of the altar. He answers thus thereto / that often receyuyng of
that blyssed sacrament / encrecyth the devotion of him that receives it / but
it lessyth other whiles his reverence that he should have to that blyssed
sacrament.

Therefore every feythfull Christian man should have both reverence and devotion
to that blyssed sacrament And when he feyleth that his reverence is lessened
by often receyuyng of that blyssed sacrament / he should absteyne a while /
that he might go thereto afterward with more reverence. And if he feel his
reverence ever hole and never lessened / but (...) encrecyd with devotion / as
o^ ever he receives it. Then he may sekerly receive it. For truly without
any doubt such a soul well dyspesed wynneth much mede in the receyuyng of
that blyssed sacrament. This holsom doctrine of this devout and holy doctoure
Saint Thomas kept this holy maid Katheryne For often time she received that
blyssed sacrament. And sum time she absteyned her there fro. All be it that
she had ever desire to be knytte to her spouse by medytacyon of the blyssed
sacrament / for the brennyng charity where by she was draw to him / in so
much other while she desired to be houseled.

That but she had received that day when she desired that blyssed sacrament
she should have a passion of syknes in her body / as though she had be vexyd
long time before with a contynuell sekenes of fever / and all that sykenes of
the body came fro the passion of the soul. Many times she was thus vexed
when she was let from houselyng / other while by the Pryoure of the freres
/ and other while by the Pryoresse of their order of her susters. Nevertheless
by cause she should not be let / our holy fader the pope Gregorye the xj for
her more comfort granted her by bull that what priest h^rde her confession
might housell her in what place that he would say mass without any leave of
any souereyne.

Of one meruayllous thing now shall I tell you yt befyll to master Reymond
this holy maids confessor. In a time when master Reymond came from Auyon to
the Cite of Seen / and thought to look how this holy maid ferde / he entered
in to her house about none days and found her in her oratorye. And this was
on Saint Markys day the Euangelyst / as soon as she saw him she rose against
him and said to him these words. O would god fadre ye wist how hongry my soul
is* Then master Reymond answered her / for he wist well enough what she
mente. And said mother it is now all most paste time of syngyng / and I am so
weary that uneath I may dyspose me to sing With that she held her pees a
little while. And soon after she brack out again the same words and said /
she was sore an hongred.

Then master Reymond went to mass in her own chapel that she had by
license of the pope / and said mass of Saint Mark. And when he had used he
turned for to give this maid general absolucyon / as the manner of holy
church axeth. He saw her face like the face of an angel sendyng out bemys of
bryghtnesse / in so much that he meruaylled and said in him self to ou^e lord
thus. This is not Katheryns face. But certain lord this is thy dear spouse /
with that he turned him to the altar / and said this words to our lord in
his soul. Come lord to thy spouse / anon as he had said that in his thought
suddenly with the same thought / the oste rose up him self and came to his
hondes

Another meruayllous thing of this blyssed sacrament I shall tell you / that
befyll to the same master Reymond. He was in a time in the Cite of Seen for
certain things that he had to done / and as soon as he had done / he
went for to speak with this holy maid and found her syke of a sykenes in her
side the which was called Ilica passio / and of other gret^ infyrmytees of her
body / de syryng that same day to be houseled if her sykenes had be cessyd.
And after time master. Reymond had commyned with her of the great excellence
of the blyssed sacrament^ of the altar / he went home to his Covent for to say
mass And as he made him ready to masseward / this holy maid sent to him by a
felawe of here is / and prayed him to abide a while / for she would be houseled
that day when her sykenesse were passyd away from her. He did so and abode her
leysyr till it was about none time / this holy maid was esyd and came to
church for to be houselyd. But her felawes considered that the time was late
for to be houseled / then by cause she had it in custom for to abide
afterward three hours or four to gyders in rauysshynge or more So that the
church doors most all that time stooden open / of the which custom many of
the freres grutcheden / therefore they counseylled her not for to be houseled
for grutchyng of sum of the freres. To the which counseyll this holy maid
mekely and obedyently conc^tyd

But for her great desire that she had to that blyssed sacrament / and might
not receive it she prayed our lord deuoutely in the ferrest place of the
church / unknowing to master Reymond that she was come / and there she prayed
in this wise. Lord Thesu endeles mercy as thou have give me gracyously this
desire. So I beseech the perfou^me it by thyself / sith I may not perform my
desire by no priest. Then almighty god that never despyseth the desire of
his servants / herd his spouse Katheryne not only mercyably. But also
meruayllously as I shall tell you. When she had comfort of our forde / she
sent to master Reymond by one of her susters and prayed him to goo to mass
when it lyked him / for she might not be houselyd that day.

Then he went to mass supposyng that she had be at home at her hows / and
not in the church. And when he had sacred / and would make the fraccyon a
fore Agnus dei in three partys as holy church has ordained. Meruayllously as
he wend to have made iij partycles / he found four partycles.

And that fourth partycle skypped above the Chaleys and come down be it self
/ and laid it self upon the corporas / as it seemed to master Reymond. But he
could never find it afterward.

For many times he sought there after both that same time / and also when
mass was down / wherefore he made great sorrow in his hert^. When he had de
so dylygent^ly sought it over all about the altar beside the altar and
upon the ground At the last he bethought him to ask counseyll of the pryour
of ye place hereof / the which pryour loved and dred our lord god right much
/ covering in the mean time the altar that none body should come there unto the
time he should come again. But suddenly as he was going to the pryour come to
him a special friend of his a pryour of the chaterhous preyng him he might
speak with this holy maid katheryne for certain matters. Then Master
Reymou^d prayed him for to abide a lityll time till he had spoke with the
pryour of his covent. And he would come anon again He said he might not tarry
by cause it was a solemn day among them and needs he must be at home at
the mete and thereto he had a mile home wherefore he prayed him for gods love
to tarry him not for his conscience constreyned him to speak with this holy maid katheryne /

Then of charity he left his own need and with his special friend to this
holy maid katheryns house wenyng yt he should have found her there: but her
felawes answered him that long a go she went to church and come not home yet /
When master Reymond herd this he was admerueylyd and came again to church
with his friend and found her there in a corner of the church knelyng and
rauysshed as she was wount to be / and sum of her felawes with her /

Off whom he asked how long that holy maid katheryne had be there: they
said all this mass time and more that he prayed them for to excite her
as soon as they might for his friends is come for to speak with her / And he
might not tarry / When she was cesyd of her rauysshyng / master Reymound took
her aside and told her of his dysese under few words by cause the other man
his friend should not be let / Anon she smylyd upon master Reymound and
askyng him thus gladly / Fader sought ye not all about / he said yes / Then
she said why have ye so great sow we therefore: And with yt she smiled ^ft /
^^is and went so forth for to speak with the pryour off the charterhous: In
the mean time master Reymound abode somewhat I comforted / but not fully unto
ye time he wist how it might be so away:

When she had full do with the Pryour of the Charterhous and delyuerd hi of
an answer that he came for. She turned her to master Reymou^de again /
Then Master Reymound said to her thus / Mother I too we it be ye that has
away that partycule of the holy host: she with smyling said nay but it was
another that took it away from you and therefore be ye no more sorry therefore /
ne for it ne seek no more for it for I tell you ye shall never find it: Then
Master Reymond prayed her that she would tell him al hole how it might be: To
whom she said thus / Fader take no more sorrow for that partycle for if I shall
and should say the soth to you as to mine confessor and mine ghostely fader
that partycule was brought to me and I received it by ye reverend hondes of our
reverend lord almyhty god sweet glorious Jhesu christ And I shall tell you the
cause why / This day I was in purpos with a great desire for to be houseled /
but mine felawes gave me counseyll for to cese that I should not be hoseled in as
much as som^e grutched with all: After whose counseyll I wrought and was purpos
for to cese / but mine desire was so great thereto / yt I prayed our lord
almighty god of help / and he in his own reverend person aperit to me and
gave me that partycle with his* own reverend hondes: And therefore fader be
not sorry there is none necligence in you as for that pertycule / After this
reuelacion Master Reymound was right ioyefull by cause the thaghte of his
concience was put away from him: Such myr^c^e our reverend lord almighty god
showed in the reverend holy sacrament of ye au^ter by the merytes of his hand
maid holy katheryne of Seen / Also there were many other feythfull folk and
true that said* they ^awe often times wha^ Master Reymo^de houselyd this
holy maid kathery^e of Seen the sweet holy ghooste flede out of his hondes in
to her mouth the which Master Reymound perceived never save this he perceived
that / The sweet reverend host made anoyse in her mouth when she had received
it / a^ though a stone had be cast in her mouth from a far contree / Now
thus shall I make an end off the great merneylousnes of that reverend sweet
holy sacrament of the altar and tell you of diverse miracles that befylle to
this holy maid saint katheryne of seen about certain relykes of saints. This
holy maid katheryne of Seen had onys a reuelacion as she told pryuely to
Master Reymound her confessor that she should be set in the same degree of
joy in the bliss of heaven / And be felawe with saint Agnes the which was a
suster of the mount of Pollycita / Wherefore this holy maid katteryn of seen
desired often times with all her heart for to bysyte the relykes of saint Agnes
But now ye maidens by cause ye shall know how bertuous a liver that saint
Agnes was when she was here in earth / I shall tell you shortly under few
words: This holy maid Saint Agnes suster of the mount of polly^yta the same
time that she should be borne off her mother there was in the chamber there her
mother chylded a great merneylous light that all th o the which were in the
same chamber might clerly see it / And when she was born it cesyd By this ye
may know of what merit she should be in the sight of our reverend lord
almighty god afterward that so soon in the beginning received the merueylous
light of our reverend lord almighty god: After time she was born she encresyd
virtuously more and more in all time of the years and at the last she made two
monasteryes of maidens and lies berye^ in the town / in the which is showed
by our reverend lord almighty god in her co^tinuelly many wou^derful miracles
And among all other miracles wha^ she was passid out of this world her body
was not buried but left upon earth all hooll without any corrup^ion: Wherefore
other devout folk that knew her by her ly^^e consyderyng how many merneylous
things our reverend lord almighty god showed in her / would have bawmed her
sweet body / that it might so be k^pte upon the earth with miracles and when
they came to bawme it / they saw how there came out of the toes of the feet and
of the fyngers of the hondes drops of bawme / the which bawme is kept yet
in to this day for a relyke among the susters of the same place / This
miracle was showed for this cause / that all folk should know that she had
none need for to be bawmed outward when our reverend lord almighty god had
bawmed her within forth / Ferthermore the same hour yt she passed out of this
world in the time of the night infantes both maid children and other as they
lay in her moders beds cryeden and sayeden that now suster agnes is passes
out of this world and is a saint in^heuen: On the morrow these in fantes drew
them together in a company and would suffer none corrupt child come among
them and went each of them as in pro^^ssyon with candeles in her hands to
this monastery where su^ter Agnes passed out of this world ofofferyng to that
maid maydenes oblacion / Many moo miracles our reverend lord almighty god
showed by that holy Maid saint Agnes in the sight of all people / wherefore she
is had every year in great reverence with devout oblacion of many brennyng
tapres for to see that holy maids body / this holy maid katheryne of Seen
took leave of her confessor as as child of obedyens and went to that
monastery there she lay / whom followed her susters and Master Reymou^d for to
see what miracle our lord and almighty god would show in metyng to gyder of
peace two glorious vyrgyns and maidens and his chosen spouses: When she was come
to the monastery she went to the same place there she lay and knelyd down /
and began to bow her head for to kiss that holy vyrgyns feet: with that
bowyng down the holy vyrgyns body off glorious Agnes lift up by miracle her
own foot as hye that the holy maid katheryn of Seen should kiss it without
any bowyng of her body or head / This miracle saw all the susters of the same
monasteryeland also the susters off penance with this holy maid katheryne of
Seen. When the holy maid katheryne of Seen perceived this / she was ye more
meke: and bowed the lower / And than this holy maid and vyrgyn saint Agnes
drew down her leg again and her fete and laid it as it was first: Another
time this holy maid katherin of Seen came again to vysyte the sweet holy body
of this holy maid saint Agnes and brought with her two cosyns of here is young
maid children for to make the^ ^usters in that monastery: there for to serve
our lord almighty god / And when she was come*to the monasterye: She went
there ye sweet holy body lay of glorious saint Agnes / and knelyd not at the
feet as she did the first time / but at the holy head eschewyng mekely as it
seemed the eleuacion of her holy feet as it was do first / And as she knelyd at
her head she laid her cheke to the sweet cheke of this holy maid glorious
Agnes long times to gyders / But wha^ she had so long tarried / she turned
her to her cosyn Lysa the which came with her and other moo of her susters and
said in this wise: Lysa why perceive ye not the gift off our reverend lord
almighty god has give to us out of heuene / why be ye so unkind with that
Lysa and other susters of here is looked up / and saw manna reyne down out of
heaven covering both glorious saint Agnes and the holy maid katheryn of Seen

And also other that stood about / So that Lysa filled her hondes with that
same white seed of manna.

This miracle appieryd not wythout^n cause / For glorious saint Agnes when she
lived in earth was wounte to have that token out of heaven when she prayed to
our reverend lord almighty god / So that sum of her susters saw ^er
mantell all white when she wos up fro her prayer and unknowing what it might
be and would have shake it away from her mantyll and she forbode it them full
esely / And also it was do for another mystery* Glorious saint Agnes knew
well that this holy maid katheryne of Seen should be felawe with her in heaven:
And therefore she began to felyshyppe with her in earth and worship her also
with that token that was wont to appe re to her when she lived in her body. By
that manna is understand puryte and mekenes for by wytnes of that manna is
understand puryte and clennes of maydenhede: and by the lytelnesse of greyne
of that man^a is understand of the mekenes of maidens that they should have /
That puryte and that meekness was right haboundaunt in these two maidens saint
Agnes and this holy maid Katheryne off Seen / As for that witness of the
miracles I showed in this chapter was Lysa and other susters of hers and also
susters of the same monasterye where these miracles weren showed / Ouermore as
for witness touching the miracles off the holy sacrament of the altar was
master Reymond her confessor / and another master of dyuynyte the which was
called Berthylmewe and other mo many moo miracles our glorious lord almighty
god showed by his holy maid katheryne and by this holy maid saint Agnes
whiles they lived here in earth the which ben not written in this book but that
is written herinne / is written to the worship of our glorious lord god and
health of soulys: And thus I make an end of this chapter of this holy
legende of this holy maid glorious saint Katheryne of Seen to the honor
worship and glory of all the glorious trinyte: Cui referantur lauds honor
et gloria in secula seculorum Amen /

Explicit secunda pars gloriosissime vite gloriosissime virginis Katerine de
Seen:
Here begins thr third book and party wherein is rehearsed the deyenge off
this holy maid glorious saint katheryne of Seen and of her miracles that were
showed after her death / And first of all of the witness which were present
at her passing and informed the auctor of this book which and what they were /
Capitulum Primum
When this holy maid katherine of Seen was sent to the Cite of Florens by
our holy Fader Gregory xj / the which was that time pope off Rome as it is
rehearsed before in the second party for to make peace betwyne our holy father
the pope and his children of Florence: she found them vnobedyent and rebel
where and among whom she suffered much persecucion in so much yt one of
them drew his sword and would have smyten of her head so wood he was with
her all be it thought he were let by the virtue of our glorious lord almighti
god And yet notwythstondyng such persecucion she would never goo thens unto
the time that peace was cried thorugh out all the Cite of Florence / And that
was not by pope gregorys days for he dyed in ye mean time* but it was by pope
vrbans time and days ye which was pope after him in whose time the peace was
made / And after time the pope was made she went home again to the Cite off
Seen / And bylefte in her own house full dylygently about the making of a
certain book the which the swte glorious holy ghost endyted by her mouth in
her own langage. She prayed her writers the which wrote the book yt they
should consydere besely that she tells the^ in time of her rauysshyng and so
she bad them write / Then she went and prayed / and sone after she was
rauysshed from her bodily wits and in that rauisshyng she spoke many swehe
words: ye which words the writers wrote as she spoke and so compyled a book
full off profitable sentence as our sweet glorious for almighty god told her /
In the which endytyng one special thing and a merueylous was showed / And
all yt was comprehended and written in the book was endyted by her by diverse
times in time of her rauysshyng and never else so that in that same time that
she was so rauysshed she saw none bodily sight with her eyes ne herd with
her eeres / ne swellyd with her nose / ne none of her bodily wits / neither
had her bodily workynge for that time yt she was in that rauysshyng / By this
ye may co^sydere and understand that ye book was not endyted by none natural
kyndely wit / But only by the infusyon of the sweet glorious holy ghost / ne
I doubt not that all tho the which be understanding men and dylygently
search the sentences shall read that book and of that book they shullen say the
same that I say After time she had made that book / our holy fader pope
vrbane the vj: that knew this holy maid in auyoun and had great deuoucion in
her words and in her virtuous living sent to Master Reymound her confessor
that he should stere her to come to Rme for to vysyte the sain^^s that been
there / Master Reymounde did so: but she was so full of dyscrecion that she
answered again in this wise Fader many of this Cite of Seen and also of our own
susters by cause of mingoyng about hider and thither ^en sklandred thereby and
seyn that it is not semely to a Relyous maid for to go so about / all be it I
hope to our glorious lord almighty god that I have not offedyd in mine going
about / For by obedyence of our glorious lord almighty god and by his vycar in
erther and for the health of soul I went thither that I went. And therefore
leest I ben to them matter of sklander by mine own will I purpos not to remeue
out of the Cite

Nevertheless if the glorious lovely Crystis vicar will algatis that I come his
will be done and not mine. And thereto I pray you goo to him and pray him that
he vouchesaf to send me word by you of his will that they the which ben so
sklandred by min going about / Now ye may clerly know that I took not that
journey upon me by min own will / Master Reymound went and told to the pope
all this matter / and he sent again by him that she should come by ye virtue of
obedyens / Then as soon as she herd this com^au^dement as a true douhter of
obediens she spedde her fast and came to Rome with a great company both men
and wym^en and many moo would have come had she not forbede the^ / * When our
holy fader ye pope saw her he was glad and ioyeful and he desired yt she should
seye som^e word of exortacio^ to ye cardinalis yt weren there present: namely
for the scisme ye which began the same time / And so she did full virtuously
and made each of them steadfastly strong with many sweet words and sentences
and counseylled them that they should not dread for nothing notwythstondynge
the scisme the which began / but to stand myghtely and dread noman / and
proceed forth in things yt longen to our glorious lord / for he is mighty ynow
to mayntene them: when she had made an end of her words our holy fader the
pope was glad and rehearsed her words tournyng to his Cardynales and said /
Loo brederen the more vnfeytfull we be / the more reprouable we ben in the
sight of our glorious lord almighty god / this woman has shamed us all. she
should rather be aferd tha^ we by cause she is a woman / yet in that we be
aferde she is not aferde but conforted us with her good counseyls: Certain we
ought all to be ashamed / wherefore should our glorious lord god Ihesus Crystus
vicar be aferd* Trewele though all ye world were against him our glorious lord
god Ihesus christ is myghtyer then it: And it is not possible that he will
forsake his church / with such words and many moo like these / our holy
fader the pope comforted the Cardinalis and commanded this holy maid in our
glorious lord god and granted her for her self and for her friends many
special graces Within a few days afterward it came to our holy fathers mind
that he should send this holy maid katheryne with a another maid that was
called katheryne and was one of the ghostely daughters of saint Brygytte of
swethe / the which saint Brygytte was canonysed by pope Bonefas the ix* to
dame Johan the queen of cycely that openly rebelled against holy church and
gave great favor to Scismatykes / that both two maidens ye which were well
known with the queen of Cycely should wythdrawe her from her error / Then
this holy maid katheryn of Seen herd this: she would in none wise wythdrawe
her fro this holy obedyens but oblysshed her self for to goon The other
katheryn of swethe in no wise would take that iournaye upon her but refused it
in presence of master Reymound / Then master Reymound bythought him that
the fame of holy maidens is right tender and a little ^^otte of sin thought
they be not gylty therein Is sklaunderous to them / Also he thought that she to
whom these maidens should be sent might by counseyll of her and many about
her to lie awayte in ye way that these maidens should not come to her presens
and so to be let off her purpos: And also they maidens might not escape
without a great sklander al be it they might be gyltles: these thoughts
Master Reyymound told our holy fader / To whom our holy fader answered and
said thus / thou seyst well master Reymou^de / It is better they goo not than
goo / After this time master Reymound went and told this to this holy maid:
/ Anon she turned her to Master Reymound and said thus with a mighty voice
/ Fader if saint Agnes and saint Margarete and other maidens should have
thought thus / they should never have had the crown of martyrdom / whether we
have not a spouse that can deliver us out of the hondes of wicked men and keep
our clennesse among the fylthy company of lecherous meyny: all such
thoughts ben but veyn thoughts: And come out rather of the defaute of little
feythe then of very wisdom: All be it yt Master Reymound was thus made
ashamed of his imperfection / yet he had a great gladness of her perfeccion
consyderyng and nothing in his heart the stedfastenesse and stabylnes of her
faith: Nevertheless by cause that our holy fader had ordyned that tho two
maidens should not go on that Journay he durst no more meue to him of the
matter. Loo maidens this is rehearsed here by cause ye should know how steadfastly
this holy maids foot was set in the feyth of perfeccio^ Furthermore when our
holy tader had ordained that these maidens should not go / he ordained that
master Reymonde should goo to France. Supposyng that he might torn king
Charles out of his error by enbassatour between / but year might he not. For
the kings heart was so enduratin malice / and would not torn / for he began
to be auctor and begy^ner of that scysme. After time master Reymond knew the
will and intent or our tader / he came to ask counseyll of this holy maid
what were best for him to do then all be it yt she was loathe to want his /
presence / yet she gave hy^ coun^eylitor to obey to the byddyng of our holy
fader: And among all other things she said: thus to him Fader understands
his for treuthe. This pope Urbanis very Crystys vycarye in er^he / and for
d^^ence of this treuth preceth and puts you ^orth as ye would for the feyth
of holy church. All be it that master Reymond understood this well before /
yet she made him ye strenger and more steadfast in his labor for when he was
most in dys^ase he had her words in mind / and so he took the holy
obedyence upon him. But a latell a fore that he went / this holy maid co^myned
with him and told him four hours. or five to g^ds of the reuelacyons and
comfortes that our lord showed to her but a little before / and when she had
do* she said this words. Fader now goth and our. lord speed you for I trow
we shall never in this life speak so much to gyder as we have do now. And like
as she said so it / was. For or then master Reymonde came again / she was
passed out of this / world / furthermore by cause that she would fully take her
leave of him she went personally to the same place / there he should take his
Galey. And when they began / to row she kneiyd down and prayed / and /
afterward blyssed the Galey with weeping chere / and said pryuely that other /
herd to master Reymond Thou lone shall go save / for the cross shall keep
the but thou shall never see thy mother in this life. And as she prophesied so
it was for there were many enemies in the ^ee and yet they went save away from
them and also in the mean time that he was out. this holy maid passyd out of
this world But first or that I tell of her blyssed passing out of this world /
I shall reherce to you the wytnes which were at her passing / and knew of
the miracles: that our lord showed here in her passing The names of the wymmen
that were most contynuell with her be^thy^e. Allexe of Seen sister of penance
of S^y^t. Domynyk / the which was a perfyte dyscyple of this holy maids / and
followed her in all as^yte of penance / as nygh as she / could / so yt this
holy maid or thenn^ he should pass told her all her preuytees / and
ordained her for to be a mother to other after her dyssece: This same Allexe /
enfourmed master Reymonde when he: was come home / and other of this holy.
maids passing / for she lived not long. after. The second wytnes was
Francysca of Seen this Francysca had a devout soul to god and to this holy
maid / with an hertely love wherefore when her. husbounde was deed she took the
abyte of penance and was made sister of Saint Domynyk: This Francysca
enfourmed master Raymonde when he came / home and many other folk of this
maids passing and then she deyed soon / after Allexe The third wytnes was.
Lysa her cosyn / the which I will notte commend / all be it she was right
true by cause she was this holy maids brothers wife where by should behold
suspect / in her wytnes among men. further more there were many men in her
passing the which beren true record othyr bussed end But four in special
I thy^ke to rehearse here ye which were right virtuous men. The first was
called friar Sanctus / the which was both holy indede and in name. This holy
man forsook all his kynne / and came to Cite of ene Where he lived virtuously
xxx year and more an ancheres life. And when / he herd speak of this holy
maid he was styred to speak with her / and so he did for to be enfourmed of
her. And at last he thout that it was better to walk out of / his cell for to win souls then for to be so enclosed. And so he did by counseyll he went
out and followed this holy maid and wan souls to Christ / but specially he
was present with her at her passing This holy man enfourmed master Raymonde
also when he came home of the passing of this holy maid / and soon after he
dyed. The second witness of men was a young man in age / but he / was old in
virtue / the which was called Barductyne. This young man forsook all his kynne /
and followed this holy / maid and was with her till that she passyd / whom she
loved yettenderly / by cause he was a maid and that was no meruaylle / for it
is semely that oo maid should love another. To whom this holy / maid said
and chargyd him that he should be governed by master Raymondis counsel: For
this cause I trow she did it in as much as she knew well of god / that he
should not long live after her / so that he did of tesyk / but first he
continued long therynne / and was amended by medycines / but at the last he
did thereon. And by cause that master Raymonde dread him that the air of Rome
shol^e enfecte him he sent him to Seen where he passyd out of this world /
and / they bear wytnes yt were at his passing that when he should pass he
looked up into heaven / and began to smyle / and so with that smylyng he passyd
/ So that after time he was passyd / the tokens of gladness appyred in his face
I trow it was therefore / by cause he saw her whom he loved so charitably
come after him.

This Barductyne also enfourmed / master Raymonde when he came home of th^s
holy maid passage. The thryde wytnes of men was also a young man: the which
was called Stephen that was one of this holy maids writers / ye why / she
wrote both her letters that she sent. and also hyrbook that the holy ghost
endyted by her. The which young man this holy maid called to her when she
should pass and said thus. Sone it is the will / of god that thou be a monk
of the Charterhous / and therefore I charge the that you so do As she bad him so
he did / and lived ever afterward a perfyt life for he hadno felawe of
perfeccyon in that Relygyon / and as soon as he was professyd / he was. made
Pryor of ye same house that he was. shorn Inn. And afterward he was made
Pryour in another place of the same order at melayne and visitour of the order
This young man Stephen wrote certain things that happed in the passing of this
holy maid and e^tfourmed afterward master Raymonde of the same / when he
came home. The fourth and last witness of men that were at ye passing of this
holy maid was one / the which was called Raynerus the sone of a worthy man
Landocte of Seen. This man after time that this holy maid was paste / was a
devout recluse that ever afterward lived a blyssed life / he was also one of
the writers of her lettres / and of her book that the holy ghoost endyted by her

He was the first of men that forsook his kynne and followed this holy maid /
and by cause he knew her virtuous living of long time / therefore master
Reymond called him to him / and made him a special wytnes in making of her
Legende / and his felawe also Stephen pryour of the Charterhous. These men and
these wymmen enfourmed master Reymond when he came home of the things /
which was done in his absence as well of tho things that she did or that she
paste as of tho things that she showed and did in her passing / and thus
ends this chapter.

Of meruayllous things which befyll a year and half to fore ye death of this
holy maiden / and of the martyrdom that she suffered bodily of wicked fendes /
where of atlast she had her bodily death. Capitulum secundum
AFter time ye master Reymond went fro this holy maid as it is rehearsed
before / by the byddyng of our holy fader the Pope / she belefte in the Cite of
Rome / and what that our Lord deed for her or that she deyed / and showed to
other how holy of living she was / and also what joy he gave her or she passyd
out of this world I shall tell you.

Leave it well maidens / when this holy maid perceived that so much disease
encrecyd in holy church by the scysme / yt was begone / and perceyuyng also
that Crystys vycarye suffered great disease / she wept day and night / and
prayed to our lord for the pees / that he would wouchesauf to set pees in holy
church. Then our lord comforted her in some manner of wise for the year before
and an half or she dyed our lord gave double vyctorye to holy church / and
to Crystys vycarye the pope as well of the castle of Saint Angel that was in
the Cite of Rome / the which was in scysmatykes hondes in to that day / as of
the people that held the castle in the name of scysmatykes / that were ye
same day take / and the castle yolde.

After that our holy fader the pope that might not dwell in Rome as he was
wont by cause of the enemies that were in the Castle of Saint Angel know
this / he came to this holy maid and axed her counseyll what he should do.
Then she gave him counseyll that he should go barfoot and all the people of
Rome with him to the mynster of Saint Peter thanking our lord god with good
devotion of that grace / and of that benefetys the which he had do for them.
Thus holy church began to quyken / and the holy maid had thereof great
comfort. But soon after her sorrow began to encrece eftsonis for that the
fend might not do by strayn gers / he assayed for to do by them that were of
the Cite of Rome. He made a dysoorde between ye people of the Cite and the
pope. That perceived this holy maid she prayed to our lord that he would
wouchesauf put to his mercyable hand / and suffer not that cursyd sin be
done And as she prayed / she saw the Cite full of fendes styryng and excytyng
the people to kylle their ghoostly fader / and cried horrybly to this holy
maid all the while she prayed / seeing to her thus Thou cursed wretch thou
art about for to let us / therefore we shall slay the with an horrible death.
To whom she answered no word / but prayed more besyly and more fervently axyng
of our lord that he would wouches auf for the worship of his holy name / and for
remedy of all holy church that then stood in great meshyef / keep her and
his vycarye without harm / and not for to suffer the people do such a sin
and so to put away the fendes fro their purpose / the which steryng the
people there to. She had an answer of our lord / and it was this. Daughter
suff^e this people / that every day blasteme mine holy name / for to fall in to
this sin / that I might so dystruye them for their cursed wretchydnesse for
my ryghtwysnes axyth that I should no more suff^e their wyckydnes. Then she
prayed more fervently with such words and said. Mekest and myldest lord /
thou know well how thy spouse holy church is dyseased and tormented /
almost thorugh out all the world and that is routhe. Thou know well also how
sewe helpers and defenders she has / and therefore now if they slay thy vy
carye as they ben in purpose / hit shall not only be grievous to this people of
Rome but to all Christian people Thempre therefore good blyssed lord thy
ryghtwyse hand and despise not thy people that you haste bought so de^ with
thy precious blood / but torn thy mercyable hand and cesse this myshyef. In
this prayer she continued many days to gyder as she wrote to master Reymond
by a letter ever our lord alledgyng his ryghtwysnes and she axyng his mercy /
and in all that time the fendes cried ho^^ybly upon her as it is rehearsed before
/ so that she was feeble for afflyccyon / yt but if our lord had kept her
strength / her her^e should to borste / at last she said to our lord these
words. Lord sith it ^^ so yt this mercy may not be granted without
ryghtwysnes / I beseech the despise not my prayers / but what manner of pain
these people should have put it on my body / and I shall glad dely ^eceyue it
for the worship of thy name / and for the sauacyon of holy church.

Then our lord alleged no more his ryghtwysnes / but held his pees and gave
her the vyctorye / and fro that hour forthward the grutchyng cessyd of the
people by ly^^ll and little / but her passions encreced so ferforth that
serpents of hell had power of god and t^rmented her body cruely that it were
vncredyble a man for to believe it but if he had seen it / as they sayden that

they saw not the serpents. They fretted and devoured so that maidens body /
that therein be left but bones without skin / as though it had been consumed
and wasted by long lyeng in the earth / and yet neuerthe^^^ she walked and
prayde as she was wont / the which was to many folk a wonder thing / for she
seemed rather a wonder thing to look upon / then ne a naturell thing Her
torments of pain encreced contynually / by the which she was consumed / and
yet she cessyd not from prayer / but she prayed ^ore fervently and more len^er
then she was wont. Her ghoostly children whom she had nourysshed in virtue
were that same time / and they saw openly the marks of the strokes that the
^endes of hell gave her in her body / and they might do thereto no remedy for
two skylles. One was for they wyste well hit was the will of god whom they
might not wythstonde. Another cause was / for they saw her glad and joyful
in her pains / and the more that she prayed the more was her bodily pain But
yet would she not cesse therefore / and the tormentours of hell faylled not /
but that they cried upon her all that time / and said to her thus. Cursed
wr^tche thou have ever be against us / and therefore thy time is come we for to

therefore we shall never cesse unto the time thou art out of this ^yf. This

which day she passed out of this world In ye which time a meruayllous thing
happed her as she said and wrote to master Reymond. Cuery day it befyll her
of custom that she had the passion on the side that is called ^lyca passio /
and other moo unto none time / wherefore often times she desired heryng of her
mass / and therefore every day by the morrow or then that the pain came
upon her / she went to Saint Peter's church thorugh out all the lenten. And
so herd her mass / and abode there till euensong and then came home again
and lay her down in her bed.

In the which bed whose had seen her / he would have sworn that she might
never remeue her thens. Yet on the next^ mo^we she wse up and went eftsonys

her Journey should have made an hole man weary. This she continued all the
lenten / and within a few days after she lay still in her bedd^ / and might
not remeue her thens for feebleness.

And at last our lord called her and she passyd out of this world.

In the same day that is rehearsed before about none days / that is the nine
and twenty day of Apryll / the which was upon a sunday. The year of our lord
a thousand three hundred and four s^ore. In the which day the feste of Saint
Peter the martyr of the order of the frece prechours was and is solempnysed in
holy church.

Many notable things were wroughte then in her passing / the which I left

god in the next chapter / and thus ends this chapter.

How this maid desired for to be unbound fro the body / and be with Christ

short^ly is written in this book with the same oryson. Capitulum ^ij
When the end of the bodily life of this blyssed maid Katheryn drew fast
