to amend. These words she said often times to tha last end of her passing
but the last word that she said was this Domine in manus tuas comnendo
spiritum meum. And so that blyssed soul paste out of the body / and was and is
complyd and knytte to her spouse Ihesu / whom she loved so hyghly with an
Indyuysyble and perpetuell on head or union The year of our lord a thousand
threhondred and four soore the nine and twenty day of Apryll / the which was
in the cite of Rome and fill upon a sunday about the hour of tyerce / that
same and the same hour the soul of this holy maid appyred to master Reymond
that was that time in far contreys / and not by open bodily apparycyon / but
by mental apparycyon seeing to him in his soul such words of comfort. Dread
the not for I am here for the / I am in heaven where I may help the and defend
/ be seker therefore and dread not for I am here for the With the which
comfortable words master Reymond was in manner astonyed and ameruaylled what
it might be / wenyng that this comfort had come from our blyssed lady mother
of mercy / by cause he stood a fore an image of here is and said an Aue maria But
yet nevertheless he was aferde to think so / by cause him thought he was
unworthy to have such a comfort of her And so what it might mean / or what it
might be / or whennys it might come he nyst never. But afterward in heryng of
another reuelacyon of this holy maid showed to a devout matrone / he
understood the better what it might mean so whens it might come. Of the which
matrone I shall tell you. The same time when this holy maid passyd out of this
world / there was in Rome a devout matrone / that was called Semya / the
which had two men to her sons / to whom she was every day both mother and
servant / in making of their mete. This devout matrone after time her husbonde
was deed / she purposed ever after to serve god / and visyte by pilgrimage holy
saints of Rome / and she continued many years

She had also in custom for to rise at mydnyght and pray / and afterward
for to take a little rest syttyng or lenyng with her head / that she might be
the more quycker on the morrow erly for to go her stacyons of Rome. It befyll
soon after that when this holy maid Katheryn was come to Rome / this devout
matrone took knowleche of her / and was often times edyfyed by her good
exhortacyons / and so had a good ghoostly affection to her / and was often
times homely with her in her hows almost every day Nevertheless a ^ytell before
this holy maid deyed / she came not to her because of certain besynes that she
had to done / what for her pylgrymages / and the purueyaunce of mete for her
sons / And therefore she wist not that this holy maid passyd This devout
matrone Semya arose up at mydnyght as she was wont / for to do and pray a
long time to gydre / she purposed for to rest a little / by cause she would
up by times on the morrow for to here nasse / and then for to be besye about
her children mete. She did so / but ever she was trayueylled in her sleep
that she should O wretch / the fend has deceived the / she ^se up then and
went about for to seek in paryshe chyrches where sum hole masses were
aseyeng / and as she went she herd a be^le ring to a mass in an hows of
Nonnys / she was glad then and thither she went and left her wortys vnpy
kyd and vnwashe for have and shytte her do ^e and bare the keye with her / when
she came the mass was in ye beginning / with that she said to her self thus.
Now I wot well the fend has not deceived me as I wend. Nevertheless as much
as she wyste well that the mete of her sons might not be ready or they came
home to mete / she was sorry / but for the comfort yt she had in her mas^e /
she committed all to god / prayeng him that he would wouche sauf to keep her
that day fro heavy words of her children / the which were grown men / for she
was sore aferde to dysplease them / and so she herd forth all the hye mass
/ when the hye mass was done / as she went^ home she met with her sons
coming homward to mete seyeng to her thus. Mother hye you fast for it is time
to go to mete. She answered ageynefull esely and said. Good sons abides a
while / and ye shall go to mete anon

When she was entered in to her house she found her mete all ready enough / and
the wortys all ready in the pot well soden at the full / she was than astonyed
/ and than ked our lord that she had herd her mass / and so badde her sons
sytte done to mete in ye name of Jhesu / thynkyng in her self that after none
she would go and vysyte the holy maid Katheryne / all the mete time she
thought much in that vysyon / and how it was co^fermed with so great miracles

In the mean whiles her sons commended their mete and said that it was beter
sesoned that time / than any mete that they had eten before many a day / but
the devout matrones ^erte was always upon the vysyon seyeng within her self
thus. O mother Katheryne and crystis spouse. Yet for all this she wend not that
she had be deed And when her sons were a gone and had et^ / she went to
Katherynes house and knockyd at the door and herd none answer / it was said
her of ye neighbors there about yt she was walked out for to vysyte holy
places / yet in treuthe her susters were within waylyng And would not suffer
none to enter in to the time they had axyd counseyll how they should be^y the
body / At the last it was determined among them that on the morrow the body
should be ladde to the friar prechours / and there for to do ye seruyse as god
would ordeyne by counseyll and so it was done / But as soon as the body was
come to ye church / ye people followed for to touch her fet^ or her clothys /
so that both ye freres and also her sustres and other of her dysciples were
aferde / lest they should have borste and toren her clothys / and therefore they
set the body within the chauntell of a chapel / that was endued in the
worship of Saint Domynyk / What that fill afterward I think to declare you in
the next chapter by the help of god Casuelly whiles this was adoyng Semya
the Matrone came Inn the mean time / and axyd what that noise and concourse of
people might mean / Hit was told her that Katheryne of Seen was passyd out
of this world / her body was in the church / wherefore the people gadred so
fast for to see it.

Anon when she herd that / she wayled and wept and went Inn there the
body ^aye seyeng to the ghoostely children of this holy maid Katheryne.

O vnpytuous woman why have ye hid this fro me / why called ye me not to her
passing / They excusyd them that they might not for certain causes / than she
prayed them for to tell her wha^ she departed from the body they said yester
day about vnderne of the day / with ye Semya wept and said thus that same
time it was that I saw mine glorious mother lad up to heaven with ang^lis with
three precious crowns on her head: Now I wot well she said that our reverend
lord almighty sent his angelys and showed me the passing of mine glorious mother
glorious saint katheryn of Seen

And more over she mynystred for me merueylously in mine kytchyn / O mother O
glorious mother why understood I not when I had that glorious visyon that
thou that time passid out of this world / Then she respyred and told to her
susters and to other ghostely children of here is what vysyon she had such a
time* al as it is rehearsed / thus ends this chapitr^

Of tokens and miracles which our reverend lord almighty god wrought after the
de^h of this holy maid and vyrgyn glorious saint Katheryn of Seen both
tofore her beryeng and after. That is to say of tho miracles were know for
many there were yt were not know / Capitulum ^
When the blessed soul of this holy maid and virgygyn glorious saint katheryn
of Seen was de liuerd out of her sweet body: and the swe holy body put in a
chaunsell of saint Do mynyk I closed by cause the people should cerce a while
of her confluence as it is ^eher^ed before in the iiij chapter: In the mean
time that it s^ode there came a suse of saint fraunceis order that was called
Domynyca the which had a sekenes in her armr / that half a ye^e before this
holy maid and vyrgyne dyed she might not by welde her arm: for it was in
manner benomme her and drped up / This suster Domynyca in hope to have help
herd seye that this holy maid and vyrgyn was deed* came to the church there
she lay and said that she might not come to this holy body for the people /
and by cause also the chaunsel door was shette / she threw in a keuerchef and
prayed the susters of saint Domynyk that they would touch ye sweet holy body
of that holy maid and vyrgin with that keuerchefe and then^e to give ^t to her
a gayn. They did so / and as soon as she had the keuerchefe again she put it
to her arm and was hole anon / with yt she cried to all the people and said
that her arm was hole by miracle of this holy maid and vyrgyn glorious
katheryne

Then the people made much noise in thankyng our reverend lord almighty god
and brought children of here is and other seek bodies that they might have help
by miracle namely by touching sum hemme of that holy maid and virgins
clothes* Among all other there was brought a ^^^^de of iiij year old whose he
de lay upon his one sholdes by cause off a certain infyrmyte that he had by
the which infyrmyte ye synowes of his neck were shronke to gyders so that he
might never lift up his head fro the sholder As Soon as this childe^ was
brought to ye holy body and was touched in the neck with the holy maid and
vyrgyn: about whose neck also was put a keuerchefe of this holy maid and
vyrgyn* ^ythin a little while and time afterward ye child began to amend and
so was at the last hole. This was the cause why the friars durst not burye
the holy body by three days to gyder in as much as our reverend lord almighty
god should show miracle by her: For there was so great a confluence of people
thoo three days that a master of ^yuynyte was steryd for to make a sermon to
the worship of our reverend lord almighty god and of this holy maid and
virgyn But when he stood up in the pulpyt he might not be herd for noise of the
people and the great concurs to the sweet holy body. So that at the last he
left of his sermon and said to all the people in this wise / Syres I see well
this holy maid and vyrgyn needs naught our prechinge for she by her self
pr^^heth suffyciauntly ynow and then he went down out of the pulpyt:

The myraclys of this holy maid and vy^gyn encresyd fast: For there was a
Roman the which was called Lucius / that had such a sickness the which
might not behelyd of none leche a joint off his knee was to broste so that he
might not walk uneath but by sustentacion of a staf: This lucius herd say
that such an holy maid and virgyn did myraclys* with great traueyle and
help of other he came there her swe^^ holy body lap: and there with great
reverence and deuoucion he took the holy maid and vyrgyn hond and put it to
his thye / and to his leg. ^ythin a little while and time after he felt more
strength in his leggys than he did a fore so that or than he went fully
thens he was all hole / praysyng our reverend lord almighty god in his
merueiles that he showed in his saints /

Also there was a young maydede child yt was called ^e^^zola ye which had an
horybyll infyrmyte of a lepyr in her face yt her noise and the ouerlyppe of her
mouth was coueryd with that horrible lepre / This maid herd speak also of ye
miracles showed by this holy may de and vyrgyn glorious saint Katheryne of Seen
/ and come to the same chriche where that her holy body lay and in to come to
that holy body / but always she was put a back by prees of the people: At the
la^t she came in to that sweet holy body and put not only her face to the holy
maid and vyrgyns hondis and feet / But also to her lovely sweet face and
vysage Soon after she felt releuyng of her sekenes so that within a short
time she was so perfyghtly hole and never afterward apperyd in her face any
naner of ^eper / spottene mark / of any manner leper /

Also there was a Roman calli^ Cypryus yt had a daughter the which daughter of
young age took a sekenes yt is called ye tysyk of that sekenes she might never
be deliueryd by none manner of me decyne / when the fader and the mother herd
say of the myraclis / showed by our reverend lord almighty god by by this holy
maid and vyrgyn glorious saint katheryn they came to the same place and her
daughter with them where the sweet holy body lay and recommendyd devoutly her
daughter to that holy maid and vyrgin As Soon as the child was hole / Also in
the mean time the sweet holy body lay vnberyed / there was a cytysyn of Rome
that was called Anthoni ye which was the same time in saint Pet^is church
when he herd of the myraclis that was wrought by this holy maid and vyrgyn:
This Anthony was enfected so yt he might not be cured with none natural
mede^in / he bethought hi^ of this holy maid and virgin and devoutly he made
a vow to her and he had not so sone made his a vow / that he ne felt his
body and his lym^es as strong as ever they were / Then he came to this holy
maid and vyrgyn and thanked our reverend lord almighty god and her of his
recoueryng /

Also there was a devout matrone yt was welknowe with this holy maid and
virgyn when she lived in earth / for often times when she came to her place she
and many of her dysciples were herberowed with her: the which matrone she
called Paula / In the same time wha^ this holy maid and vyrgyne passyd out of
this world This pau^a was seek and had lay seek iiij months before upon a
sekenes that is called podagra and upon another sekenes on her side that is
called Ilycapassio / And by cause the remedies of thoo two sykenesses ben
contrary each to other for the tone sickness required openenyng / and the
other closinge / therefore this matrone was much more vexed* so that other
whiles she was nere deed: ^han t^is matrone herd say that this holy made and
virgyn was ^passyd: She asked for charity that she might hau^ som^e manner of
clothe / that her sweet holy body was coueryd with or touched as she desired
so she had: that same night at even she leyde that clothe upon her as she
lay in her bed all night:

On the morrow she roos up all hole and walked on her fete as though she had
never that sickness. Such myrac^es and many moo our reverend lord almighty
god wrought in that blessed maid and holy vyrgyn or than it was buried. Yet
our reverend ^lorde almyghty^ god cecyd not for to work health to seek folk
For in werkyng it rather encresyd than dymynused:

There was a woman that was called ^one which had a little child yt might not
stand right up on his fetene goo / This ^one herd how our reverend lord
almighty god wrought many fair my ra^^ys by this holy maid and vyrgyne
glorious saint katheryne she made auowe to our reverend lord almighty god and
to here for the ^elthe of her child

After time she had made her a vow she took her child with her and came to
the grave where the holy maid and vyrgyn was buried / And she laid her
child upon the grave / And anon the child began to stand right up and go as
though he had had never sickness in his legs: Also there was a man of Tose
yt was also called Johan ye which had an horrible sekenes in his eyes so ye
worms bredde in his eye / this ^ohn made a vow devoutly to our reue^^nde
lord almighty god and to this holy maid and vyrgyn glorious saint Katheryne
off Seen / and anon he was delyuerd of his sekenes / when he was so delyueryd
he came to the sepulcre of that blessid maid and virgin and set^^ up a toke^
of wax as ye manner is in sign and toke^ of delyu^ra^ce than he told to all
folk yt would h^re it the merueyle of our reverend lord almighty god showed by
this holy maid and virgyn: Also there was a woman pilgrim of duchelond whose
name was not wryton because it was foryete of negligence the which pilgrim
had desuche a sickness in both her eyes that she had almost lost her syghte
The pilgrim made a vow devoutly to our reverend lord almighty god and to
this holy maid and vyrgyn glorious saint Katheryn of seen / And within a
little time after she had clear ^ yght and her sickness was gone when she was
to her sepulcre for to thank our reverend lord almighty god and her / She
saw as clerly as eue^ she did / Also there was a lady of Rome that was called
Mary^ the which the which had in her head a grievous sekenes that
notwithstondyng many sundry medecyns the which she used she might never be
help thereby / but lost her eyes / Wherefore for sorrow and shame that she had
thereof / she would never pass her house after ne appear in the sight of men:
This lady herd speak of the gteate myraclis that our reverend lord almighty
god wrought by that holy maid and vyrgyn glorious saint katherin / she made
auowe to our reverend lord almighty god and to her devoutly / After time her
vow was made: the next night sueing this holy maid and vyrgyn apperyd to the
servant of this lady in her sleep and bad her sey to her lady that she should
do no more medecyns to her sight. but every day in the morrow she should goo to
church and here ye service of our reverend lord almighty god and then she
shall be hole When this servant had told her lady thus / she deed so / and
at the last by lytil and little she began to see with that blind eye and was
fully restoryd to health: Loo dear susters by this miracle ye may consydere
that this holy maid and vyrgyn followed the deeds of our lord almighty god
sweet Ihesu Christ / For when our reverend lord almighty god sweet Jhesu
Christ was sought whiles he was in earth here for the health of body / Him
thought it was not ynow for him to hele only the body but if he helyd the soul
When he said to one that came to him for to be helyd in body thus:

Fili remittuntur tibi peccata / That is to say / thyn sins be forgyuen /
Right so this holy maid and virgyn there she was asked of health / She gave
also health of soul in that she badde her here her dyuyne service The which
is health and comfort to thesoule:

Also there was a young man ye which was called James the sone of a Roman
that was called Peers / the which was in a time so seek in body that none
leche might hele him / But alegates he drew fast to death: Then was there a
deuote woman that was called Ceccola / The which woman saw this young man in
point of death: and made avowe for hi to this holy maid and vyrgyn glorious
saint katheryn / She had not so soon made her vow / but that the young man
began to recouere and was fully delivered from his sekenes /

Also there was a woman called gallya that was sore seek and might not be
helped by none lechecrafte So that lechee said by course of natural kind that
she should be deed within a short time then this woman Gallya thought upon
saint glorious katheryne of Seen and recommended her lyff to her / She had not
so soon do so / but that she felt comfort and amendment / And so little
and little she was restoryd to health /

Also there was a devout lady that was called dame Jone the which knew well
this holy maid and virgyn glorious saint katheryn whiles she lived / And she
counseyled seek folk when she spoke with them to recommende her sekenes to ye
merytes of ye holy maid and vyrgyn in as much as she herd speak of ye great
miracles that our reverend lord almighty god wrought in her trusting fully that
they should be help by her merytes. So that by her steryng and exortacio^
many were help / Then it fill in a time that off the children of that worthy
Lady dame Jone sodenli as he went upon an hye steire fill down hedelyng a fore
this Lady his mother / So that she wend as it was lykely to be that the child
either was ded or else should have caughte a mayme thereby all the days of his
life after / With that this lady the mother of the child cried to this holy maid
and virgyn glorious saint katheryn off Seen thus glorious saint katheryn off
Seen to the recommau^de mine child / she had not so soon said so* but that
the child stood up wythouten any harm less or more: for he was as hole
then as ever he was a fore: Then the mother thanked our reverend lord
almighty god and this holy maid and virgyn glorious saint katheryne of the
blessed miracle /

Also there was another woman the which was a general launder and lived by
that manner of besynes that was cally d bone Johan. i. bona Johanna / In a time
as this woman should goo to the River there beside and washed clothes /

It behapped her that she should wasshe a quylte: and in the mean time she
held the ton end under her arms while that the other end was a wasshyng /
It behapped yt the heuyer end in the water drew down the lyghter end under
her arms and so fletted feer within the River*

When she perceived that she wyste well if it were lost she might not pay
therefore by cause she was right pour. She tha^ a rechyd after the quylte for
to have it again and suddenly she her self fell in to the water / so that the
water bare her far within: with that she bethought her of glorious saint
katheryn and said thus O thou glorious saint Katheryne help me now in this
need: This word was not so sone I said but that she was help in so much
that she was lift up above the water and took the clothe and came to land
without help of man when she was recouereude she was sore astonyed merneylyng
how that might be / that she was so soon help then she conceived well that
it thus by the help of our reverend lord almighty god and this holy maid and
virgyn glorious saint katheryn of Seen

Of another miracle now I shall tell you of the which Master Reymound bears
witness as it was told him It befell on a time when Master Reymound was come to
the Cite of Rome upon a day when this holy maidens and virgyn body should be
translated as she prophesied long before whiles she lived as it shall be
declared afterward / that her fylle seek then came to him a physycion yt was
called Master James of saint Mary the round upon a day: when this physycien
came to visyte Master Reymond

And for to give him medycyne he told Master Reymound of a young man that was
called Nycholas a worthy mannys sone of Rome that was passing seek off a
sekenes that is called the quynauncie so that every leche said by nature he
might notlyue / For to all mennys sight he drew fast to the death /

This perceived Alixa a suster of penance of saint Domynyke in as much as she
knew well that the fader and the mother loved this holy maid and vyrgyn
glorious saint Katheryne: When she lived: came to this young man and brought
with her a tooth of this holy maid and vyrgyn glorious saint katheryne that
she kept always for a relyke. The which tooth she put in that young man's
mouth / She had not so soon do so: But that the posteme that was within
brake and the matter fill out off the childs mouth / and within a while after
he was hoole and thanked our reuerede lord almighty god and this holy maid
and vyrgyn glorious saint katheryn. Also afterwar he told that miracle openly
to all that world here it / So that in a time when master Reymond preached he
told that miracle to the people as he herd off other / When that young man
herd him speak thereof the which was at the sermon for that time / he stood up
openly and said to Master Reymound thus / Syrye say sothe for I am the same
that this miracle was showed to: Many mo miracles were showed by our reverend
lord almighty god of this holy maid and virgyn which ben not wryton in this
book / But they might be known wythouten any writing openly ynoto by ye images
of wax that were offered up to her sepulcre / soon after she was buried
Nevertheless of one miracle I shall tell you that Master Reymou^d bears
record of / It befyll soon after that this holy maid and vyrgyne was buried
that queen Johan of Cecyly sent in a time Reynold of vrsyne with a great host
off armyd folk to the Cite of Rome for to make Pope vrbane the vj either for
to put him out of the Cite / or else for to slay him* All be it the Romans
hylde with the pope as true children with ye Fader / Of the which Romans
sum of the common people were take of thoo scismatykes and crruelly punisshed /
sum were bound to a tree so to deye myscheuously sum were led to a
field and I payned with certain infirmytes and instrumentis of iron so for to
take her bodily death / But as many as asked help of this holy maid and virgyn
glorious saint katheryn of seen preuily in her heart or openly in word with
deuoucion They merueylously and suddenly were undo of her hondes without any
help of any man /

Of such myraclis that were many ye which ben not written in this book / Loo
dear friends thus ends this chapitre where ye may see many fair miracles by
the which ye may understand that this holy maid and virgyn was and is a
dear spose of our lord reverend lord almighty god: I will thus make an end of
this book: save by cause holy church commendyth more the virtue of patience
then showing of myraclis as saint Gregrye says therefore I think to write to
you a chapter of the virtue of patience that this holy maid and virgyn had
wherein ye may gader flonres and fruit to encrece of your virtuous living by
the help and socour of our reverend lord almighty god sweet Ihesu Christ:

Qui cum patre et spiritu sancto viuit et regnat deus per omnia secula
seculorum Amen:

Of the might and strong paciens which this holy maid and virgyn glorious
saint katheryn of Seen showed openly from her first young age unto her death by
the which virtu clerly is prouyd that ryghtfully she is worthy to have the
name in gods church of earth when she is made so fair and so glorious in
goddis church in heaven / And in this chapter is a recapytulacion of all the
holy fill of this glorious saint and virgyn before said for werynesse of reders
/ Also if: each man may not have all ye hole holy life of this glorious saint
and virgyne before said / Then may he have ye substance of it here
compendyously rehersyd / Capitulum vltimum
THe holy doctor saint Gregorye seyth in his dyalogus yt the virtue of
pacyence is more commendable then showing of miracles This is the cause why
our mother holy church / wha^ she wodel Canonyze any saint / first she
enquyreth of the virtue of pacyence. Then of the showing of miracles / and
that is for two skylles. One is for many evil lyuers have do wond things /
and shall do yt seems miracles / all though they be none / as Simon magus did
/ and Antecryst shall do in his time. Another is by cause some there has been
that have done and showed miracle by ^tue of our lord Ihesu / the which have
be dampened afterward as Judas / and all tho you our lord speaks of in the
gospel / where he says that some shall stand on ye lift side on the day of
the general dome / and say to him in excusing of them self. Lord have we not
in thy name showed and do wonderful miracles To whom our lord shall answer
again and say Go ye from me werkers of wickydnes / by these two skylles ye may
understand ye holy church in earth may not only be certyfyed by miracles /
whether ye person be holy or not / by whom they be showed / all be it yt they
show presumpcyon of holiness. And namely tho miracles that been showed after
the death of a person / for they were no saints / at whose graves miracles ben
showed. Yet were possible yt our mercyable lord should have them excused / and
yield them after their meke believe / the which beleuen that they be saints.
Not for them that been there beryed but for the glory and the joy of his own
name / lest they the which believe in him be defrawded from their desire
wherefore our mod holy church in earth / that is governed by the holy ghost /
desyryng for to be certefyed of tho merits of holy saints as much as it is
possible in this life enquyreth specially of their virtuous living / and of tho
things yt they wrought whiles they lived in earth. So our lord Ihesu her
spouse taught her to do when he said Ex fructibus eorum cognoscetis eos That is
of her werkys ye shall know them / for it followed aftward in the same place
where that clause is written before / yt a good tree may not bring forth evil
fruit. What ben these fruytes. Trewely no thing else but werkys of love and
charity / both of god and of our neighbors But by cause of these werkys of
charity / right as they be plesaunt to our lord / right so they ben dysplesaunt
to the fend So that he is about in all yt he can and may for to let the
deeds of charity / both by him self and also by the world / that is by
worldly lyuers. Wherefore it is full necessary to holy lyuers to have pacyence
and perceuerau^ce if they will be rewarded for their mede in bliss / by the
which pacyence they may conserve them and keep them in good love of god and of
their good neighbors / notwythsto^dyng all manner persecucyons. Therefore it was
that Saint Powle assygned the first condycyon of charity pacyence when he said.
Caritas paciens est. That is charity is pacyence Loo maidens this is the cause
why our mother holy church in earth / requires more after the pacyence of a
saint if he should be Canonyzed then after the miracles / for among all
^tuous werkys / yet pacyens is the grettest witness of holiness. And this is
said maidens be cause that ye should not be in doubt of this holy maidens
holiness / for she had that virtue of pacyence full blyssedly / As I shall tell
you by the help of god and of your good prayers rehersyng all her deeds of
pacyence / by recapytulacyon of this hole legende namely for weary reders that
thynken an hour in devout redyng is longer than a day / and if they were
occupied in tales and tryfles / then them seems ye long day ^hort then an
hour. Understand well maidens that this holy maid Katherin perceived / that
the virtue of pacyence myt not have his gracious werkyng in a soul / but first
unlawful things were remeuyd away from it / and namely such unlawful thyngys
that been e^^ytable to the lusts of ye flesh / wherefore or then she came to
the age of experyence of flesshly lusts. She ^emeuyd away myghtly all such /
as such things that should styre her when she came to age. And yet she did
not this without Inspyracion / and notable vision of our lord by ye which
Inspiraco^n when she was ^j year of age / she saw our lord arayde as a bishop
sytting in a ry^t fair chamber over the church of the f^ere p^echours / With
whom she saw also saint Johan Euangelyst / and whiles she beheld our lord /
he lokyd upon her full benyngly and mekely and blyssed her. After this holy
vysyon her soul was fulfilled with per^y^e love / that she put away all
children condycyons / and gave her self anon to prayer and to penance / and
therein she encrecyd perfytly / that in the next year after / when she was of
vij year of age she made a vow of madenhode before an image of our lady / not
sode^^ly but with great delyberacyon before / as it is openly declared in the
second and the thrydde chapter of the first pertye. Furthermore by cause that
this holy maid wist well that abstynence was necessary for to keep ye purpose
of maydenhode. Therefore she gave her to great abstynence in her young age / and
performed it meruayllously For as it is reher^^d in the thrydde chapter of
the first per^ye / and in the vj chapter of the same party more largely the
began preuely to leave flesh. And then as she encrecyd in age little and
little / she left all manner etynge of flesh / and thereto she drank no wine
but when it was meddled with wat^r / so that it had all most lost his ^ast and
his color of wine. And when she was xv year of age / she left both wine and
flesh / and all manner of metes out take bread and raw herbs. Also when she
was xx year of age / she left bread and took her only to dyetyng of raw
herbys / and so continued in that manner of living unto the time our lord gave
her a new manner of gracious living / when she lived without any manner of mete
/ and that was when she was xxv or xxvj year of age / as it is openly declared
in the vj chapter of the first party / where is rehearsed the cause and the
manner why and wherefore she came to such estate And where also is answered
suffycyentely to them that grutched to that manner of living. When this holy
maid had thus fully o^come the styryng of sins that she came to the
perfyte virtue of pacyence / as I shall tell you by the help of god The first
prove of pacyence that she had / was by her mother Lapa that would that she had
be wedded / when she came to the age of xij year. And when that she saw that
she might not bring her daughter well thereto / then she put hy^* out of
her chamber that was assygned to her before of honest / and put her to all
manner defoule of the kechen / that another she might have lesyr for to pray ne
for to have medytacyon ne contemplacyon as she was wont / what pacyence she
had in this persecucyons / and how glad she was there Inn / it is clearly
declared in the fourth chapter of the first party. Meruayllously and
virtuously always she stood in the purpose of maydenhode / and yet served the
household with a glad chere. And never for such occupacyons and pryuacyons
of her pure chamber she cessyd fro prayer and other ghoostly excercyses / un to
the time she had overcome both her persecucyons and her pursuers / as it is
rehearsed in the same fourth chapter / but yet ouermore / when the fend
styred her mother Lapa for to set this holy maid from holy dyscyplynes and
wakynges / and also herd lyggyng^s. This holy maid then with a mighty
pacyence / and a meruayllous tempred right dyscretely her moders heaviness
against her. And yet nevertheless kept forth her hardenes of living / as it
is declared in the vj chapter of the first party fully enough And moreover
what Impediment she suffered in her soul by the fend in time of prayer / and
of other ghoostly excercyses / in tormentyng of her flesh / and other alms
deeds that she did as it is openly showed in many diverse chapytres of this
legende before as I shall declare to you. The fend besyed him that he might
first to remeue this holy maid away from her spouse Jhesu / afterward to
wythdrawe her fully from him. Or else at the last for to let her / namely
for a time / but she with a mighty fervor first ouerthrewe her enemy the
fend. Afterward by wit and counseyll of the holy ghoost overcome him. At the
last with stedefast virtue shamed him / that was about to let her. As for
the first the fend began to remeue her fro her holy purpose First by her
suster Bonauenture / the which was wedded curyosyte of her here and clothys /
as it is declared openly in the fourth chapter of the first party. The
second time by her brethern and her mother that were in full purpose for to
marye her as hit is showed in the same chapter. And the thrydde time by him
self / puttyng to her diverse heaviness of temptacyons / and diverse Illusyons /
or then she received the habyte of penance / as it is rehearsed in the vij
chapter of the first party. Also master Reymond of her beside all this as he
was enfourmed of other that were true folk / that in a time wha^ she prayed
before a crucifyxe of our lords passion / the fend stood before her having in
his hand a clothe of sylke / and was about to array her with the same clothe
The which Illusyon of curyosyte she despised and blyssed her and turned her to
the crucyfyxe. After that the fend vanysshed away / but yet he left in her
mind temptacyon of curyosytre of clothyng. Then anon she had mine of her
purpose of maydenhode / and spak to our lord in this wise. Dear lord and sweet
spouse / thou know well that I desired never husbonde but the Therefore I
pray the help me that I may overcome these temptacyons of curyosyte by virtue
of thine holy name. I axe not lord / that thou sholdest take them away fro me
/ but yt thou wouchesauf to give me the vyctorye of thy mercy. As soon as she
had said these words. Our blyssed Lady queen of maidens apperyd to her
sight / semyng to her sight that she took out a right fair clothe out of her
sons side / with the which clothe she arrayed her / And afterward she said
to this holy maid thus* I do the well to wete daughter / that the clothes
which comen out of my sons side passen all other clothes in fayrnes and in
beauty. Then all her temptacyon went away / and she was gretely comforted.
As for the second there the fend was about to wythdrawe her fully from our
lord / by wytty counseyll of the holy ghoost / she overcome him and let him
of his wicked purpose in that that she pesyd her mother Lapa with great wit
cessyd her of her hastynes when she was about for to let her of her penance
doing / and continued afterward nevertheless in her penance as she began*
also when she bare her self so wisely to her confessor and to other
counseyllours the which counseylled her to leave her great abstynence and to
live after a comyndyete / as it is declared in the fyfthe chapter of the
second party And also wisely and meruayllously she pesyd her soueraynes that
forbode her to go to places thither that our lord sent her. But yet she
fulfilled gods byddynges / and esely pesyd her soueraynes / what pacyence she
had in this work / there can no tongue tell ne pen write. Furthermore the
fend saw that he might by no while remeue ne wythdrawe this holy maid from
her devout purpose / he besyed him namely for a certain time for to let her
not only by him self / but by diverse persons / the which shall be told you
specially wythinne forth what they were.

First by her own mother Lapa that brought her to a bath for to be bathed /
that she might by that esy bath be wythdrawe for a time fro her sharp
dysciplynes / and from other hardenesse of penance But yet she could find
there more sharp penance then in her own chamber when she suffered the hot
brennyng water upon her naked body / a^ it is rehearsed in the seuenthe chapter
of the first party. Also another time he would had let her by the byddyng
of indiscreet soueraynes that were ever about to let her from confession /
from prayer / and from all other ghoostly exercyses / as it is declared openly
enough in the first chapter of the secounde party. Nevertheless sum shall
I rehearse here in special that been not spoken of in the same chapter.

And all be it that sum things may not be rehearsed here without shame of some
Relygyous personys / the which were contrary to her holy purpose. Yet better
it were that I rehearsed them / then the gifts of the holy ghoost be hid /
where by ye maidens may have love and dread / both for to here such
trespasses of such Relygyous folk / and love in seyeng of the virtue of
pacyence in this holy maid.

This holy maid Katheryne after time that she had sauoure and swetenes of
devotion / she might never do deed of virtue openly without sclaundre and
bacbytyng of such / namely that she should rather had favored her and
comforted her therein / as ghoostly lyuers both of Relygyous and seculerys /
meruaylleth noothyng here of / for as I said before in the fyfthe chapter of
the secounde party.

But if ghoostly lyuers quench perfytely her propre will of them self / they
fall more cruelly in the dyche of envy then other flesshely lyuers. As I
put an exsample thereof. Of the monks of an holy Abbotte Pachamye / that for
the great abstynence of a new monk / that was come among them / they said
theywold goo out of the momasterye / but if that new monk were avoided. Right
so it befyll with this holy maid. All the susters of penance saw that
Katheryne passyd them all in hardenes of living / in sadness of virtue / in
devotion of prayer and contemplacyon. Anon the serpente of envy entered in
them and styred them for to bacbyte this holy maid / both pryuely and also
openly to the prelates and the order with great boldenes / and yet they that
were hold most sad / held with them and said that it might not be else
but that she wrought all that ever she did in Belsabub the prince of all
deuelys.

This womman by such false suggestyon drew unto their error many sad folk /
both Relygyous and seculers / so that by their counseyll this holy maid was
often times let from her confession and her confessor / and also from
receyuyng of the blyssed sacrament / and all this she suffered pacyently without
any grutchyng or playnyng. Rather supposyng of them that so let her / that
they did it for an holy entente / and for the health of her soul / where fore
her seemed that she was ye more bound to pray for them not as for her enemies
/ but as for her special friends. Yet above all this when she was other while
suffered to be houselyd / in receyuyng of ye blyssed sacrament of the altar /
they would not suffer her afterward to abide long in prayer as she was wont to
do / the which was to her impossible / by cause she received it with such a
passing fervor of devotion / so that ever soon after her spyryte was
rauysshed fro her bodily wits / and so she abode many hours to gydre / as it
is declared before in the second and in the last chapter of the second
party As soon as she was aspyed in that wise / some that were dysceyued by the
forsayde susters would come Inn and draw her out of the church / where often
times she should lie in the son when it was most hotest about mydde day
long time to gyders or then she cessyd of her rauysshynge and restored to her
bodily wits. And there with weeping and waylyng sum* of her susters that were
virtuously styred to grace kept her till she was restoryd.

Also there came another man that came in a time and found her lie there as a
deed womman in rauysshyng / and with a great anger he went to her and sporlyd
her with his feet. And when she was restoryd to her bodily wits again / it
was told her how she was ferde with / yet she would never blame hem therefore /
but rather excuse hem when other spoke evil of hem. Nevertheless they were
punysshed of our lord full hard / and that was a great sorrow to her / save
she durst not long strive against his ryghtwysnesse. For in a time there was a
lady / that had great Indygnacyon of this holy maid when she saw her in
such rauysshyng / wherefore she came to her and sporlyd her with her feet. But
as soon as she was come home to her own place / she dyed without receyuyng of
any sacrament. There was also another wretch that sporled her in the same wise
/ wha^ she was so rauysshed. And also was one of tho that one time bare her
out of the church when she was so rauysshed full vyolently / but he was
punysshed afterward that I am a ferde to tell it. This wretchyd man was so
enuyous and so odyous to this blyssed maid / that not wythstondyng all the
formest cursed dedys that he showed to her / yet he was about in a time for to
kylle her / and there was no thing that let him / but only he had her not
there he would have her

This holy maid knew no thing hereof / but our lord Jhesu punysshed him
therefore full sore / and that was in this wise within a little time after /
this wretchyd man / as he went to a certain place he was take with the frensye
that he cried night and day such words / help me help me / for the hang
man comet^ for to smite of my head. Other that were nyghe him and herd him /
they saw that he was so from him self comforted him that he should not be
aferde / and for fere that he should slay him self / as he showed by certain
tokenes that he would / they kept him the more dylygently Soon after it seemed
that he was amended / so that he was not kept so dylygently as he was But
pryuely anyghtes time he went out of the Cite / and henge and strangelyd him
self meruayllou^ly. He took a cord and tied it upon the foot of a tree even
by the ground / and that other end of the cord he put about his neck /
and so with pure vyolence he slyded upon the ground and killed him self / as
it was demed of them that found the deed body was not beryed in holy place /
but in the dongehyll as it was right semely that it should. By this maidens ye
may know what virtue of pacyence this holy maid had / and how pleasant her
dedys were to our lord / that so auengyd her wrongs unknowing to her.

Also yet shall I rehearse to you by manner of recapytulacyon three meruayllous
things that be written in the fourth chapter yt of secounde party / by the
which things ye may consydre that this holy maid had passyngly the virtue
of pacyence. As for the first it is written in the same chapter of a leprose
womman that was called Secta lyeng in an hospytall / the which womman not
only lacked necessaryes but also a keeper / for there was none that would keep
her by cause of her lepre. This holy maid herd here often she went to her and
was to her a servant / and ordained gladly for all that she neded. Of this
mynystracyon the syke leprous womman was proud / and styred what she could
this holy maid with many Iniuryes reproues and sclaundres puttyng against her*
But yet this holy maid was so armed with mighty pacyence that she was no
thing meued by her words / then the fend saw that he might in no wise
meue her from her merytorye service / he enfected and desouled her hondes with
the same lepre that the same leprous womman had / yet for that would she not
leave / but rather desired to be a lepre then for to leave her vnseruyd And so
she continued in her service unto the time she had beryed that syke womman.
And aftertyme she was beryed / our lord by miracle clensyd her from her lepre
in her hondes. Charity that is pacyence and benyngne taught her for to overcome
all this. As for the second / there is also written in the same chapter of
another womman that is called Palmarya / the which was one of the sustres of
penance. I shall tell you this womman Palmarya was hyghly set in a wicked
hate against this holy maid / so ferforthe that she dyffamed her wretchedly /
wherefore our lord gaf her first a sykenes in her body. Afterward she began to
perysshe body and soul / so that she might not esha^e dampnacyon / but if this
holy maid Katheryne by perfyte pacyence that charity formyd in her soul / had
prayed for her as it is rehearsed in the same for the chapter of the second
party. Also there was another suster of penance / that was called Andrea as
it is written in ye same chapter / the which had in her breast a foul stynkyng
kancre / yt there was never one yt would minystre to her for stenche Of this
herd this holy maid / and she came to ye syke wo^man and served her gladly
without any squeymousnes / in washyng and wypyng of her wound / and when she
felt in her self any manner squeymousnes she would then put her nose to ye
wound long time to gyds unto ye time her body defaylled / but ye lothenes went
away there by. Then ye fend Satan entered in to ye syke suster / and made
her to grutche with this holy maid and for to have her in suspeccion / and so
wood she was with her yt she sclau^dred her openly to her susters and said that
she had sinned flesshely and lost her maydenhode.

Al be it that this holy maiden and vyrgyn was heavy of this shlaunder: yet she
left never her service to her / but over came by meke seruyse and mighty pacy
ence her malice / and went to prayer as for a souerayn remedy against such
accusacions / at the last by grace of this holy maid and vyrgyns prayers and
by ye merytes of her strong patience / this seek suster saw this holy maid
and vyrgyn in time of her prayers transformed a fore her in to a great light
that she had thereby great comfort and repented here of her falls accusacion
Tha^ she called this holy maid and vyrgyr to her and asked her forgyuenes af
her cursed accusacion and all other to whom she had shlaundred her / she sent
after and told them that she had falsely accused this holy maid and
vyrgyn wherefore she asked them forgyuenes / and then she told them what
she saw of this holy maid and vyrgyn affermyng to them all that she was not
only a pure maid and virgyn but also an holy maid and vyrgin Loo dear friends
there the fend went to the fame this holy maid and vyrgyn by his malycious
excitacio^ / there he magnefyed her virtuous name all against his will: yet
all this our reverend lord almighty god by medytacion of the virtue of
patience that was in her / Then from that time forward this holy vyrgyns name
encrecyd so hyghely among the people / that it come to the audyence of two
popes which were in her time and many cardynals /

Ferthermore of another thing I shall tell you the which is written in the
same chapyter of the same woman Andrea. It befell in a time when this holy may
de and vyrgyn wasshyd and wyped her stynkyng wound / The fend made her so
skeymous that her stomach was meruey lously steryd for to cast with that she
aroos and said to her sefl thus Trewely wretch thou that art so skaymous off
thine susters sykenes: leave it well thou shall receive the fylte of her wound
with in thyn own body / Then she went and wysshe that stynkyng wound and
received the fylthe that came there fro in to a dysshe and went a side and
drank it of The next night after our reverend lord apperyd to her and said:
Daughter in this deed thou passyst in mine syngh / And thou have thereby pleasyd
me more than in any work that ever thou dedest And therefore by cause thou have
do so merueylously a deed for my love / I shall give the a merueylous drink
by the which thou shall be had in great merueyle among all creatours with
that as it seemed to her he putt her mouth to ye reverend wound of his sweet
blody side / And said daughter drink ynongh of the drink of mine side that is
merueylous and delectable by the which not oonly thyn soul but thyn boody
shall be fulfilled the which thou have despised for mine love / Fro that time
forword her s^omake had none appetyte to any matery al mete ne it night not
defye any mete and that was none merueyle For where that any creature has
received drink habundauntly of the well of life / what merueyle is it though it
need none help of other bodily mete / Out of this grace came that merueylous
fast the which is rehersyd in the first Chapter off the second party:
Wherefore was all this grace granted trow ye dear friends trewely for the
charytable pacyens that she had to syke folk and to all other for the great
charity that was so habou^daunt in her heart received and took the word of life
ye which brought forth fruit in patience that is thrytty fold fruit: syxty
fold fruit and an hundred fold fruit Thrytty fold fruit she brought forth
by paciens that she showed to Cecca the leprous woman / syxty fold fruit she
brought forth by patience that she showed to Palmarya / and an hundred fold
fruit she brought forth by the patience that she showed to Andrea this last
seek suster / Now I shall I tell you of sum things that been not rehearsed in
ye book before uneath was there any body that had conuersacio^ with this holy
maid and vyrgyn / but that they deed to her many iniutyes and wrongs one way
or other / so that there was one of the friars that was so fulfilled with the
fend that in the presens of all her susters he put to her full reproues and
defamacio^s She was never the more meued out off paciens but she charged her
susters that they should not trouble him ne tell nothing afterward to other
thar should soune to her repreff / what that ever they herd him speak the more
pacient the holy maid and vyrgyn was / ye more wood was he against her so that
in a time he stale her monye that was given to her for to do alms with / yet
for all this she was notfynge steryd but kept always patiently her charity /
and so at the last over came him by her patience /

Ouermore if I should tell you of the great patience that she had in suffering
of diverse infyrmytes of the body: my pain should not oonly fail me but also
mine understanding / she suffered ever co^tynuelly the pain of ylica passyo as
it is rehearsed in the vj / Chapter of the second party / where is declared
and told clerly the cause why she had that infirmyte / And therwyth she
had a pain in the head contynuelly /

And above all this she had a synguler continuell pain in her breast fro
that day that our reverend lord almighty god made her taste pains of his
precious passion as it is rehersyd in the vj / Chapter of the second party:
That same pain in her breast left with her the which passed all her other
bodily pains And yet more over with all these pains she had de right often the
feueres /

For all these pains she showed never sorry there / but ever glad there to
all folk and never pleyned her /

But all those that came to her to be comforted she comforted them with word
if it need were notwythstondynge her great infyrmytes she would labor for
them so that her sickness should not let to her. But that she would arise
out of her bed and traueyle both for her bodily hele and ghostely hele as it
is rehersyd in the vij / Chapter of the second party:

Ferthermore what pain she suffered of fendes it may not lyghtely be told
you by cause it was so often: It is touched before in the second Chapter of the
second party how often she was cast off fendes in to the fire albe it she was
in no wise I hurt / But specially of one thing Master Reymound bears
record yt in a time that he and certain of his brethren were out for the
health of sowles And this holy maid and virgyn with them and as they came
homward again a little a thyshalf the Cite of Seen / this holy maid and virgyn
for werynesse was set upon an horse / she had not ryden but a little time
that the fend drew here down in to a pyt^e so that the ^y^st that came to the
ground was her head: when master Reymou^de perceived that he cried help of
our glorious lady glorious virgyn Mary and came and found this holy maid and
virgyn all smelyng as she lay and despysynge the fend and she had none harm:
but she said to Master Reymound loo ye fend has do this / Then she was
take up and set upon the horse again eftsoon / And she rode not as ferve as
a man might shete an arow^ but that the send had eftsoon throw her down in
to a foul fenne or lake and the horse lay upon her side / Then she smelyd
and said this horse warmeth well my side there I suffer ^he pain of ylica
passio / and so she s^^rned the fend and had none harm / Master Reymound
and his fe law then took her up and would no more suffer her ride but ladde
her betwyne them both. By cause also they were nyghe the ^yte / Yet the cursed
fend / would not ase but always he tourmentyd her and drew her now on that
one side / now on that other side / And but ^he had be hold she should have
fall to the ground / Nevertheless always in suffryng of such tourmentis she
showed e^uer glad pacient chere and despised the fend / After such I^^usyons
followed great profyght of souls as it is made mention of the vij chapter of
the second party: And that knew well the fend wherefore he tourmentyd her in
that ^ wise that he did. And right as these tourmentis beren witness of her
great pacyence: Right so they may well bear witness that she was and is an
holy maid and vyrgyn in suffryng of them as it is openly declared in the
second chapter off the third party where it is rehearsed that she ended her
bodily life in such martyrdom / Ensample hereof I may tell you dear friends of
Saint Antony when he was in deserte he knew well that martyr dome was a
sovereign thing in the sight of our reverend l^rde almighty god and therefore
he desired martyrdom whom our reuer^nd lord almighty god suffered to be
tormentyd of ^endes for a martyrdom but yet he left not his bodily lyff for
such tourment / This holy maid and vyrgyn was so vyolently tormented by such
pains that she ended her bodly lyff with them ever thankyng our reave rend
lord almighty god. This was a geete token of holiness for to suffer martyrdom
of fendes:

Loo dear friends now have ye herd the virtue of paciens which this holy maid
and virgyn used wherefore she is oned and spoused to our reverend lord
almighty god sweet ^hesu Christ in the bl^sse off heaven / And thus I make an
end of this recapytulacion of this holy book to the honor and worship of
our glorious reverend lord almighty god all the ^euerend Trynyte / Cui
referantur lauds / honor e^ gloria in scla^ sclo^^^ Amen /

Here ends the lyff of that glorious vyrgyn and Martyr saint Katheryn off
Seen /
Here begynnen the reuelacio^s of Saint Elysabeth the kings daughter of
hungarye /
ON a day when saint Elisabeth was in preuy prayer: and sought her spouse Ihesu
Christ / with devout heart and drery spyryte: and found him not / as she was
wounte / She began to think her and egerly to syghe in her soul what were the
cause that her spouse vysy ted her not by insendynge of sweet comfortes / as he
was wont to do other times / And when she stylye dysposed her to goo to sum
spyrytualle brother for to have counseylle thereof: The blessed maiden marye
apperyd to her and said Elysa^eth yff thou would ^ee my dyscyple / I would be
thy maystres / and if you would be my servant: I would be thy lady / To whom
Elysabeth said / Lady who be ye that would have me dyscyple and s^^uaunt / To
whom maid Marye answered I am mother to the sone of god a live / whom thou have
chosen to be thy lord and spouse / Then she said there is no brother in the
world that may better inform the of thy spouse / than I may Then Saint
Elysabeth faylyng upon the earth / honouryd her and kneling she laid her
hondes ionyd to gyder bytwyxte the hondes of the blessed virgyn And eftsonys

By process of time in the feste of saint Soolaste. whiles Elysabeth Crystis

this thou shall love thy neyggbour as thy self / Thou shall love thy ^rende /
and thou shall have thyn enemy In hatred / man and good angel / I understand

hatred is of thy enemy that is the devil and sin /

Therefore if thou wylt get this love: do as I did in the temple in the

The first was that he would give me grace / thorugh the which he would give

After that he tou^^edand ordained with the finger of his ghost all my saweys

All this things my dear daughter the which I asked were granted to me as
thou may understand by the Angellys salutacyon / which I was haylled of
Gabryell the Angel.

Another time as Elisabeth Cristys servant stood in prayer and thought how /
much grace god hadd done to the glorious vyrgyn mary. She apperyd to her and
said my daughter thou thynkest that I had so much grace without traueylle of
my creator / but it is not so out / take the grace of halowynge in my mods
womb. All other grace I had with much travel of soul and body contynually
prayeng day and night with fulle brennyng desire and weeping with full bitter
morning / and ever thynkyng spekyng and workyng that I trowed were / most
plesyng to my creator Eschewing with sovereign keeping me fro all offenses of
him / ye were it never so little and. then she said / have thou for certain
/ daughter that no moystour of pleasyng devotion or gift of grace or virtue
desce^dyth perfytely from god in to man's heart but by devout prayer of soul
and sharp bodily traueyll: For after that a man perfytely offers to god two
mytes the / which he has that is his soul and his body and ordeyneth him to
his seruyse and honor our lord god of his high graces begins to glad:
that man's soul in so much that he n ay not bear it / but for swetnes and
for wondryng it fares as it were in hit self / as a man that were drunk of
sweet wine and mighty / put out of him self that may not bear it for
feblynes of head.

And then that soul knowed that she has no thing down pleasyng to god for
to have so great comfort before.

And she holds more under vile / and more worthy dyspyte / then ever she
held her before / but afterward when such a soul torneth again to her
self / she yeldeth thankynges and louynges to god / with devotion and affection
of will / and woldeth her unworthy of grace. And with much dread storeth her
self as unkind ageynste so great a benefactour.

And god seyeng her ever wax more meke thorught the gifts that she receives
/ he took more head to give her moogyftes of grace in so much / that as it
were that he fulfilled her desire in this world. So that her thinks / that
her dwelling is in heaven with god / and not in earth with men here / and
thynked also that she has paradyse in her self.

So I knowleche that it befyll with me while I lived in earth / and when I
was all brennyng in gods love / and felyd so much swetenes in him / that
for him all the world was vile to me / Ones when I was a lone with devotion
in my preuy chamber.

Loo suddenly the Angel Gabryell stood by me / and as the Gospel seyth /
sheylled me and said. Aue gracia plena etc. Off the which salutacyon when I
herd it first / I was fer^e / but afterward that I was comfor^ed with his
holy and sweet speech and made seker / not doubtyng these things to be sothe
that he showed. I fill to the earth / and knelynge with my hondes ioynde I
honored and said. Ecce ancilla domini. fiat michi secundum verbum tuum. That
is to say. Loo here the servant of god / be it done to me after thy word.
The which word said anon I was rauysshed / and in so great fullness of
gods grace enbasshed me that I never felt so much sweetness and comfort
in my soul.

And in that rauysshyng gods son took flesh of my puryst blood / with
out any wem of me / or (...) delight.

The cause why god deed this grace to me / was feyth and mekenes / with which
I troweth in fulfeyth the Aungellys words / and meked me and dressed me all to
gods will. And therefore he wouchesaue to give me so much grace.

And so thou my daughter in all things that god heteth or does to the /
have thou not in mistrowyng / ne yensto^d him not seyeng lord / why do thou
this to me. But by exsample of me say.

Ecce ancilla domini etc. And any time be not fulfilled / as it is hight to the
or else it is taken fro the that was given to the of god. Blame thy own self
/ and think that thou have done sum trespass before the syghte of gods
mageste / for the which gods sentence is changed for he has will to
purchase the life wythouten end / he needs to be buxom of heart to the
commandments and love him self to god / by very meekness and obedyence /
for the contrayous of tho sins / pride and Inobedyence of our fore faders
Adam and Eve / for the which they lost the grace and the dygnyte that they
were made in.

Over that then in another time on the vygyle of the natyuyte of our lord /

as saint Elysabeth prayed / and in her prayeng she thought with devotion of
soul and in what wise the blyssed maid prayed as she had showed her as it is
said before.

The blyssed maid answered her / In prayeng daughter I did as he that will
new make a fair well / first he gothe to the root of the hill under which
the water spryngeth / and herken^th besyly vn^ what side the veins of water
gothe / and when he sought him by herkynge / then he begins to delue in
that side of the hill till he find an able beginning of a welstede fro the
spryngyng veins / and afterward he dressyth water in to the well stead / the
which he makes large and fair and clean After that he makes a wall all
about the well / and in the mids of the well a stone pylar fastened in it
pypes all about thorugh the which the water may pass out of each half / more
prop^^tably to the use of men. This did I ghostely / for then went I to the
hill / where I besyly herkened and learned the law of moses / and all the x
commandementes / Then fond I the vein of water when I learned in redyng
thynkyng and prayeng that the wellhede and beginning of all good is for to

show / when I conceived a styff desire to love all things that god loves /

b^usome to my wrongs* he shall find grace and heeale thorugh my procuryng*
And certainly wit thou daughter that he that loves me not. may find no
grace of my sone: and as it follows thereby another of the fader ne of holy
ghost / These things my dear daughter I say to the that thou learn to ask
grace of god in prayer with faith and meekness as thou knew that I did by

god /

Neuerthelater virtues and grace bennot given of god to all I like: For whi
they can not ask them alyke off god al in prayer* In mekenes and faith ne

prayer / that echosen come to other that god has give to him and take off
other that he has not him self.

Wherefore daughter I would that thou pray besely / not only for thyn own
heal / but also of other / For there by shall grace be encresyd to the and to
other: And thy prayers shall be fruytfull / It happened that Elysabeth was

full mind of all her sins. and when she shroue her to any other confessor /
She had uneaths mind what she should say: She was not glad and iocunde
after her assoyling* as wha^ she shroue her to Saint Johan /

It befyll on a day that Elysabeth gods servant suffered a great notable
wrong of another wicked woman / wherefore as to mennys sight / She was gretely
dysplesyd. At the last when she came again to her self and thought that she

For they sins / and satysfaction is fully made to him / for them all / after

have offendyd with all thy body / My body was shorged so that from the sole of
the foot unto the tope of my head / apperyd in me no stead hole.

Therefore daughter think not but that dew satysfaccion for thy sins* is do
full right wysly to god my fader: Sothely I ^uffred the pains of all sinful
and the wrongs of them / I bare in my heart that did not sin / ne gyle was
founden in my mouth:

On another time when Elysabeth gods servant was prayeng / Suddenly she saw
with her ghostely eyes: a full fair hand that had long fyngers and the
palm large and broad: And in the mids of the palm was a wound all read of
blood / And as soon as she understood that it was the hand of Christ: She
wondrede that it was so small and so long / And also ne it was answerde to
her* that it was so small / For which christ lived in flesh / On nyghtes when
he prayed / he held his hondes streyth forth / And on days* he t^aueyled with
hondes and his fete / and all his body by tounes and castellys prechynge the
kingdom of god. And after this she herd a voice saying to her / Elysabeth loo
/ This third time I say to the / thy sins ben fogyuen / And thou have my
grace: To the which voice she answerde. Lord if I be hallowed as thou sayste
whero^ is it that I may not wythholde me but that I offend thy mayeste each
day in sum thing

And the voice said to her / For if thou no time offended / thou should not
be so mocho mekyd / And by that I followed / that thou would not love me so
much. And thus thou sholdest wax worse then fendes that both trusts and

Therefore I have not so haloweth / ye but that thou may sin* But it
suffyseth to the that I have give the so much grace: that would suffer thy
self be slain rather then thou sholdest offe^de dedely: And when this was
said / Christ apperyd to her openly / And her thought that thyke lopred blood
largely flowed out of his side / wherefore she began to / wonder / To whom
Christ said daughter wonder the not For why when I hangyd on the cross all my
membrys were dysioynyd out of ioynte for undone trespass / And mine entrayles
were broken and my veins opened / And therefore so haboundaunt and thyke
lopered b^ode followed out of my side / All these things before said. Sayn^
Elysabeth a boute the endyng of her lyff / the which was in the year of Our
lord a M CClxi affermyng that she had seyn and herd. as it is above wryton.
And she said that she had so great certain off them all / that she would
rather suffer death the^ ne to doubt any little part of them that they were
not true.

Here ends the reuelacyons of saint / Elysabeth the kings daughter of
hu^garye /
Enprynted at westemynster by Wynkyn. de word.
